_Thought for 41s_

Agent 1 report. I am using the coordinator brief as the assignment source. 

## 1. Clean Gate 1 theorem

Let \(Q\ge e^e\) be the main height/complexity parameter. Let

\[
I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X,\qquad X\subset[-X_0,X_0],
\]

where \(X_0\asymp 1\), and where \(\lambda\) is the packet scale:

\[
\lambda=d \quad\text{in the ordinary same-scale packet regime},
\]

and

\[
\lambda=c \quad\text{in the singular/shallow packet regime}.
\]

Define the normalized canonical source-curvature function

\[
F_\lambda(x)
:=
\lambda^3 q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)=\lambda^{-3}F_\lambda(x).
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
=
\lambda^{-5}\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Therefore the physical Gate 1 estimate

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

is exactly equivalent to the normalized estimate

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge
Q^{-B}\lambda^6 |X|.
}
\]

The clean theorem to prove is therefore:

### Gate 1, normalized form

For every admissible off-line packet interval \(I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X\), with \(\lambda=d\) in the ordinary regime and \(\lambda=c\) in the singular regime, the actual canonical source curvature satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\int_X
\left|
\lambda^3 q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
\right|^2
\,dx
\ge
Q^{-B}\lambda^6 |X|.
}
\]

No proxy object is allowed here. The object is

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

In particular, this is not the affine-subtracted complement curvature \(q''_{\source,R}\), not a zero-kernel toy model, and not a free Dirichlet polynomial.

---

## 2. Minimal finite-jet anti-design theorem

The interval estimate follows from a finite-jet anti-design estimate plus standard analytic-complexity control.

Let

\[
R=R(Q)
\]

with either

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or, more conservatively,

\[
R(Q)=C_R\log Q.
\]

The finite-jet theorem should be stated as follows.

### Finite-jet Gate 1 theorem

There exist constants \(B_{\jet},C_R>0\) such that, for every admissible packet interval and every distinguished packet point \(x_\ast\in X^\circ\), one has

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\partial_x^r F_\lambda(x_\ast)
\right|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\jet}}\lambda^3.
}
\]

Equivalently, in physical \(m\)-coordinates,

\[
\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x)
=
\lambda^{r+3}
\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
=
\lambda^{r+3}q_{\can}^{(r+2)}(m_0+\lambda x),
\]

so the same statement is

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\lambda^{r+3}q_{\can}^{(r+2)}(m_\ast)
\right|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\jet}}\lambda^3.
}
\]

After cancelling the common \(\lambda^3\), this can also be written as

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\lambda^r q_{\can}^{(r+2)}(m_\ast)
\right|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\jet}}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest local anti-design target.

---

## 3. Interval anti-design theorem

A slightly stronger but more directly useful version avoids dependence on a distinguished point.

### Interval anti-design theorem

For every admissible interval \(X\), there is a point \(x_\ast\in X^\circ\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\jet}}\lambda^3.
}
\]

Together with analytic-complexity control, this implies

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge
Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

This is probably the most convenient theorem for Agents 2 and 3, because it allows the proof to find non-flatness anywhere in the packet rather than exactly at \(x=0\).

---

## 4. Failure of Gate 1 implies finite-jet flattening

The main reduction is contrapositive.

Assume the normalized Gate 1 estimate fails:

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
<
Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

Then, under the analytic-complexity package

\[
\sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^rF_\lambda|
\le
Q^{C_r}
\qquad
0\le r\le R+1,
\]

on a fixed enlargement \(X^\ast\supset X\), one obtains for every \(x_\ast\) in a slightly shrunken interval \(X_-\subset X\),

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\le
Q^{-B'}\lambda^3
}
\]

provided \(B\) is chosen sufficiently large compared with \(B'\), \(R\), and the analytic-complexity exponents \(C_r\).

Thus:

\[
\text{Gate 1 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{finite-jet source flattening}.
\]

So a finite-jet anti-design theorem rules out Gate 1 failure.

---

## 5. Proof sketch of the reduction

Let \(X_-\Subset X\) and let

\[
\delta=\operatorname{dist}(X_-,\partial X)>0.
\]

For analytic \(F_\lambda\), local Sobolev/Bernstein/Cauchy control gives

\[
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|^2
\le
C_{r,\delta}
\left(
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
+
\sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^{R+1}F_\lambda|^2 \cdot \epsilon^{2(R+1-r)}
\right)
\epsilon^{-2r-1}
\]

for any \(0<\epsilon<\delta\). Choosing

\[
\epsilon=Q^{-C_\epsilon}
\]

and using the polynomial derivative bound

\[
\sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^{R+1}F_\lambda|
\le
Q^{C_{R+1}},
\]

one can make the high-derivative remainder smaller than \(Q^{-B'}\lambda^3\), provided \(R\) is chosen logarithmic and \(B\) is large enough.

Therefore, if

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda|^2
<
Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|,
\]

then all derivatives up to order \(R\) are polynomially small on \(X_-\). This is exactly the source-flattening event.

Hence the logical chain is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-jet anti-design}
+
\text{analytic complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## 6. Minimal analytic-complexity assumptions

The reduction does not need detailed zeta arithmetic. It only needs a finite-order regularity package.

A sufficient package is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{x\in X^\ast}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x)|
\le
Q^{C_r},
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q)+1.
}
\]

In physical coordinates this is

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
|\lambda^{r+3}q_{\can}^{(r+2)}(m)|
\le
Q^{C_r},
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q)+1.
}
\]

For \(R(Q)=O(\log Q/\log\log Q)\), this is a mild finite-order package.

For \(R(Q)=O(\log Q)\), the constants are larger but still polynomially trackable if the zero/prime tails are organized into polynomial-complexity core plus controlled residual.

---

## 7. Ordinary packet regime

In the ordinary same-scale regime,

\[
\lambda=d,
\]

where \(d\) is the local packet scale. After normalization,

\[
m=m_0+dx,
\]

nearby same-scale zero contributions become kernels of the schematic form

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

Their derivatives satisfy

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)
=
n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Thus finite-jet source flattening becomes the trigonometric anti-design condition

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

The ordinary-regime Gate 1 problem is therefore equivalent to proving that actual zeta packets cannot realize such a same-scale sine anti-design to polynomial accuracy.

Clean ordinary anti-design target:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\ad}}.
}
\]

Here \(\mathcal B_k\) denotes the contribution of the canonical background, regularized tails, dual AFE terms, and other nonlocal canonical corrections.

Without actual zeta arithmetic this is false, because deterministic positive quadrature can make

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0
\]

for all \(3\le k\le R+3\).

So the ordinary packet theorem must be genuinely arithmetic.

---

## 8. Singular packet regime

In the singular or shallow regime,

\[
\lambda=c.
\]

The normalized coordinate is

\[
m=\gamma+cx.
\]

A single dominant shallow term gives

\[
q''_{\can}\sim c^{-3},
\]

so

\[
F_c(x)=c^3q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
\]

is order \(1\), not small. Therefore singular packets are harmless unless there is same-scale cancellation among singular contributors.

Thus the singular regime splits cleanly.

### Singular dominance case

If one shallow contributor dominates, then

\[
\int_X |F_c(x)|^2\,dx
\gg |X|,
\]

which is much stronger than

\[
\int_X |F_c(x)|^2\,dx
\ge
Q^{-B}c^6|X|.
\]

### Singular cancellation case

If singular dominance fails, then the normalized singular packet again satisfies a finite-jet source-flattening condition:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_c(x_\ast)|
\le
Q^{-B'}c^3.
\]

Thus the singular regime reduces to the same anti-design theorem as the ordinary regime, but with \(\lambda=c\).

So no separate singular Gate 1 theorem is needed. One theorem covering arbitrary admissible \(\lambda\in\{d,c\}\) suffices.

---

## 9. Strongest clean reduction statement

The project can now use the following theorem as the formal target.

### Theorem A: finite-jet anti-design implies Gate 1

Assume the canonical normalized source curvature

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)
\]

satisfies the analytic-complexity package

\[
\sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^rF_\lambda|
\le
Q^{C_r},
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q)+1.
\]

Assume further that for every admissible packet interval there exists \(x_\ast\in X^\circ\) such that

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\jet}}\lambda^3.
\]

Then there exists \(B>0\) such that

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge
Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

---

## 10. Converse diagnostic

The useful contrapositive is:

### Theorem B: Gate 1 failure produces finite anti-design

Assume the same analytic-complexity package. If

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
<
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\]

then in normalized variables,

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
<
Q^{-B'}\lambda^3
\]

for every \(x_\ast\in X_-\Subset X\), after weakening \(B\) to \(B'\).

In ordinary same-scale coordinates this implies

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
=
O(Q^{-B'})
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Thus Gate 1 failure forces an actual-zeta same-scale anti-design.

This is the precise reduction Agents 2 and 3 should attack arithmetically.

---

## 11. What Agent 1 concludes

The minimal theorem is not the full interval estimate directly. The correct proof target is the finite-jet anti-design statement:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-B_{\jet}}\lambda^3.
}
\]

The key reduction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{actual-zeta same-scale source anti-design}.
}
\]

Therefore, proving that actual zeta arithmetic forbids the anti-design proves Gate 1.

The remaining non-formal input is arithmetic, not local analytic geometry:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta zeros/primes cannot realize the sine-quadrature flattening pattern}
}
\]

to polynomial accuracy at depth

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or, conservatively,

\[
R(Q)=O(\log Q).
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-26 18:55:03)

I’ll run the Agent 1 recurrence-budget lane only: codimension, tube volume, recurrence time, and whether the budget is plausibly polynomial or larger.

_Thought for 29s_

Agent 1 / A report. Task source: finite prime-phase recurrence budget for Gate 1 anti-design. 

## 1. Model

Use the prime phase torus

\[
\Theta_P(m)
=
\bigl(e^{-im\log p}\bigr)_{p\le P}
\in \mathbb T^{N},
\qquad N=\pi(P).
\]

A bad Gate 1 event requires simultaneous smallness of

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\]

and

\[
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

On the AFE side,

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Ignoring \(E_2\) for the recurrence-budget model, the jet constraints become a finite collection of real equations in the prime phases:

\[
\mathcal F_r(\Theta_P(m);m)+B_{2,r}(m)+D_{2,r}(m)\approx 0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Here

\[
\mathcal F_r
\sim
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\log n)^r n^{-im},
\]

after applying the relevant normalization \(\Delta^r\partial_m^r\).

The recurrence question is therefore:

\[
\Theta_P(m)
\in
\mathcal T_\varepsilon,
\]

where \(\mathcal T_\varepsilon\subset\mathbb T^N\) is an \(\varepsilon\)-tube around the bad jet locus, with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C}.
\]

---

## 2. Codimension count

There are \(R+1\) real jet constraints:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)\approx0,\quad
\Delta\partial_m q''_{\can}(m)\approx0,\quad
\dots,\quad
\Delta^R\partial_m^Rq''_{\can}(m)\approx0.
\]

The center condition \(Z_\alpha(m)=0\) contributes \(\kappa_Z\) real constraints.

The free transverse parameter \(\alpha\) removes one real constraint if \(\alpha\) genuinely ranges over an interval and enters nondegenerately.

Thus the effective codimension is

\[
\boxed{
K_{\eff}
=
(R+1)+\kappa_Z-1
=
R+\kappa_Z.
}
\]

Typical cases:

\[
\kappa_Z=1
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
K_{\eff}=R+1,
\]

\[
\kappa_Z=2
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
K_{\eff}=R+2.
\]

So, up to constants,

\[
\boxed{
K_{\eff}=R+O(1).
}
\]

If \(Z_\alpha=0\) can always be solved by choosing \(\alpha\), then \(\kappa_Z-1=0\) and

\[
K_{\eff}=R+1.
\]

If \(\alpha\) is not genuinely free, or if \(Z_\alpha\) imposes a complex condition, then

\[
K_{\eff}=R+2
\]

or slightly larger. None of these variants changes the main scaling.

---

## 3. Tube volume

Assume the bad-jet map has full rank \(K_{\eff}\) with respect to the active prime phases. Then an \(\varepsilon\)-tube around the bad locus has torus measure

\[
\mu(\mathcal T_\varepsilon)
\asymp
\varepsilon^{K_{\eff}}.
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C},
\]

this gives

\[
\mu(\mathcal T_\varepsilon)
\asymp
Q^{-C K_{\eff}}
=
Q^{-C(R+O(1))}.
\]

Therefore the expected Kronecker recurrence time is

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{\rec}
\asymp
\mu(\mathcal T_\varepsilon)^{-1}
\asymp
Q^{C(R+O(1))}.
}
\]

So the recurrence cost is

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{\rec}=Q^{O(R)}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\tau_{\rec}
=
\exp(O(R\log Q)).
\]

---

## 4. Plugging in expected jet depth

### Case 1: optimistic depth

If

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then

\[
\tau_{\rec}
=
Q^{O(\log Q/\log\log Q)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is super-polynomial in \(Q\), but far below \(\exp(cQ)\).

### Case 2: conservative depth

If

\[
R(Q)=O(\log Q),
\]

then

\[
\tau_{\rec}
=
Q^{O(\log Q)}
=
\exp(O((\log Q)^2)).
\]

Again, super-polynomial in \(Q\), but still subexponential in \(Q\).

Thus the recurrence cost is not merely \(Q^{O(1)}\), but it is also not as large as \(\exp(cQ)\) unless \(R\) is taken much larger.

---

## 5. Comparison with admissible height budget

Here the interpretation of \(Q\) matters.

If \(Q\) is essentially logarithmic height,

\[
Q\sim \log m,
\]

then the available height range up to \(m\le e^Q\) is exponentially large in \(Q\).

The recurrence time

\[
\tau_{\rec}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right)
\]

or even

\[
\exp(O((\log Q)^2))
\]

is much smaller than

\[
e^Q.
\]

So over the full height range, finite prime-phase recurrence is **too cheap** to rule out bad jets by volume alone.

In other words, a pure torus-volume/Kronecker heuristic predicts that there should be many approximate recurrences somewhere below height \(e^Q\).

If, however, the admissible comparison is only a local polynomial-in-\(Q\) search window, then

\[
\tau_{\rec}=Q^{O(R)}
\]

is too expensive for a local recurrence. But Gate 1 is a pointwise theorem over arbitrary admissible centers, not a local search problem. Therefore the global proof cannot rely merely on the fact that bad recurrences are not expected inside a short polynomial window.

---

## 6. Active dimension caveat

The above assumes the bad conditions cut codimension

\[
K_{\eff}=R+O(1)
\]

inside the active prime phase torus.

This requires at least

\[
N_{\eff}\ge K_{\eff}.
\]

If the effective number of independent active prime phases is smaller,

\[
N_{\eff}<K_{\eff},
\]

then the rank is capped:

\[
K_{\eff}\le N_{\eff}.
\]

In that case the recurrence cost is even cheaper:

\[
\tau_{\rec}
\asymp Q^{O(N_{\eff})}.
\]

Thus uncertainty in the active dimension does not rescue the finite recurrence argument. It either leaves the cost at \(Q^{O(R)}\) or makes it cheaper.

The only way to make recurrence genuinely prohibitive is to force a **full high-dimensional phase box** rather than a codimension-\(R\) tube. That would cost

\[
Q^{O(N_{\eff})},
\]

with \(N_{\eff}\gg R\). But the bad Gate 1 event is not obviously a full phase-box condition. It is a finite jet target, hence naturally codimension \(R+O(1)\).

---

## 7. Effect of main/dual/background terms

The background \(B_2\) shifts the jet target:

\[
\mathcal J_R[P_2+D_2](m_0)
\approx
-\mathcal J_R[B_2](m_0).
\]

The dual term \(D_2\) also shifts or couples the target. But unless \(D_2\) introduces a new independent phase system with a nontrivial incompatibility, these terms do not change the codimension count. They change the location and conditioning of the bad tube, not its volume exponent.

So at the recurrence-budget level:

\[
B_2,D_2
\quad\text{do not by themselves make recurrence expensive.}
\]

They only help if one proves a genuine main/dual incompatibility theorem, namely that the shifted target cannot be hit because the main and dual phases are arithmetically coupled in a rigid way.

That is outside plain recurrence volume.

---

## 8. Effect of \(Z_\alpha(m)=0\)

The condition \(Z_\alpha(m)=0\) is not enough, by itself, to make recurrence expensive.

If it contributes one real independent condition and \(\alpha\) is free, then it contributes essentially zero net codimension.

If it contributes two real independent conditions and \(\alpha\) is free, then it contributes one net codimension.

Either way,

\[
K_{\eff}=R+O(1).
\]

Therefore the recurrence time remains

\[
Q^{O(R)}.
\]

The \(Z_\alpha\) condition helps only if it is not merely an extra scalar constraint but is arithmetically correlated with the same prime phases in a way that forbids the jet target. That would again be a transversality or fixed-coefficient theorem, not a volume recurrence theorem.

---

## 9. Verdict

The recurrence budget is:

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{\rec}
\asymp Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp(O(R\log Q)).
}
\]

For

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{\rec}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}
\right)
\right).
}
\]

For

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

this is

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{\rec}
=
\exp(O((\log Q)^2)).
}
\]

This is too expensive for a local polynomial search, but too cheap globally if \(Q\sim\log m\) and the available height range is \(m\le e^Q\).

Final classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite prime-phase recurrence alone is too cheap to prove Gate 1.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-side Gate 1 needs extra fixed actual-zeta structure beyond Kronecker/volume recurrence.}
}
\]

The next viable inputs are therefore:

\[
\text{main/dual AFE incompatibility},
\]

\[
\text{Wronskian/transversality with a determinant lower bound},
\]

\[
\text{explicit-formula packet leakage},
\]

or

\[
\text{a global trace statistic coupled to }Z_\alpha.
\]

Plain finite phase recurrence does not rule out the bad anti-design.
## User (2026-04-26 18:59:26)

## Assistant (2026-04-26 18:59:27)

I’ll treat this as the Agent 1 / A prompt from the attached coordinator message: test whether \(Z_\alpha\) adds independent symbol rank to the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet system.

_Thought for 25s_

Agent 1 / A report. Task source: \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality test. 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ probably adds genuine symbol rank, but only on a sufficiently thick active block.}
}
\]

In the simplest canonical AFE model, the symbol ratio

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\]

is not polynomial in \(\log n\). It has the schematic form

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\approx
\frac{n^{-\alpha}}{\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2}
\cdot
\frac{V_\alpha(n/N)}{W_2(n/N)}.
\]

On a prime block \(n=p\), this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
\approx
\frac{p^{-\alpha}}{(\log p)^3}
\cdot
\frac{V_\alpha(p/N)}{W_2(p/N)}.
}
\]

As a function of

\[
u=\log p,
\]

this is roughly

\[
f_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}\cdot A_\alpha(u),
\]

where \(A_\alpha\) is a smooth AFE weight ratio.

This is not a polynomial in \(u\), nor close to one on a thick interval except with approximation error of order \(\exp(-O(R))\). For the intended depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

that gives separation at least

\[
\exp(-O(R))
=
Q^{-O(1/\log\log Q)},
\]

which is stronger than any required fixed polynomial lower threshold \(Q^{-C}\) after weakening constants.

So the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank contribution is real in the model.

The caveat is important: this conclusion requires a thick active block and nonvanishing AFE weights. If the active block contains only \(R+1\) usable frequencies, or lies in a log-width so small that Taylor interpolation becomes effectively exact, then the test becomes degenerate.

---

## 1. Active block

Use a prime block

\[
\mathcal B
=
\{p:\ u_- \le \log p\le u_+\},
\]

with

\[
u_+-u_-=\delta_u.
\]

The block must satisfy four conditions.

First, both symbols are non-negligible:

\[
|z_p(\alpha)|\ge Q^{-C_z},
\qquad
|c_p|\ge Q^{-C_c},
\qquad
p\in\mathcal B.
\]

Second, the AFE weights are not near zero:

\[
|V_\alpha(p/N)|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|W_2(p/N)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Third, the block contains more than \(R+1\) independent frequencies:

\[
|\mathcal B|\gg R+2.
\]

Fourth, the block has nontrivial logarithmic thickness:

\[
\boxed{
\delta_u=u_+-u_-\ge Q^{-C_\delta}
}
\]

and ideally

\[
\delta_u\asymp 1.
\]

If \(\delta_u\) is too small, then every smooth function of \(u\) becomes polynomial-like to high order by Taylor expansion, and the symbol transversality test loses force.

---

## 2. Simplest canonical AFE symbols

Model

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
\sim
\sum_n z_n(\alpha)e^{-im\log n}
+
\text{dual/background}.
\]

For the main AFE piece,

\[
z_n(\alpha)
\approx
n^{-1/2-\alpha}V_\alpha(n/N).
\]

For the prime-side source curvature,

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
\sim
\Re\sum_n c_n e^{-im\log n}
+
\text{dual/background},
\]

with the logarithmic derivative structure giving

\[
c_n
\approx
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}W_2(n/N).
\]

This is because, schematically,

\[
\log\zeta(s)
=
\sum_n\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\log n}n^{-s},
\]

and three \(m\)-derivatives contribute \((\log n)^3\), leaving

\[
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\log n}(\log n)^3
=
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\approx
\frac{n^{-\alpha}}{\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2}
\frac{V_\alpha(n/N)}{W_2(n/N)}.
}
\]

On primes,

\[
\Lambda(p)=\log p,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
\approx
\frac{p^{-\alpha}}{(\log p)^3}
\frac{V_\alpha(p/N)}{W_2(p/N)}.
}
\]

Let

\[
u=\log p.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
f_\alpha(u)
:=
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
\approx
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}A_\alpha(u),
}
\]

where

\[
A_\alpha(u)=\frac{V_\alpha(e^u/N)}{W_2(e^u/N)}.
\]

---

## 3. Polynomial-span test

The jet symbols of \(q''_{\can}\) are

\[
c_n(-i\log n)^r,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Thus \(Z_\alpha\) fails to add rank if

\[
z_n(\alpha)
\approx
c_n P(\log n)
\]

for some polynomial

\[
P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\approx
P(\log n).
\]

On the prime block, this asks whether

\[
f_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}A_\alpha(u)
\]

is approximable by degree-\(R\) polynomials in \(u\).

It is not exactly polynomial unless an impossible cancellation occurs in the AFE weight ratio \(A_\alpha(u)\).

In particular, ignoring the slowly varying \(A_\alpha\) first,

\[
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}
\]

is non-polynomial for every relevant \(\alpha\), including \(\alpha=0\), where it reduces to

\[
u^{-3}.
\]

So symbol degeneracy is not expected.

---

## 4. Quantitative separation

The desired estimate is

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
\left|
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
-
P(\log p)
\right|
\ge
Q^{-C}.
}
\]

A more natural analytic form is

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|f_\alpha-P\|_{L^\infty([u_-,u_+])}
\ge
\exp(-C R),
\]

provided:

\[
u_+-u_-\asymp 1,
\]

\[
u_-\gg1,
\]

and

\[
A_\alpha(u)
\]

is analytic/nonvanishing with controlled distortion on a fixed complex neighborhood of the block.

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this gives

\[
\exp(-CR)
=
Q^{-C/\log\log Q}
\ge
Q^{-C'}
\]

after weakening constants.

Therefore a polynomial separation of the required strength is plausible.

If instead

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

then

\[
\exp(-CR)=Q^{-O(1)},
\]

which is still compatible with a polynomial lower bound, but the constants become tight. This is another reason the depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

is safer for this route.

---

## 5. When the rank contribution degenerates

There are four degeneration modes.

### Degeneration 1: too few active frequencies

If

\[
|\mathcal B|\le R+1,
\]

then a degree-\(R\) polynomial can interpolate arbitrary values on \(\mathcal B\). In that case,

\[
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
\]

being non-polynomial is irrelevant.

So one needs

\[
|\mathcal B|\ge R+2
\]

at minimum, and preferably

\[
|\mathcal B|\gg R.
\]

### Degeneration 2: too narrow a block

If

\[
u_+-u_-=\delta_u
\]

is extremely small, then Taylor approximation gives

\[
f_\alpha(u)
=
T_R(u)+O\left(
\sup|f_\alpha^{(R+1)}|\delta_u^{R+1}
\right).
\]

If

\[
\delta_u^{R+1}
\ll Q^{-C},
\]

then \(f_\alpha\) becomes polynomial-like at the required resolution.

So the active block must satisfy something like

\[
\delta_u^{R+1}\ge Q^{-C}
\]

or more simply

\[
\delta_u\ge Q^{-C/R}.
\]

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this means

\[
\delta_u\ge \exp(-O(\log\log Q))=(\log Q)^{-O(1)}.
\]

A fixed-width block is more than enough.

### Degeneration 3: vanishing or unstable AFE weights

If

\[
W_2(p/N)
\]

is very small or crosses zero in the block, then the ratio

\[
z_p/c_p
\]

is not a stable symbol test.

Therefore the active block should be chosen away from transition/turning regions of the AFE weights.

### Degeneration 4: exact dual/background cancellation

The test above is for the main AFE symbols. Full canonical rank requires that the dual and background pieces do not algebraically reinsert \(Z_\alpha\) into the span of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jets.

That seems unlikely, but it is not excluded without the exact canonical AFE coefficients.

So the main-symbol result is Yellow, not Green.

---

## 6. Consequence for the Wronskian route

Let

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}
=
\Delta^j\partial_m^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

The main-symbol rows are approximately

\[
z_n(\alpha)
\]

and

\[
c_n(\log n)^j,
\qquad 0\le j\le R.
\]

The Wronskian has genuine symbolic rank on an active block if the vector

\[
(z_n(\alpha))_{n\in\mathcal B}
\]

is not in the span of

\[
(c_n(\log n)^j)_{n\in\mathcal B},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

After dividing by \(c_n\), this is exactly the condition

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\notin
\mathcal P_{\le R}(\log n).
\]

The model ratio

\[
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}A_\alpha(u)
\]

passes this test on thick active blocks.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ should add one genuine Wronskian row of rank.}
}
\]

But this only proves symbolic nondegeneracy. It does not yet prove the pointwise determinant lower bound

\[
|\mathcal W_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That remains a separate fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence problem.

---

## 7. Clean theorem candidate

A useful theorem for the next agent is:

### Symbol transversality theorem

Let \(\mathcal B\) be a prime block satisfying

\[
|\mathcal B|\gg R,
\qquad
u_+-u_-\ge (\log Q)^{-C},
\]

and suppose the main AFE weights satisfy

\[
Q^{-C}\le |V_\alpha(p/N)|, |W_2(p/N)|\le Q^C
\]

with controlled analytic distortion on the corresponding log block.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
\left|
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
-
P(\log p)
\right|
\ge
\exp(-C R).
}
\]

Consequently, for

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
\left|
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
-
P(\log p)
\right|
\ge
Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

This proves main-symbol transversality of \(Z_\alpha\) against the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows.

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rank contribution: real in the simplest canonical AFE model.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Degenerate only on too-small, too-thin, or weight-singular active blocks.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Full canonical verdict: Yellow, not Green, until exact }B_2,D_2,E_2
\text{ symbols are included.}
}
\]

The main useful conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ likely adds genuine Wronskian rank, but rank is not enough.}
}
\]

The remaining hard theorem is still the pointwise subset-product determinant/nonrecurrence bound for the resulting Wronskian.
## User (2026-04-26 19:02:57)

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:02:58)

I’ll run the Agent 1/A lane against the exact-symbol question. Since the paper’s precise AFE normalization is not present in the coordinator note, I’ll state the result in a convention-invariant way and isolate where convention-specific constants enter.

_Thought for 1m 4s_

Agent 1 / A report. Task source: exact \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality with canonical AFE weights. 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ adds genuine symbol rank only under a scale-normalized, thick-block hypothesis.}
}
\]

The simplified model

\[
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
\approx
p^{-\alpha}(\log p)^{-3}A_\alpha(\log p)
\]

is structurally correct. However, the previous “thick active block” condition needs sharpening.

If the active block has only **absolute** log-width

\[
L=u_+-u_-\asymp 1,
\qquad u=\log p,
\]

and if

\[
u_0\asymp Q,
\qquad \alpha\approx0,
\]

then

\[
u^{-3}
\]

is extremely well approximated by a degree-\(R\) polynomial on that short block. For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

Taylor approximation can be much smaller than any fixed \(Q^{-C}\). So exact symbol transversality is **not automatic**.

The rank contribution becomes polynomially visible if at least one of the following holds:

\[
\boxed{\alpha L \gtrsim R^{-C_0}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{L/u_0 \gtrsim R^{-C_0}}
\]

or the canonical AFE weight ratio

\[
A_\alpha(u)=\frac{V_{Z,\alpha}(u)}{V_q(u)}
\]

has non-polynomial variation of size \(\gtrsim R^{-C_0}\) on the block.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{main-symbol transversality is Yellow, not Green.}
}
\]

It is real in the exact AFE symbol model, but it requires a quantitative non-flatness condition on the active block or weight ratio.

---

## 1. Exact main-side symbol for \(Z_\alpha\)

Use the completed/Hardy-normalized off-line equation in the schematic form

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
Z_\alpha^{M}(m)+Z_\alpha^{D}(m)+Z_\alpha^{B}(m)+E_Z(m).
\]

The main AFE side has the form

\[
Z_\alpha^{M}(m)
=
\sum_{n}
z_n(\alpha;m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
z_n(\alpha;m)
=
\mathfrak a_Z(\alpha,m)\,
n^{-1/2-\alpha}
V_{Z,\alpha}\!\left(\frac{n}{N_Z(m,\alpha)};m,\alpha\right).
}
\]

Here:

- \(\mathfrak a_Z(\alpha,m)\) is a global completed-phase/gamma normalization independent of \(n\);
- \(V_{Z,\alpha}\) is the main AFE smoothing weight;
- \(N_Z(m,\alpha)\) is the usual saddle/conductor length;
- lower-order \(m\)-dependence of the weight is retained.

Since symbol-rank tests are invariant under nonzero row scalings, the \(n\)-independent factor \(\mathfrak a_Z(\alpha,m)\) may be removed.

Thus the operative main symbol is

\[
\boxed{
z_n(\alpha;m)
\sim
n^{-1/2-\alpha}
V_{Z,\alpha}\!\left(\frac{n}{N_Z}\right).
}
\]

---

## 2. Exact main-side symbol for \(q''_{\can}\)

The canonical object is

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

On the prime/AFE side, the oscillatory main contribution is log-derivative-like. Starting from

\[
\log\zeta(s)
=
\sum_n \frac{\Lambda(n)}{\log n}n^{-s}
\]

in the convergent half-plane and continuing by the canonical AFE/regularization, three \(m\)-derivatives contribute

\[
(-i\log n)^3.
\]

Thus the main oscillatory symbol of \(q''_{\can}\) is of the form

\[
q_{\can}^{\prime\prime,M}(m)
=
\sum_n c_n(m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
c_n(m)
=
\mathfrak a_q(m)\,
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}
V_q\!\left(\frac{n}{N_q(m)};m\right)
+
c_n^{\mathrm{amp}}(m).
}
\]

The term \(c_n^{\mathrm{amp}}\) denotes corrections from differentiating the \(m\)-dependent smoothing weights, saddle factors, and completed gamma normalization. These are lower-order in the normalized derivative calculus unless the block is chosen near a weight transition.

On a stable active block away from weight zeros and transition edges,

\[
\boxed{
c_n(m)
=
\mathfrak a_q(m)\,
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}
V_q\!\left(\frac{n}{N_q}\right)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(r))\right).
}
\]

Again, the \(n\)-independent factor \(\mathfrak a_q(m)\) may be row-normalized away.

---

## 3. Ratio on a prime block

Restrict to primes

\[
n=p,
\qquad u=\log p.
\]

Then

\[
\Lambda(p)=\log p=u.
\]

The main-symbol ratio is

\[
r_p(\alpha;m)
=
\frac{z_p(\alpha;m)}{c_p(m)}.
\]

Using the formulas above,

\[
\boxed{
r_p(\alpha;m)
=
C(\alpha,m)\,
\frac{p^{-\alpha}}{(\log p)^3}
\frac{
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z;m,\alpha)
}{
V_q(p/N_q;m)
}
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

Writing \(u=\log p\),

\[
\boxed{
r_\alpha(u)
=
C(\alpha,m)\,
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}A_\alpha(u;m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right),
}
\]

where

\[
A_\alpha(u;m)
=
\frac{
V_{Z,\alpha}(e^u/N_Z;m,\alpha)
}{
V_q(e^u/N_q;m)
}.
\]

After harmless row normalization at a base point \(u_0\), define

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_\alpha(u;m)}{A_\alpha(u_0;m)}.
}
\]

This is the correct object for symbol transversality. The raw ratio \(r_\alpha(u)\) may be exponentially small when \(\alpha u_0\gg1\), but row-normalization removes that irrelevant size.

---

## 4. Polynomial-span test

The \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows have symbols

\[
c_n(\log n)^j,
\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]

up to normalized derivative factors and lower-order amplitude corrections.

Therefore \(Z_\alpha\) is symbolically redundant precisely when

\[
z_n(\alpha)
\approx
c_nP(\log n)
\]

for some

\[
P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
r_n(\alpha)
\approx P(\log n).
}
\]

On a prime block \(\mathcal B\), the desired separation is

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
|\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

The normalized ratio is non-polynomial unless the weight ratio is specially degenerate. But non-polynomiality alone is not enough; degree-\(R\) polynomial approximation can be extremely accurate on short blocks.

---

## 5. Correct quantitative scale condition

Let

\[
u_0=\frac{u_-+u_+}{2},
\qquad
L=u_+-u_-.
\]

For

\[
\widehat r_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_\alpha(u)}{A_\alpha(u_0)},
\]

the intrinsic variation scale is approximately

\[
\boxed{
\sigma
=
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\left\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\right\|_{L^\infty([u_-,u_+])}
\right).
}
\]

If

\[
\sigma\ll R^{-C_0},
\]

then \(\widehat r_\alpha\) is effectively polynomial-like on the block, and the desired \(Q^{-C}\) separation can fail.

If

\[
\boxed{
\sigma\gtrsim R^{-C_0},
}
\]

then the degree-\(R\) polynomial separation is plausibly polynomial:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|\widehat r_\alpha-P\|_{L^\infty([u_-,u_+])}
\ge
\exp(-O(R\log R)).
}
\]

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R))=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

Thus the desired bound follows.

---

## 6. The main subtlety: short dyadic blocks

If the active block is a standard dyadic-style block in \(n\), then

\[
L=u_+-u_-\asymp 1.
\]

If also

\[
u_0\asymp Q
\]

and

\[
\alpha\approx0,
\]

and if the weight ratio \(A_\alpha\) is nearly constant, then

\[
\sigma\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Then Taylor approximation gives a degree-\(R\) polynomial error of size roughly

\[
O\left((L/u_0)^{R+1}\right)
=
O(Q^{-R-1}).
\]

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
\exp\left(
-\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}
\right),
\]

which is much smaller than \(Q^{-C}\).

Therefore the old statement

\[
L\asymp1 \Rightarrow Q^{-C}\text{ separation}
\]

is false in the \(\alpha\to0\), flat-weight case.

This is the principal correction.

---

## 7. Exact theorem candidate

A usable exact-symbol theorem should be stated as follows.

### Theorem candidate: normalized \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality

Let \(\mathcal B\) be a prime block

\[
\mathcal B=\{p:u_-\le\log p\le u_+\}
\]

with

\[
|\mathcal B|\ge C(R+2),
\]

and suppose the canonical AFE weights satisfy

\[
Q^{-C}\le
|V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)|,\ |V_q(p/N_q)|
\le Q^C
\]

on \(\mathcal B\), with controlled normalized derivatives through order \(R+1\).

Define

\[
\widehat r_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_\alpha(u)}{A_\alpha(u_0)}.
\]

Assume the non-flatness condition

\[
\boxed{
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_{L^\infty}
\right)
\ge R^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
|\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)|
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R).
}
\]

In particular, for

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
|\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)|
\ge Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

This proves that \(Z_\alpha\) contributes genuine Wronskian symbol rank under the stated non-flatness hypothesis.

---

## 8. Degeneration cases

### 8.1 Too few active frequencies

If

\[
|\mathcal B|\le R+1,
\]

then interpolation kills the test: any values of \(r_n\) can be matched by a degree-\(R\) polynomial.

So one needs

\[
|\mathcal B|\ge R+2,
\]

preferably with spacing/conditioning strong enough for stable Vandermonde estimates.

---

### 8.2 Too thin a log block

If

\[
\sigma
=
L\left(
|\alpha|+u_0^{-1}+\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty
\right)
\ll R^{-C_0},
\]

then \(r_\alpha\) is polynomial-like at degree \(R\).

This is not a technical nuisance; it is a real obstruction to the symbol test.

---

### 8.3 AFE weight zeros

If either

\[
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)
\]

or

\[
V_q(p/N_q)
\]

is small or crosses zero on the block, then the ratio

\[
r_p=z_p/c_p
\]

is unstable.

The active block must avoid AFE transition zeros and saddle-edge cancellation.

---

### 8.4 \(\alpha\to0\)

At \(\alpha=0\),

\[
\widehat r_0(u)
=
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_0(u)}{A_0(u_0)}.
\]

If \(A_0\) is flat and \(L\ll u_0/R^{C_0}\), this is too polynomial-like.

Thus \(\alpha\to0\) is a genuine degeneration unless compensated by weight-ratio variation or a wide relative log block.

---

### 8.5 Dual/background cancellation

The main-symbol test ignores the folded dual system and background terms.

The background \(B_2\) does not produce an \(n\)-symbol row, so it cannot by itself remove main-symbol rank; it shifts the target.

The dual term \(D_2\), however, may introduce a folded frequency block whose symbols interact with the main block. It is unlikely to make \(Z_\alpha\) polynomially dependent on the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows, but this is not excluded without the exact dual coefficients.

So the theorem remains Yellow until the main+dual symbol matrix is checked.

---

## 9. Consequence for Wronskian route

The Wronskian route wants the row

\[
Z_\alpha
\]

to be independent of

\[
q''_{\can},\ \mathcal Dq''_{\can},\dots,\mathcal D^Rq''_{\can}.
\]

Main-symbol independence is equivalent to

\[
\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)
\notin
\mathcal P_{\le R}(\log p)
\]

with polynomial separation.

The exact-symbol calculation gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{independence holds if the active block has enough intrinsic variation.}
}
\]

But it also gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{independence can become invisible on short, flat, }\alpha\approx0\text{ blocks.}
}
\]

So the next Wronskian sprint should not merely assume “thick block.” It must specify one of:

\[
\alpha L\gtrsim R^{-C_0},
\]

\[
L/u_0\gtrsim R^{-C_0},
\]

or

\[
L\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty\gtrsim R^{-C_0}.
\]

Without one of these, \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality may be too weak to support a polynomial determinant lower bound.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rank contribution: conditionally real.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact-symbol status: Yellow.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Primary obstruction: short-block polynomial approximation, especially when }\alpha\to0.
}
\]

The clean next target is not just

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}\notin \mathcal P_{\le R}(\log n),
\]

but the quantitatively scaled version:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
|\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)|
\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

under an explicit intrinsic-variation condition on \(\mathcal B\), \(\alpha\), and the canonical AFE weight ratio.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:06:09)

I’ll re-run Agent 1/A as a stricter exact-symbol pass. I’ll separate what is convention-invariant from what depends on the paper’s AFE normalization and state the actual obstruction cleanly.

_Thought for 14s_

Agent 1 / A report: exact \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality with canonical AFE weights. Source prompt cited here. 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ adds genuine symbol rank only after a quantitative non-flatness condition is imposed.}
}
\]

The exact main-symbol ratio still has the form

\[
\frac{z_p(\alpha)}{c_p}
=
C(\alpha,m)\,
p^{-\alpha}(\log p)^{-3}
A_\alpha(\log p;m)
\cdot
(1+\mathrm{lower\ order}),
\]

where

\[
A_\alpha(u;m)
=
\frac{V_{Z,\alpha}(e^u/N_Z;m,\alpha)}
     {V_q(e^u/N_q;m)}.
\]

So \(Z_\alpha\) is not symbolically redundant in principle. But the previous “non-polynomial, therefore separated” heuristic is too weak. On a short log-block, especially when \(\alpha\to0\), the ratio can be approximated by a degree-\(R\) polynomial much better than \(Q^{-C}\).

The correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Yellow: transversality is plausible, but only on active blocks with enough intrinsic variation.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Exact main-side symbol for \(Z_\alpha\)

Write the completed AFE main term schematically as

\[
Z_\alpha^{M}(m)
=
\sum_n z_n(\alpha;m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Up to an \(n\)-independent completed gamma/phase factor, the main coefficient is

\[
\boxed{
z_n(\alpha;m)
=
n^{-1/2-\alpha}
V_{Z,\alpha}\!\left(\frac{n}{N_Z(m,\alpha)};m,\alpha\right).
}
\]

Any global factor depending only on \((m,\alpha)\) can be ignored for row-rank purposes because it rescales the \(Z_\alpha\) row.

---

## 2. Exact main-side symbol for \(q''_{\can}\)

The canonical object is

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta'''.
\]

On the prime/log-derivative side,

\[
\log \zeta(s)
=
\sum_n \frac{\Lambda(n)}{\log n} n^{-s},
\]

and three \(m\)-derivatives contribute \((\log n)^3\). Hence the dominant main-side coefficient of \(q''_{\can}\) is

\[
\boxed{
c_n(m)
=
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}
V_q\!\left(\frac{n}{N_q(m)};m\right)
+
c_n^{\mathrm{amp}}(m).
}
\]

The amplitude-differentiation correction \(c_n^{\mathrm{amp}}\) comes from differentiating the \(m\)-dependent conductor, smoothing weights, and gamma normalization. On a stable block away from saddle edges and weight zeros,

\[
c_n^{\mathrm{amp}}
=
c_n^{\mathrm{main}}\cdot O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R)),
\]

after normalized differentiation.

---

## 3. Ratio on a prime block

Restrict to primes \(n=p\), with

\[
u=\log p.
\]

Since \(\Lambda(p)=\log p\), the main-symbol ratio becomes

\[
\boxed{
r_p(\alpha;m)
:=
\frac{z_p(\alpha;m)}{c_p(m)}
=
C(\alpha,m)\,
\frac{p^{-\alpha}}{(\log p)^3}
\frac{
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z;m,\alpha)
}{
V_q(p/N_q;m)
}
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
r_\alpha(u;m)
=
C(\alpha,m)\,
e^{-\alpha u}u^{-3}A_\alpha(u;m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

Normalize at a base point \(u_0\) to remove irrelevant row size:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha(u;m)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_\alpha(u;m)}{A_\alpha(u_0;m)}.
}
\]

The row-rank question is whether \(\widehat r_\alpha(u;m)\) lies near a degree-\(R\) polynomial in \(u\).

---

## 4. Symbol transversality condition

The \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols are

\[
c_n(\log n)^j,
\qquad 0\le j\le R.
\]

Therefore \(Z_\alpha\) is symbolically redundant exactly when

\[
z_n(\alpha)
\approx
c_nP(\log n)
\]

for some

\[
P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
r_n(\alpha)
\approx P(\log n).
}
\]

The desired transversality estimate is

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
\left|
\widehat r_\alpha(\log p;m)-P(\log p)
\right|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This does **not** follow merely from non-polynomiality.

---

## 5. Correct intrinsic-variation parameter

Let

\[
\mathcal B=\{p:u_-\le \log p\le u_+\},
\]

\[
u_0=\frac{u_-+u_+}{2},
\qquad
L=u_+-u_-.
\]

Define the intrinsic variation scale

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\mathcal B}
=
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha(u;m)\|_{L^\infty([u_-,u_+])}
\right).
}
\]

This measures how much the ratio actually varies across the active block after row-normalization.

If

\[
\sigma_{\mathcal B}\ll R^{-C_0},
\]

then \(\widehat r_\alpha\) is effectively polynomial-like on the block. Taylor interpolation can make the approximation error far below \(Q^{-C}\).

If

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\mathcal B}\gtrsim R^{-C_0},
}
\]

then a polynomial separation of size

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R))
\]

is plausible by divided-difference/Remez-type estimates. For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this gives

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R))=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

So the useful theorem is polynomially strong only under this intrinsic-variation hypothesis.

---

## 6. The corrected theorem candidate

### Exact-symbol \(Z_\alpha\)-transversality theorem

Let \(\mathcal B\) be a prime block satisfying

\[
|\mathcal B|\ge C(R+2),
\]

and suppose the AFE weights obey

\[
Q^{-C}
\le
|V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)|,\ |V_q(p/N_q)|
\le
Q^{C}
\]

on \(\mathcal B\), with normalized derivatives through order \(R+1\) bounded by

\[
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

Assume the intrinsic-variation condition

\[
\boxed{
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty
\right)
\ge R^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
\left|
\widehat r_\alpha(\log p;m)-P(\log p)
\right|
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R).
}
\]

Consequently, for

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one obtains

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B}
\left|
\widehat r_\alpha(\log p;m)-P(\log p)
\right|
\ge Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

This supplies genuine \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank for the normalized Wronskian.

---

## 7. Degeneration cases

### Too few active frequencies

If

\[
|\mathcal B|\le R+1,
\]

then a degree-\(R\) polynomial can interpolate the values on \(\mathcal B\). The rank test is void.

Required:

\[
|\mathcal B|\ge R+2,
\]

preferably with stable spacing.

### Too thin a log block

If

\[
L\left(
|\alpha|+u_0^{-1}+\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty
\right)
\ll R^{-C_0},
\]

then \(\widehat r_\alpha\) is too close to its Taylor polynomial. This is the main obstruction.

### AFE weight zeros

If either

\[
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)
\]

or

\[
V_q(p/N_q)
\]

is near zero, then the ratio is unstable. The active block must avoid transition zeros and saddle-edge cancellation.

### \(\alpha\to0\)

When \(\alpha=0\),

\[
\widehat r_0(u)
=
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_0(u)}{A_0(u_0)}.
\]

If \(A_0\) is flat and \(L/u_0\) is small, this is very well approximated by a degree-\(R\) polynomial. Thus \(\alpha\to0\) is a genuine degeneracy unless the block is relatively wide or the AFE weight ratio varies.

### Dual/background cancellation

The background \(B_2\) shifts the target but does not create a competing \(n\)-symbol row. It should not destroy main-symbol rank.

The dual term \(D_2\) is more serious. It creates a folded frequency system. Main-symbol transversality remains Yellow until the combined main+dual symbol matrix is checked.

---

## 8. Consequence for the Wronskian route

The normalized Wronskian row set is

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

At symbol level, \(Z_\alpha\) contributes a new row iff

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\notin
\mathcal P_{\le R}(\log n)
\]

with polynomial separation.

The exact-symbol calculation gives:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ contributes rank on intrinsically varying active blocks.}
}
\]

But it also gives:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha \text{ may fail to contribute usable polynomial rank on short, flat, }\alpha\approx0\text{ blocks.}
}
\]

So the Wronskian proof must either:

\[
\text{choose an active block satisfying } \sigma_{\mathcal B}\gtrsim R^{-C_0},
\]

or prove that admissible off-line centers force such a block.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact }Z_\alpha\text{-symbol transversality: Yellow.}
}
\]

It is not degenerate in the canonical main-symbol model, but a valid theorem needs the intrinsic-variation condition

\[
\boxed{
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty
\right)
\ge R^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Without this, a short-block Taylor-polynomial countermechanism can make the \(Z_\alpha\) row polynomially indistinguishable from the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows.

_Thought for 51s_

Agent 1 / A report: active-block intrinsic variation theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{An active block with visible }Z_\alpha\text{-symbol variation exists, provided low-prime AFE plateau blocks are admissible.}
}
\]

The previous short-block obstruction is real, but it is avoidable if the Wronskian construction is allowed to use a low-prime plateau block such as

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}(Q)=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\},
\qquad 0<a<b<\infty.
\]

On this block,

\[
u=\log p\asymp \log Q,
\qquad
L=u_+-u_-\asymp \log Q,
\]

so

\[
\frac{L}{u_0}\asymp 1.
\]

Therefore, even in the worst case

\[
\alpha=0,
\qquad
A_\alpha(u)\equiv \text{constant},
\]

the factor

\[
u^{-3}
\]

has enough relative variation to make

\[
\widehat r_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_\alpha(u)}{A_\alpha(u_0)}
\]

polynomially separated from \(\mathcal P_{\le R}\), with loss at worst

\[
\exp(-O(R)).
\]

At the safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is still

\[
Q^{-o(1)},
\]

hence stronger than \(Q^{-C}\) after weakening constants.

So the correct theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Active-block symbol variation is available on low-prime plateau blocks.}
}
\]

The caveat is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If the determinant route requires near-saddle or short log blocks only, the obstruction returns.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Canonical active blocks

Let the canonical AFE lengths be

\[
N_Z=N_Z(m,\alpha),
\qquad
N_q=N_q(m).
\]

Assume the usual high-conductor regime where, for fixed \(0<a<b\),

\[
Q^b\ll N_Z^\eta,
\qquad
Q^b\ll N_q^\eta
\]

for some fixed \(\eta>0\). Then the low-prime block

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{a,b}
=
\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\}
}
\]

lies deep inside the main AFE plateau.

On this block the AFE smoothing weights satisfy

\[
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)=1+O(Q^{-A_0}),
\]

\[
V_q(p/N_q)=1+O(Q^{-A_0}),
\]

after choosing \(A_0\) large enough, or more generally

\[
Q^{-C}\le |V_{Z,\alpha}|,|V_q|\le Q^C
\]

with normalized derivatives bounded.

The number of primes in the block is

\[
|\mathcal B_{a,b}|
\sim
\frac{Q^b}{b\log Q}
-
\frac{Q^a}{a\log Q},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal B_{a,b}|\gg R
}
\]

for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Thus the interpolation degeneracy

\[
|\mathcal B|\le R+1
\]

is avoided.

---

## 2. Ratio on the low-prime plateau

The canonical main-symbol ratio remains

\[
r_p(\alpha;m)
=
\frac{z_p(\alpha;m)}{c_p(m)}
\approx
C(\alpha,m)
\frac{p^{-\alpha}}{(\log p)^3}
\frac{V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z;m,\alpha)}
     {V_q(p/N_q;m)}.
\]

On the low-prime plateau,

\[
A_\alpha(u;m)
=
\frac{V_{Z,\alpha}(e^u/N_Z;m,\alpha)}
     {V_q(e^u/N_q;m)}
=
1+O(Q^{-A_0}),
\]

so after row-normalizing at \(u_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\left(1+O(Q^{-A_0})\right).
}
\]

The dangerous case is therefore

\[
\alpha=0,
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_0(u)
=
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
+O(Q^{-A_0}).
}
\]

This is still non-flat on a relative-width block.

---

## 3. Intrinsic variation estimate

For

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\},
\]

we have

\[
u_- = a\log Q,
\qquad
u_+ = b\log Q,
\]

\[
L=(b-a)\log Q,
\qquad
u_0=\frac{a+b}{2}\log Q.
\]

Hence

\[
\frac{L}{u_0}
=
\frac{2(b-a)}{a+b}
\asymp 1.
\]

The intrinsic variation parameter is

\[
\sigma_{\mathcal B}
=
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty
\right).
\]

Even if

\[
\alpha=0
\]

and

\[
\partial_u\log A_\alpha=0,
\]

one gets

\[
\sigma_{\mathcal B}
\ge
L u_0^{-1}
=
\frac{2(b-a)}{a+b}
\asymp 1.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\mathcal B}\ge c_{a,b}>0.
}
\]

In particular,

\[
\sigma_{\mathcal B}\ge R^{-C_0}
\]

for all large \(Q\).

Thus the intrinsic-variation condition is automatically satisfied on low-prime plateau blocks.

---

## 4. Polynomial separation on the low-prime block

Rescale

\[
t=\frac{u}{u_0}.
\]

Then \(t\) ranges over a fixed interval

\[
t\in[t_-,t_+]\subset(0,\infty),
\]

with

\[
t_+-t_-\asymp1.
\]

At \(\alpha=0\) and flat \(A_\alpha\), the normalized ratio becomes

\[
f(t)=t^{-3}.
\]

The nearest degree-\(R\) polynomial approximation to \(t^{-3}\) on a fixed compact interval away from \(0\) cannot decay faster than exponentially in \(R\). Thus one expects a lower bound of the form

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|t^{-3}-P(t)\|_{L^\infty([t_-,t_+])}
\ge
e^{-C_{a,b}R}.
}
\]

With the small AFE-weight perturbation included,

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_{a,b}}
|\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)|
\ge
e^{-C R}
-
O(Q^{-A_0}).
}
\]

Choosing \(A_0\) large enough gives

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_{a,b}}
|\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)|
\ge
e^{-C R}.
}
\]

At

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this becomes

\[
e^{-CR}
=
Q^{-C/\log\log Q}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
e^{-CR}\ge Q^{-C'}
}
\]

for a weakened constant \(C'\).

So the desired polynomial separation follows.

---

## 5. Theorem candidate

### Active-block intrinsic variation theorem

Assume the canonical AFE has a low-prime plateau in the following sense: for some fixed \(0<a<b\),

\[
Q^b\ll N_Z^\eta,
\qquad
Q^b\ll N_q^\eta,
\]

and on

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\}
\]

the AFE weights satisfy

\[
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)=1+O(Q^{-A_0}),
\qquad
V_q(p/N_q)=1+O(Q^{-A_0}),
\]

with controlled normalized derivatives.

Then

\[
|\mathcal B_{a,b}|\gg R
\]

and

\[
L\left(
|\alpha|
+
u_0^{-1}
+
\|\partial_u\log A_\alpha\|_\infty
\right)
\ge c_{a,b}>0.
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_{a,b}}
\left|
\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)
\right|
\ge
e^{-CR}.
}
\]

For

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this implies

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_{a,b}}
\left|
\widehat r_\alpha(\log p)-P(\log p)
\right|
\ge Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

Thus \(Z_\alpha\) contributes polynomially visible symbol rank on \(\mathcal B_{a,b}\).

---

## 6. The \(\alpha\to0\) regime

The \(\alpha\to0\) regime is harmless **on the low-prime plateau block**.

When

\[
\alpha=0,
\]

the ratio reduces to

\[
\widehat r_0(u)
=
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
\frac{A_0(u)}{A_0(u_0)}.
\]

If \(A_0\) is flat, the \(u^{-3}\) factor alone gives visible variation because \(u\) ranges over a fixed relative interval:

\[
u\in[a\log Q,b\log Q].
\]

Hence

\[
\frac{u}{u_0}
\]

varies by a fixed amount. No off-line condition is needed to force this.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\to0 \text{ is only dangerous on short relative-width blocks.}
}
\]

It is not dangerous if low-prime relative-width blocks are allowed.

---

## 7. Genuine obstruction if only short blocks are allowed

If the Wronskian construction is forced to use a short block

\[
u\in[u_0,u_0+O(1)]
\]

with

\[
u_0\asymp Q,
\]

and if

\[
\alpha\approx0,
\qquad
A_\alpha(u)\approx\text{constant},
\]

then

\[
\frac{L}{u_0}\asymp \frac1Q.
\]

The intrinsic variation is

\[
\sigma_{\mathcal B}\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
Q^{-1}\ll R^{-C_0}
\]

for every fixed \(C_0\).

Then Taylor approximation gives

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|\widehat r_\alpha-P\|_\infty
\lesssim
\left(\frac{L}{u_0}\right)^{R+1}
\asymp
Q^{-(R+1)},
\]

which is far smaller than any fixed \(Q^{-C}\).

Thus the active-block theorem is false under the restriction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{only short absolute-width blocks near }u_0\asymp Q\text{ are allowed.}
}
\]

This is the precise degeneration.

---

## 8. What this does and does not solve

This solves only the symbol-rank existence problem, conditional on allowing low-prime plateau blocks.

It does **not** solve the determinant incidence theorem:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It also does not solve coefficient dominance or subset-product cancellation. In fact, using low-prime blocks may create separate conditioning questions for the Wronskian determinant:

\[
\prod_{p\in S} c_p,
\qquad
\det(p_j(\lambda\log p)).
\]

Those are Agent 3 / Agent 4 / Agent 6 issues, not symbol-rank issues.

The key separation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Symbol rank can be forced by low-prime plateau blocks.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pointwise determinant nonrecurrence remains unsolved.}
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Active-block intrinsic variation: Green conditional on low-prime plateau admissibility.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Red/false if the construction is restricted to short log-blocks near }u_0\asymp Q.
}
\]

The best theorem to carry forward is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists\,\mathcal B_{a,b}=\{Q^a\le p\le Q^b\}
\text{ with }
|\mathcal B_{a,b}|\gg R
\text{ and }
\sigma_{\mathcal B}\gg1.
}
\]

On such a block,

\[
Z_\alpha
\]

is polynomially separated from the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbol span, even in the flat \(\alpha=0\) regime.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:16:49)

I’ll now test whether low-prime plateau blocks are usable for the actual Wronskian, not just for the \(Z_\alpha\)-rank symbol check. The key issue is no longer rank; it is determinant mass and normalized node spread.

_Thought for 48s_

Agent 1 / A report: low-prime plateau admissibility for the actual Wronskian construction. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Low-prime plateau blocks are admissible for AFE symbol-rank testing, but not obviously admissible for the actual packet-scale Wronskian determinant.}
}
\]

They solve the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol variation problem, but introduce two new obstructions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coefficient mass loss}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{too-small normalized node spread }x_p=\lambda\log p.
}
\]

For ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and low-prime blocks

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}(Q)=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\},
\]

one has

\[
\log p\asymp\log Q,
\]

so

\[
x_p=\lambda\log p\asymp \frac{\log Q}{Q}\ll1.
\]

The node spread is only

\[
\delta_x
=
\lambda(\log Q^b-\log Q^a)
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{Q}.
\]

A rank-\(R\) Wronskian with

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

cannot use such a compressed node interval without paying a non-polynomial rescaling cost.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Low-prime blocks give rank, but probably not usable determinant mass at packet scale.}
}
\]

They remain useful as an auxiliary symbol-rank witness, but the actual Wronskian determinant likely needs frequencies with

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

i.e. roughly

\[
\log n\asymp \lambda^{-1}.
\]

For ordinary scale \(\lambda\asymp Q^{-1}\), that means

\[
\log n\asymp Q,
\]

not

\[
\log n\asymp\log Q.
\]

---

## 1. AFE conductor lengths and plateau condition

Let the analytic conductor at height \(m\) be

\[
\mathfrak C(m)\asymp 1+|m|.
\]

For the zeta AFE, the natural main/dual lengths are of size

\[
N_Z(m,\alpha)\asymp \mathfrak C(m)^{1/2},
\]

and similarly

\[
N_q(m)\asymp \mathfrak C(m)^{1/2}
\]

up to convention-dependent gamma and smoothing normalizations.

If the project parameter is

\[
Q\asymp \log \mathfrak C(m),
\]

then

\[
N_Z,N_q\asymp e^{Q/2}.
\]

Hence for every fixed \(b\),

\[
Q^b\ll N_Z^\eta,
\qquad
Q^b\ll N_q^\eta
\]

for any fixed \(\eta>0\) and all large \(Q\).

So the low-prime block

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}(Q)=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\}
\]

lies deep in the main AFE plateau. There,

\[
V_{Z,\alpha}(p/N_Z)=1+O(Q^{-A}),
\]

\[
V_q(p/N_q)=1+O(Q^{-A}),
\]

for arbitrarily large \(A\), assuming standard smooth cutoff with flat interior.

Thus low-prime plateau blocks are AFE-admissible in the weak sense:

\[
\boxed{
\text{they are present, stable, and away from weight zeros.}
}
\]

---

## 2. Coefficient size on low-prime blocks

For the canonical source curvature

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta''',
\]

the main prime coefficient has size

\[
c_p
\asymp
\Lambda(p)(\log p)^2p^{-1/2}V_q(p/N_q).
\]

Since

\[
\Lambda(p)=\log p,
\]

on the plateau,

\[
\boxed{
c_p\asymp(\log p)^3p^{-1/2}.
}
\]

For

\[
p\in[Q^a,Q^b],
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
Q^{-b/2}(\log Q)^3
\lesssim
|c_p|
\lesssim
Q^{-a/2}(\log Q)^3.
}
\]

A Wronskian minor of size

\[
s=R+2
\]

contains a product

\[
\prod_{p\in S}c_p.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\prod_{p\in S}|c_p|
\asymp
(\log Q)^{3s}Q^{-\frac12\sum_{p\in S}\theta_p},
\qquad p=Q^{\theta_p}.
}
\]

With \(\theta_p\in[a,b]\),

\[
\boxed{
\prod_{p\in S}|c_p|
\le
(\log Q)^{3s}Q^{-as/2}.
}
\]

At

\[
s\asymp R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
Q^{-aR/2}(\log Q)^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(
-\frac{a}{2}\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}
+
O(\log Q)
\right).
\]

That is much smaller than any fixed polynomial \(Q^{-A}\).

So a **single low-prime minor** does not have polynomial determinant mass unless one introduces row/column normalizations whose costs are later recovered.

This is the first obstruction.

---

## 3. Packet-scale sensitivity

The normalized derivative is

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\]

or comparably

\[
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m.
\]

For one prime phase,

\[
\mathcal D e^{-im\log p}
=
-i(\lambda\log p)e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Thus the Wronskian node is

\[
\boxed{
x_p=\lambda\log p.
}
\]

On the low-prime block,

\[
\log p\in[a\log Q,b\log Q].
\]

Hence

\[
x_p\in[\lambda a\log Q,\lambda b\log Q],
\]

with spread

\[
\boxed{
\delta_x
=
\lambda(b-a)\log Q.
}
\]

In the ordinary packet regime,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\delta_x\asymp \frac{\log Q}{Q}\ll1.
}
\]

Thus all low-prime nodes are clustered very near zero in packet-scale frequency.

This is the second obstruction.

---

## 4. Rank-\(R\) Wronskian node-spread condition

For a stable rank-\(R\) Wronskian, the active nodes should occupy a normalized interval of at least polynomial size. A reasonable necessary condition is

\[
\boxed{
\delta_x
=
\lambda L
\gtrsim R^{-C_0},
}
\]

where

\[
L=u_+-u_-.
\]

For low-prime plateau blocks,

\[
L\asymp \log Q.
\]

So the condition becomes

\[
\lambda\log Q
\gtrsim R^{-C_0}.
\]

In ordinary scale,

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

so

\[
\lambda\log Q
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{Q}.
\]

But

\[
\frac{\log Q}{Q}
\ll
R^{-C_0}
\]

for every fixed \(C_0\), since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Therefore low-prime blocks fail the packet-scale node-spread condition.

---

## 5. Why basis normalization does not automatically fix this

One may try to rescale the clustered nodes by defining

\[
t_p=\frac{x_p-x_0}{\delta_x}.
\]

This gives a well-conditioned polynomial basis in \(t\). But the corresponding operator is no longer merely a bounded polynomial in \(\mathcal D\); it contains powers of

\[
\delta_x^{-1}.
\]

A degree-\(j\) basis element costs roughly

\[
\delta_x^{-j}.
\]

Across \(R\) rows, the determinant scaling cost is at least

\[
\delta_x^{-O(R)}
\]

and in raw Vandermonde coordinates may be as bad as

\[
\delta_x^{-O(R^2)}.
\]

Even the optimistic cost

\[
\delta_x^{-O(R)}
\]

is already too large:

\[
\delta_x^{-O(R)}
=
\left(\frac{Q}{\log Q}\right)^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(
\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}
\right)
\right).
\]

That is not polynomial in \(Q\).

So the compressed-node defect cannot be dismissed as a coordinate artifact unless one proves a special renormalized Wronskian-to-Gate-1 transfer theorem that absorbs this loss. No such theorem is currently available.

---

## 6. Ordinary packet-scale verdict

In the ordinary regime,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Low-prime plateau blocks satisfy:

\[
\log p\asymp\log Q,
\]

\[
x_p=\lambda\log p\asymp\frac{\log Q}{Q},
\]

\[
\delta_x\asymp\frac{\log Q}{Q}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{low-prime blocks are too low-frequency for the packet-scale Wronskian.}
}
\]

They provide \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank, but the determinant built from them is too compressed in normalized derivative coordinates.

For the Wronskian itself, the natural frequency range is instead

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp1.
\]

Thus one wants

\[
\boxed{
\log n\asymp \lambda^{-1}.
}
\]

For ordinary scale,

\[
\lambda^{-1}\asymp Q,
\]

so the natural block is

\[
\boxed{
\log n\asymp Q,
}
\]

or

\[
n\asymp e^{cQ}.
\]

This is conductor-scale or sub-conductor-scale, not low-prime polynomial in \(Q\).

---

## 7. Singular packet-scale verdict

In the singular regime,

\[
\lambda Q\ll1.
\]

Then for low primes,

\[
x_p=\lambda\log p
\ll
\frac{\log Q}{Q}.
\]

The node-spread obstruction is even worse.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{low-prime blocks are not suitable for a singular-scale Wronskian.}
}
\]

The singular regime should probably continue to be handled by dominance or singular cancellation reduction, not by a low-prime Wronskian.

---

## 8. What low-prime blocks still prove

Low-prime plateau blocks remain valuable for one thing:

\[
\boxed{
\text{they prove that }Z_\alpha\text{ is not symbolically redundant with the }q''_{\can}\text{ jet rows.}
}
\]

Indeed, on

\[
p\in[Q^a,Q^b],
\]

one has

\[
\widehat r_\alpha(u)
=
e^{-\alpha(u-u_0)}
\left(\frac{u}{u_0}\right)^{-3}
(1+O(Q^{-A})),
\]

and because

\[
u/u_0
\]

varies by a fixed amount, the \(\alpha=0\) degeneration is avoided.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank: yes;}
}
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-scale determinant admissibility: no, unless extra normalization is justified.}
}
\]

---

## 9. Conditional theorem statement

### Low-prime plateau admissibility theorem, corrected

Assume

\[
Q^b\ll N_Z^\eta,
\qquad
Q^b\ll N_q^\eta.
\]

Then the low-prime block

\[
\mathcal B_{a,b}=\{p:Q^a\le p\le Q^b\}
\]

is AFE-plateau admissible and gives polynomially visible \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank.

However, for the packet-scale normalized Wronskian with

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

the same block is determinant-admissible only if

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\log Q\gtrsim R^{-C_0}
}
\]

and if the coefficient product loss

\[
\prod_{p\in S}|c_p|
\]

can be renormalized with only \(Q^{O(1)}\) cost.

In the ordinary regime

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

this condition fails:

\[
\lambda\log Q
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{Q}
\ll R^{-C_0}.
\]

In the singular regime

\[
\lambda Q\ll1,
\]

it fails even more strongly.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{low-prime plateau blocks are not currently admissible for the actual packet-scale Wronskian determinant.}
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE plateau admissibility: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha\text{-symbol rank: Green on low-prime blocks.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Coefficient mass for a fixed minor: Red/Yellow, because }\prod c_p=Q^{-O(R)}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-scale node spread: Red for ordinary and singular scales.}
}
\]

Final verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Low-prime plateau blocks cannot be the main Wronskian determinant block without a new renormalized transfer lemma.}
}
\]

The Wronskian proof should use active frequencies satisfying

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\log n\asymp1,
}
\]

while retaining the low-prime block only as an auxiliary check that \(Z_\alpha\) is not intrinsically symbol-redundant.
## User (2026-04-26 19:37:57)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:37:58)

I’ll answer as Agent 1/A: locate packet-frequency AFE blocks with \(\lambda\log n\asymp1\), check support, coefficient mass, node spread, and ordinary/singular viability.

_Thought for 49s_

Agent 1 / A report: packet-frequency active block admissibility. Source instruction and shared background cited here.  

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-frequency active blocks exist and are admissible in the ordinary regime } \lambda Q\asymp1.
}
\]

The correct determinant blocks are not low-prime plateau blocks

\[
p\in[Q^a,Q^b],
\]

but blocks with

\[
\boxed{
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp 1
}
\]

or, more precisely,

\[
x_n\in[x_0,x_0+\delta_x],
\qquad
x_0\asymp1,
\qquad
\delta_x\gtrsim R^{-C}.
\]

In ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

this means

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

Such blocks lie inside the main AFE support provided we choose

\[
\log n=cQ,
\qquad
0<c<\frac12
\]

under the usual zeta AFE length

\[
N\asymp e^{Q/2}.
\]

They also have enough usable frequencies, stable node spread, and polynomial aggregate coefficient mass. The fixed-minor coefficient product is exponentially small, but the block’s total \(\ell^2\) mass is polynomially large after summing over the exponentially many frequencies. Therefore the block is admissible for a **basis-normalized aggregate Wronskian**, not for a single-subset dominance proof.

---

## 1. Conductor and support

Let

\[
Q\sim \log \frac{m}{2\pi}
\]

so that the usual zeta AFE length satisfies

\[
N_Z(m,\alpha)\asymp e^{Q/2},
\qquad
N_q(m)\asymp e^{Q/2},
\]

up to harmless \(\alpha\)- and smoothing-dependent factors.

Thus the main AFE branch has usable support roughly

\[
0\le \log n\le \frac Q2+O(1).
\]

The dual branch, after folding, has complementary frequency

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
=
Q-\log n+O(1).
\]

Therefore if we choose

\[
\log n=cQ,
\qquad 0<c<\frac12,
\]

then:

\[
n\asymp e^{cQ}
\]

lies inside the main AFE support, while the folded dual frequency satisfies

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
\asymp (1-c)Q.
\]

Both are packet-frequency scale when \(\lambda Q\asymp1\).

---

## 2. Packet-frequency block definition

Let

\[
\mu:=\lambda Q.
\]

In the ordinary regime,

\[
\mu\asymp1.
\]

Choose a fixed

\[
0<c_0<c_1<\frac12,
\]

and pick

\[
c\in[c_0,c_1].
\]

Let

\[
u=\log n,
\qquad
u_0=cQ.
\]

Choose a normalized node-width

\[
\delta_x=R^{-C_\delta}
\]

or, for the cleanest conditioning,

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Define the packet-frequency log block

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\left\{
n:
u_0\le \log n\le u_0+L
\right\},
\qquad
L:=\frac{\delta_x}{\lambda}
=
\frac{\delta_x Q}{\mu}.
}
\]

Then the normalized nodes

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

satisfy

\[
x_n\in[x_0,x_0+\delta_x],
\qquad
x_0=\lambda u_0=c\mu\asymp1.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
x_n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}\{x_n:n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\}=\delta_x\gtrsim R^{-C_\delta}.
}
\]

This is the correct packet-frequency analogue of the low-prime block.

---

## 3. Frequency count

Restricting to primes for simplicity,

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}
=
\{p:e^{u_0}\le p\le e^{u_0+L}\}.
\]

By the prime number theorem heuristic,

\[
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}|
\sim
\frac{e^{u_0}}{u_0}(e^L-1).
\]

At

\[
u_0=cQ,
\qquad
L=\frac{\delta_xQ}{\mu},
\]

and

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}
\]

with

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we get

\[
L\asymp \frac{Q}{R}\asymp \log\log Q.
\]

Hence

\[
e^L\asymp \log Q
\]

up to powers, and

\[
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}|
\gg
\frac{e^{cQ}}{Q}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}|\gg R+2.
}
\]

There are far more than enough usable frequencies for a rank-\(R\) Wronskian.

---

## 4. Coefficient size on packet-frequency blocks

For the canonical source curvature

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta''',
\]

the main prime coefficient has size

\[
c_p
\asymp
\Lambda(p)(\log p)^2p^{-1/2}V_q(p/N_q).
\]

On primes,

\[
\Lambda(p)=\log p.
\]

Inside the main support and away from transition edges,

\[
V_q(p/N_q)\asymp1.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
c_p\asymp(\log p)^3p^{-1/2}.
}
\]

On the packet-frequency block

\[
\log p\asymp cQ,
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
|c_p|\asymp Q^3e^{-cQ/2}.
}
\]

A fixed minor using \(s=R+2\) primes has coefficient product

\[
\prod_{p\in S}|c_p|
\asymp
Q^{3s}e^{-cQs/2},
\]

which is exponentially small in \(QR\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{single-subset coefficient dominance is not viable.}
}
\]

But the aggregate \(\ell^2\) mass over the block is polynomially large:

\[
\sum_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}}|c_p|^2
\asymp
\int_{u_0}^{u_0+L}
u^6e^{-u}\frac{e^u}{u}\,du
=
\int_{u_0}^{u_0+L}u^5\,du.
\]

Since

\[
u\asymp Q,
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}}|c_p|^2
\asymp
Q^5L.
}
\]

For

\[
L\asymp Q/R,
\]

this is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}^{\prime}}|c_p|^2
\asymp
\frac{Q^6}{R}.
}
\]

So the block has strong aggregate mass. The determinant construction must use basis normalization / aggregate minors, not one dominant subset.

---

## 5. Node spread and basis conditioning

The normalized nodes are

\[
x_p=\lambda\log p.
\]

On the block,

\[
x_p\in[x_0,x_0+\delta_x],
\qquad
x_0=c\mu.
\]

For ordinary scale,

\[
\mu=\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so

\[
x_0\asymp1.
\]

Choosing

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}
\]

gives a rank-\(R\) node interval of width \(1/R\). Rescaling this interval to a standard interval costs

\[
\delta_x^{-O(R)}
=
R^{O(R)}
=
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

At the safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
\boxed{
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus node-spread conditioning is polynomially admissible.

If instead one tried \(\delta_x\ll R^{-C}\) with a large exponent, the rescaling cost would become too expensive. The natural choice is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}
\quad\text{or another fixed polynomial width in }R^{-1}.
}
\]

---

## 6. Main and dual support

### Main branch

For

\[
\log n=cQ,
\qquad 0<c<\frac12,
\]

the main branch lies safely inside

\[
n\le N_q\asymp e^{Q/2}.
\]

Therefore the block is main-AFE admissible.

### Dual branch

The folded dual frequency is

\[
u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
=
Q-u+O(1)
=
(1-c)Q+O(1).
\]

The normalized dual node is

\[
x_n^-=\lambda u^-
=
\mu(1-c)+O(\lambda).
\]

For \(\mu\asymp1\),

\[
x_n^-\asymp1.
\]

Thus the same \(n\)-block gives a folded dual branch with packet-frequency nodes. Its node spread is also

\[
\delta_x^-=\lambda L=\delta_x.
\]

So the packet-frequency block is compatible with both main and folded dual branches.

The dual coefficient size must be tracked with the exact gamma factor, but at the level of support and normalized node spread, the dual branch is admissible.

---

## 7. Ordinary-scale theorem candidate

### Packet-frequency active block theorem

Assume

\[
Q\sim\log\frac{m}{2\pi},
\qquad
\lambda Q=\mu\asymp1,
\]

and take

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Fix

\[
0<c_0<c_1<\frac12
\]

and choose

\[
c\in[c_0,c_1].
\]

Let

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad
L=\frac{\delta_x Q}{\mu},
\]

and define

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:e^{cQ}\le n\le e^{cQ+L}\}.
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\log n\asymp1
\quad\text{on }\mathcal B_{\rm pf}.
}
\]

The normalized node diameter satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{diam}\{\lambda\log n:n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\}
=
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}.
}
\]

The block lies inside the main AFE support:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\subset \{n\le N_q,N_Z\}
}
\]

provided \(c_1<1/2\).

There are many usable primes:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\cap\mathbb P|\gg R.
}
\]

The aggregate source-coefficient mass satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}|c_p|^2
\asymp Q^5L
\asymp \frac{Q^6}{R}.
}
\]

Therefore \(\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\) is admissible for a basis-normalized aggregate Wronskian determinant in the ordinary packet regime.

---

## 8. Mild singular regime

Let

\[
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

The same construction gives

\[
x_n=\lambda cQ=c\mu.
\]

If

\[
\mu\gtrsim R^{-C_\mu},
\]

then one can still keep

\[
x_n\gtrsim R^{-C_\mu}
\]

and choose node diameter

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}
\]

by taking

\[
L=\frac{\delta_x Q}{\mu}.
\]

This remains inside the main support provided

\[
L\ll Q,
\]

i.e.

\[
\frac{1}{R\mu}\ll1.
\]

Thus a mild singular extension is plausible if

\[
\boxed{
\mu=\lambda Q\gtrsim R^{-1+\epsilon}
}
\]

or more generally if the basis-normalization losses in \(\mu^{-1}\) remain polynomial.

But if

\[
\mu\ll R^{-C}
\]

for large \(C\), then the packet-frequency nodes collapse toward zero and the Wronskian route loses rank.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary scale: admissible;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{mild singular scale: Yellow with explicit }\mu\text{-loss;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{deep singular scale: not suitable for this Wronskian block.}
}
\]

---

## 9. What remains unresolved

Packet-frequency blocks solve the previous low-prime determinant defect:

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\ll1.
\]

They also provide aggregate coefficient mass and enough frequencies.

They do **not** solve the final arithmetic incidence theorem:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

They also do not by themselves prove the full two-branch \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol-rank condition. That is Agent 2’s task. The important result here is only block admissibility.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-frequency blocks with }\log n=cQ,\ 0<c<1/2,\text{ are admissible in ordinary scale.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{They lie inside main AFE support, have }|\mathcal B|\gg R,\text{ and have stable node spread.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed subset coefficients are tiny, but aggregate }\ell^2\text{ coefficient mass is polynomially large.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use basis-normalized aggregate Wronskians, not single-minor dominance.}
}
\]

The corrected active-block target is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\left\{
n:
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+\frac{Q}{R}
\right\},
\qquad
0<c<\frac12,
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
}
\]
