I’ll handle Agent 1/A: exact packet-frequency \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank, including the main/dual ratios and the hard \(\alpha\to0\), saddle-overlap, and matching-ratio cases.

_Thought for 44s_

Agent 1 / A report: packet-frequency \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol non-cancellation. Source instruction: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-frequency }Z_\alpha\text{-symbol rank is Green-feasible in the ordinary regime.}
}
\]

On determinant-admissible blocks

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad
0<c<\frac12,
\]

with

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

the main-branch ratio has the normalized form

\[
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
=
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}
A_+(x)
+
\text{lower-order}.
\]

If the block is chosen away from the saddle and inside the AFE plateau, then

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q})
\]

or at worst has controlled analytic distortion. Hence \(Z_\alpha\) is not polynomially redundant with the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows.

The hard case

\[
\alpha\to0
\]

is no longer fatal, because now \(x\asymp1\), not \(x\ll1\). Even when

\[
\alpha=0,\qquad A_+(x)\equiv1,
\]

the residual function

\[
(x/x_0)^{-3}
\]

has a singularity at \(x=0\), a fixed positive distance away from the packet-frequency block. On an interval of width

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1},
\]

degree-\(R\) polynomial approximation can be as good as

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R)),
\]

but not better in the relevant scale. Since

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is still

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R))=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

Thus the desired symbol-rank lower bound

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is plausible and, on a main packet-frequency block away from the saddle, essentially follows from the \(x^{-3}\) factor alone.

---

## 1. Main AFE symbols

Write the main AFE branch for \(Z_\alpha\) as

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_n z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Up to an \(n\)-independent completed gamma/phase factor, the main symbol is

\[
\boxed{
z_n^+(\alpha,m)
=
n^{-1/2-\alpha}
V_Z^+\!\left(\frac n{N_Z(m,\alpha)};\alpha,m\right).
}
\]

For the canonical source curvature

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta''',
\]

the main oscillatory symbol is log-derivative-like. Starting from

\[
\log\zeta(s)
=
\sum_n\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\log n}n^{-s},
\]

three \(m\)-derivatives produce \((\log n)^3\), hence

\[
\boxed{
c_n^+(m)
=
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}
V_q^+\!\left(\frac n{N_q(m)};m\right)
+
c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^+(m).
}
\]

The amplitude-differentiation correction satisfies, on a stable packet-frequency block away from cutoff transitions,

\[
c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^+
=
c_{n,\mathrm{main}}^+\,O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R)).
\]

For primes \(n=p\), since \(\Lambda(p)=\log p\),

\[
\boxed{
c_p^+(m)
=
(\log p)^3p^{-1/2}V_q^+(p/N_q)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
r_p^+(\alpha,m)
:=
\frac{z_p^+(\alpha,m)}{c_p^+(m)}
=
p^{-\alpha}(\log p)^{-3}
\frac{V_Z^+(p/N_Z;\alpha,m)}
     {V_q^+(p/N_q;m)}
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

---

## 2. Main packet-frequency normalization

Let

\[
u=\log p,
\qquad
x=\lambda u.
\]

On the packet-frequency block,

\[
u\in[cQ,cQ+Q/R],
\]

and in the ordinary regime

\[
\lambda Q=\mu\asymp1.
\]

Thus

\[
x\in[c\mu,c\mu+\mu/R],
\]

so

\[
x\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Normalize the ratio at a base point \(x_0=\lambda u_0\):

\[
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
=
\frac{r_p^+(\alpha,m)}{r_{p_0}^+(\alpha,m)}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
=
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}
A_+(x;\alpha,m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right),
}
\]

where

\[
A_+(x;\alpha,m)
=
\frac{
V_Z^+(e^{x/\lambda}/N_Z;\alpha,m)
}{
V_q^+(e^{x/\lambda}/N_q;m)
}
\Bigg/
\frac{
V_Z^+(e^{x_0/\lambda}/N_Z;\alpha,m)
}{
V_q^+(e^{x_0/\lambda}/N_q;m)
}.
\]

If

\[
0<c<c_1<\frac12,
\]

the block lies inside the main AFE plateau. Then

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q})
\]

for some \(\eta>0\), assuming standard smoothed AFE cutoffs.

Hence the leading shape is

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
\approx
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}.
}
\]

---

## 3. Dual AFE symbols

The folded dual branch has phase frequency

\[
u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}+O(Q^{-1}),
\]

and normalized node

\[
\boxed{
x_n^-=\lambda u^-
=
\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
+
O(\lambda Q^{-1}).
}
\]

The dual \(Z_\alpha\) symbol has the schematic form

\[
\boxed{
z_n^-(\alpha,m)
=
n^{-1/2+\alpha}
V_Z^-\!\left(\frac n{N_Z^-(m,\alpha)};\alpha,m\right)
\times \mathfrak g_Z^-(\alpha,m),
}
\]

where \(\mathfrak g_Z^-\) is the \(n\)-independent gamma/folding factor.

The dual source-curvature symbol has the form

\[
\boxed{
c_n^-(m)
=
\Lambda(n)(u_n^-)^2n^{-1/2}
V_q^-\!\left(\frac n{N_q^-(m)};m\right)
\times \mathfrak g_q^-(m)
+
c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^-(m).
}
\]

Equivalently, after folding to the \(u^-\)-frequency variable, each \(m\)-derivative contributes powers of \(u^-\), not merely \(\log n\).

Thus, on primes,

\[
\boxed{
r_p^-(\alpha,m)
=
\frac{z_p^-(\alpha,m)}{c_p^-(m)}
\approx
e^{+\alpha u^-}(u^-)^{-3}A_-(u^-;\alpha,m),
}
\]

after removing \(n\)-independent gamma factors.

In normalized \(y=x^-= \lambda u^-\), and after row normalization at \(y_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha^-(y)
=
e^{+(\alpha/\lambda)(y-y_0)}
\left(\frac{y}{y_0}\right)^{-3}
A_-(y;\alpha,m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

For the same block

\[
u=\log n=cQ+O(Q/R),
\]

the folded dual node is

\[
u^-=Q-u+O(1)=(1-c)Q+O(Q/R),
\]

so

\[
y=\lambda u^-=(1-c)\mu+O(\mu/R)\asymp1.
\]

Thus the dual branch also has packet-frequency nodes.

---

## 4. Two-branch symbol-rank condition

The exact two-branch condition should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max
\left(
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_+}
|\widehat r_\alpha^+(x_p^+)-P(x_p^+)|,
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_-}
|\widehat r_\alpha^-(x_p^-)-P(x_p^-)|
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

However, if the main branch alone is chosen in a plateau region

\[
0<c<c_1<\frac12,
\]

then it is enough to prove

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_+}
|\widehat r_\alpha^+(x_p^+)-P(x_p^+)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

The dual branch can improve the rank test, but is not needed to prevent \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol redundancy on the ordinary main packet-frequency block.

---

## 5. Polynomial approximation lower bound

Let

\[
I_+=[x_0,x_0+\delta_x],
\]

with

\[
x_0\asymp1,
\qquad
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Assume

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q})
\]

or more generally that \(A_+\) is analytic in a fixed complex neighborhood after rescaling and has distortion bounded by

\[
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

Then

\[
f_\alpha(x)
=
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}A_+(x)
\]

is not a degree-\(R\) polynomial unless an exact AFE weight cancellation occurs.

The quantitative lower bound should be:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|f_\alpha-P\|_{L^\infty(I_+)}
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R).
}
\]

At safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
\exp(-C R\log R)=Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

So the desired rank bound follows.

The \(R\log R\) exponent is the correct scale because \(I_+\) has width \(1/R\), while the nearest structural singularity of \(x^{-3}\) is at \(x=0\), distance \(\asymp1\). After rescaling \(I_+\) to a unit interval, that singularity is distance \(\asymp R\), yielding polynomial-approximation scale roughly

\[
R^{-O(R)}
=
\exp(-O(R\log R)).
\]

This is still polynomial in \(Q\).

---

## 6. Hard case analysis

### Case 1: \(\alpha\to0\)

At

\[
\alpha=0
\]

and with flat weights,

\[
\widehat r_0^+(x)
=
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}.
\]

Since

\[
x_0\asymp1,
\]

the singularity at \(x=0\) is a fixed positive distance from the block. Therefore the best degree-\(R\) polynomial approximation is no better than

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R)).
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\to0 \text{ is not a rank degeneration on packet-frequency blocks.}
}
\]

This is the main improvement over low-prime and short-log-block tests.

---

### Case 2: \(x^+\approx x^-\)

Saddle overlap occurs when

\[
x^+\approx x^-.
\]

Since

\[
x^+=\lambda u,
\qquad
x^-=\lambda(Q-u),
\]

this means

\[
u\approx Q/2.
\]

Therefore saddle overlap corresponds to

\[
c\approx\frac12.
\]

Avoid it by choosing

\[
\boxed{
0<c<c_1<\frac12.
}
\]

Then

\[
x^+\asymp c\mu,
\qquad
x^-\asymp(1-c)\mu,
\]

and

\[
|x^+-x^-|
\asymp
|1-2c|\,\mu
\gg1
\]

if \(c\) is bounded away from \(1/2\).

Thus saddle overlap is avoidable.

---

### Case 3: \(r^+\approx r^-\)

Matching ratios could occur if

\[
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
\approx
\widehat r_\alpha^-(y)
\]

after identifying \(x\) and \(y\) through the same polynomial coordinate.

But when \(c\neq1/2\), the branches live on separated node intervals:

\[
x^+\in[c\mu,c\mu+O(1/R)],
\]

\[
x^-\in[(1-c)\mu+O(1/R)].
\]

A single degree-\(R\) polynomial fitting both branches would need to fit

\[
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}x^{-3}A_+(x)
\]

on one interval and

\[
e^{+(\alpha/\lambda)(y-y_0)}y^{-3}A_-(y)
\]

on another separated interval.

This generally strengthens the rank condition. It degenerates only if the exact AFE weight ratios satisfy a tuned identity causing the two branch functions to lie on one common degree-\(R\) polynomial graph to accuracy \(Q^{-C}\).

That would be a real canonical obstruction, but it is not expected in the plateau case.

---

### Case 4: exact AFE weight-ratio cancellation

The only serious symbolic obstruction is:

\[
A_+(x)
\approx
e^{+(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^3P_R(x)
\]

on the packet-frequency block, for some degree-\(R\) polynomial \(P_R\).

On plateau blocks,

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q}),
\]

so this would reduce to \(x^{-3}\) being polynomial-like beyond the expected \(\exp(-O(R\log R))\) scale, which is false.

Near AFE transition regions this obstruction is less obviously impossible. Therefore choose

\[
c<c_1<1/2
\]

and stay away from the cutoff transition.

---

## 7. Theorem candidate

### Packet-frequency two-branch \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank theorem

Assume:

\[
\lambda Q=\mu\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Choose

\[
0<c_0<c<c_1<\frac12
\]

and define

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{p:cQ\le \log p\le cQ+Q/R\}.
\]

Let

\[
x_p^+=\lambda\log p.
\]

Let the folded dual block be defined by

\[
x_p^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi p}.
\]

Suppose the AFE weight ratios satisfy plateau bounds

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q}),
\]

and

\[
A_-(y)
\]

has controlled analytic distortion on the corresponding dual interval.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{p\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|\widehat r_\alpha^\pm(x_p^\pm)-P(x_p^\pm)|
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R).
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{p\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|\widehat r_\alpha^\pm(x_p^\pm)-P(x_p^\pm)|
\ge
Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

This supplies polynomially visible \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank on packet-frequency determinant-admissible blocks.

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main packet-frequency symbol rank: Green-feasible.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dual branch: Yellow/beneficial; exact symbols still need convention-level checking.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\to0\text{ is not fatal on packet-frequency blocks.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Saddle overlap is avoided by choosing }c<1/2-\varepsilon.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The only serious obstruction is exact AFE weight-ratio cancellation near transition regions.}
}
\]

Thus the working rank theorem is positive:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha
\text{ is not symbolically redundant with the }
q''_{\can}\text{-jet rows on ordinary packet-frequency blocks.}
}
\]

This does not prove the incidence theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but it removes the current symbol-rank objection for determinant-admissible ordinary blocks.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:46:09)

_Thought for 11s_

Agent 1 / A report: exact AFE weight-ratio non-cancellation on packet-frequency blocks. Source instruction: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-frequency }Z_\alpha\text{-symbol rank is Green-feasible on ordinary blocks }cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R,\ 0<c<c_1<1/2.
}
\]

The main branch alone should already give the required polynomial residual, provided the block stays in the AFE plateau and away from the saddle/cutoff transition. The exact dual branch is useful but not required for rank unless the proof construction forces a two-branch matrix.

The desired condition is:

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_\pm\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm(\alpha,m)-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

On packet-frequency blocks,

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n^+)\asymp R^{-1},
\]

and

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The key normalized main ratio is

\[
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
=
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}
A_+(x)
+
O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R)).
\]

In the plateau region,

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q})
\]

or at worst has analytic distortion bounded by \(e^{O(R\log R)}\). Therefore even in the hardest case

\[
\alpha=0,
\qquad
A_+(x)\equiv1,
\]

one has

\[
\widehat r_0^+(x)=\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3},
\]

which cannot be approximated by degree-\(R\) polynomials on an \(R^{-1}\)-width interval to better than

\[
\exp(-C R\log R).
\]

Since

\[
\exp(-C R\log R)=Q^{-O(1)},
\]

this gives the required \(Q^{-C}\)-scale symbol residual.

---

## 1. Canonical main and dual AFE symbols

Use the ordinary-scale regime

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
Q\sim \log \frac{m}{2\pi}.
\]

Let

\[
N_Z(m,\alpha)\asymp e^{Q/2},
\qquad
N_q(m)\asymp e^{Q/2}
\]

denote the main AFE lengths, up to convention-dependent completed gamma factors.

### Main branch for \(Z_\alpha\)

The main AFE branch has the form

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_n z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
z_n^+(\alpha,m)
=
\mathfrak g_Z^+(\alpha,m)\,
n^{-1/2-\alpha}
V_Z^+\!\left(\frac n{N_Z(m,\alpha)};\alpha,m\right).
}
\]

The global factor \(\mathfrak g_Z^+\) is independent of \(n\) and can be removed in row-rank tests.

### Main branch for \(q''_{\can}\)

For

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta''',
\]

the log-derivative main branch has coefficients

\[
\boxed{
c_n^+(m)
=
\mathfrak g_q^+(m)\,
\Lambda(n)(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}
V_q^+\!\left(\frac n{N_q(m)};m\right)
+
c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^+(m).
}
\]

The term \(c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^+\) comes from differentiating conductor, smoothing, and gamma amplitudes. On an interior packet-frequency block,

\[
c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^+
=
c_{n,\mathrm{main}}^+\,O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R)).
\]

Restricting to primes \(n=p\), since \(\Lambda(p)=\log p\),

\[
\boxed{
c_p^+(m)
=
\mathfrak g_q^+(m)\,
(\log p)^3p^{-1/2}
V_q^+(p/N_q;m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
r_p^+(\alpha,m)
:=
\frac{z_p^+}{c_p^+}
=
C_+(\alpha,m)
p^{-\alpha}(\log p)^{-3}
\frac{V_Z^+(p/N_Z;\alpha,m)}
     {V_q^+(p/N_q;m)}
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

---

## 2. Main packet-frequency block

Take

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{p:cQ\le\log p\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad
0<c<c_1<1/2.
\]

Let

\[
x=\lambda\log p,
\qquad
x_0=\lambda cQ.
\]

Because

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

we have

\[
x\asymp1,
\qquad
x\in[x_0,x_0+\delta],
\qquad
\delta\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

After normalizing the ratio at a base point \(p_0\), define

\[
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
=
\frac{r_p^+(\alpha,m)}{r_{p_0}^+(\alpha,m)}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha^+(x)
=
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}
A_+(x;\alpha,m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right),
}
\]

where

\[
A_+(x;\alpha,m)
=
\frac{
V_Z^+(e^{x/\lambda}/N_Z;\alpha,m)
}{
V_q^+(e^{x/\lambda}/N_q;m)
}
\bigg/
\frac{
V_Z^+(e^{x_0/\lambda}/N_Z;\alpha,m)
}{
V_q^+(e^{x_0/\lambda}/N_q;m)
}.
\]

Since \(c_1<1/2\), this block lies inside the main AFE plateau:

\[
e^{x/\lambda}\le e^{c_1Q+O(Q/R)}\ll e^{Q/2}\asymp N_Z,N_q.
\]

Therefore, for standard smoothed AFE weights,

\[
\boxed{
A_+(x;\alpha,m)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q})
}
\]

on the block, or more generally

\[
\|\partial_x^j A_+\| \le e^{O(j\log j)}
\]

for \(j\le R+1\).

---

## 3. Dual branch symbols

The folded dual frequency is

\[
u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}+O(Q^{-1}),
\]

and the normalized dual node is

\[
\boxed{
x_n^-=\lambda u^-.
}
\]

For \(n=p\) with \(\log p=cQ+O(Q/R)\),

\[
u^-=(1-c)Q+O(Q/R),
\]

so

\[
x_n^-=(1-c)\lambda Q+O(1/R)\asymp1.
\]

The dual \(Z_\alpha\) symbol has schematic form

\[
\boxed{
z_n^-(\alpha,m)
=
\mathfrak g_Z^-(\alpha,m)\,
n^{-1/2+\alpha}
V_Z^-\!\left(\frac n{N_Z^-(m,\alpha)};\alpha,m\right).
}
\]

After gamma-phase folding, the dual \(q''_{\can}\) coefficient has the schematic form

\[
\boxed{
c_n^-(m)
=
\mathfrak g_q^-(m)\,
\Lambda(n)(u^-)^2n^{-1/2}
V_q^-\!\left(\frac n{N_q^-(m)};m\right)
+
c_{n,\mathrm{amp}}^-(m).
}
\]

Equivalently, after expressing the dual branch in the folded variable \(u^-\), three phase derivatives again produce the \((u^-)^{-3}\)-type ratio.

For primes,

\[
\boxed{
r_p^-(\alpha,m)
=
\frac{z_p^-}{c_p^-}
=
C_-(\alpha,m)
e^{+\alpha u^-}(u^-)^{-3}
A_-(u^-;\alpha,m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

In normalized \(y=x^-=\lambda u^-\), after row normalization,

\[
\boxed{
\widehat r_\alpha^-(y)
=
e^{+(\alpha/\lambda)(y-y_0)}
\left(\frac{y}{y_0}\right)^{-3}
A_-(y;\alpha,m)
\left(1+O(Q^{-1}\operatorname{poly}(R))\right).
}
\]

The exact convention may alter the harmless global gamma factors and the precise definition of \(A_-\), but it does not remove the folded \((y/y_0)^{-3}\) structure unless there is an unexpected canonical cancellation.

---

## 4. Polynomial approximation lower bound

The main branch already gives the required rank unless its AFE weight ratio is tuned to cancel the \((x/x_0)^{-3}\) shape.

Let

\[
I=[x_0,x_0+\delta],
\qquad
x_0\asymp1,
\qquad
\delta\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Consider

\[
f_\alpha(x)
=
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}
A_+(x).
\]

On plateau blocks,

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q}).
\]

The worst case for non-cancellation is

\[
\alpha=0,
\qquad
A_+(x)=1,
\]

so

\[
f_0(x)=\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^{-3}.
\]

The nearest singularity is at \(x=0\), a fixed distance from \(I\). Rescale \(I\) to a unit interval. The singularity moves to distance \(\asymp R\). Therefore the best degree-\(R\) approximation error has scale

\[
R^{-O(R)}
=
\exp(-O(R\log R)).
\]

Thus the symbol residual satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\|f_\alpha-P\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R)
}
\]

unless the AFE weight ratio \(A_+\) is specifically tuned to cancel the \(x^{-3}\)-shape.

At

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

\[
\boxed{
\exp(-C R\log R)=Q^{-O(1)}.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{p\in\mathcal B_+}
|\widehat r_\alpha^+(x_p^+)-P(x_p^+)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

The two-branch version follows a fortiori, unless the construction insists on fitting both branches and the exact dual weights introduce a cancellation. Generically, the second branch strengthens the condition.

---

## 5. Hard cases

### 5.1 \(\alpha\to0\)

When

\[
\alpha=0,
\]

the exponential factor disappears:

\[
e^{-(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}=1.
\]

But the ratio still contains

\[
(x/x_0)^{-3}.
\]

Since \(x\asymp1\), the short-block Taylor error is only

\[
R^{-O(R)}=Q^{-O(1)},
\]

not super-polynomially small. Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\to0\text{ is not fatal on packet-frequency blocks.}
}
\]

---

### 5.2 \(c\to1/2\)

If

\[
c\to1/2,
\]

then the main and folded dual nodes approach one another:

\[
x^+\approx x^-.
\]

This is saddle overlap. It can create branch degeneracy and transition-weight instability.

Avoid by imposing

\[
\boxed{
0<c<c_1<1/2.
}
\]

Then

\[
|x^- - x^+|
\asymp
(1-2c)\lambda Q
\gg1
\]

if \(c_1\) is fixed below \(1/2\).

---

### 5.3 AFE transition

If the block approaches the transition region

\[
\log n\approx Q/2,
\]

then \(V_Z^\pm,V_q^\pm\) may vary rapidly or interact with the saddle.

Again, choosing

\[
c<c_1<1/2
\]

keeps the main branch inside the plateau, where

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q}).
\]

Thus transition cancellation is avoided.

---

### 5.4 Exact AFE weight-ratio cancellation

The only serious symbolic obstruction is an identity of the form

\[
A_+(x)
\approx
e^{+(\alpha/\lambda)(x-x_0)}
\left(\frac{x}{x_0}\right)^3P_R(x)
\]

to accuracy better than \(Q^{-C}\) on the packet-frequency interval.

Inside the plateau,

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q}),
\]

so this would require \(x^{-3}\) to be degree-\(R\)-polynomial to accuracy better than \(\exp(-O(R\log R))\), which is false.

Thus exact AFE cancellation is not expected away from the transition.

---

## 6. Theorem candidate

### Packet-frequency exact-symbol rank theorem

Assume:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Choose

\[
0<c_0<c<c_1<1/2
\]

and define

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{p:cQ\le\log p\le cQ+Q/R\}.
\]

Let

\[
x_p^+=\lambda\log p,
\]

and define the folded dual nodes

\[
x_p^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi p}+O(\lambda Q^{-1}).
\]

Suppose the smoothed AFE weights satisfy the plateau bounds

\[
A_+(x)=1+O(e^{-\eta Q})
\]

on \(\mathcal B_+\), and the dual branch \(A_-(y)\) has controlled analytic distortion on its folded interval.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_\pm\max_{p\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|\widehat r_\alpha^\pm(x_p^\pm)-P(x_p^\pm)|
\ge
\exp(-C R\log R).
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_\pm\max_{p\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|\widehat r_\alpha^\pm(x_p^\pm)-P(x_p^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C'}.
}
\]

This proves polynomially visible \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank on determinant-admissible packet-frequency blocks.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main-branch symbol rank: Green under }0<c<c_1<1/2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dual branch: Yellow but beneficial; exact convention still needs checking.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\to0\text{ no longer degenerates the test.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
c\to1/2\text{ and AFE transition are the real danger zones; avoid them.}
}
\]

The symbol-rank subclaim can now be treated as closed modulo exact convention bookkeeping for the AFE weights. It does **not** prove the incidence theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but it removes the current \(Z_\alpha\)-rank obstruction for ordinary packet-frequency blocks.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:49:12)

_Thought for 12s_

Agent 1 / A report: quantitative \(Z_\alpha\)-zero non-flatness. Source instruction: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Simplicity of }Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\text{ is insufficient.}
}
\]

A usable theorem needs one extra local input:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
}
\]

together with analytic-complexity control in a larger complex disk. With that input, the desired finite derivative lower bound follows by a Taylor/Cauchy tail argument.

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative zero non-flatness is Yellow: reducible to a local amplitude or zero-crowding theorem.}
}
\]

The key theorem candidate is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,\quad
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},\quad
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1}
\]

with

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
A>a,
\]

imply

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le \ell\le R+1}|C_\ell F(0)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

provided

\[
\left(\frac aA\right)^{R+2}Q^{A_1}\le \frac12 Q^{-A_0}.
\]

At

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

it suffices to take a fixed radius ratio \(a/A<1\). No delicate shrinking is needed.

---

## 1. Normalized setup

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

The derivative vector in the Wronskian expansion is

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left(
(-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}.
\]

In normalized coordinates,

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m=\partial_t.
\]

So \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\) is a stable basis-normalized linear combination of

\[
F^{(1)}(0),\ldots,F^{(R+1)}(0).
\]

For the present non-flatness problem, it is enough to prove

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

because the change from monomial derivatives to stable basis operators costs at most

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

---

## 2. Basic analytic lemma

Let \(F\) be holomorphic on

\[
|t|\le A
\]

and satisfy

\[
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le M,
\qquad
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge m,
\]

where

\[
0<a<A.
\]

Let

\[
L=R+1.
\]

Assume

\[
M\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}\le \frac m2.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le L}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
\frac{m}{2La^L}.
}
\]

### Proof sketch

Taylor expand

\[
F(t)=\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k+T_L(t),
\qquad
a_k=\frac{F^{(k)}(0)}{k!}.
\]

Cauchy gives the tail bound

\[
|T_L(t)|
\le
M\frac{(|t|/A)^{L+1}}{1-|t|/A}
\]

for \(|t|\le a\), after enlarging constants. Under the displayed hypothesis, this is at most \(m/2\) on \(|t|\le a\).

If all

\[
|a_k|<\frac{m}{2La^k},
\]

then for \(|t|\le a\),

\[
\left|\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k\right|
<
\frac m2.
\]

Hence

\[
|F(t)|<m
\]

on \(|t|\le a\), contradicting

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge m.
\]

Thus at least one coefficient satisfies the lower bound.

---

## 3. Applying the lemma at safe depth

Set

\[
M=Q^{A_1},
\qquad
m=Q^{-A_0},
\qquad
L=R+1.
\]

We need

\[
Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{R+2}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
(R+2)\log(A/a)
\ge
(A_0+A_1)\log Q+O(1).
\]

If

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then a fixed radius ratio \(A/a>1\) is not enough if \(A_0+A_1\) is fixed and \(R\ll\log Q\). More precisely, fixed \(A/a\) only gives

\[
(R+2)\log(A/a)
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

which is too small to dominate

\[
(A_0+A_1)\log Q.
\]

So we need one of the following:

### Option 1: larger radius ratio

Take

\[
\log(A/a)\asymp \log\log Q.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
A/a\asymp(\log Q)^C.
}
\]

Then

\[
(R+2)\log(A/a)
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\cdot \log\log Q
\asymp
\log Q.
\]

This is exactly enough.

### Option 2: stronger upper bound

If the analytic upper bound is not \(Q^{A_1}\) but closer to \(Q^{o(1)}\), a fixed radius ratio may suffice. That seems unlikely for \(Z_\alpha\) without strong normalization.

### Option 3: increase derivative depth

If one used

\[
R\asymp \log Q,
\]

then fixed \(A/a\) would suffice. But that depth is currently unsafe for the Wronskian/AFE derivative budget.

Therefore, at the safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

the local non-flatness lemma wants a complex analytic annulus ratio

\[
\boxed{
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C.
}
\]

This is the main technical radius issue.

---

## 4. Resulting derivative lower bound

Under the amplitude and radius assumptions, the lemma gives

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{2(R+1)a^{R+1}}.
\]

If \(a\asymp1\), this is

\[
Q^{-A_0}\exp(-O(\log R))
=
Q^{-A_0-o(1)}.
\]

If the stable basis operators \(C_\ell\) have condition cost

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for some finite \(A\).

So the proof is straightforward **once** local amplitude and analytic-radius control are supplied.

---

## 5. Jensen / Cartan alternative

Instead of assuming

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

one can try to derive it from zero distribution.

A standard route would be:

1. \(F\) has controlled upper growth on \(|t|\le A\):

   \[
   \sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1}.
   \]

2. The disk \(|t|\le a\) does not contain too many zeros of \(F\), counted with multiplicity.

3. \(F\) has some nontrivial value at a reference point in \(|t|\le A\).

Then Jensen/Cartan gives a lower bound away from small exceptional disks. But this does **not** automatically give lower amplitude near a prescribed zero \(t=0\). It gives lower bounds outside small zero-neighborhoods.

To get derivative lower at the zero, one needs either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative zero separation near }m_0
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a bound on local zero multiplicity/crowding plus a nearby amplitude lower bound.}
}
\]

A possible theorem is:

### Jensen zero-crowding theorem candidate

Suppose \(F(0)=0\), \(F\) is holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\), and

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A/2}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Suppose also that the number of zeros of \(F\) in \(|t|\le a\), counted with multiplicity, is at most

\[
N_0\le C_0R.
\]

Then at least one derivative satisfies

\[
\max_{1\le k\le C_0R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This works because if all derivatives through \(C_0R+1\) are tiny, then \(F\) has a high-order flat zero at \(0\), forcing either a large zero-count or suppressed amplitude by Jensen/Cartan.

But this still needs a local zero-crowding theorem.

---

## 6. Does off-line admissibility provide the needed input?

At present:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No, not by itself.}
}
\]

The condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

marks the off-line packet center, but it does not imply:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

nor does it imply a polynomial zero-separation bound.

A simple analytic function can have a simple zero at \(0\) and still satisfy

\[
|F'(0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

for arbitrarily large \(A\), while having modest upper growth. For example,

\[
F(t)=\varepsilon t
\]

with tiny \(\varepsilon\).

Therefore one needs actual-zeta input, such as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local amplitude lower bound for }Z_\alpha,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative simplicity of }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero separation / anti-clustering at scale }\lambda,
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency AFE nonrecurrence for the }Z_\alpha\text{ derivative vector.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Best theorem candidate to carry forward

### Quantitative \(Z_\alpha\)-zero non-flatness theorem

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume:

1. **AFE analytic-complexity bound:**

   \[
   \sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1}.
   \]

2. **Local amplitude lower bound:**

   \[
   \sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
   \]

3. **Radius ratio:**

   \[
   A/a\ge(\log Q)^C
   \]

   for \(C\) large enough relative to \(A_0+A_1\).

4. **Stable basis conditioning:**

   \[
   \|C_\ell\|,\ \|C_\ell^{-1}\|
   \le \exp(O(R\log R)).
   \]

Then, for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is a clean analytic reduction.

---

## 8. What remains genuinely arithmetic

The missing input is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

or a replacement via Jensen/Cartan/zero separation.

In original \(m\)-scale, the needed disk has radius

\[
a\lambda.
\]

The outer analytic disk has radius

\[
A\lambda
\]

with

\[
A/a\asymp(\log Q)^C.
\]

Since

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

this is an \(m\)-scale window of size roughly

\[
\frac{(\log Q)^C}{Q}.
\]

So the necessary actual-zeta theorem is local at a very small scale, but still larger than the packet interval by a polylog factor.

A possible arithmetic statement is:

### Local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude theorem

For every admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zero \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le \lambda(\log Q)^C}
|Z_\alpha(m)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

This would imply the derivative lower bound.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic reduction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Required actual-zeta input: local amplitude / zero-separation theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Off-line admissibility alone: insufficient.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

is not a consequence of simplicity, but it follows from a local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude lower bound on a polylog-enlarged packet disk plus standard AFE analytic-complexity control.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:51:58)

_Thought for 13s_

Agent 1 / A report: local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude / zero non-flatness. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

does **not** follow from simplicity or off-line admissibility alone. It follows from a clean analytic lemma once one supplies a local amplitude theorem for \(Z_\alpha\) on a polylog-enlarged packet disk.

So the correct current theorem is conditional:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local }Z_\alpha\text{-amplitude}
+
\text{analytic complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{quantitative zero non-flatness}.
}
\]

The genuinely arithmetic missing input is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}
}
\]

for \(a\) at least packet-scale, preferably with an outer analytic-control radius \(A\) satisfying

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C.
\]

---

## 1. Normalized setup

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\]

with ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

The derivative vector is

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\bigl((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\bigr)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}.
\]

In normalized coordinates,

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m=\partial_t.
\]

Thus \(\mathbf z'\) is a stable-basis transform of

\[
F'(0),F''(0),\ldots,F^{(R+1)}(0).
\]

Since the basis-normalization cost is

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

it is enough to prove

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## 2. Analytic non-flatness lemma

Let \(F\) be holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\), with

\[
F(0)=0,
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le M,
\]

and

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge m,
\qquad 0<a<A.
\]

Let

\[
L=R+1.
\]

If

\[
M\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}\le \frac m4,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le L}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
\frac{m}{4L\,a^L}.
}
\]

### Proof sketch

Write

\[
F(t)=\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k+T_L(t),
\qquad
a_k=\frac{F^{(k)}(0)}{k!}.
\]

Cauchy gives, for \(|t|\le a\),

\[
|T_L(t)|
\le
C M\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}.
\]

By the hypothesis, this is \(\le m/2\). If every coefficient obeys

\[
|a_k|<\frac{m}{4L\,a^k},
\]

then

\[
\left|
\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k
\right|
<
\frac m4
\sum_{k=1}^{L}1
\le
\frac m4
\]

after adjusting constants. Hence

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|<m,
\]

contradiction.

---

## 3. Required radius ratio

Take

\[
M=Q^{A_1},
\qquad
m=Q^{-A_0}.
\]

The tail condition requires

\[
Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{R+2}
\le
Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
(R+2)\log(A/a)
\ge
(A_0+A_1)\log Q.
\]

At the safe Wronskian depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this requires

\[
\boxed{
\log(A/a)\gtrsim \log\log Q,
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C.
}
\]

Thus a fixed radius ratio is not enough unless the analytic upper bound is much sharper than \(Q^{A_1}\), or unless the derivative depth is increased to \(R\asymp\log Q\), which is currently not safe for the Wronskian/AFE budget.

---

## 4. Resulting derivative lower bound

Under the local amplitude and radius-ratio assumptions,

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4(R+1)a^{R+1}}.
\]

If \(a\asymp1\), this is

\[
Q^{-A_0-o(1)}.
\]

After transforming to the stable operators \(C_\ell\), the loss is at most

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## 5. Candidate theorem

### Quantitative \(Z_\alpha\)-zero non-flatness theorem

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C,
\]

and stable operator conditioning

\[
\|C_\ell\|,\ \|C_\ell^{-1}\|
\le
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

Then, for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem is analytically solid. The missing part is proving the local amplitude hypothesis for actual \(Z_\alpha\).

---

## 6. Jensen/Cartan route

A possible replacement for direct local amplitude is a zero-crowding theorem.

Suppose \(F\) is holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\), with

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

and has a reference lower bound

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A/2}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

If the zero count in \(|t|\le a\) is controlled by

\[
N_F(a)\le C_0R,
\]

then Jensen/Cartan-style estimates should imply that \(F\) cannot vanish to effective order \(>C_0R\) at \(0\) while remaining locally small throughout \(|t|\le a\). This gives a theorem of the shape:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
+
N_F(a)\le C_0R
+
\sup_{|t|\le A/2}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But this route still needs actual-zeta input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero crowding control at normalized scale }a,
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a nearby value lower bound for }Z_\alpha.
}
\]

---

## 7. Can the needed amplitude follow from AFE alone?

Not from the AFE representation in a purely formal way.

The AFE writes \(Z_\alpha\) as a fixed exponential sum, but fixed exponential sums can have a zero at \(m_0\) and be extremely flat there if their coefficients/phases cooperate. The packet-frequency symbol-rank theorem prevents algebraic redundancy with \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows; it does not by itself lower-bound the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative vector at a zero.

A possible AFE-based route would be an \(L^2\)-mass theorem:

\[
\int_{|t|\le A}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

plus a concentration/zero-crowding argument to force

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0'}.
\]

But this is again a local nonrecurrence theorem for the actual prime-log orbit.

---

## 8. Can off-line admissibility imply it?

Currently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No.}
}
\]

The condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

defines the off-line center, but does not exclude an arbitrarily flat simple zero. Nor does it give an amplitude lower bound nearby.

Thus off-line admissibility must be supplemented by one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quantitative simplicity of }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero separation at scale }\lambda(\log Q)^C;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{local }Z_\alpha\text{ amplitude lower bound;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency AFE nonrecurrence for }Z_\alpha.
}
\]

---

## 9. Sharp obstruction

A simple countermodel is

\[
F(t)=\varepsilon t
\]

with

\[
0<\varepsilon\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
F(0)=0,
\]

the zero is simple, but

\[
|F'(0)|=\varepsilon
\]

is smaller than any polynomial threshold. This violates no purely local analytic principle unless one imposes amplitude normalization.

More generally, one can take

\[
F(t)=\varepsilon t+\sum_{k>R+1}b_kt^k
\]

with controlled outer growth, making all derivatives through \(R+1\) tiny while amplitude appears only outside the packet unless the radius-ratio/local-amplitude hypotheses are imposed.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{simplicity alone cannot support the Wronskian incidence theorem.}
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic lemma: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Off-line admissibility: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Needed actual-zeta input: local amplitude, zero separation, or zero-crowding theorem.}
}
\]

The clean theorem to carry forward is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\quad
+
\quad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Without such a local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude theorem, the Wronskian route cannot certify the derivative side of the incidence estimate.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:54:45)

_Thought for 12s_

Agent 1 / A report: local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No unconditional local }Z_\alpha\text{-amplitude theorem is available from the current inputs.}
}
\]

The analytic reduction is solid:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\quad+\quad
\sup_{|t|\le A}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\le Q^{A_1}
\quad+\quad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C
\]

implies

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But the missing lower bound

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
}
\]

does not follow from off-line admissibility, AFE representation alone, or simplicity of the zero. It requires a genuine local value / zero-crowding / nonrecurrence theorem for \(Z_\alpha\).

---

## 1. Refined analytic lemma

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume \(F\) is holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\), and

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

with

\[
0<a<A.
\]

Let

\[
L=R+1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Then if

\[
Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}\le \frac12 Q^{-A_0},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le L}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
Q^{-A}
}
\]

for some \(A\).

Since

\[
L\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

the displayed tail condition requires

\[
\boxed{
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C.
}
\]

So the derivative lower bound is available if the function has polynomial-scale amplitude on a packet window and polynomial upper control on a polylog-enlarged packet window.

After converting monomial derivatives to the basis-normalized operators \(C_\ell\), the loss is

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## 2. Local \(L^2\) approach

A natural candidate is to prove

\[
\int_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This would imply

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Using the packet-frequency AFE,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)
\approx
\sum_n z_n(\alpha,m_0)
e^{-im_0\log n}
e^{-it\lambda\log n}
+
\text{dual/background/error}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|^2dt
\]

expands as

\[
\sum_{n,n'}
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\widehat{\mathbf 1}_{[-a,a]}
\bigl(\lambda(\log n-\log n')\bigr)
+
\cdots.
\]

The diagonal contribution is positive, but the off-diagonal terms are not controlled on a short packet window because the frequency resolution is only

\[
|\lambda(\log n-\log n')|\gtrsim a^{-1}.
\]

On packet-frequency blocks, many nearby terms satisfy

\[
|\lambda(\log n-\log n')|\ll1,
\]

so the kernel does not diagonalize the AFE sum. Therefore an \(L^2\)-lower bound is itself a nontrivial local prime-log nonrecurrence theorem.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE coefficient mass alone does not give local }L^2\text{ amplitude.}
}
\]

It gives a plausible route, but only after proving that packet-frequency phases cannot cancel too coherently near \(m_0\).

---

## 3. Jensen / Cartan route

A second route is zero-crowding control.

A useful theorem would be:

### Zero-crowding non-flatness theorem

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A/2}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

and the number of zeros of \(F\) in \(|t|\le a\), counted with multiplicity, satisfies

\[
N_F(a)\le C_0R.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The logic is that a zero at \(0\) that is effectively flat through order \(R+1\) either behaves like a high-multiplicity zero or forces \(F\) to remain small throughout the inner disk. Jensen/Cartan then requires either many zeros nearby or small outer amplitude.

This route reduces the missing input to:

\[
\boxed{
N_F(a)\le C_0R
}
\]

plus one nearby amplitude lower bound. But neither follows from the current off-line hypotheses.

---

## 4. Does off-line admissibility help?

At present, no.

The condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

selects the off-line center, but it does not imply:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

nor does it imply a local zero-spacing bound.

A simple analytic countermodel is

\[
F(t)=\varepsilon t,
\qquad
0<\varepsilon\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Then \(F(0)=0\) is simple, but every normalized derivative through the first order is too small. Higher-order variants can make all derivatives through \(R+1\) small while preserving bounded outer growth unless a local amplitude or zero-crowding hypothesis is imposed.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line admissibility alone is insufficient.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Sharp theorem candidate

The clean theorem to carry forward is:

### Local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude theorem

For every admissible ordinary off-line center \(m_0\) satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

there exist constants \(a\asymp1\), \(C,A_0>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

A slightly weaker but sufficient version is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a(\log Q)^C}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

Together with analytic AFE upper control on the larger disk, this yields

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

---

## 6. If proving amplitude directly is too hard

Then the replacement target is:

### Local zero-crowding theorem

For every admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zero \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}
\bigl(
|m-m_0|\le \lambda a
\bigr)
\le C_0R
}
\]

on a normalized packet or polylog-enlarged packet, plus a nearby value lower bound on the outer circle.

This would also imply

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But this is still an actual-zeta zero distribution theorem at microscopic scale.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic implication to }|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}: Green.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local }Z_\alpha\text{-amplitude from current hypotheses: not proved.
}}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE mass alone: insufficient without local nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Needed new input: local amplitude, zero-crowding, or microscopic zero-separation theorem for }Z_\alpha.
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Wronskian route requires an independent quantitative }Z_\alpha\text{-zero non-flatness theorem.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:59:12)

_Thought for 13s_

Agent 1 / A report: local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude via AFE \(L^2\), Jensen, or zero-crowding. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local amplitude theorem remains open.}
}
\]

The best current result is a conditional analytic reduction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local }Z_\alpha\text{ amplitude}
+
\text{outer analytic control}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

But the amplitude input

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

does **not** follow from packet-frequency AFE coefficient mass alone. The short-window \(L^2\) integral has a severe off-diagonal obstruction. Jensen/Cartan can replace the amplitude hypothesis, but only if one supplies a microscopic zero-crowding or zero-separation theorem for \(Z_\alpha\). That is a new actual-zeta arithmetic input.

---

## 1. Normalized setup

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

The Wronskian derivative vector is

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and in normalized variables

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m=\partial_t.
\]

Thus it is enough to prove

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}\ge Q^{-A},
\]

because passing to the stable basis operators costs only

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

---

## 2. Analytic implication: amplitude implies derivative size

The following lemma is the clean reduction.

### Lemma

Assume \(F\) is holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\), \(F(0)=0\), and

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

with

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C
\]

for \(C\) large enough. Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The proof is the Taylor/Cauchy tail argument already isolated: truncate \(F\) at degree \(R+1\), use the outer disk to control the tail, and force at least one coefficient through order \(R+1\) to be polynomially large.

So the analytic side is Green. The problem is proving the local amplitude hypothesis for actual \(Z_\alpha\).

---

## 3. Packet-frequency \(L^2\) attempt

The AFE gives, schematically,

\[
F(t)
=
\sum_n z_n(\alpha,m_0)
e^{-im_0\log n}
e^{-it\lambda\log n}
+
\text{dual/background/error}.
\]

On a packet-frequency block,

\[
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R,
\]

so

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

A local \(L^2\) integral gives

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt
=
\sum_{n,n'}
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
K_a\!\left(\lambda(\log n-\log n')\right)
+\cdots,
\]

where

\[
K_a(\xi)=\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-it\xi}dt.
\]

The diagonal contribution is positive:

\[
2a\sum_n |z_n|^2.
\]

But the off-diagonal terms are not small because the frequency bandwidth is only

\[
\lambda(\log n-\log n')=O(R^{-1})
\]

inside the block. For \(a\asymp1\),

\[
K_a(\xi)\approx 2a
\]

for most pairs in the same packet-frequency block. So the local \(L^2\) norm behaves like the square of a coherent short exponential packet, not a diagonalized mean square.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency coefficient mass does not imply local }L^2\text{ amplitude.}
}
\]

A diagonal \(L^2\) argument would require a much longer \(t\)-interval, roughly long enough to resolve the normalized frequency spacing. For adjacent primes near \(e^{cQ}\), the spacing in normalized frequency can be extremely small. Such a long interval is incompatible with the local derivative lemma.

So the \(L^2\) route reduces to a local non-cancellation theorem for the actual prime-log phases.

---

## 4. Jensen/Cartan alternative

A more realistic path is to replace direct amplitude by zero-crowding control.

A sufficient theorem is:

### Zero-crowding-to-nonflatness theorem

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A/2}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

and the zero count in the inner disk satisfies

\[
N_F(|t|\le a)\le C_0R.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The reason: if all derivatives through \(R+1\) are too small, then either \(F\) has effective multiplicity \(>R+1\) at \(0\), or \(F\) stays too small on the inner disk. Jensen/Cartan forces this behavior to be accompanied by either excessive zero crowding or a contradiction with the outer amplitude lower bound.

This theorem is plausible analytically, but it moves the arithmetic burden to:

\[
\boxed{
N_F(|t|\le a)\le C_0R
}
\]

or a comparable microscopic zero-spacing theorem.

---

## 5. What is needed from actual zeta

The missing input can be stated in three equivalent useful forms.

### A. Local amplitude theorem

For every admissible ordinary center \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

A weaker sufficient version allows

\[
a\asymp(\log Q)^C,
\]

provided the outer analytic disk is larger by another polylog factor.

### B. Local zero-crowding theorem

For every admissible \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}
\left(
|m-m_0|\le a\lambda
\right)
\le C_0R.
}
\]

This plus an outer value lower bound gives the amplitude theorem.

### C. Local derivative nonrecurrence theorem

Directly prove

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
|\partial_t^k Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|_{t=0}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest input for the Wronskian, but it is essentially a local actual-zeta nonflatness theorem.

---

## 6. No-go from current hypotheses

The following model shows why current hypotheses are insufficient:

\[
F(t)=\varepsilon t + t^{R+2},
\qquad
\varepsilon\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
F(0)=0
\]

is simple, but all derivatives through order \(R+1\) can be too small at the origin if the higher term is arranged to appear outside the local packet. With bounded outer growth, this violates no purely local analytic principle unless one imposes amplitude or zero-crowding hypotheses.

The AFE representation rules out arbitrary analytic functions, but not by coefficient mass alone on a short packet. The phase coherence obstruction must be handled arithmetically.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line admissibility + AFE formalism + simplicity do not prove local amplitude.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Best theorem candidate to carry forward

### Local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude theorem candidate

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume \(m_0\) is an admissible ordinary off-line center. Then there exist constants \(a,A_0>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

Together with standard analytic AFE upper bounds on

\[
|t|\le a(\log Q)^C,
\]

this implies

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

At present, this theorem is not proved. It is an independent actual-zeta local value/zero-spacing input.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic reduction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE }L^2\text{ coefficient mass route: blocked by off-diagonal coherence.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Jensen/Cartan route: viable conditional on microscopic zero-crowding or nearby amplitude.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Unconditional local amplitude from current hypotheses: not available.}
}
\]

Therefore Agent 1’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Wronskian proof requires a new actual-zeta local amplitude/zero-crowding theorem for }Z_\alpha.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 02:33:30)

_Thought for 18s_

Agent 1 / A report: local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude / zero-crowding theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The needed local amplitude theorem is not available from diagonal AFE mass alone.}
}
\]

The sharpest usable reduction remains:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad+\quad
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

provided one also has analytic upper control on a disk larger by a factor

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C.
\]

The new point from this pass is that the most plausible amplitude window is not necessarily \(a\asymp1\). A window as large as

\[
a\asymp R
\quad\text{or}\quad
a\asymp(\log Q)^C
\]

is still compatible with the derivative reduction, because

\[
a^R\le \exp(O(R\log\log Q))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

for the safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

So the best theorem to target is a **polylog-enlarged local amplitude theorem**, not a strict one-packet theorem.

---

## 1. Sharp local amplitude theorem needed

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

The sufficient theorem is:

### Local amplitude theorem candidate

For every admissible ordinary zero \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
}
\]

for some

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^C.
\]

Together with

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\qquad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C,
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The derivative loss from using \(a>1\) is

\[
a^R.
\]

If \(a\le(\log Q)^C\), then

\[
a^R
\le
\exp(CR\log\log Q)
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So a polylogarithmic normalized window is still safe.

---

## 2. Packet-frequency AFE \(L^2\) calculation

The packet-frequency AFE has schematic form

\[
F(t)
=
\sum_n a_n e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-it\lambda\log n}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
a_n=z_n(\alpha,m_0).
\]

On a packet-frequency block,

\[
cQ\le\log n\le cQ+\frac QR,
\]

so

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

lies in an interval of diameter

\[
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2\,dt
=
\sum_{n,n'}a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
K_a(x_n-x_{n'})
+\cdots,
\]

where

\[
K_a(\xi)=\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-it\xi}\,dt
=
\frac{2\sin(a\xi)}{\xi}.
\]

The diagonal contribution is

\[
2a\sum_n|a_n|^2.
\]

But for \(a\asymp1\),

\[
|x_n-x_{n'}|\lesssim R^{-1}
\]

implies

\[
K_a(x_n-x_{n'})=2a+O(a^3R^{-2}).
\]

Thus the local \(L^2\) integral sees the whole packet as a coherent lump:

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2\,dt
\approx
2a\left|
\sum_n a_n e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\]

rather than

\[
2a\sum_n|a_n|^2.
\]

Since \(F(0)=0\), precisely this coherent sum can be small. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{short-window }L^2\text{ does not diagonalize the packet-frequency AFE.}
}
\]

This is the exact off-diagonal obstruction.

---

## 3. Can a larger window help?

If one takes

\[
a\asymp R,
\]

then the kernel begins to resolve the packet **diameter**:

\[
a\cdot \operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp1.
\]

This improves orthogonality between separated portions of the packet, but it still does not diagonalize individual prime frequencies. Adjacent prime normalized spacings are much smaller than \(R^{-1}\), so a true diagonal mean-square estimate would require a much longer interval.

However, \(a\asymp R\) may be enough for a **coarse block decomposition**. Split the packet into \(O(R)\) sub-blocks of normalized width \(\asymp R^{-1}\). An \(a\asymp R\) window can distinguish sub-blocks at different \(x\)-locations. A possible theorem is:

### Coarse packet \(L^2\) amplitude theorem candidate

If the packet-frequency AFE mass cannot concentrate into a single sub-block cancellation pattern compatible with

\[
F(0)=0,
\]

then

\[
\int_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|^2\,dt\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This would imply

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Since \(a=R\) is safe for the derivative lemma, this is a viable direction.

But the nonconcentration statement is again an actual prime-log arithmetic theorem. It is not automatic from coefficient mass.

---

## 4. Jensen/Cartan zero-crowding replacement

A second sufficient route is zero-crowding.

Let

\[
D_A=\{|t|\le A\},
\qquad
D_a=\{|t|\le a\}.
\]

Assume

\[
\sup_{D_A}|F|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{D_{A/2}}|F|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

and

\[
N_F(D_a)\le C_0R.
\]

Then a Jensen/Cartan argument should give

\[
\max_{1\le k\le C_0R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So a sufficient zero-crowding theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}\left(|m-m_0|\le a\lambda\right)\le C_0R
}
\]

for

\[
a\le(\log Q)^C.
\]

Since

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

this is a microscopic \(m\)-interval of length

\[
a\lambda\asymp \frac{a}{Q}.
\]

For \(a\asymp(\log Q)^C\), this is still far below the natural mean zero spacing in the usual \(t\)-aspect if \(Q\sim\log m\). So such a zero-crowding theorem is plausible heuristically, but proving it at the needed uniformity is a genuine zeta zero-spacing input.

---

## 5. Does known zeta/AFE structure plausibly give microscopic zero-crowding?

Heuristically, yes; from standard zero-density expectations, one would not expect \(O(R)\) zeros in an interval of length

\[
\frac{(\log Q)^C}{Q}
\]

around a typical high point if \(Q\sim\log m\). The expected number is much smaller than \(R\).

But for a proof, current inputs do not give the needed deterministic local bound. Existing global zero-counting controls do not by themselves prevent exceptional microscopic clusters. The AFE gives analytic complexity but not a zero-repulsion theorem at this scale.

Thus the rigorous status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{plausible but not derivable from the current framework.}
}
\]

A usable theorem would need to be imported or proved as an independent local zero-spacing / zero-crowding statement for \(Z_\alpha\).

---

## 6. Best theorem candidate

### Polylog-local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude theorem

For every admissible ordinary off-line zero \(m_0\),

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

there exists

\[
a\le(\log Q)^C
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

Together with the analytic complexity bound

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a(\log Q)^C}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

this implies

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalent zero-crowding version:

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}\left(
|m-m_0|\le \lambda(\log Q)^C
\right)
\le C_0R
}
\]

plus one outer amplitude value lower bound implies the same result.

---

## 7. No-go from current inputs

The obstruction remains:

\[
F(t)=\varepsilon t + t^{R+2}
\]

or a coherent short exponential packet analog. Such a function has

\[
F(0)=0
\]

and all derivatives through \(R+1\) can be made too small unless either:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|
\]

is forced to be polynomially large, or zeros are prevented from crowding.

The packet-frequency AFE excludes arbitrary functions, but its local \(L^2\) mass is not diagonal on the required window, so the current AFE input alone does not rule out this behavior.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local amplitude requires new microscopic actual-zeta input.}
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic reduction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Naive AFE }L^2\text{ diagonal method: fails by off-diagonal coherence.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Coarse }L^2\text{ on }a\asymp R\text{ window: plausible but still arithmetic.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Jensen/Cartan route: viable conditional on microscopic zero-crowding.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Unconditional theorem from current inputs: not available.}
}
\]

So the precise output is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 1 reduces }|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ to a new polylog-local }Z_\alpha\text{-amplitude / zero-crowding theorem.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 03:43:38)

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: polylog-local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude / zero-crowding. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Polylog-local amplitude is the right target, but it remains a new arithmetic input.}
}
\]

The analytic implication is now clean:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\qquad
a\le(\log Q)^C,
\]

plus analytic upper control on a larger disk implies

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The key improvement is that \(a\) may be polylogarithmic rather than \(O(1)\). This relaxes the amplitude theorem substantially, while staying compatible with the safe derivative depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

because

\[
a^R\le Q^{O(1)}
\]

for \(a\le(\log Q)^C\).

However, the local amplitude theorem still does not follow from AFE coefficient mass alone. Packet-frequency coherence can persist across \(O(1)\)-windows and partially across \(R\)-windows. A proof needs either a coarse packet non-cancellation theorem or microscopic zero-crowding/zero-spacing input for \(Z_\alpha\).

---

## 1. Sharp theorem needed

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

The needed local amplitude theorem can be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\exists a\le(\log Q)^C
\quad\text{such that}\quad
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

A stronger but cleaner version is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

This \(a=R\) version is especially natural because packet-frequency blocks have normalized diameter

\[
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1},
\]

so a window of length \(R\) starts to resolve the packet at the block scale.

---

## 2. Analytic implication to \(|\mathbf z'|\)

Assume \(F\) is holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\), with

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

and

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C.
\]

Let

\[
L=R+1.
\]

Taylor expand:

\[
F(t)=\sum_{k=1}^{L}\frac{F^{(k)}(0)}{k!}t^k+T_L(t).
\]

Cauchy bounds the tail on \(|t|\le a\) by

\[
|T_L(t)|
\ll
Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}.
\]

Because

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

choosing

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^C
\]

with \(C\) large gives

\[
Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{R+2}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Therefore at least one Taylor coefficient must obey

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{C_R a^R},
\]

with \(C_R\le \operatorname{poly}(R)\).

If

\[
a\le(\log Q)^C,
\]

then

\[
a^R
\le
\exp(CR\log\log Q)
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Hence

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Finally, passing from monomial derivatives to the basis-normalized operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) costs

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## 3. Coarse \(L^2\) packet decomposition

The packet-frequency AFE has the schematic form

\[
F(t)=
\sum_n a_n e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-itx_n}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

On the block

\[
cQ\le\log n\le cQ+\frac QR,
\]

one has

\[
x_n\in[x_0,x_0+O(R^{-1})].
\]

The local second moment is

\[
\int_{-a}^a |F(t)|^2\,dt
=
\sum_{n,n'}
a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
K_a(x_n-x_{n'})
+\cdots,
\]

where

\[
K_a(\xi)=\frac{2\sin(a\xi)}{\xi}.
\]

For \(a=O(1)\), since \(|x_n-x_{n'}|\lesssim R^{-1}\), one has

\[
K_a(x_n-x_{n'})\approx 2a,
\]

so the whole block behaves coherently. The diagonal mass

\[
2a\sum_n|a_n|^2
\]

does not dominate.

For \(a\asymp R\), the kernel begins to distinguish different parts of the packet because

\[
a\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp1.
\]

This suggests a coarse decomposition: split the packet-frequency block into sub-blocks

\[
\mathcal B_\nu
=
\{n:x_n\in I_\nu\},
\qquad
|I_\nu|\asymp R^{-1},
\]

or more finely into \(K\) sub-blocks with separation \(\gtrsim 1/a\). Then

\[
\int_{-a}^a |F(t)|^2dt
\]

detects the vector of coarse packet sums

\[
S_\nu(m_0)=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_\nu}
a_n e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

A plausible theorem would be:

### Coarse packet \(L^2\) theorem candidate

For every admissible zero \(m_0\),

\[
\sum_\nu |S_\nu(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|F(t)|^2dt\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and therefore

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But this theorem is not formal. It is a prime-log non-cancellation statement for the actual orbit at \(m_0\). It is weaker than full diagonalization, but still arithmetical.

---

## 4. Can packet coherence persist across \(a\asymp R\)?

Yes, in principle.

The condition \(F(0)=0\) imposes cancellation of the total coherent packet sum. On a window \(a\asymp R\), cancellation must persist across the packet’s first few coarse Fourier modes. This is stronger than cancellation at \(t=0\), but still possible in relaxed models.

More explicitly, if

\[
F(t)\approx e^{-itx_0}\sum_\nu S_\nu e^{-it(y_\nu/R)},
\]

then requiring \(F(t)\) small for \(|t|\le R\) means the trigonometric polynomial

\[
\sum_\nu S_\nu e^{-is y_\nu}
\]

is small for \(|s|\le 1\). This forces multiple moment cancellations among the \(S_\nu\), but a phase-relaxed model can arrange them.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
a\asymp R \text{ helps, but does not remove the need for arithmetic.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Zero-crowding sufficient condition

A clean replacement for amplitude is zero-crowding.

Let

\[
N_F(a)=\#\{t: F(t)=0,\ |t|\le a\},
\]

counted with multiplicity. A sufficient condition is:

\[
\boxed{
N_F(a)\le C_0R
}
\]

for some

\[
a\le(\log Q)^C,
\]

together with an outer amplitude lower bound

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A/2}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then Jensen/Cartan gives a derivative lower bound. The logic is:

If all derivatives through \(R+1\) at \(0\) are \(<Q^{-A}\), then \(F\) is effectively flat at \(0\). A flat zero at \(0\), combined with bounded outer growth and nontrivial outer amplitude, forces either:

\[
\text{many nearby zeros}
\]

or

\[
\text{large suppression of }F\text{ on the inner disk}.
\]

The zero-crowding bound rules this out.

In original \(m\)-coordinates, this requires

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}
\left(
|m-m_0|\le a\lambda
\right)
\le C_0R.
}
\]

Since

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

and \(a\le(\log Q)^C\), the window length is

\[
\frac{(\log Q)^C}{Q}.
\]

This is microscopic. A deterministic proof would be a genuine local zero-spacing or zero-density theorem.

---

## 6. Does known zeta/AFE structure plausibly give zero-crowding?

Heuristically, yes. If \(Q\sim\log m\), then an interval of length

\[
(\log Q)^C/Q
\]

is far below ordinary macroscopic height scale. One would not expect \(C_0R\) zeros of \(Z_\alpha\) to cluster there.

But the currently available inputs do not prove such a bound. Global zero-counting and ordinary density estimates do not exclude exceptional microscopic clusters at the level needed here.

So the rigorous status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{plausible but independent.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Final theorem candidate

### Polylog-local amplitude theorem

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0.
\]

For every admissible ordinary zero \(m_0\), there exists

\[
a\le(\log Q)^C
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
}
\]

Together with analytic AFE control on

\[
|t|\le a(\log Q)^C,
\]

this implies

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalent sufficient zero-crowding version:

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}
\left(
|m-m_0|\le \lambda(\log Q)^C
\right)
\le C_0R
}
\]

plus one outer amplitude lower bound.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative implication: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Strict one-packet amplitude: too strong; not necessary.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Polylog-local amplitude: correct target.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Coarse }L^2\text{ route at }a\asymp R: plausible but arithmetic.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Zero-crowding route: cleanest sufficient theorem, but new input.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s output is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ reduces to polylog-local }Z_\alpha\text{-amplitude or microscopic zero-crowding.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 03:46:59)

_Thought for a couple of seconds_

Agent 1 / A report: exact polylog-local amplitude-to-derivative theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The analytic reduction is Green.}
}
\]

If

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),\qquad F(0)=0,
\]

has polynomially large amplitude on a normalized window

\[
|t|\le a,\qquad 1\le a\le(\log Q)^C,
\]

and polynomial upper control on a larger disk

\[
|t|\le A,
\qquad A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]

then the normalized derivative vector satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for some finite exponent \(A'\).

This is now theorem-ready. The only unresolved part is proving the amplitude hypothesis for actual \(Z_\alpha\).

---

# 1. Theorem statement

Let

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad L=R+1.
\]

Let \(F\) be holomorphic on

\[
D_A=\{|t|\le A\},
\]

with

\[
F(0)=0.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

where

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^{C_a},
\]

and

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*}.
\]

If \(C_*\) is chosen so that

\[
C_*(R+2)\log\log Q
\ge
(A_0+A_1+C_{\rm tail})\log Q,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
Q^{-A_2}
}
\]

with

\[
A_2=A_0+O(C_a)+O(1).
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

it is enough to take

\[
\boxed{
C_* > A_0+A_1+C_{\rm tail}
}
\]

after absorbing the implicit constant in \(R\).

---

# 2. Proof

Write the Taylor expansion at \(0\):

\[
F(t)=\sum_{k=1}^{L} a_k t^k+T_L(t),
\qquad
a_k=\frac{F^{(k)}(0)}{k!}.
\]

By Cauchy estimates, for \(|t|\le a\),

\[
|T_L(t)|
\le
C Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}.
\]

The radius condition gives

\[
Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}
\le
Q^{A_1}(\log Q)^{-C_*(R+2)}
\le
\frac14Q^{-A_0}
\]

for \(C_*\) large enough.

Thus

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|T_L(t)|
\le
\frac14Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Since

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

we get

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}
\left|
\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k
\right|
\ge
\frac34Q^{-A_0}.
\]

If every coefficient obeyed

\[
|a_k|<
\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4L a^k},
\qquad 1\le k\le L,
\]

then for \(|t|\le a\),

\[
\left|
\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k
\right|
<
\sum_{k=1}^{L}\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4L}
=
\frac14Q^{-A_0},
\]

a contradiction.

Therefore, for some \(1\le k\le L\),

\[
|a_k|
\ge
\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4L a^k}
\ge
\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4L a^L}.
\]

Because

\[
a\le(\log Q)^{C_a}
\]

and

\[
L\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
a^L
\le
(\log Q)^{C_aL}
=
\exp(C_aL\log\log Q)
=
Q^{O(C_a)}.
\]

Also

\[
L=Q^{o(1)}.
\]

Hence

\[
|a_k|\ge Q^{-A_2}
\]

for some fixed \(A_2\). That proves

\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Dependence on \(a\)

The theorem works for all the relevant window sizes.

### Case \(a=1\)

The loss is only

\[
a^R=1.
\]

The derivative lower bound is essentially

\[
Q^{-A_0-o(1)}.
\]

This is the strongest case, but it requires a strict one-packet amplitude theorem.

### Case \(a=R\)

Since

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
R^R
=
\exp(R\log R)
=
Q^{1+o(1)}.
\]

So

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
Q^{-A_0-O(1)}.
\]

This is still fully polynomial.

### Case \(a=(\log Q)^C\)

Then

\[
a^R
=
\exp(CR\log\log Q)
=
Q^{O(C)}.
\]

So the loss remains polynomial:

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge
Q^{-A_0-O(C)}.
\]

Thus the amplitude theorem may safely be polylog-local.

---

# 4. Conversion to basis-normalized operators

The Wronskian uses operators

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D),
\qquad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m=\partial_t.
\]

Assume the basis-normalized operator system satisfies the conditioning bounds

\[
\|C_\ell\|,\ \|C_\ell^{-1}\|
\le
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

At safe depth,

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore the monomial derivative lower bound implies

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

after possibly increasing \(A\).

More explicitly, if

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}
\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}
\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

then

\[
\left\|
\bigl(C_\ell(\partial_t)F(0)\bigr)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
\right\|
\ge
Q^{-A_2-O(1)}
=
Q^{-A}.
\]

---

# 5. Annular amplitude version

The theorem still works if the amplitude lower bound holds only on an annulus

\[
a/2\le |t|\le a.
\]

Indeed,

\[
\sup_{a/2\le |t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

implies

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

The proof above uses only the disk supremum, so it applies immediately.

A slightly sharper annular statement is useful for Jensen/Cartan applications:

If

\[
\sup_{a/2\le |t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

and

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

then the same conclusion follows, with identical radius requirement

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*}.
\]

Thus an amplitude point anywhere in the annulus suffices.

---

# 6. Black-box theorem for the Wronskian route

### Polylog-local amplitude-to-\(\mathbf z'\) theorem

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Let

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^{C_a},
\]

\[
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]

with \(C_*\) sufficiently large in terms of \(A_0,A_1,C_a\) and the implicit constant in \(R\).

Assume also that the basis-normalized operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) have conditioning cost

\[
\exp(O(R\log R)).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the desired black-box analytic theorem.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Amplitude-to-derivative theorem: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
a=1,\ a=R,\ a=(\log Q)^C\text{ are all safe.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Annular amplitude also suffices.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining unsolved part is proving the polylog-local amplitude or zero-crowding hypothesis for actual }Z_\alpha.
}
\]
