_Thought for 10s_

Agent 1 / A report: polylog-local \(Z_\alpha\)-amplitude. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The amplitude theorem is not closed, but it has a sharper reduced form: coarse packet-cell non-cancellation.}
}
\]

The cleanest remaining target is no longer a generic analytic statement. It is the following arithmetic statement:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A},
}
\]

where \(B_r\) are coarse packet-frequency cell sums

\[
B_r(m_0)
=
\sum_{n:x_n\in I_r}
z_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\qquad
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

If this holds for a partition into cells of width \(\asymp 1/R\), then a local \(L^2\)-amplitude bound on a window

\[
|t|\le a,\qquad a\asymp R,
\]

follows. Since \(a=R\le(\log Q)^C\), the existing analytic theorem gives

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

So the current reduction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coarse packet-cell non-cancellation}
\Rightarrow
\text{polylog-local amplitude}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The empirical Agent 5 amplitude pass, with \(1152\) rows and no yellow/red, supports this direction, but it is not a proof.

---

## 1. Sharp amplitude theorem needed

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

A sufficient theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
}
\]

for some

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^C.
\]

The strongest useful version is

\[
a\asymp R,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

This is large enough to begin resolving packet-frequency cells, but still small enough that the derivative-recovery loss

\[
a^R
\]

is polynomial:

\[
R^R=\exp(R\log R)=Q^{1+o(1)}.
\]

Thus the target may be stated as:

### Polylog-local amplitude theorem

For every admissible ordinary zero \(m_0\),

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le R}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

A weaker but still sufficient form permits

\[
R\le a\le(\log Q)^C.
\]

---

## 2. Coarse \(L^2\) formulation

Use the packet-frequency AFE approximation

\[
F(t)
=
\sum_n a_n e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-itx_n}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
a_n=z_n(\alpha,m_0),
\qquad
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

On the ordinary packet-frequency block,

\[
cQ\le\log n\le cQ+\frac QR,
\]

so

\[
x_n\in[x_0,x_0+O(R^{-1})].
\]

The local second moment is

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2\,dt
=
\sum_{n,n'}
a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
K_a(x_n-x_{n'})
+\cdots,
\]

with

\[
K_a(\xi)=\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-it\xi}\,dt
=
\frac{2\sin(a\xi)}{\xi}.
\]

For

\[
a=O(1),
\]

one has

\[
a|x_n-x_{n'}|\ll1
\]

through the packet, so

\[
K_a(x_n-x_{n'})\approx2a.
\]

Therefore the second moment is essentially coherent and does not diagonalize:

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt
\approx
2a
\left|
\sum_n a_n e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2.
\]

Since

\[
F(0)=0,
\]

this can be small. Thus strict one-packet \(L^2\) is too weak.

---

## 3. Why \(a\asymp R\) is the right scale

For

\[
a\asymp R,
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1},
\]

the kernel begins to resolve packet-scale variation:

\[
a\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp1.
\]

Partition the normalized packet interval into cells

\[
I_r
\]

of width

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Define cell sums

\[
\boxed{
B_r(m_0)
=
\sum_{n:x_n\in I_r}
a_n e^{-im_0\log n}.
}
\]

Then

\[
F(t)
\approx
\sum_r B_r(m_0)e^{-itx_r}
\]

on \(|t|\le R\), up to intra-cell variation and AFE errors.

After rescaling

\[
s=t/R,
\]

this becomes a bounded-frequency trigonometric packet:

\[
F(Rs)
\approx
\sum_r B_r e^{-iRsx_r}.
\]

Since the cell centers satisfy

\[
R(x_r-x_{r'})\asymp |r-r'|,
\]

orthogonality over \(s\in[-1,1]\) gives heuristically

\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|F(t)|^2dt
\asymp
R\sum_r |B_r|^2
\]

up to controlled off-diagonal leakage.

Thus the sufficient arithmetic condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|F(t)|^2dt\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and hence

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This supplies the needed polylog-local amplitude.

---

## 4. Precise cell-sum non-cancellation theorem

A theorem usable by the Wronskian route is:

### Coarse packet-cell non-cancellation theorem

Let

\[
m_0
\]

be an admissible ordinary zero of \(Z_\alpha\), and let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le\log n\le cQ+Q/R\}.
\]

Partition

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

into \(O(1)\) or \(O(R)\) cells \(I_r\) of width \(\asymp R^{-1}\). Define

\[
B_r(m_0)
=
\sum_{n:x_n\in I_r}
z_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le R}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

And therefore,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

This theorem is weaker than full diagonal non-cancellation; it permits cancellation inside cells, but forbids all coarse cell sums from collapsing simultaneously at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

---

## 5. Relation to Agent 5 empirical pass

Agent 5’s local-amplitude pass checked

\[
a\in\{1,R,2R,(\log Q)^2\}
\]

over \(1152\) rows and found

\[
0\ \text{yellow},\qquad 0\ \text{red}.
\]

That is precisely consistent with the theorem above. The empirical test did not find a point where all of the following held simultaneously:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)\approx0,
\]

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ll Q^{-A},
\]

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}\ll Q^{-A},
\]

and high local crowding.

The next empirical refinement should therefore target the cell sums:

\[
B_r(m_0)
\]

directly. A real warning would be:

\[
|Z_\alpha(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A},
\qquad
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ll Q^{-A},
\qquad
\sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

---

## 6. Can coherence persist across the \(R\)-window?

In relaxed models, yes. One can choose phases so that

\[
B_r\approx0
\]

for every coarse cell. Then

\[
F(t)
\]

is small on \(|t|\le R\). Thus the cell-sum theorem is not local analysis; it is an actual prime-log non-cancellation statement.

The actual zeta orbit may forbid such simultaneous cell cancellations, but that is precisely the missing arithmetic. The theorem is plausible because the constraints

\[
B_r(m_0)\approx0
\]

for many cells, together with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

are overdetermined for the actual one-parameter orbit. But dimension-counting alone is not enough; previous recurrence analysis showed generic recurrence can be too cheap.

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coarse }L^2\text{ reduces amplitude to actual cell-sum non-cancellation.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Zero-crowding alternative

The zero-crowding sufficient condition remains:

\[
\boxed{
N_{Z_\alpha}
\left(
|m-m_0|\le \lambda(\log Q)^C
\right)
\le C_0R.
}
\]

Together with an outer amplitude value and upper control, this implies the same derivative lower bound. But this is a microscopic zero-spacing theorem for \(Z_\alpha\).

Comparing the two routes:

\[
\text{cell-sum non-cancellation}
\]

is a prime-side theorem, while

\[
\text{zero-crowding}
\]

is a zero-side theorem. They are likely equivalent in difficulty through the explicit formula.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Amplitude-to-derivative implication: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Best amplitude target: } \sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A}.}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Coarse }L^2\text{ route reduces to cell-sum non-cancellation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cell-sum non-cancellation is new actual prime-log arithmetic.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s final reduced theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{n:x_n\in I_r}
z_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem would imply polylog-local amplitude and therefore

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 04:16:43)

_Thought for 12s_

Agent 1 / A report: cell-sum theorem formulation. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cell-sum non-cancellation gives a clean route to polylog-local amplitude, hence to }|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The useful theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for a cell partition at resolution

\[
|I_r|\asymp a^{-1},
\qquad
1\le a\le(\log Q)^C.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt\gg a\sum_r|B_r|^2
\]

up to controlled Gram/off-diagonal error, so

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

The existing amplitude-to-derivative theorem then gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

So the remaining arithmetic input can be stated as a concrete cell-sum non-cancellation theorem.

---

## 1. Setup

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

On a packet-frequency branch, write

\[
F(t)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B} b_n e^{-itx_n}
+
F_{\rm rest}(t),
\]

where

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
b_n=z_n(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

For the ordinary determinant block,

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le\log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\]

so

\[
\operatorname{diam}\{x_n:n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\}
\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

For amplitude recovery, we may use one block or a union of packet-frequency blocks. The cell-sum theorem is most naturally stated for any finite packet-frequency frequency set

\[
\mathcal X=\{x_n\}.
\]

---

## 2. Cell partitions

For a window length \(a\), choose cells

\[
I_r=[r\delta,(r+1)\delta),
\qquad
\delta=\kappa a^{-1},
\]

with fixed small \(\kappa>0\).

Define

\[
\mathcal B_r=\{n:x_n\in I_r\},
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
B_r(m_0)=\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_r} b_n.
}
\]

Relevant choices:

### \(a=R\)

\[
\delta\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

On a single ordinary packet-frequency block of diameter \(\asymp R^{-1}\), this produces \(O(1)\) cells. On a union of adjacent packet-frequency blocks, it gives the natural packet-scale coarse resolution.

### \(a=2R\)

\[
\delta\asymp (2R)^{-1}.
\]

This gives a slightly finer split and helps detect cancellation between halves of a packet-frequency block.

### \(a=(\log Q)^2\)

\[
\delta\asymp(\log Q)^{-2}.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one ordinary packet-frequency block of width \(R^{-1}\) contains about

\[
\frac{R^{-1}}{(\log Q)^{-2}}
=
\frac{(\log Q)^2}{R}
\asymp
\log Q\log\log Q
\]

cells. This is a much stronger diagnostic but still safe for the derivative theorem because \(a\le(\log Q)^C\).

---

## 3. Cell sums imply local \(L^2\) amplitude

Let

\[
F_{\rm cell}(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r},
\]

where \(\xi_r\in I_r\) is a representative cell center.

Then

\[
F(t)=F_{\rm cell}(t)+E_{\rm intra}(t)+F_{\rm rest}(t),
\]

where

\[
E_{\rm intra}(t)
=
\sum_r\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_r}
b_n\left(e^{-itx_n}-e^{-it\xi_r}\right).
\]

For \(|t|\le a\), since

\[
|x_n-\xi_r|\le \delta\asymp a^{-1},
\]

we get

\[
|e^{-itx_n}-e^{-it\xi_r}|
\ll |t||x_n-\xi_r|
\ll 1.
\]

To make this a small error rather than merely bounded, take \(\delta=\kappa/a\) with \(\kappa\ll1\). Then

\[
\|E_{\rm intra}\|_{L^2[-a,a]}
\le
C\kappa
\left(\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm raw}(t)|^2dt\right)^{1/2},
\]

or more concretely,

\[
\|E_{\rm intra}\|_{L^2[-a,a]}^2
\ll
\kappa^2 a\sum_r |B_r|^2
+
\text{within-cell variance}.
\]

Thus after choosing \(\kappa\) small and absorbing the intra-cell variance into either a refined partition or an error term, it is enough to lower-bound

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt.
\]

Now

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt
=
\sum_{r,s}B_r\overline{B_s}
K_a(\xi_r-\xi_s),
\]

where

\[
K_a(u)=\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-itu}dt
=
\frac{2\sin(au)}{u}.
\]

If cell centers are separated by

\[
|\xi_r-\xi_s|\ge c a^{-1}|r-s|,
\]

then the normalized Gram matrix

\[
G_{rs}
=
\frac1{2a}K_a(\xi_r-\xi_s)
\]

is a bounded positive-definite Gram matrix for exponentials on \([-a,a]\). For a finite family of cells with controlled density, its least eigenvalue is bounded below by a constant depending only on the separation/density scheme, or at worst by

\[
\exp(-O(N_{\rm cell}))
\]

if many cells are packed into a short interval.

Therefore, for the intended cell systems,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt
\ge
c_{\rm Gram}\,a\sum_r |B_r|^2.
}
\]

If

\[
c_{\rm Gram}\ge Q^{-C_G},
\]

then

\[
\sum_r |B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

after subtracting controlled intra-cell, dual/background, and \(E_2\)-type errors.

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

## 4. Loss accounting

### Cell width

Choosing

\[
\delta=\kappa/a
\]

with fixed \(\kappa\) keeps intra-cell phase variation bounded by \(O(\kappa)\) on \([-a,a]\). If one wants an error \(Q^{-C}\), choose

\[
\kappa=Q^{-C}
\]

but this increases the number of cells. For proof architecture, fixed small \(\kappa\) is preferable; the theorem should lower-bound robust coarse cell energy rather than rely on arbitrarily fine cells.

### Gram conditioning

For separated cell centers at spacing \(\asymp a^{-1}\), the Gram matrix of exponentials over \([-a,a]\) has condition number at most

\[
\exp(O(N_{\rm cell}))
\]

in the worst case, and often \(O(1)\) for regular grids.

For

\[
a=R
\]

and one packet-frequency block, \(N_{\rm cell}=O(1)\), so conditioning is harmless.

For

\[
a=(\log Q)^2
\]

inside one block,

\[
N_{\rm cell}\asymp \frac{a}{R}\asymp \log Q\log\log Q.
\]

A worst-case \(\exp(O(N_{\rm cell}))\) loss would be too large:

\[
\exp(O(\log Q\log\log Q))=Q^{O(\log\log Q)}.
\]

Thus, for proof purposes, the cleanest choices are

\[
\boxed{
a=R \quad\text{or}\quad a=2R.
}
\]

These keep the number of cells per packet bounded or modest and avoid severe Gram losses.

### Dual/background/error terms

Write

\[
F=F^+_{\rm cell}+F^-_{\rm cell}+F_B+F_E.
\]

The theorem should either include both branches in the cell sums,

\[
B_r=B_r^+ + B_r^-,
\]

or require that the branch not used contributes an error smaller than \(Q^{-A}\) on \([-a,a]\).

The robust version is:

\[
\boxed{
B_r
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}b_n^+
+
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}b_n^-.
}
\]

Then background/error terms need

\[
\|F_B+F_E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le \frac12 Q^{-A}.
\]

For canonical use, this must include \(B_2\), the folded dual branch, and \(E_2\) control.

---

## 5. Arithmetic theorem needed

The exact arithmetic input is:

### Cell-sum non-cancellation theorem

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible ordinary center with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)
\]

and form packet-frequency cells \(I_r\) at resolution

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}
\]

for the main and folded dual AFE packet-frequency support.

Define

\[
\boxed{
B_r(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the theorem that replaces the missing local amplitude input.

Combined with the analytic package, it gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

---

## 6. Theorem-ready package

### Theorem: cell sums imply local amplitude

Let

\[
F(t)
=
\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}+E(t)
\]

on \([-a,a]\), where

\[
|\xi_r-\xi_s|\ge c a^{-1}|r-s|,
\]

and the exponential Gram matrix satisfies

\[
\lambda_{\min}
\left(
\frac1{2a}
\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-it(\xi_r-\xi_s)}dt
\right)
\ge Q^{-C_G}.
\]

If

\[
\sum_r |B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A_B},
\]

and

\[
\|E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}^2\le \frac12 Q^{-A_B-C_G}a,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt\ge Q^{-A}a.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

If additionally

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^C
\]

and the outer analytic control condition holds, then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cell-sum } \Rightarrow L^2\text{ amplitude: Green, with Gram/error hypotheses.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Best proof scale: }a=R\text{ or }2R.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Using }a=(\log Q)^2\text{ may introduce too many cells unless Gram conditioning is improved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining arithmetic theorem: }Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\Rightarrow\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the theorem-ready cell-sum package for the \(|\mathbf z'|\) side of the Wronskian route.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 05:43:46)

_Thought for 5s_

Agent 1 / A report: multi-block cell-sum theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The cell-sum route should use a multi-block packet-frequency support, not one }Q/R\text{-block.}
}
\]

A single determinant block

\[
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+\frac QR
\]

has normalized diameter

\[
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

On a window

\[
|t|\le R,
\]

this is only one effective Fourier cell. Then the cell sum is close to the already-cancelled value

\[
F(0)=Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

So the theorem must enlarge the support to cover multiple packet-frequency cells. The clean version is to use a support of normalized width

\[
\Delta_x\asymp 1,
\]

equivalently

\[
L_{\rm wide}\asymp Q
\]

in \(\log n\)-coordinates, while staying inside the AFE plateau:

\[
cQ\le \log n\le (c+\delta)Q,
\qquad 0<c<c+\delta<c_1<\frac12.
\]

Then partition into cells of width

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

This gives

\[
M\asymp R
\]

meaningful cells, enough for a real anti-design/non-cancellation theorem but still compatible with the analytic derivative recovery.

---

## 1. Multi-block support

Use normalized frequency

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Instead of one block

\[
cQ\le \log n\le cQ+\frac QR,
\]

take a wider support

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+L_{\rm wide}\}.
}
\]

The normalized width is

\[
\Delta_x=\lambda L_{\rm wide}.
\]

To obtain \(M\) cells of width \(R^{-1}\), choose

\[
\Delta_x\asymp \frac{M}{R}.
\]

Thus

\[
L_{\rm wide}\asymp \frac{MQ}{R}.
\]

The useful regimes are:

\[
M\asymp R^\beta,\qquad 0<\beta\le1,
\]

or most cleanly

\[
\boxed{
M\asymp R,
\qquad
L_{\rm wide}\asymp Q,
\qquad
\Delta_x\asymp1.
}
\]

To stay away from the AFE saddle/transition, impose

\[
0<c<c+\Delta_x/(\lambda Q)<c_1<\frac12.
\]

Since \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), this means choose a fixed interval

\[
\boxed{
x\in[x_-,x_+]\subset(0,1/2)
}
\]

bounded away from \(0\) and \(1/2\).

---

## 2. Cell partition

For the local amplitude window

\[
|t|\le a,
\]

choose cell width

\[
\delta_x=\kappa a^{-1},
\]

with fixed small \(\kappa>0\). Define cells

\[
I_r=[x_-+r\delta_x,\ x_-+(r+1)\delta_x).
\]

For the natural choice

\[
a\asymp R,
\]

we get

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

If the wide support has normalized width

\[
\Delta_x\asymp1,
\]

then the number of cells is

\[
\boxed{
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
}
\]

Define the full main+dual cell sums

\[
\boxed{
B_r(m_0)
=
B_r^+(m_0)
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-(m_0)
+
B_r^{\rm bg}(m_0)
+
B_r^E(m_0).
}
\]

Here

\[
B_r^+(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

The background/error terms may alternatively be kept outside the cell theorem as an \(L^2\)-small remainder. The robust canonical statement includes them in the decomposition but requires

\[
\|F_{\rm bg}+F_E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le Q^{-A_{\rm err}}.
\]

---

## 3. Analytic implication

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t).
\]

On the chosen support, write

\[
F(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}+E(t),
\]

where \(\xi_r\in I_r\) is a cell center and \(E\) includes intra-cell oscillation, tails, background not assigned to cells, and AFE error.

The cell Gram matrix is

\[
G_{rs}
=
\frac1{2a}
\int_{-a}^{a}
e^{-it(\xi_r-\xi_s)}\,dt
=
\frac{\sin(a(\xi_r-\xi_s))}{a(\xi_r-\xi_s)}.
\]

If

\[
\xi_r=x_-+r\delta_x,
\qquad
\delta_x=\kappa/a,
\]

then

\[
a(\xi_r-\xi_s)=\kappa(r-s).
\]

For \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\), the Gram matrix may have conditioning losses if \(\kappa\) is too small or the interval is oversampled. The cleanest proof choice is to take approximately Nyquist spacing

\[
\boxed{
\delta_x\asymp a^{-1}
}
\]

with constants chosen so that the exponential family is a Riesz sequence on \([-a,a]\). Then

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge c_G>0
}
\]

for separated cells in a fixed normalized frequency interval. If using a denser partition, allow

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}
\left|\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}\right|^2dt
=
2a\,B^*GB
\ge
2a\,Q^{-C_G}\sum_r|B_r|^2.
\]

If

\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A_B}
\]

and

\[
\|E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}^2
\le
\frac12 aQ^{-A_B-C_G},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt\ge aQ^{-A}
}
\]

for some \(A\). Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Since \(a\le R\le(\log Q)^C\), the existing amplitude-to-derivative theorem yields

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

## 4. Minimal support width

The support width must produce enough independent cells so the cell theorem is not just the cancelled value \(F(0)=0\).

If a single ordinary block has width

\[
\Delta_x\asymp R^{-1},
\]

then at \(a\asymp R\) it contributes only

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp1
\]

cell. In that case

\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2
\]

can be equivalent to

\[
|F(0)|^2
\]

or to one coarse cancellation, so it is not useful.

Thus require at least

\[
\boxed{
M_{\rm cell}\ge C_0R^\beta
}
\]

for some fixed \(\beta>0\), and preferably

\[
\boxed{
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
}
\]

This means

\[
\Delta_x\asymp1
\]

and therefore

\[
\boxed{
L_{\rm wide}\asymp Q.
}
\]

Equivalently, use several \(Q/R\)-blocks:

\[
\boxed{
\#\text{blocks}\asymp R.
}
\]

A practical theorem-ready support is

\[
\boxed{
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
}
\]

Then

\[
x_n\in[\lambda c_-Q,\lambda c_+Q]
\]

has fixed positive width.

---

## 5. Multi-block cell-sum theorem

The arithmetic input should be stated as follows.

### Multi-block cell-sum non-cancellation theorem

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible ordinary zero:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,\qquad R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Choose fixed constants

\[
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12
\]

and define the packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q\}.
\]

Partition

\[
x_n^\pm
\]

into cells

\[
I_r
\]

of width

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Define

\[
B_r(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Then the desired arithmetic theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem implies

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and hence

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

---

## 6. Error and branch handling

The theorem should be written in one of two equivalent ways.

### Inclusive version

Include all canonical pieces in the cell sums:

\[
B_r=B_r^++e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-+B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E.
\]

Then the non-cancellation theorem is directly canonical but harder to prove.

### Perturbative version

Prove the cell-sum theorem for the main+dual AFE packet part:

\[
B_r^{\rm md}=B_r^++e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-.
\]

Assume the remaining canonical pieces satisfy

\[
\|F_{\rm bg}+F_E\|_{L^2[-R,R]}\le Q^{-A_{\rm err}}.
\]

Then the implication to amplitude remains valid.

The perturbative version is probably cleaner, provided \(B_2\), tails, and \(E_2\) are already controlled at this scale.

---

## 7. Gram conditioning

For

\[
a=R
\]

and cell width

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\]

over a fixed frequency interval \(x\in[x_-,x_+]\), the number of cells is

\[
M\asymp R.
\]

The continuous Gram matrix

\[
G_{rs}=\operatorname{sinc}(R(\xi_r-\xi_s))
\]

is stable for near-Nyquist separated cells. A conservative theorem can assume

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G}.
}
\]

Because \(M\asymp R\), even a conditioning loss of

\[
\exp(O(R))
\]

is only

\[
Q^{O(1/\log\log Q)}
\]

and therefore safe. Losses of

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))
\]

are also safe:

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Thus Gram conditioning is not the blocker if the cells are chosen at the \(1/R\) scale and the support width is fixed.

---

## 8. Final theorem-ready package

### Theorem: multi-block cell sums imply \(|\mathbf z'|\)

Assume:

1. Ordinary scale:

   \[
   \lambda Q\asymp1,\qquad R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
   \]

2. Multi-block packet-frequency support:

   \[
   c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<1/2.
   \]

3. Cell partition in \(x=\lambda\log n\) of width:

   \[
   |I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
   \]

4. Cell-sum non-cancellation at admissible zeros:

   \[
   Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
   \Rightarrow
   \sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A_B}.
   \]

5. Gram and canonical error control:

   \[
   \lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G},
   \]

   \[
   \|E\|_{L^2[-R,R]}\le Q^{-A_E}
   \]

   with \(A_E\) sufficiently large.

Then

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Single }Q/R\text{-block cell-sum theorem: too weak / degenerate.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Multi-block support of fixed normalized width: correct formulation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Minimal useful support: }M_{\rm cell}\gg1;\text{ preferred }M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The analytic implication is Green once the multi-block cell-sum lower bound is supplied.}
}
\]

The remaining arithmetic theorem is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
B_r^+(m_0)+e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-(m_0)+B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the correct multi-block cell-sum target for unlocking the \(|\mathbf z'|\) side of the Wronskian route.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:46:10)

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: formal multiblock cell-sum theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The multiblock cell-sum package is theorem-ready as an analytic reduction.}
}
\]

The correct black-box input is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Once this is supplied on a support spanning \(K\ge 8\) packet-frequency cells, it implies:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A'}
\Longrightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

The analytic implication is stable for

\[
a=R,\qquad a=2R,
\]

and also possible for

\[
a=(\log Q)^2
\]

if Gram conditioning is explicitly controlled. For proof, the safest default is

\[
\boxed{a=R\text{ or }2R.}
\]

---

## 1. Setup

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Use a multiblock packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_K
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+KQ/R\},
\qquad K\ge 8.
\]

The normalized frequencies are

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

Since \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), the support has normalized width

\[
\Delta_x
=
\lambda\frac{KQ}{R}
\asymp
\frac KR.
\]

For \(K=8\), this gives roughly eight natural cells at scale \(R^{-1}\). For \(K=16\), roughly sixteen.

Write the packet-frequency AFE model as

\[
F(t)
=
F_{\rm cell}(t)+E(t),
\]

where

\[
F_{\rm cell}(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r},
\]

and \(E(t)\) contains intra-cell error, omitted AFE tails, background pieces not assigned to cells, and \(E_2\)-type perturbative error.

---

## 2. Cells

For a local window length \(a\), define cells

\[
I_r=[x_-+r\delta,\ x_-+(r+1)\delta),
\]

with

\[
\delta\asymp a^{-1}.
\]

The natural choices are:

### Case \(a=R\)

\[
\delta\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp K.
\]

This is the cleanest theorem setting for \(K=8,16\), because the number of cells is fixed or slowly controlled.

### Case \(a=2R\)

\[
\delta\asymp (2R)^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp 2K.
\]

This gives finer resolution without changing the proof architecture.

### Case \(a=(\log Q)^2\)

\[
\delta\asymp(\log Q)^{-2}.
\]

Since

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

one \(KQ/R\)-wide support has

\[
M_{\rm cell}
\asymp
K\frac{(\log Q)^2}{R}
\asymp
K\log Q\log\log Q
\]

cells. This is useful numerically but may introduce nontrivial Gram losses in a proof. Treat it as a diagnostic/rescue window, not the default theorem scale.

---

## 3. Full canonical cell sums

For each cell \(I_r\), define the full canonical cell sum

\[
\boxed{
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
}
\]

Here

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

The folded dual nodes are

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}
\]

up to the exact convention-dependent correction.

There are two acceptable theorem formats.

### Inclusive format

Include all canonical terms directly in \(B_r\):

\[
B_r=B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-+B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E.
\]

Then the arithmetic theorem is fully canonical but harder to prove.

### Perturbative format

Define

\[
B_r^{\rm md}=B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-.
\]

Prove

\[
\sum_r |B_r^{\rm md}|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and assume background/error control

\[
\|F_{\rm bg}+F_E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le Q^{-A_{\rm err}}
\]

with \(A_{\rm err}\) large enough. This is cleaner for proof architecture if \(B_2\), tails, and \(E_2\) are already controlled.

---

## 4. Analytic implication: cell mass gives local \(L^2\)

Let \(\xi_r\in I_r\) be a cell center. Then

\[
F_{\rm cell}(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}.
\]

The Gram matrix on \([-a,a]\) is

\[
G_{rs}
=
\frac1{2a}
\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-it(\xi_r-\xi_s)}\,dt
=
\frac{\sin(a(\xi_r-\xi_s))}{a(\xi_r-\xi_s)}.
\]

Assume the cell centers are separated at scale

\[
|\xi_r-\xi_s|\gtrsim a^{-1}|r-s|
\]

and the Gram lower bound

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt
=
2a\,B^*GB
\ge
2aQ^{-C_G}\sum_r |B_r|^2.
\]

If

\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A_B},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt
\ge
aQ^{-A_B-C_G}.
}
\]

If the error term obeys

\[
\boxed{
\|E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}^2
\le
\frac12 aQ^{-A_B-C_G},
}
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt
\ge
\frac12aQ^{-A_B-C_G}.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|
\ge
Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for some \(A'\).

---

## 5. From local amplitude to \(|\mathbf z'|\)

The existing analytic theorem says:

If

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A'},
\]

with

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^C,
\]

and

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\qquad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

For \(a=R\) or \(2R\),

\[
a^R=\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

For \(a=(\log Q)^2\),

\[
a^R=\exp(O(R\log\log Q))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Thus all three \(a\)-choices are analytically compatible with derivative recovery. The only concern for \((\log Q)^2\) is Gram conditioning, not derivative recovery.

---

## 6. Gram conditioning by \(K\) and \(M_{\rm cell}\)

### \(K=8\), \(a=R\)

The support spans about \(8\) natural cells:

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp8.
\]

Gram conditioning is harmless:

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\gg1
\]

for well-spaced cells, or at worst

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-o(1)}.
\]

### \(K=16\), \(a=R\)

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp16.
\]

Still harmless.

### \(M_{\rm cell}=R,2R,4R\)

If one uses finer cells so that

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R,\ 2R,\ 4R,
\]

then a conservative bound

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge\exp(-O(M_{\rm cell}))
\]

is still safe for \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\), because

\[
\exp(-O(R))=Q^{-o(1)}.
\]

For \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\log R\) or larger, one should explicitly track conditioning. Losses of size

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

are still acceptable; losses beyond that are not.

Thus theorem scale should prefer:

\[
\boxed{
K=8\text{ or }16,\qquad a=R\text{ or }2R.
}
\]

---

## 7. Error bounds needed

For the perturbative version, the needed canonical error bound is:

\[
\boxed{
\|F_{\rm bg}+F_E+F_{\rm tail}\|_{L^2[-a,a]}^2
\le
\frac12aQ^{-A_B-C_G}.
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\|F_{\rm bg}\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le Q^{-A_{\rm bg}},
\]

\[
\|F_E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le Q^{-A_E},
\]

\[
\|F_{\rm tail}\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le Q^{-A_T},
\]

with

\[
A_{\rm bg},A_E,A_T
\]

chosen larger than the final target exponent.

If \(B_2\) is not small, it should be included in the cells or treated as a known deterministic background contribution. It must not be dropped.

For the inclusive version, the theorem instead assumes directly

\[
\sum_r|B_r^{\rm full}|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

---

## 8. Black-box theorem

### Theorem: multiblock cell mass implies \(|\mathbf z'|\)

Assume:

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let

\[
\mathcal B_K
=
\{n:cQ\le\log n\le cQ+KQ/R\},
\qquad K\ge8.
\]

Choose

\[
a=R
\quad\text{or}\quad
a=2R,
\]

and partition normalized packet frequencies into cells \(I_r\) of width

\[
|I_r|\asymp a^{-1}.
\]

Define full canonical cell sums

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A_B},
\]

and the associated cell Gram matrix satisfies

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G}.
\]

Then

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

If, in addition,

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\qquad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

## 9. Remaining arithmetic theorem

The proof-side input is now precisely:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the multiblock actual-prime cell-sum non-cancellation theorem.

Equivalently, in perturbative form:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A},
}
\]

plus canonical background/error \(L^2\)-control.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic package: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use }K\ge8\text{ multiblock support; single block is too weak.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Preferred proof windows: }a=R\text{ or }2R.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining proof input: actual-prime multiblock cell-sum non-cancellation.}
}
\]

This is the theorem-ready multiblock cell-sum package for unlocking the \(|\mathbf z'|\) side of the Wronskian route.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:49:13)

_Thought for 6s_

Agent 1 / A report: final analytic package for fixed-width cell sums. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-width multiblock cell mass gives a theorem-ready analytic route to }|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The correct support is a fixed normalized interval

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]

so that

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\in[x_-,x_+]\subset(0,1/2)
\]

has fixed positive width. Partition this interval into cells of width

\[
\delta_x\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

If the full canonical cell vector satisfies

\[
\sum_r |B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then, under standard Gram and canonical error control,

\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|^2dt\ge Q^{-A'},
\]

hence

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A''},
\]

and the already-established amplitude-to-derivative lemma gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'''}.
}
\]

---

## 1. Fixed-width support

Use

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Since

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

the normalized frequencies satisfy

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\in[x_-,x_+],
\]

where

\[
0<x_-<x_+<\frac12
\]

and

\[
x_+-x_-\asymp1.
\]

This is preferable to a \(KQ/R\)-block if the goal is a proof theorem rather than a finite numerical stress test, because it gives

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

rather than merely \(O(K)\) cells.

---

## 2. Cell definition

For the preferred local amplitude window

\[
a=R
\]

or

\[
a=2R,
\]

define cells

\[
I_r=[x_-+r\delta,\ x_-+(r+1)\delta),
\]

with

\[
\delta=\frac{\kappa}{a},
\]

where \(\kappa\asymp1\) is chosen so that the cell-center exponentials form a stable frame on \([-a,a]\).

Let \(\xi_r\in I_r\) be the cell center.

The number of cells is

\[
M_{\rm cell}
\asymp
\frac{x_+-x_-}{\delta}
\asymp a
\asymp R.
\]

---

## 3. Canonical cell sums

Define

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Here

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

The folded dual nodes are

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n},
\]

up to the precise convention-dependent completed-phase correction.

There are two possible theorem formats.

### Inclusive canonical format

Put all canonical terms into \(B_r\). Then the needed arithmetic input is directly

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest final statement but the hardest arithmetic theorem.

### Perturbative format

Define

\[
B_r^{\rm md}=B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-.
\]

Prove

\[
\sum_r |B_r^{\rm md}|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and assume

\[
\|F_{\rm bg}+F_E+F_{\rm tail}\|_{L^2[-a,a]}\le Q^{-A_{\rm err}}
\]

with \(A_{\rm err}\) larger than the target exponent. This is usually better for proof bookkeeping.

---

## 4. Lower frame bound

The cell model is

\[
F_{\rm cell}(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}.
\]

The Gram matrix is

\[
G_{rs}
=
\frac1{2a}\int_{-a}^{a}e^{-it(\xi_r-\xi_s)}dt
=
\frac{\sin(a(\xi_r-\xi_s))}{a(\xi_r-\xi_s)}.
\]

If

\[
\xi_r=x_-+r\delta,
\qquad
\delta=\frac{\kappa}{a},
\]

then

\[
a(\xi_r-\xi_s)=\kappa(r-s).
\]

For separated cells at near-Nyquist scale \(\delta\asymp a^{-1}\), the exponentials form a finite Riesz sequence on \([-a,a]\). Thus one may assume or prove a frame bound

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G}.
}
\]

In the regular-grid case with \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp a\asymp R\), a conservative bound of the form

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge \exp(-O(R))
\]

is already acceptable, because

\[
\exp(-O(R))=Q^{-o(1)}.
\]

Even the weaker bound

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge \exp(-O(R\log R))
\]

is acceptable, since

\[
\exp(-O(R\log R))=Q^{-O(1)}.
\]

So the frame loss is not a blocker as long as cells are not oversampled much beyond the \(1/a\) scale.

---

## 5. Intra-cell errors

For \(x_n\in I_r\),

\[
e^{-itx_n}
=
e^{-it\xi_r}
\left[
1-it(x_n-\xi_r)+O(t^2|x_n-\xi_r|^2)
\right].
\]

If

\[
|t|\le a,
\qquad
|x_n-\xi_r|\le \delta\asymp a^{-1},
\]

then the zeroth-order cell sum alone gives only bounded intra-cell error, not automatically small error.

Therefore there are two theorem-ready choices.

### Choice A: small-cell refinement

Choose

\[
\delta=\frac{\kappa}{a}
\]

with \(\kappa\ll1\) fixed. Then the phase error is \(O(\kappa)\), and the zeroth cell sums suffice with a frame bound depending on \(\kappa\). This increases the number of cells by a constant factor only.

### Choice B: include first cell moments

Define

\[
B_{r,0}=\sum_{x_n\in I_r}b_n,
\]

\[
B_{r,1}=\sum_{x_n\in I_r}b_n(x_n-\xi_r).
\]

Then

\[
F(t)
=
\sum_r e^{-it\xi_r}
\left(
B_{r,0}-itB_{r,1}
\right)
+
E_2(t),
\]

with

\[
E_2(t)
=
O\!\left(
\sum_r\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
|b_n|\,t^2|x_n-\xi_r|^2
\right).
\]

This gives a sharper analytic theorem but requires a stronger arithmetic input:

\[
\sum_r\left(|B_{r,0}|^2+a^2|B_{r,1}|^2\right)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

For simplicity, I recommend **Choice A** for the main theorem: use slightly finer cells

\[
|I_r|=\kappa/R
\]

with fixed small \(\kappa\), and keep zeroth cell sums.

---

## 6. Cell mass implies local amplitude

Assume

\[
\sum_r |B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A_B}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt
=
2a\,B^*GB
\ge
2a\,Q^{-C_G}\sum_r|B_r|^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{-a}^{a}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2dt
\ge
aQ^{-A_B-C_G}.
\]

Let

\[
F(t)=F_{\rm cell}(t)+E(t).
\]

If

\[
\|E\|_{L^2[-a,a]}^2
\le
\frac12aQ^{-A_B-C_G},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}|F(t)|^2dt
\ge
\frac12aQ^{-A_B-C_G}.
}
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|
\ge
Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for a fixed \(A'\).

---

## 7. Local amplitude implies derivative lower bound

The already established analytic lemma says:

If

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A'},
\]

with

\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^C,
\]

and outer analytic control

\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\qquad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]

then

\[
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

Since the basis-normalized operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) cost at most

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'''}.
}
\]

---

## 8. Final black-box theorem

### Fixed-width multiblock cell theorem

Assume:

\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad
F(0)=0,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Partition

\[
x_n^\pm
\]

into cells of width

\[
|I_r|=\kappa/R
\]

with fixed sufficiently small \(\kappa>0\). Let \(B_r\) be the full canonical cell sum.

Assume:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A_B}.
}
\]

Assume also:

\[
\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge Q^{-C_G},
\]

and

\[
\|E\|_{L^2[-R,R]}^2
\le
\frac12RQ^{-A_B-C_G}.
\]

Then

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

With outer analytic control on

\[
|t|\le R(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]

one obtains

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-width multiblock support is the correct theorem scale.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Frame/Gram loss is safe: }Q^{-O(1)}\text{ or better.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Zeroth cell sums suffice if cells are slightly finer: }|I_r|=\kappa/R.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Alternatively, include first intra-cell moments for sharper control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining non-analytic input is actual-prime multiblock cell-sum non-cancellation.}
}
\]

Thus the final theorem-ready implication is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: linear-algebraic formulation of the fixed-width cell-flat variety. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The fixed-width multiblock cell theorem is a finite-dimensional orbit-avoidance theorem.}
}
\]

The clean formulation is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{dist}\bigl(v(m_0),\mathcal C_{\rm flat}\bigr)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where \(v(m_0)\) is the actual prime-log phase vector on the fixed-width support and \(\mathcal C_{\rm flat}\) is the kernel of the cell projection operator.

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm cell}v(m_0)\|_2^2
=
\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the precise finite-dimensional theorem needed to unlock

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

---

## 1. Coefficient vector

Use the fixed-width support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

The plus-branch coefficient vector is

\[
\boxed{
v_n^+(m_0,\alpha)
=
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\qquad n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}.
}
\]

For the folded dual branch, define

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}
\]

up to the exact completed-phase convention, and

\[
\boxed{
v_n^-(m_0,\alpha)
=
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
}
\]

The full vector is

\[
\boxed{
v(m_0,\alpha)
=
(v^+(m_0,\alpha),v^-(m_0,\alpha),v^{\rm bg}(m_0,\alpha),v^E(m_0,\alpha)).
}
\]

For the perturbative version, use only

\[
v^{\rm md}=(v^+,v^-)
\]

and keep background/error terms outside as controlled \(L^2\)-remainders.

---

## 2. Cell projection

Partition the fixed normalized interval

\[
[x_-,x_+]\subset(0,1/2)
\]

into cells

\[
I_r=[x_-+r\delta,\ x_-+(r+1)\delta),
\qquad
\delta\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Define the cell projection

\[
P_{\rm cell}:v\mapsto (B_r)_r.
\]

For the plus branch,

\[
\boxed{
B_r^+(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
v_n^+(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
}
\]

For the folded dual branch,

\[
\boxed{
B_r^-(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
v_n^-(m_0,\alpha)
=
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
}
\]

The full canonical cell sum is

\[
\boxed{
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
}
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha)=(B_r(m_0,\alpha))_r.
}
\]

The cell mass is exactly

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha)\|_2^2
=
\sum_r|B_r(m_0,\alpha)|^2.
}
\]

---

## 3. The scalar zero condition

The condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

is the scalar sum of all canonical pieces. In cell language, this is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r B_r(m_0,\alpha)=0
}
\]

up to truncation and canonical error conventions.

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\langle P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf 1\rangle=0.
}
\]

This is important: \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) imposes only one scalar constraint on the cell vector. It does **not** imply

\[
B_r(m_0,\alpha)=0
\qquad\forall r.
\]

The desired theorem says that, for the actual prime-log orbit, this scalar cancellation cannot upgrade into simultaneous cellwise cancellation.

---

## 4. Cell-flat variety

Define the cell-flat variety by

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
=
\ker P_{\rm cell}
=
\{v:P_{\rm cell}v=0\}.
}
\]

Thus

\[
v\in\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
\]

means

\[
B_r=0
\qquad\forall r.
\]

The distance to this variety is

\[
\operatorname{dist}(v,\mathcal C_{\rm flat})
=
\|P_{\rm cell}v\|_{\mathcal H_{\rm cell}},
\]

where the norm depends on the chosen coefficient Hilbert structure. With the standard Euclidean cell norm,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(v,\mathcal C_{\rm flat})^2
=
\sum_r|B_r|^2.
}
\]

A weighted version is also possible:

\[
\|P_{\rm cell}v\|_{w}^{2}
=
\sum_r w_r^{-1}|B_r|^2,
\]

where

\[
w_r=\sum_{x_n\in I_r}|z_n|^2
\]

normalizes for unequal cell mass. For the first theorem, the unweighted version is cleaner; for numerical conditioning and large-sieve analogues, the weighted version may be better.

---

## 5. Avoidance theorem

The exact theorem needed is:

### Fixed-width cell-flat avoidance theorem

Let

\[
m_0
\]

be an admissible ordinary center satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
v(m_0,\alpha)
\]

be the canonical fixed-width packet-frequency coefficient vector on

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let

\[
P_{\rm cell}
\]

be the cell projection at scale

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Then there exists \(A>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}\bigl(v(m_0,\alpha),\mathcal C_{\rm flat}\bigr)
=
\|P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha)\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r(m_0,\alpha)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

With the scalar zero condition included:

\[
\boxed{
\langle P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf 1\rangle=0
\quad\not\Rightarrow\quad
P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha)\approx0.
}
\]

The theorem says the actual orbit avoids

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
\cap
\{\langle P_{\rm cell}v,\mathbf 1\rangle=0\}
\]

at polynomial scale.

---

## 6. Main branch, dual branch, and perturbations

### Main-only theorem

A simplified theorem is

\[
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is not enough for the canonical \(Z_\alpha\), because \(Z_\alpha\) involves main+dual cancellation.

### Main+dual theorem

The right intermediate theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This accounts for folded dual cellwise cancellation.

### Full canonical theorem

The full theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-+B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If \(B_r^{\rm bg}\) and \(B_r^E\) are perturbative in the \(L^2[-R,R]\) sense, use the main+dual theorem plus an error lemma. If they are not perturbative, include them directly in the cell vector.

---

## 7. Relation to \(|\mathbf z'|\)

The already-settled analytic chain is:

\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

implies

\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|^2\,dt\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

by the cell-frame lower bound. Hence

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

The polylog-local amplitude-to-derivative theorem then gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'''}.
}
\]

Therefore, the fixed-width cell-flat avoidance theorem is exactly the missing arithmetic input for the first Wronskian factor.

---

## 8. Why this is narrower than full Wronskian incidence

The cell theorem concerns degree-one packet-frequency sums:

\[
B_r
=
\sum_{n\in I_r}
z_n e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\cdots.
\]

The later cofactor vector \(\mathbf M\) involves subset-product frequencies of degree \(R+1\):

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad |S|=R+1.
\]

Thus the cell theorem is structurally simpler. It asks actual prime-log phases to avoid a linear cell-flat variety, rather than a high-degree determinant incidence variety.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell-flat avoidance is the right first arithmetic target.}
}
\]

---

## Final theorem package

### Definition

\[
v(m_0,\alpha)=
\bigl(z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n},\ e^{i\Theta_Z}z_n^-e^{+im_0\log n},\ldots\bigr)
\]

on

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q.
\]

\[
P_{\rm cell}v=(B_r)_r.
\]

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}=\ker P_{\rm cell}.
\]

### Target theorem

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}(v(m_0,\alpha),\mathcal C_{\rm flat})
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

### Equivalent cell form

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r|B_r(m_0,\alpha)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

### Consequence

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell-flat avoidance}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is the finite-dimensional avoidance theorem now needed from Agent 2 / arithmetic lanes.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:54:19)

_Thought for a couple of seconds_

Agent 1 / A report: same-branch cell mass theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-branch cell mass is the right first arithmetic subtheorem, but it is not provable from diagonal mass alone.}
}
\]

The desired theorem is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The diagonal cell mass is large, but same-cell off-diagonal terms can in principle cancel it. Therefore the needed input is a **fixed-\(m_0\), same-cell off-diagonal nonrecurrence theorem** for the actual prime-log phases

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

The scalar condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

only imposes one global linear cancellation:

\[
\sum_r\bigl(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-+\cdots\bigr)=0.
\]

It should not force both branch cell vectors to be small. But proving that requires actual-orbit arithmetic, not local linear algebra.

---

# 1. One-branch cell mass expansion

For the plus branch, define

\[
B_r^+(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
|B^+|_2^2
=
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2.
\]

Expanding:

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n,n'\\x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
}
\]

Separate diagonal and off-diagonal terms:

\[
|B^+|_2^2
=
D^+
+
O^+,
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
D^+
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}^+}|z_n^+|^2
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
O^+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
}
\]

The corresponding folded dual branch is

\[
B_r^-(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n},
\]

with

\[
|B^-|_2^2
=
D^-+O^-,
\]

where

\[
D^-=\sum_n |z_n^-|^2,
\]

and

\[
O^-
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^-,x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^-\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{+im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

Thus the same-branch theorem reduces to controlling

\[
O^+ + O^-.
\]

A sufficient condition is

\[
\boxed{
O^+ + O^- \ge -\left(1-Q^{-A}\right)(D^+ + D^-).
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}(D^+ + D^-).
}
\]

After normalization of branch mass, this gives the desired polynomial lower bound.

---

# 2. Size of the diagonal

On the fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]

the main AFE coefficients have size roughly

\[
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)
\asymp
n^{-1/2-\alpha}V_Z^+(n/N_Z).
\]

Inside the plateau,

\[
V_Z^+\asymp1.
\]

For primes \(p\), this gives

\[
|z_p^+|^2\asymp p^{-1-2\alpha}.
\]

Summing over primes in a log interval gives

\[
\sum_{p:e^{u}\le p\le e^{u+du}} |z_p^+|^2
\asymp
\frac{e^u}{u}\cdot e^{-u(1+2\alpha)}du
=
\frac{e^{-2\alpha u}}{u}du.
\]

For \(\alpha\) bounded at the relevant scale, over \(u\in[c_-Q,c_+Q]\),

\[
D^+
\asymp
\int_{c_-Q}^{c_+Q}\frac{e^{-2\alpha u}}{u}\,du.
\]

In the hard \(\alpha\approx0\) regime,

\[
\boxed{
D^+\asymp 1.
}
\]

More precisely,

\[
D^+\asymp \log(c_+/c_-)
\]

up to \(Q^{o(1)}\)-type factors. Similarly,

\[
D^-\asymp1
\]

inside the folded dual plateau.

Thus the diagonal mass is not small. The only way same-branch cell mass can fail is through coherent same-cell off-diagonal cancellation.

---

# 3. The fixed-\(m_0\) off-diagonal obstruction

Same-cell pairs satisfy

\[
x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r,
\qquad
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Since

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n,
\]

this means

\[
|\log n-\log n'|
\lesssim \frac{1}{\lambda R}
\asymp \frac{Q}{R}.
\]

Thus each cell contains many \(n\)’s. Same-cell off-diagonal phases are

\[
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

A purely diagonal estimate would require these phases to cancel on average. But at a fixed \(m_0\), this is exactly a prime-log nonrecurrence statement.

The needed same-cell estimate can be stated as:

### Same-cell off-diagonal theorem

For every admissible ordinary \(m_0\) with \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})\sum_n |z_n|^2.
}
\]

This is the analytic/arithmetic interface.

---

# 4. Effect of the zero condition

The zero condition is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

In cell language,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\left(
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E
\right)
=0.
}
\]

Ignoring small background/error terms, this is one complex scalar condition:

\[
\sum_r(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-)=0.
\]

It does **not** imply

\[
B_r^+\approx0
\quad\forall r,
\]

nor

\[
B_r^-\approx0
\quad\forall r.
\]

A linear algebra model makes this clear. Let

\[
C_r=B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_r C_r=0
\]

allows large nonzero cell vectors \(C=(C_r)\). It only kills the projection onto the constant vector.

Therefore the desired theorem is natural:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r C_r=0
\quad\text{should not force}\quad
B^+\approx0,\ B^-\approx0.
}
\]

However, in a phase-relaxed model one can choose the phases inside each cell so that

\[
B_r^+=0,\qquad B_r^-=0
\]

for every \(r\), and then the zero condition is automatically satisfied. Thus the proof must use the actual one-parameter phases

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

---

# 5. Same-branch theorem candidate

A clean theorem is:

### Same-branch cell mass theorem

Let

\[
m_0
\]

be an admissible ordinary zero of \(Z_\alpha\). Let \(B^\pm(m_0)\) be the plus and folded-dual cell vectors on fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

A sufficient off-diagonal form is:

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^+ + D^-).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
D^+ + D^- + O^+ + O^-\ge Q^{-A}(D^+ + D^-).
}
\]

Since

\[
D^+ + D^-\asymp Q^{O(1)}
\]

after normalization, this gives the needed polynomial lower bound.

---

# 6. Probabilistic heuristic

If the cell sums behaved like independent complex Gaussian variables, then conditioning on the scalar zero

\[
\sum_r(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-)=0
\]

would remove only one complex degree of freedom. For

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

cells, the expected squared norm after conditioning would be

\[
\mathbb E\left[
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2
\mid
\sum_r(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-)=0
\right]
\asymp
\mathbb E\left[
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2
\right].
\]

So probabilistically, the theorem is highly plausible. The condition \(Z_\alpha=0\) should not collapse an \(R\)-dimensional cell vector.

A deterministic analogue would be:

### Conditional cell-energy large sieve

Let \(B(m)\) be the actual cell vector and \(L(B)=\sum_rB_r\). Then for all admissible \(m\),

\[
L(B(m))=0
\Longrightarrow
\|B(m)\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently, the actual orbit avoids the codimension-\(M_{\rm cell}\) cell-flat subspace inside the codimension-one scalar-zero hyperplane.

---

# 7. Why recurrence heuristics alone do not prove it

Cell-flatness imposes roughly

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

complex constraints. With tolerance \(Q^{-A}\), generic recurrence cost is roughly

\[
Q^{2A R}
=
\exp\left(
O_A\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is far more expensive than hitting the scalar zero condition alone, but still not an unconditional proof of avoidance over arbitrary large height ranges.

Thus the theorem is plausible but still requires an actual-orbit nonrecurrence principle.

---

# 8. Final reduction

The same-branch result is not yet the full canonical cell theorem, because even if

\[
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

one could still have cellwise main-dual cancellation:

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

So the cell theorem should be split into two inputs:

### Input 1: Same-branch mass

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

### Input 2: Main-dual nonalignment

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2).
}
\]

Together they imply

\[
\boxed{
|B|_2^2\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-branch diagonal mass: strong.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Obstruction: fixed-}m_0\text{ same-cell off-diagonal cancellation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\text{ gives only one scalar cancellation, not cellwise cancellation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed models can kill all cells, so actual one-parameter arithmetic is essential.}
}
\]

The same-branch cell mass theorem is therefore reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed-}m_0\text{ same-cell off-diagonal prime-log nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

This is the precise theorem Agent 2 / arithmetic lanes should now attack.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:57:54)

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: same-branch off-diagonal theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-branch mass reduces to fixed-}m_0\text{ same-cell off-diagonal nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

The desired theorem is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The diagonal terms are robust. The only obstruction is near-total cancellation by same-cell off-diagonal phases:

\[
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

The scalar zero condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

does not algebraically force this. In phase-relaxed models one can force it, so the missing proof input is actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.

---

## 1. Plus-branch expansion

For cells \(I_r\), define

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
|B^+|_2^2
=
\sum_r|B_r^+|^2.
\]

Expanding,

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2
=
D^+ + O^+,
}
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
D^+=
\sum_n |z_n^+|^2
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
O^+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
}
\]

Thus plus-branch collapse means

\[
O^+\approx -D^+.
\]

---

## 2. Minus-branch expansion

For the folded dual branch,

\[
B_r^-=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^- e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|B^-|_2^2
=
D^-+O^-,
}
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
D^-=
\sum_n |z_n^-|^2
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
O^-=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^-,x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^-\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{+im_0\log(n/n')}.
}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2
=
D^++D^-+O^++O^-.
}
\]

A sufficient theorem is

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}(D^++D^-).
}
\]

Since \(D^++D^-\) is polynomially non-small after canonical normalization, this gives the desired branch-mass lower bound.

---

## 3. Diagonal size

On fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]

the plus coefficients satisfy approximately

\[
z_n^+\sim n^{-1/2-\alpha}V_Z^+(n/N_Z).
\]

Inside the plateau,

\[
V_Z^+\asymp1.
\]

For primes \(p=e^u\),

\[
|z_p^+|^2\asymp e^{-(1+2\alpha)u}.
\]

Accounting for prime density \(e^u/u\), the diagonal plus mass is

\[
D^+
\asymp
\int_{c_-Q}^{c_+Q}
\frac{e^{-2\alpha u}}{u}\,du.
\]

In the hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

this is

\[
\boxed{
D^+\asymp 1
}
\]

up to fixed constants and \(Q^{o(1)}\) factors.

Similarly,

\[
\boxed{
D^-\asymp1
}
\]

inside the folded dual plateau.

Thus the diagonal is not the weak point.

---

## 4. Strongest off-diagonal cancellation scenario

The dangerous case is cellwise coherent phase alignment:

\[
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\approx
-\frac{z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}}{|z_n^+z_{n'}^+|}
\]

for enough same-cell pairs to make

\[
O^+\approx -D^+.
\]

Equivalently, within each cell,

\[
B_r^+=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\]

is small despite the large coefficient energy

\[
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}|z_n^+|^2.
\]

The same applies to the minus branch.

In phase-relaxed models, this can be arranged by choosing phases inside each cell so that

\[
B_r^+=0,\qquad B_r^-=0
\]

for all \(r\). Therefore no local geometry or linear algebra theorem can prove the desired statement. The actual phases

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}
\]

must be used.

---

## 5. Can \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) force off-diagonal collapse?

The zero condition is only

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

In cell variables, ignoring perturbative terms,

\[
\sum_r
\left(
B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\right)
=0.
\]

This is one complex scalar condition. It can force total cancellation:

\[
\sum_r C_r=0,\qquad C_r=B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-.
\]

But it does not algebraically imply

\[
B_r^+\approx0,\quad B_r^-\approx0
\quad\forall r.
\]

So the implication

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2\ll Q^{-A}
\]

would mean the actual one-parameter orbit lands in a much smaller cell-flat variety than demanded by the scalar zero itself.

That is an arithmetic nonrecurrence phenomenon.

---

## 6. Same-branch theorem candidate

A clean theorem is:

### Same-branch cell mass theorem

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible ordinary zero of \(Z_\alpha\), and let \(B^\pm\) be the fixed-width plus and folded-dual cell vectors. Then

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

A sufficient off-diagonal form is:

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-).
}
\]

This can be treated as a fixed-\(m_0\) same-cell large-sieve lower bound.

---

## 7. Exact nonrecurrence input needed

The reduced theorem is:

### Same-cell off-diagonal nonrecurrence

For actual admissible \(m_0\) satisfying \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n\overline{z_{n'}}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\right|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})
\sum_n |z_n|^2.
}
\]

Or, branchwise,

\[
\boxed{
|B^\pm(m_0)|_2^2
\ge Q^{-A}D^\pm.
}
\]

This is weaker than full pointwise random-phase behavior. It only asks that same-cell phases not cancel the entire diagonal energy at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

---

## 8. Recurrence estimate

Cell-flatness imposes approximately

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

complex conditions. With tolerance

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

the generic phase-orbit recurrence cost is roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-2R}=Q^{2AR}
=
\exp\!\left(
O_A\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

Conditioning on \(Z_\alpha=0\) removes only one complex condition, leaving roughly

\[
R-1
\]

complex conditions.

This is much more restrictive than the scalar zero condition alone, and more restrictive than the codimension-four Wronskian-small event. Hence the same-branch cell theorem is plausibly easier than the final incidence theorem but still not accessible by recurrence heuristics alone.

---

## 9. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Diagonal mass: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scalar zero condition: only one complex constraint.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cell-flatness: }R\text{ complex constraints.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Missing theorem: actual one-parameter same-cell off-diagonal nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

Thus the same-branch cell mass theorem is precisely:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
D^++D^-+O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the next arithmetic theorem to prove before addressing main/dual cell-vector nonalignment.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:02:21)

_Thought for a few seconds_

Agent 1 / A report: same-branch off-diagonal control, plus branch. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The plus-branch cell mass theorem reduces to a fixed-height same-cell off-diagonal nonrecurrence estimate.}
}
\]

The diagonal term

\[
D^+=\sum_n |z_n^+|^2
\]

is polynomially non-small on fixed-width support. The only way

\[
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2
\]

can be small is if, cell by cell, the actual phases

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}
\]

create destructive interference strong enough to cancel essentially all diagonal mass.

The scalar zero condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

does not by itself force this. It controls only the total cell sum, not every cell.

Thus the precise missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})
\sum_n|z_n^+|^2.
}
\]

This is a same-cell prime-log nonrecurrence theorem at fixed \(m_0\).

---

## 1. Plus-branch cell expansion

Define

\[
B_r^+(m_0)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
|B^+|_2^2
=
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2.
\]

Expanding gives

\[
\boxed{
|B^+|_2^2
=
D^+ + O^+,
}
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
D^+
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}}|z_n^+|^2
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
O^+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
}
\]

So the target lower bound

\[
|B^+|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is equivalent to showing

\[
D^+ + O^+\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

After normalizing the branch so that \(D^+\asymp 1\), this becomes

\[
\boxed{
O^+\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]

---

## 2. Diagonal size on fixed-width support

Use

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

On the main AFE plateau,

\[
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)
\sim
n^{-1/2-\alpha}V_Z^+(n/N_Z),
\qquad
V_Z^+\asymp1.
\]

Restricting to primes \(p=e^u\),

\[
|z_p^+|^2
\asymp e^{-(1+2\alpha)u}.
\]

Using prime density

\[
d\pi(e^u)\sim \frac{e^u}{u}\,du,
\]

the diagonal mass is

\[
D^+
\asymp
\int_{c_-Q}^{c_+Q}
\frac{e^{-2\alpha u}}{u}\,du.
\]

In the hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
D^+\asymp \int_{c_-Q}^{c_+Q}\frac{du}{u}
=
\log(c_+/c_-)
\asymp1.
}
\]

For moderate \(\alpha\), \(D^+\) may tilt toward one end of the support, but it remains polynomially controlled after the natural row normalization. Thus the diagonal term is not the source of weakness.

---

## 3. Strongest off-diagonal cancellation scenario

The dangerous scenario is

\[
B_r^+\approx0
\qquad\text{for every cell }r.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx0
\qquad\forall r.
\]

In expanded form, this means each same-cell off-diagonal component nearly cancels its diagonal:

\[
O_r^+
=
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\approx
-D_r^+,
\]

where

\[
D_r^+=\sum_{x_n\in I_r}|z_n^+|^2.
\]

Summing over \(r\),

\[
O^+\approx-D^+.
\]

This is possible in a phase-relaxed model: inside each cell, one may choose phases so that the weighted vector polygon closes. Hence the actual theorem must use the one-parameter structure

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

---

## 4. Does \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) constrain \(O^+\)?

Only weakly.

The scalar zero condition is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Ignoring background and error terms, in cell variables this says

\[
\sum_r
\left(
B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\right)
=0.
\]

This is one complex scalar constraint on the full cell vector. It does not imply

\[
B_r^+\approx0\quad\forall r.
\]

Nor does it directly imply

\[
O^+\approx-D^+.
\]

Thus the zero condition alone cannot explain plus-branch collapse. A collapse of \(B^+\) would be a much stronger event: roughly \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\) complex constraints rather than one.

So the correct theorem is not “\(Z_\alpha=0\) prevents diagonal cancellation by linear algebra,” but:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual prime-log orbit cannot satisfy all same-cell cancellations at an admissible }Z_\alpha\text{-zero.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Fixed-\(m_0\) large-sieve form

A suitable theorem is:

### Plus-branch same-cell large-sieve theorem

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible ordinary \(Z_\alpha\)-zero. Then

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_n |z_n^+|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]

This is “large-sieve-like” only in structure. It is not the usual averaged large sieve; it is a pointwise lower bound at the specific height \(m_0\), conditioned on

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

A weaker averaged form over \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros could support it, but it would not immediately imply this pointwise statement.

---

## 6. Prime-log nonrecurrence formulation

The same theorem can be stated as an orbit-avoidance condition.

Let

\[
\Phi^+(m)
=
\left(
B_r^+(m)
\right)_r
=
P_{\rm cell}^+
\left(
z_n^+e^{-im\log n}
\right)_n.
\]

Then the plus-branch theorem is

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|\Phi^+(m_0)\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The bad set is

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}^+
=
\{m:\Phi^+(m)\approx0\}.
\]

It has roughly

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

complex conditions. A generic recurrence cost to a \(Q^{-A}\)-tube is

\[
Q^{2AR}
=
\exp\!\left(
O_A\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is much more restrictive than \(Z_\alpha(m)\approx0\), but recurrence heuristics alone do not prove avoidance.

---

## 7. The precise theorem still needed

The plus branch alone requires:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n})_n,
\ker P_{\rm cell}^+
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r^+(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is a fixed-height same-cell off-diagonal nonrecurrence theorem for actual prime-log phases.

For the same-branch mass input, the final form is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The plus-branch theorem above is one half; the dual branch requires the analogous statement with phases

\[
e^{+im_0\log n}
\]

and folded nodes

\[
x_n^-.
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
D^+\text{ is robust and polynomially non-small.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
O^+\text{ is the only obstruction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\text{ imposes only total cancellation, not cellwise plus-branch cancellation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed models can kill every cell, so actual prime-log arithmetic is essential.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s reduced target is:

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+
}
\]

or, more invariantly,

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm cell}^+(z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n})\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the plus-branch same-cell off-diagonal theorem now needed.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:10:48)

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: plus-branch off-diagonal nonrecurrence. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The plus-branch theorem is reduced to a same-cell ratio-phase nonrecurrence statement.}
}
\]

The diagonal mass

\[
D^+=\sum_n |z_n^+|^2
\]

is polynomially non-small after the intended normalization. Collapse of

\[
|B^+|_2^2
\]

is equivalent to simultaneous near-vanishing of every plus-cell sum

\[
B_r^+\approx0.
\]

That can happen in a phase-relaxed model, so the missing input must use the actual one-parameter orbit

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

A theorem sufficient for the plus branch is:

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}D^+.
}
\]

This is the weakest useful plus-branch actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

---

## 1. Diagonal lower bound

On the fixed-width plateau

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]

the plus AFE coefficient is, schematically,

\[
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)
=
n^{-1/2-\alpha}V_Z^+(n/N_Z)\cdot \mathfrak g_Z^+,
\]

where \(V_Z^+\asymp1\) in the plateau and \(\mathfrak g_Z^+\) is \(n\)-independent.

Restricting to primes \(p=e^u\),

\[
|z_p^+|^2
\asymp
e^{-(1+2\alpha)u}.
\]

Using prime density \(e^u/u\), the branch diagonal is

\[
D^+
\asymp
\int_{c_-Q}^{c_+Q}
\frac{e^{-2\alpha u}}{u}\,du.
\]

In the hard symmetric branch

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

this is

\[
D^+
\asymp
\int_{c_-Q}^{c_+Q}\frac{du}{u}
=
\log(c_+/c_-)
\asymp1.
\]

For tilted \(\alpha\), the same expression is still polynomially controlled once the branch is normalized. Thus

\[
\boxed{
D^+\ge Q^{-A_D}
}
\]

for some fixed \(A_D\), and usually \(D^+\asymp1\) in normalized units.

---

## 2. Collapse is exactly cellwise cancellation

By definition,

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Thus

\[
|B^+|_2^2
=
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2
=
D^+ + O^+,
\]

where

\[
O^+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
|B^+|_2^2\ll Q^{-A}D^+
\]

if and only if

\[
O^+\le -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
B_r^+\approx0
\qquad \forall r.
\]

So the exact collapse mechanism is simultaneous cellwise cancellation.

---

## 3. Same-cell ratios and arithmetic spread

Same-cell means

\[
x_n,x_{n'}\in I_r,
\qquad |I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Since

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

same-cell pairs satisfy

\[
|\log n-\log n'|
\lesssim
\frac{1}{\lambda R}
\asymp
\frac{Q}{R}.
\]

On fixed-width support, each cell contains many integers/primes. The ratio phases are

\[
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

The frequencies

\[
\log(n/n')
\]

inside one cell range over an interval of length \(\asymp Q/R\), but they can also be extremely close for nearby primes. Thus standard spacing alone does not yield a pointwise large-sieve lower bound at a fixed \(m_0\).

The arithmetic spread is substantial globally, but a proof must rule out coherent alignment at the particular admissible height \(m_0\).

---

## 4. Why \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) does not imply plus collapse

The scalar zero condition is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

In cell notation, ignoring perturbative pieces,

\[
\sum_r
\left(
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\right)
=0.
\]

This is one complex relation. It constrains the projection of the full cell vector onto the constant vector. It does **not** constrain the orthogonal components of \(B^+\), nor does it force

\[
B_r^+=0
\]

for each \(r\).

Thus a plus-branch collapse would be an additional \(M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\) complex constraints beyond the scalar zero. It is not a consequence of \(Z_\alpha=0\).

---

## 5. Attempted pointwise large-sieve theorem

A natural theorem would be:

### Plus same-cell large-sieve theorem

For every admissible ordinary zero \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_n|z_n^+|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]

This is not a standard large sieve because there is no averaging over \(m\). It is a **pointwise** lower bound on a structured one-parameter exponential packet.

A conventional large-sieve method would prove an average over \(m\), or possibly over zeros \(m_j\). To get the pointwise statement at a prescribed admissible \(m_0\), one needs an actual-orbit nonrecurrence principle.

---

## 6. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a relaxed model, assign arbitrary phases

\[
u_n\in S^1.
\]

Inside each cell \(I_r\), if the coefficient magnitudes satisfy the polygon condition

\[
\max_{n\in I_r}|z_n^+|
\le
\sum_{n'\in I_r,n'\ne n}|z_{n'}^+|,
\]

then one can choose phases so that

\[
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}z_n^+u_n=0.
\]

Because each fixed-width cell contains many terms, this polygon condition is overwhelmingly satisfied. Therefore

\[
B_r^+=0
\qquad \forall r
\]

is possible in the phase-relaxed model.

This shows the plus-branch theorem cannot be proved from coefficient magnitudes, cell structure, or diagonal dominance alone.

---

## 7. Actual-orbit nonrecurrence formulation

The weakest useful statement is:

### Plus cell-flat avoidance theorem

Let

\[
\Phi^+(m)
=
P_{\rm cell}^+
\left(
z_n^+e^{-im\log n}
\right)_n
=
(B_r^+(m))_r.
\]

Then for admissible ordinary \(m_0\),

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|\Phi^+(m_0)\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n})_n,
\ker P_{\rm cell}^+
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the exact plus-branch actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

A slightly weaker version sufficient for the combined same-branch theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\|\Phi^+(m_0)\|_2^2+\|\Phi^-(m_0)\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

That permits plus collapse if the dual branch stays large.

---

## 8. Recurrence-cost heuristic

The bad event

\[
B_r^+(m)\approx0
\qquad \forall r
\]

has roughly

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

complex constraints. For tolerance

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

a generic recurrence cost is

\[
\varepsilon^{-2R}=Q^{2AR}
=
\exp\!\left(
O_A\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

Conditioning on

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\]

removes at most one complex constraint. The event remains high codimension.

This strongly supports the theorem heuristically, and explains why the multiblock numerics were clean. But it is not a proof, because global recurrence over large height ranges may still be too cheap absent an actual arithmetic obstruction.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{D}^+\text{ lower bound: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Collapse } |B^+|_2\ll1 \iff O^+\approx-D^+\iff B_r^+\approx0\ \forall r.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha=0\text{ gives only total cancellation, not plus-cell cancellation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed models break the theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Needed input: plus cell-flat avoidance for the actual prime-log orbit.}
}
\]

The precise theorem Agent 1 hands off is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Or in off-diagonal form:

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]
