## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:19:40)

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: plus-branch proof attempt beyond formulation. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No unconditional proof found. The plus branch should now be packaged as a named actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

The theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}D^+.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]

This is not a consequence of diagonal mass, cell geometry, or the scalar condition \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\). It requires actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.

---

## 1. Cell equations as exponential-polynomial constraints

For each cell \(I_r\), define

\[
B_r^+(m)
=
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+ e^{-im\log n}.
\]

The plus-branch collapse event is

\[
B_r^+(m_0)\approx0
\qquad
\forall r.
\]

This is a system of approximately

\[
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R
\]

complex exponential-polynomial equations in the single real parameter \(m\):

\[
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+ e^{-im\log n}
\approx0,
\qquad r=1,\ldots,M_{\rm cell}.
\]

The scalar zero condition is instead only

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

or cellwise,

\[
\sum_r(B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-+\cdots)=0.
\]

So plus-cell collapse is far stronger than the defining zero condition.

---

## 2. Deterministic polygon closure does not apply to the actual orbit

Inside each cell, a phase-relaxed model can force

\[
B_r^+=0
\]

by choosing independent phases. Since each cell contains many terms, the polygon condition is generically satisfied:

\[
\max_{x_n\in I_r}|z_n^+|
\le
\sum_{x_{n'}\in I_r,\ n'\ne n}|z_{n'}^+|.
\]

But the actual phases are not free. They are

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

Thus cellwise cancellation requires the single parameter \(m_0\) to solve all the cell equations simultaneously. The phase-relaxed construction therefore does not threaten the actual theorem except as evidence that true arithmetic is needed.

---

## 3. Prime spacing alone is insufficient

Same-cell pairs satisfy

\[
|\lambda(\log n-\log n')|\lesssim R^{-1},
\]

so

\[
|\log n-\log n'|\lesssim Q/R.
\]

The ratios \(n/n'\) therefore range over a substantial interval, and the off-diagonal phases

\[
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}
\]

have many distinct frequencies. However, at a fixed height \(m_0\), frequency spread alone does not imply cancellation. A standard large-sieve argument would require averaging over \(m\), while the target is pointwise at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

Thus a proof cannot simply quote spacing of \(\log(n/n')\). It needs a one-parameter nonrecurrence or zero-conditioned sampling principle.

---

## 4. Best proof mechanism candidate

A viable route would be a **zero-conditioned cell large sieve** for the plus branch:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)
\sum_r |B_r^+(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}w_J(m_j)D^+.
\]

This expands through the zero-sampling kernel

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

The required estimate is that the matrix

\[
K_J(\log n-\log n')
\]

is diagonally dominant, or at least has a lower frame bound, when restricted to same-cell pairs.

However, even this averaged theorem does not directly give the required pointwise statement unless one adds a **bad-zero exclusion principle**:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2\ll Q^{-A}
\]

cannot occur as an isolated exceptional zero while the average is healthy.

So the proof mechanism becomes:

\[
\text{zero-set large sieve}
+
\text{bad-zero exclusion}
\Rightarrow
\text{pointwise plus-cell nonrecurrence}.
\]

This is plausible but not presently proved.

---

## 5. Final importable theorem

The plus branch should now be carried as a named theorem.

### Theorem: Plus-branch fixed-width cell-flat avoidance

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Partition

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

into cells

\[
I_r,\qquad |I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

Define

\[
B_r^+(m)
=
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and

\[
D^+=\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}}|z_n^+(\alpha,m)|^2.
\]

For every admissible ordinary zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\sum_r|B_r^+(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}D^+.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)\ge -(1-Q^{-A})D^+.
}
\]

In finite-dimensional form,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n})_n,
\ker P_{\rm cell}^+
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}\|z^+\|_2.
}
\]

This theorem is the exact plus-branch actual-orbit nonrecurrence input needed.

---

## 6. Relation to the full cell theorem

This theorem alone gives only

\[
|B^+|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The full canonical cell theorem still needs:

\[
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and then the main/dual nonalignment estimate

\[
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2).
\]

So the full remaining package is:

1. plus fixed-width cell-flat avoidance;
2. minus fixed-width cell-flat avoidance;
3. folded main/dual cell-vector nonalignment.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proof candidate: zero-set large sieve + bad-zero exclusion.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Direct deterministic proof from spacing alone: not available.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed countermodels exist, so actual orbit arithmetic is essential.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Best current action: name and import the plus-branch fixed-width cell-flat avoidance theorem.}
}
\]

This is the final reduced form of the plus-branch side.

_Thought for 7s_

Agent 1 / A report: final attempt on **Same-Branch Cell Nonrecurrence**. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No unconditional proof found. This should now be named as a black-box actual-orbit theorem.}
}
\]

The same-branch theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-).
}
\]

The diagonal terms \(D^\pm\) are polynomially non-small. Collapse can only occur through near-total same-cell off-diagonal cancellation. Phase-relaxed models can force that cancellation, so the theorem must use actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.

Thus the correct final form is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Same-Branch Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Exact hypotheses

Work in the ordinary regime:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use fixed-width support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Define normalized nodes

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n,
\]

and folded-dual nodes

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n},
\]

up to the completed-phase convention.

Partition the relevant fixed \(x\)-interval into cells

\[
I_r,
\qquad
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

Define branch cell vectors

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

---

## 2. Branch expansions

For the plus branch,

\[
|B^+|_2^2
=
D^+ + O^+,
\]

where

\[
D^+
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}}|z_n^+|^2,
\]

and

\[
O^+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

For the folded dual branch,

\[
|B^-|_2^2
=
D^-+O^-,
\]

where

\[
D^-=
\sum_n|z_n^-|^2,
\]

and

\[
O^-=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\x_n^-,x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^-\overline{z_{n'}^-}
e^{+im_0\log(n/n')}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|B^+|_2^2+|B^-|_2^2
=
D^++D^-+O^++O^-.
\]

Inside the AFE plateau, and after the intended normalization,

\[
\boxed{
D^++D^-\ge Q^{-A_D}.
}
\]

In the hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

one expects

\[
D^+\asymp1,
\qquad
D^-\asymp1.
\]

So the only possible failure is

\[
O^++O^-\approx-(D^++D^-).
\]

---

## 3. Final proof attempt

A direct proof would need a pointwise same-cell large-sieve estimate:

\[
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
\right|^2
+
\sum_r
\left|
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-e^{+im_0\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}(D^++D^-).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-).
\]

The obstruction is that usual large-sieve estimates average over \(m\), while here \(m=m_0\) is fixed and constrained by

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

The zero condition gives only

\[
\sum_r
\left(
B_r^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-+\cdots
\right)
=0.
\]

It is one complex scalar relation. It does not prohibit

\[
B_r^+\approx0,\qquad B_r^-\approx0
\qquad\forall r.
\]

To prove the theorem, one needs a genuinely arithmetic statement that the actual orbit

\[
m\mapsto(e^{-im\log n})_n
\]

does not hit the same-cell flat subspace at an admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

No purely deterministic obstruction from cell geometry, diagonal mass, or \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) closes this.

---

## 4. Why the standard ingredients are insufficient

### Diagonal mass

The diagonal is strong:

\[
D^\pm\ge Q^{-A_D}.
\]

But diagonal mass alone says nothing if the off-diagonal term can be almost \(-D^\pm\).

### Scalar zero condition

The equation

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

is equivalent to total cancellation of the full cell vector, not cellwise cancellation:

\[
\sum_r B_r=0
\not\Rightarrow
B_r=0\quad\forall r.
\]

### Cell geometry

Cells only group nearby frequencies. They do not prevent polygon closure inside each cell in a phase-relaxed model.

### Phase-relaxed countermodel

If the phases \(u_n\in S^1\) are free, then because each cell contains many terms, one can arrange

\[
\sum_{x_n^\pm\in I_r}
z_n^\pm u_n
=0
\]

for every \(r\). Thus the theorem is false without the actual phase law.

---

## 5. Named theorem

### Same-Branch Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Partition the plus and folded-dual normalized nodes into cells

\[
I_r,\qquad |I_r|\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

For every admissible ordinary zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-).
}
\]

A stronger branchwise form is:

\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}D^+,
\qquad
|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}D^-.
}
\]

The weaker combined form is enough for the cell theorem once paired with folded main/dual nonalignment.

---

## 6. Dependence on actual prime-log arithmetic

This theorem is exactly an actual-orbit avoidance statement:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n},z_n^-e^{+im_0\log n})_n,
\ker(P_{\rm cell}^+\oplus P_{\rm cell}^-)
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

It cannot be derived from the phase-relaxed model. It requires arithmetic information about the one-parameter phase curve

\[
m\mapsto(e^{-im\log n})_n
\]

at points satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0.
\]

A plausible route is:

\[
\text{zero-set large sieve}
+
\text{bad-zero exclusion}
\Rightarrow
\text{same-branch cell nonrecurrence}.
\]

But absent such an input, this theorem should be carried as a named black box.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proof candidate from local algebra: failed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Diagonal mass: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scalar zero condition: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed model: false.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final status: named actual-orbit arithmetic input.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s final output is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Same-Branch Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence}
}
\]

as the exact same-branch input required for the full Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence Theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:41:49)

_Thought for 6s_

Agent 1 / A report: zero-set sampling kernel for \(\mathbf M\). Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }\mathbf M\text{ zero-set large sieve reduces to a new zero-correlation theorem for }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros.}
}
\]

The required kernel is

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

For the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve, we need operator control of

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
|S|=R+1.
\]

The diagonal term is

\[
K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
\]

The obstruction is the off-diagonal operator

\[
\sum_{S\ne T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T).
\]

A usable theorem would say this off-diagonal operator is at most a fixed fraction of the diagonal. I do **not** see a way to prove that from standard argument-principle manipulations alone. It requires actual control of exponential sums over \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

---

## 1. Desired kernel estimate

The zero-set large sieve for \(\mathbf M\) expands as

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
=
\sum_{S,T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
+\text{dual/background/error}.
\]

The desired theorem is an operator inequality:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{S,T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\ge
Q^{-A}
K_J(0)
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
}
\]

A sufficient kernel condition is

\[
\boxed{
|K_J(\xi)|\le \eta(\xi)K_J(0),
\qquad
\xi\ne0,
}
\]

with the induced off-diagonal matrix norm satisfying

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\right)_{S\ne T}
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
(1-Q^{-A})K_J(0).
}
\]

This is the exact zero-set spectral large-sieve input needed.

---

## 2. Argument-principle representation

Let \(\Omega\) be a rectangle enclosing the real interval \(J\), with boundary avoiding zeros of \(Z_\alpha\). Let \(w_J(s)\) be an analytic or almost-analytic continuation of the sampling weight. Then formally

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds.
}
\]

This is valid when:

1. \(Z_\alpha\) has no zeros on \(\partial\Omega\);
2. zeros inside the contour are counted with multiplicity;
3. \(w_J\) is analytic in the contour or replaced by a controlled analytic approximation;
4. horizontal and vertical boundary integrals are controlled.

This representation is useful, but it does not by itself give the required decay. It transfers the problem to bounding

\[
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}
\]

on zero-avoiding contours.

---

## 3. Contour requirements

To make the argument-principle route quantitative, one needs:

### Boundary zero avoidance

The contour must avoid zeros by at least a distance

\[
\delta_{\partial}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or one must use Cartan-type exceptional arcs. Without this,

\[
Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha
\]

can blow up.

### Lower bounds for \(Z_\alpha\) on the boundary

Need something like

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(s)|\ge Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega
}
\]

outside controlled exceptional sets.

This is the same kind of local amplitude / Cartan input that appeared in the \(|\mathbf z'|\) problem.

### Upper bounds for \(Z_\alpha\) and \(Z_\alpha'\)

Need

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(s)|+|Z_\alpha'(s)|\le Q^A
}
\]

or at worst \(e^{Q^{o(1)}}\), depending on contour height and width.

### Control of \(Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha\)

Need

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\partial\Omega}
\left|
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}(s)
\right|
\,|ds|
\le Q^A N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
}
\]

or a sharper oscillatory version after multiplying by \(e^{-is\xi}\).

Without these, the argument-principle formula is too soft.

---

## 4. Expected regimes for \(\xi\)

The relevant frequencies are

\[
\xi=\Omega_S-\Omega_T=\log(N_S/N_T).
\]

### Small \(\xi\)

If

\[
|\xi|\lesssim |J|^{-1},
\]

then the kernel may be as large as

\[
K_J(\xi)\approx K_J(0).
\]

This is dangerous. These near-collisions must be treated by Agent 2’s subset-product resonance analysis. The large sieve cannot suppress them analytically.

### Medium \(\xi\)

If

\[
|J|^{-1}\ll |\xi|\ll Q^A,
\]

one expects oscillation over the zero set. A desired bound is

\[
\boxed{
|K_J(\xi)|
\le
K_J(0)\,(1+|J\xi|)^{-c}
+
Q^{-A}K_J(0).
}
\]

This is a genuine pair-correlation / zero-exponential-sum estimate for \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

### Large \(\xi\)

If

\[
|\xi|\gg Q^A,
\]

smoothness of \(w_J\) and integration by parts in the argument-principle integral might give decay, but only if \(Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha\) is controlled on the contour. The relevant subset-product differences may be large, but many medium-sized differences remain.

---

## 5. Kernel theorem candidate

A usable theorem would be:

### \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large-sieve kernel theorem

Let \(J\) be a height interval containing many admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros and let \(w_J\) be a smooth nonnegative weight. For all frequencies \(\xi\) arising as

\[
\xi=\Omega_S-\Omega_T,
\qquad
|S|=|T|=R+1,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)
=
\delta_{\xi=0}K_J(0)
+
\mathcal E_J(\xi),
}
\]

where the matrix

\[
\mathcal E_{S,T}
=
\mathcal E_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\]

satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal E\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
(1-Q^{-A})K_J(0).
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j}
w_J(m_j)|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
}
\]

This is the exact averaged theorem needed for the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve.

---

## 6. What the argument principle can and cannot prove

The argument principle can represent

\[
K_J(\xi)
\]

as a contour integral. It can plausibly give coarse bounds of the form

\[
|K_J(\xi)|\le Q^A
\]

or

\[
|K_J(\xi)|\le N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\]

but those are not enough.

To prove a large sieve, one needs **off-diagonal cancellation**:

\[
K_J(\xi)\ll K_J(0)
\]

for the relevant nonzero subset-product differences, in operator norm.

That is essentially a zero-correlation theorem for the zeros of \(Z_\alpha\), weighted by the subset-product frequency set.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{argument principle alone gives a representation, not a proof of decay.}
}
\]

The missing input is a genuine spectral estimate for the zero set.

---

## 7. No-go from current inputs

From current tools, I do not see a proof of

\[
|K_J(\xi)|\ll K_J(0)
\]

uniformly over relevant \(\xi\ne0\).

Known-style global zero counting gives \(K_J(0)\), but not cancellation for

\[
\sum_{m_j}e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

Cartan/Jensen controls local crowding and boundary behavior, but again does not give spectral cancellation at subset-product frequencies.

Therefore the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve currently requires a new input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a }Z_\alpha\text{-zero spectral large-sieve / zero-correlation theorem.}
}
\]

---

## 8. Final named input

### \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve

For the subset-product frequency family

\[
\mathcal \Omega
=
\{\Omega_S=\log N_S: |S|=R+1\},
\]

and admissible zero set

\[
\mathcal Z_J
=
\{m_j\in J: Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\},
\]

the sampling operator

\[
T:\ (a_S)_S
\mapsto
\left(
\sum_S a_S e^{-im_j\Omega_S}
\right)_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
\]

satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\|Ta\|_{\ell^2(\mathcal Z_J)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J)\|a\|_{\ell^2(\mathcal \Omega)}^2
}
\]

after removing exact/near subset-product collision degeneracies.

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
}
\]

defines a positive Gram matrix with lower bound

\[
\boxed{
G_{\mathcal Z,\Omega}\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

This theorem, plus exterior coefficient mass, would prove the averaged \(\mathbf M\) lower bound.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Kernel representation by argument principle: Green/formal.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Kernel decay/operator lower bound: open.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Small } \xi\text{ regime must be handled by subset-product resonance control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Medium/large } \xi\text{ requires a new zero-correlation theorem.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s final output is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }\mathbf M\text{ large sieve requires a }Z_\alpha\text{-Zero Spectral Large Sieve for subset-product frequencies.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:44:51)

_Thought for 5s_

Agent 1 / A report: \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large-sieve kernel for \(\mathbf M\). Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }\mathbf M\text{-large-sieve route requires a new }Z_\alpha\text{-zero spectral-correlation input.}
}
\]

The argument principle gives a useful representation of

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi},
\]

but it does **not** by itself give the operator bound needed for

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S,\quad |S|=R+1.
\]

The needed black-box theorem is a zero-set large sieve:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{S,T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently, the Gram matrix

\[
G_{S,T}=K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\]

must have a polynomial lower frame bound on the relevant subset-product frequency family after exact/near resonances are removed or quotiented.

---

## 1. Kernel theorem needed

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J
=
\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}.
\]

Define

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

The desired structural form is

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)=\delta_{\xi=0}K_J(0)+\mathcal E_J(\xi),
}
\]

where the off-diagonal operator

\[
\mathcal E_{S,T}
=
\mathcal E_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\]

satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal E\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
(1-Q^{-A})K_J(0).
}
\]

Then, for

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+\cdots,
\]

we get

\[
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
=
\sum_{S,T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
+\cdots
\]

and hence

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2
}
\]

after dual/background/error terms are included or controlled.

---

## 2. Argument-principle representation

For a rectangle \(\Omega\) enclosing \(J\), with boundary avoiding zeros of \(Z_\alpha\), one formally has

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds.
}
\]

This representation is valid under the usual conditions:

\[
Z_\alpha(s)\neq0
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega,
\]

zeros are counted with multiplicity, and \(w_J\) has an analytic or controlled almost-analytic extension.

This is useful because it converts zero sums into contour estimates. But it only proves an identity. The large-sieve theorem requires oscillatory decay or operator control for \(K_J(\xi)\), which is much stronger.

---

## 3. Contour requirements

A proof through the argument principle would need all of the following.

### Zero-avoiding boundary

Need a contour with

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\partial\Omega,\mathcal Z_{Z_\alpha})
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

or a Cartan-exceptional boundary construction.

### Lower bounds for \(Z_\alpha\)

Need

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(s)|\ge Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega
}
\]

outside controlled exceptional pieces. This is the same species of input as the local amplitude/zero-crowding theorem used for the parked cell theorem.

### Upper bounds

Need

\[
|Z_\alpha(s)|+|Z_\alpha'(s)|\le Q^A
\]

or similarly polynomially controlled growth on the contour.

### Logarithmic derivative control

Need

\[
\boxed{
\int_{\partial\Omega}
\left|
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}(s)
\right|\,|ds|
\le Q^A K_J(0)
}
\]

plus an oscillatory improvement after inserting \(e^{-is\xi}\).

Without these, the argument-principle representation is too weak to control the off-diagonal Gram operator.

---

## 4. Frequency regimes

The relevant frequencies are

\[
\xi=\Omega_S-\Omega_T=\log(N_S/N_T).
\]

They split into three regimes.

### Small frequencies

\[
|\xi|\lesssim |J|^{-1}.
\]

Here

\[
K_J(\xi)\approx K_J(0)
\]

is possible. These are dangerous. They must be handled by subset-product resonance control: exact collisions, near-collisions, or quotienting of degenerate frequency clusters.

### Medium frequencies

\[
|J|^{-1}\ll |\xi|\ll Q^A.
\]

This is the true zero-correlation regime. A desired estimate is something like

\[
\boxed{
|K_J(\xi)|
\le
K_J(0)(1+|J\xi|)^{-c}
+
Q^{-A}K_J(0),
}
\]

or, more realistically, an operator-norm version over the actual frequency family

\[
\{\Omega_S\}.
\]

This is not available from generic zero-counting.

### Large frequencies

\[
|\xi|\gg Q^A.
\]

Here integration by parts in the argument-principle representation may give decay, provided \(w_J\) is sufficiently smooth and \(Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha\) is controlled. This regime is probably not the main obstruction.

---

## 5. Do current cell inputs help?

The parked Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence Theorem gives

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_j,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

at admissible zeros. This helps with **local non-flatness of individual zeros**, but it does not directly give spectral cancellation of the zero set:

\[
\sum_{m_j}e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

It may help indirectly with contour construction and exclusion of extremely clustered, flat zeros, but it does not imply the needed kernel decay.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell theorem helps boundary/local zero control, not the }K_J\text{ off-diagonal operator bound.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Candidate theorem

### \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve for subset-product frequencies

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J=\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}
\]

and let

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
|S|=R+1.
\]

After removing exact collisions and grouping near-collisions at scale \(|J|^{-1}\), the sampling operator

\[
T:(a_S)_S
\mapsto
\left(
\sum_S a_S e^{-im_j\Omega_S}
\right)_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
\]

satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\|Ta\|_{\ell^2(\mathcal Z_J,w_J)}^2
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\|a\|_{\ell^2}^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\bigl(K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\bigr)_{S,T}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
}
\]

as a positive operator on the nonresonant subset-product coefficient space.

This theorem, plus exterior coefficient mass, gives the averaged \(\mathbf M\) lower bound.

---

## 7. No-go from current tools

Current tools give:

\[
K_J(0)=\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j),
\]

and the argument principle gives a representation for \(K_J(\xi)\). They do not give the needed off-diagonal cancellation:

\[
K_J(\xi)\ll K_J(0),
\qquad \xi\ne0,
\]

nor the stronger matrix lower bound over

\[
\xi=\Omega_S-\Omega_T.
\]

Thus the kernel lane is not closed by standard contour methods alone. It requires a genuinely new zero-correlation theorem for \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, specialized to the subset-product frequency family.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Argument-principle representation: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Contour implementation: Yellow; requires Cartan/lower-bound input.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Small-\(\xi\) regime: delegated to subset-product resonance control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Medium-\(\xi\) regime: main open zero-correlation problem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final named input: }Z_\alpha\text{-Zero Spectral Large Sieve for subset-product frequencies.}
}
\]

This is the kernel theorem the \(\mathbf M\)-large-sieve route needs.

_Thought for 6s_

Agent 1 / A report: kernel theorem after resonance quotienting. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quotienting resonance clusters is necessary, but it does not close the } \mathbf M\text{-large sieve.}
}
\]

After quotienting exact and near subset-product resonances, the remaining required input is still a genuine zero-correlation theorem for \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros:

\[
\boxed{
G_{\nu\mu}=K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\quad\text{must satisfy}\quad
G\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

The argument principle gives a representation of \(K_J(\xi)\), but not the required medium-frequency off-diagonal cancellation. Quotienting only removes the small-\(\xi\) obstruction. It does not prove spectral decay for

\[
|J|^{-1}\ll |\xi|\ll Q^A.
\]

So the needed named input remains:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after subset-product resonance quotienting.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Resonance clusters

Let

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad |S|=R+1.
\]

Define a near-resonance scale

\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1}
\]

or a slightly larger scale dictated by the support of the smooth weight \(w_J\).

Form clusters

\[
\mathcal C_\nu
=
\{S:|\Omega_S-\omega_\nu|\le \eta_0\},
\]

where \(\omega_\nu\) are representative frequencies.

For each cluster, define the aggregated coefficient

\[
\mathcal A_\nu
=
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im\left(\Omega_S-\omega_\nu\right)}
\]

or, for the averaged large-sieve form, simply treat the intra-cluster coefficient vector as a degenerate block.

The quotient frequency set is

\[
\Omega_{\rm quot}=\{\omega_\nu\}.
\]

---

## 2. Reduced Gram matrix

The zero-sampling kernel is

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{m_j:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

After clustering, the reduced Gram matrix is

\[
\boxed{
G_{\nu\mu}
=
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu).
}
\]

The quotient-space large sieve needs

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\nu,\mu}
\langle \mathcal A_\nu,\mathcal A_\mu\rangle
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_\nu|\mathcal A_\nu|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
G\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
}
\]

on the quotient coefficient space.

This statement deliberately separates two issues:

1. subset-product resonance geometry, handled by clustering;
2. zero-set spectral cancellation, handled by \(K_J\).

---

## 3. Kernel theorem needed after quotienting

The required theorem is:

### Quotient \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large sieve

Let \(\{\omega_\nu\}\) be a subset-product frequency set with pairwise spacing

\[
|\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu|\ge \eta_0
\qquad(\nu\ne\mu),
\]

where \(\eta_0\gtrsim |J|^{-1}\). Then

\[
\boxed{
\left(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\right)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

A sufficient but stronger condition is

\[
\boxed{
|K_J(\xi)|
\le
K_J(0)\Psi(|J\xi|)
}
\]

with

\[
\sum_{\mu\ne\nu}\Psi(|J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)|)
\le 1-Q^{-A}
\]

uniformly in \(\nu\). But an operator-norm condition is the correct target because the frequency set may not be uniformly sparse.

---

## 4. Argument-principle representation

For a zero-avoiding contour \(\partial\Omega\) around \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds.
}
\]

This requires:

\[
Z_\alpha(s)\ne0\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega,
\]

controlled analytic continuation of \(w_J\), and multiplicity accounting.

The contour method needs:

\[
|Z_\alpha(s)|\ge Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega
\]

outside Cartan-exceptional arcs, plus

\[
|Z_\alpha'(s)|\le Q^A
\]

and integral control of

\[
Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha.
\]

Even with those, the formula gives a representation, not the desired spectral decay.

---

## 5. What quotienting fixes

Quotienting handles the small-frequency obstruction:

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\lesssim |J|^{-1}.
\]

For such pairs,

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\approx K_J(0),
\]

so no kernel cancellation is possible. These must be grouped into the same cluster or treated as exact degeneracy.

After quotienting, the remaining pairs satisfy

\[
|\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu|\gtrsim |J|^{-1}.
\]

This is necessary for any large-sieve inequality.

---

## 6. What quotienting does not fix

For medium frequencies,

\[
|J|^{-1}\ll |\xi|\ll Q^A,
\]

we still need cancellation in

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

This is a spectral statistic of the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero set. Quotienting subset products says nothing about whether the zero set has cancellation at those frequencies.

Thus the open theorem remains:

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)\text{ is small enough, in operator norm, for the quotient frequency set.}
}
\]

This is a zero-correlation theorem, not a multiplicative-combinatorics theorem.

---

## 7. Candidate named input

### \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J=\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}
\]

and let \(\{\omega_\nu\}\) be the quotient subset-product frequency set after merging all clusters of diameter at most \(\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1}\). Then, for all coefficient vectors \(a=(a_\nu)\),

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)
\left|
\sum_\nu a_\nu e^{-im_j\omega_\nu}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_\nu |a_\nu|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\left(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\right)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

This theorem, combined with exterior coefficient mass, yields the averaged \(\mathbf M\) lower bound.

---

## 8. Remaining dependencies

This named theorem still depends on:

1. **Subset-product resonance control**  
   To define clusters with manageable size and ensure quotient spacing.

2. **Zero-correlation of \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros**  
   To control \(K_J(\xi)\) in the medium-frequency regime.

3. **Contour/local amplitude inputs**  
   To justify argument-principle estimates if that route is used.

4. **Canonical transfer**  
   To ensure the frequency coefficients \(\mathbf A_S\) actually come from \(\mathbf M_{\can}\), not a toy model.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Resonance quotienting: necessary and structurally clean.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Small-\(\xi\) obstruction: handled by clustering.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Medium-\(\xi\) obstruction: unresolved zero-correlation theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Argument principle: representation only, not decay.}
}
\]

Therefore Agent 1’s output is the named input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

This is the kernel theorem the \(\mathbf M\)-large-sieve route now requires.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:53:31)

_Thought for a few seconds_

Agent 1 / A report: quotient \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large sieve. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The quotient large-sieve formulation is clean, but the kernel theorem remains a new black-box zero-correlation input.}
}
\]

Resonance clustering removes the unavoidable small-frequency obstruction

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\lesssim |J|^{-1}.
\]

But after quotienting, the remaining medium-frequency estimate is still not implied by the argument principle or known local amplitude inputs. The required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
G_{\nu\mu}=K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
}
\]

on the quotient frequency space.

So Agent 1’s final named input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Resonance clusters

Let

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
|S|=R+1.
\]

Choose the near-collision scale

\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1}.
\]

Define clusters

\[
\mathcal C_\nu
=
\{S:|\Omega_S-\omega_\nu|\le \eta_0\},
\]

where \(\omega_\nu\) is a representative frequency.

Inside a cluster,

\[
e^{-im_j\Omega_S}
=
e^{-im_j\omega_\nu}
e^{-im_j(\Omega_S-\omega_\nu)}.
\]

Since \(m_j\in J\) and

\[
|\Omega_S-\omega_\nu|\lesssim |J|^{-1},
\]

the residual phase varies by \(O(1)\) across \(J\). Therefore intra-cluster modes cannot be separated by zero-set sampling over \(J\). They must be treated as a single degenerate block, or one must enlarge \(J\).

---

## 2. Quotient coefficients

For a coefficient family \(\mathbf A_S\), define the cluster coefficient at zero \(m_j\) by

\[
\mathcal A_\nu(m_j)
=
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im_j(\Omega_S-\omega_\nu)}.
\]

For an averaged norm, this yields

\[
\sum_{m_j}
w_J(m_j)
\left|
\sum_S \mathbf A_S e^{-im_j\Omega_S}
\right|^2
=
\sum_{m_j}
w_J(m_j)
\left|
\sum_\nu
\mathcal A_\nu(m_j)e^{-im_j\omega_\nu}
\right|^2.
\]

If intra-cluster variation is ignored, replace

\[
\mathcal A_\nu(m_j)
\]

by the block coefficient

\[
\mathcal A_\nu=
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}\mathbf A_S.
\]

The rigorous quotient theorem should either:

1. treat \(\mathcal A_\nu(m_j)\) as a slowly varying coefficient with controlled distortion; or  
2. define the coefficient space after quotienting by the near-collision relation, with the cluster norm

\[
\|\mathcal A_\nu\|^2
=
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}|\mathbf A_S|^2
\]

and accept that intra-cluster directions are invisible to this \(J\)-scale large sieve.

The second option is cleaner.

---

## 3. Reduced Gram matrix

After quotienting, define

\[
\boxed{
G_{\nu\mu}
=
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu).
}
\]

The desired quotient large sieve is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\nu,\mu}
\langle \mathcal A_\nu,\mathcal A_\mu\rangle
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)
\sum_\nu|\mathcal A_\nu|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
G\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

This is the exact quotient kernel theorem.

---

## 4. Argument-principle representation

The kernel has the formal representation

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds.
}
\]

This requires:

\[
Z_\alpha(s)\ne0
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega,
\]

a suitable analytic or almost-analytic extension of \(w_J\), and zero multiplicity bookkeeping.

To use it quantitatively, one needs:

\[
|Z_\alpha(s)|\ge Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega
\]

outside controlled exceptional arcs,

\[
|Z_\alpha'(s)|\le Q^A,
\]

and

\[
\int_{\partial\Omega}
\left|
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}(s)
\right||ds|
\le Q^AK_J(0).
\]

Even with these bounds, the integral formula gives representation, not the required decay.

---

## 5. What quotienting removes

For

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\lesssim |J|^{-1},
\]

one may have

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\approx K_J(0).
\]

No zero-set oscillation can distinguish such frequencies over \(J\). These must be clustered or handled as exact degeneracies.

Thus quotienting is necessary. It solves the small-\(\xi\) obstruction.

---

## 6. What quotienting does not remove

For

\[
|J|^{-1}\ll|\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu|\ll Q^A,
\]

one still needs cancellation in

\[
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
=
\sum_{m_j}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)}.
\]

This is a genuine spectral statistic of the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero set.

Current local amplitude/cell theorem inputs may help control zero clustering and contour placement, but they do not imply

\[
|K_J(\xi)|\ll K_J(0)
\]

for medium \(\xi\). Therefore the medium-frequency regime remains the core zero-correlation problem.

---

## 7. Candidate theorem

### \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J=\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}.
\]

Let \(\{\omega_\nu\}\) be the quotient subset-product frequency set obtained by clustering all

\[
\Omega_S
\]

at scale

\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1}.
\]

Assume the cluster multiplicities and coefficient norms are controlled. Then for every quotient coefficient vector \((a_\nu)\),

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)
\left|
\sum_\nu a_\nu e^{-im_j\omega_\nu}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_\nu|a_\nu|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu))_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

This is the theorem needed for the averaged \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve.

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Resonance quotienting: necessary and clean.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Small-frequency obstruction: handled only after quotienting.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Argument principle: gives representation, not decay.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Medium-frequency zero correlation: still open.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final required input: } \textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

This is the precise kernel theorem Agent 1 contributes to the \(\mathbf M\)-branch.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:11:33)

_Thought for 9s_

Agent 1 / A report: quotient \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral kernel. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Resonance quotienting gives the correct large-sieve formulation, but does not prove the kernel bound.}
}
\]

After clustering subset-product frequencies at scale

\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1},
\]

the required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\left(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\right)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

This is a genuine zero-correlation theorem for the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero set. The argument-principle formula gives a representation of \(K_J(\xi)\), but not the medium-frequency decay/operator lower bound required for the \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve.

Thus the final named input from this lane is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

---

# 1. Resonance clusters and quotient coefficients

Let

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,\qquad |S|=R+1.
\]

Choose a near-collision scale

\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1}.
\]

Define clusters

\[
\mathcal C_\nu
=
\{S:|\Omega_S-\omega_\nu|\le \eta_0\},
\]

with representative frequency \(\omega_\nu\).

The original cofactor expansion is

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_S \mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}.
\]

For \(S\in\mathcal C_\nu\),

\[
e^{-im\Omega_S}
=
e^{-im\omega_\nu}e^{-im(\Omega_S-\omega_\nu)}.
\]

Since

\[
|\Omega_S-\omega_\nu|\le |J|^{-1},
\]

the residual factor

\[
e^{-im(\Omega_S-\omega_\nu)}
\]

varies by \(O(1)\) across \(J\), so it cannot be resolved by sampling only on \(J\).

There are two possible quotient definitions.

### Frozen-cluster quotient

Define

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_\nu
=
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}\mathbf A_S.
}
\]

Then approximate

\[
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
\approx
\mathcal A_\nu e^{-im\omega_\nu}.
\]

This is clean but loses intra-cluster directions.

### Invisible-direction quotient

Define the cluster norm by

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal A_\nu\|^2
=
\sum_{S\in\mathcal C_\nu}|\mathbf A_S|^2,
}
\]

but regard all intra-cluster distinctions as unresolved at scale \(J\). Then the large sieve is stated only on the quotient coefficient space.

This is the safer theorem form: quotient all unresolved directions first, then demand a lower frame bound on separated cluster representatives.

---

# 2. Quotient-space large sieve

The quotient kernel is

\[
\boxed{
G_{\nu\mu}
=
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu).
}
\]

The desired averaged lower bound is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\nu,\mu}
\langle \mathcal A_\nu,\mathcal A_\mu\rangle
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_\nu|\mathcal A_\nu|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
G\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
}
\]

on the quotient frequency space.

This is the exact kernel theorem needed after subset-product resonance quotienting.

---

# 3. Argument-principle representation

The zero-sampling kernel is

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

For a zero-avoiding contour \(\partial\Omega\) around \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds.
}
\]

This requires:

\[
Z_\alpha(s)\neq0
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega,
\]

zeros counted with multiplicity, and an analytic or controlled almost-analytic extension of \(w_J\).

To use this quantitatively, one needs:

\[
|Z_\alpha(s)|\ge Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }\partial\Omega
\]

outside Cartan exceptional arcs,

\[
|Z_\alpha'(s)|\le Q^A,
\]

and

\[
\int_{\partial\Omega}
\left|
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}(s)
\right|\,|ds|
\le Q^AK_J(0).
\]

Even if all these hold, the formula only gives a representation. It does not prove the needed cancellation in \(K_J(\xi)\).

---

# 4. Frequency regimes

Let

\[
\xi=\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu.
\]

There are three relevant regimes.

## 4.1 Small frequencies

\[
|\xi|\lesssim |J|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
K_J(\xi)\approx K_J(0)
\]

is possible. No spectral cancellation can be expected over \(J\). These modes must be clustered before applying the large sieve.

Thus resonance quotienting is necessary.

## 4.2 Medium frequencies

\[
|J|^{-1}\ll|\xi|\ll Q^A.
\]

This is the main unresolved regime. The desired estimate is an operator bound such as

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\right)_{\nu\ne\mu}
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
(1-Q^{-A})K_J(0).
}
\]

A pointwise decay estimate of the form

\[
|K_J(\xi)|
\le
K_J(0)(1+|J\xi|)^{-c}
+
Q^{-A}K_J(0)
\]

would be sufficient only if the quotient frequency set has enough spacing/sparsity. In general, the operator-norm version is the correct theorem.

## 4.3 Large frequencies

\[
|\xi|\gg Q^A.
\]

With a very smooth \(w_J\), integration by parts in the argument-principle representation may give decay, provided \(Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha\) is controlled on \(\partial\Omega\). This regime is probably not the main obstruction.

---

# 5. Does quotienting plus local amplitude help?

The parked cell theorem gives local non-flatness:

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_j,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

at admissible zeros. This can help with:

\[
\text{zero multiplicity control},
\]

\[
\text{zero-avoiding contour construction},
\]

and possibly Cartan boundary estimates.

But it does not imply

\[
K_J(\xi)\ll K_J(0)
\]

for medium \(\xi\). Local non-flatness is not the same as global spectral cancellation of the zero set.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{current local }Z_\alpha\text{ inputs do not prove the medium-frequency kernel bound.}
}
\]

They are auxiliary contour tools, not the zero-correlation theorem itself.

---

# 6. Final theorem candidate

### \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J
=
\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}.
\]

Let

\[
\{\omega_\nu\}
\]

be the quotient subset-product frequency set formed by clustering all

\[
\Omega_S
\]

within radius

\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1}.
\]

Assume cluster multiplicities and coefficient norms are controlled by a separate subset-product resonance theorem.

Then for every quotient coefficient vector \((a_\nu)\),

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)
\left|
\sum_\nu a_\nu e^{-im_j\omega_\nu}
\right|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_\nu|a_\nu|^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\left(
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)
\right)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

This theorem, plus exterior coefficient mass and canonical transfer, proves the averaged \(\mathbf M\) lower bound.

---

# 7. What remains necessary

This theorem depends on:

1. **Subset-product resonance control**

   Needed to form clusters with manageable size and to remove unresolved small-\(\xi\) modes.

2. **Zero-set spectral cancellation**

   Needed for medium frequencies

   \[
   |J|^{-1}\ll|\xi|\ll Q^A.
   \]

3. **Contour/local amplitude control**

   Needed only if one proves \(K_J\) estimates via the argument principle.

4. **Canonical transfer**

   Needed because \(\mathbf M\) is built from

   \[
   q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
   \]

   not a toy prime-only model.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Resonance quotienting: necessary and correctly formulated.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Small-frequency obstruction: removed by quotienting.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Medium-frequency kernel decay: still open.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Argument principle: representation only; not enough by itself.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final named input: } \textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

This is the kernel theorem the \(\mathbf M\) branch now requires.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:14:21)

_Thought for 5s_

Agent 1 / A report: direct angle/incidence theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No structural proof of the final angle bound was found.}
}
\]

Assuming the parked inputs

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

the remaining theorem is genuinely an **angle/nonalignment** theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0)|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

I do not see a Hodge-dual, sign, positivity, exterior-algebra, or orientation mechanism that forces this once the two norm bounds are assumed. The bad event

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0
\]

is exactly the statement that the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative row is nearly contained in the span of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows. That is not excluded by the previous norm lower bounds.

Therefore this should be named as the third ordinary-route arithmetic input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Precise angle theorem

At

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the basis-normalized Wronskian expands as

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

Here:

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left(
(-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and \(\mathbf M\) is the cofactor/Hodge-dual vector of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block.

The desired theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'|\,|\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Combined with the parked inputs

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

this gives

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A_3}.
\]

---

## 2. Bad event as actual-orbit incidence

The bad event is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

but

\[
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\le Q^{-B}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Equivalently, if \(V(m_0)\) denotes the row span of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block, then

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)\perp V(m_0),
\]

so

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V(m_0))\approx0.
\]

Thus the final incidence theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}\bigl(\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),V(m_0)\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]

This is stronger than merely saying \(Z_\alpha\) has symbol rank against the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet system. Symbol rank is a coefficient-level or generic-row statement; this angle theorem is a pointwise actual-orbit statement at the specific zero \(m_0\).

---

## 3. Codimension heuristic

Once the norm inputs are assumed, the remaining small-angle condition is essentially one real constraint:

\[
\cos\angle(\mathbf z',\mathbf M)\approx0.
\]

In complex notation, depending on whether the relevant determinant is treated as complex or real-normalized, it may behave like one or two real constraints. In any case, it is much lower codimension than:

\[
\text{cell-flatness},
\]

or

\[
\mathbf M\text{-flatness}.
\]

Therefore recurrence heuristics alone are **not** favorable here. The angle event is comparatively cheap unless actual zeta arithmetic supplies extra rigidity.

This is why the final incidence theorem is likely harder than the norm lower bounds: it is not a large codimension avoidance statement after \(|\mathbf z'|\) and \(|\mathbf M|\) have already been secured.

---

## 4. Exterior algebra check

Let the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block define rows

\[
Q_0,Q_1,\ldots,Q_R.
\]

Let

\[
V=\operatorname{span}(Q_0,\ldots,Q_R).
\]

The cofactor vector

\[
\mathbf M
\]

is a Hodge-dual normal to \(V\). Hence

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\]

is the oriented volume of

\[
(\mathbf z',Q_0,\ldots,Q_R).
\]

The bad event

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0
\]

means

\[
\mathbf z'\in V.
\]

Exterior algebra gives this equivalence, but it does not give a lower bound. In particular:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

only say that \(\mathbf z'\) is nonzero and \(V\) is nondegenerate. They do not prevent \(\mathbf z'\) from lying almost inside \(V\).

So exterior/Hodge geometry clarifies the condition but does not close it.

---

## 5. Why previous symbol-rank results are insufficient

Earlier \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank results showed, roughly, that the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol is not polynomially generated by the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols on packet-frequency blocks.

That is a **symbolic/transversality** statement over active frequencies.

The present theorem is a **pointwise actual-orbit angle** statement:

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)
\not\approx
V(m_0).
\]

The actual phases may in principle create accidental pointwise dependence even when the symbol rows are independent. Therefore symbol rank is necessary but not sufficient.

To upgrade symbol rank to a quantitative pointwise angle lower bound, one would need a further actual-orbit determinant nonrecurrence theorem. That is essentially the Wronskian angle theorem itself.

---

## 6. Search for structural sign or positivity

I checked the usual possible structural closures:

\[
\text{positivity},
\quad
\text{Hermitian form},
\quad
\text{symplectic/skew form},
\quad
\text{orientation sign},
\quad
\text{Hodge-dual lower bound},
\quad
\text{main/dual sign asymmetry}.
\]

None gives a uniform lower bound for

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|.
\]

The determinant is an oscillatory, complex-valued actual-zeta expression. There is no evident positivity principle forcing it away from zero once the row norms are nonzero.

The tilted \(\alpha\)-regime may allow branch dominance in subpieces, but the hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1
\]

still permits plausible main/dual and subset-product cancellation. Thus no global structural sign proof is visible.

---

## 7. Final named theorem

### Wronskian Angle Nonalignment

Assume:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

and assume the parked norm inputs:

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A_3}
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0)|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),
\operatorname{span}\{q''_{\can}\text{-jet rows}\}
\bigr)
\ge
Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]

Equivalently again,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem is a pointwise actual-zeta incidence/nonrecurrence input.

---

## 8. Relation to the full ordinary route

The ordinary route now has three named arithmetic inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 1: Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence}
}
\]

giving

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 2: Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence}
}
\]

giving

\[
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 3: Wronskian Angle Nonalignment}
}
\]

giving

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Together they imply

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

which supplies the finite-jet anti-flatness input for the ordinary Gate 1 route.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Norm inputs do not imply angle input.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exterior algebra explains the bad event but does not preclude it.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Symbol-rank is necessary but not sufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No sign/positivity/Hodge mechanism found.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Final status: named input } \textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment.}
}
\]

This is the direct final incidence theorem required after the parked cell and cofactor-vector inputs.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:24:01)

_Thought for 7s_

Agent 1 / A report: direct common-small-value theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No direct proof found. The common-small-value theorem should be named as an actual-orbit input.}
}
\]

The final ordinary incidence theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, using

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle,
\]

and assuming the parked inputs

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

the missing statement is the angle bound

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

This is not implied by the two norm lower bounds. It is a separate actual-zeta incidence theorem.

---

## 1. Common-small set

Define

\[
\mathcal S_\varepsilon
=
\left\{
m:
|Z_\alpha(m)|\le\varepsilon,\ 
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\le\varepsilon
\right\}.
\]

The desired theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{Q^{-A}}=\varnothing
}
\]

on admissible ordinary packet centers, or more flexibly,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(m,\mathcal S_{0})\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

in the relevant normalized scale.

At the exact zero \(m_0\), this reduces to

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)\not\approx0.
\]

---

## 2. AFE/exponential-polynomial form

Schematically,

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
Z_\alpha^+(m)+Z_\alpha^-(m)+Z_{\alpha,B}(m)+E_Z(m),
\]

where

\[
Z_\alpha^+(m)
=
\sum_n z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and

\[
Z_\alpha^-(m)
=
e^{i\Theta_Z(m,\alpha)}
\sum_n z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n},
\]

with the usual folded-dual convention.

The Wronskian determinant is built from

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R,
\]

where

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Thus

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\]

is a finite but high-degree actual exponential-polynomial expression involving:

\[
e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
e^{+im\log n},
\qquad
B_2(m),
\qquad
\text{gamma/conductor factors},
\qquad
E_2.
\]

In expanded cofactor form at a zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

So common smallness is a coupled condition between the \(Z_\alpha\)-row and the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet cofactor system.

---

## 3. Phase-relaxed model

In a phase-relaxed model, where the phases

\[
e^{-im\log n}
\]

are replaced by independent variables

\[
u_n\in S^1,
\]

there is no obstruction to common smallness.

One can impose:

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0
\]

as one complex scalar equation, and independently impose

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0
\]

as another complex scalar equation. Since the phase-relaxed torus has many active dimensions, these constraints are underdetermined.

Even adding

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

does not prevent

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

Thus the theorem is false in relaxed models and must use the actual one-parameter orbit

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

---

## 4. Actual one-parameter orbit obstruction needed

The desired theorem is an avoidance statement:

\[
\boxed{
m\mapsto
\bigl(
Z_\alpha(m),\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\bigr)
}
\]

must avoid the bidisk

\[
\{|z|\le Q^{-A},\ |w|\le Q^{-A}\}
\]

at admissible centers.

Equivalently, the actual prime-log orbit must avoid the incidence set

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}
=
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0\}
\]

to polynomial scale.

A recurrence heuristic alone is unfavorable: after the two norm inputs are assumed, the additional small-angle condition is only low codimension. So generic one-parameter recurrence cannot prove avoidance. One needs actual zeta arithmetic: coefficient rigidity, folded main/dual coupling, explicit-formula constraints, or a zero-repulsion mechanism.

No such mechanism is currently established.

---

## 5. Resultant / Wronskian-of-Wronskians attempt

A natural idea is an effective resultant between

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha).
\]

For ordinary polynomials, a nonzero resultant excludes common zeros. For exponential polynomials, one can analogously ask whether the two functions have a common exponential-polynomial factor or a forced common zero structure.

This does not appear to help directly.

Reasons:

1. **Non-identical nonvanishing is too weak.**  
   Showing \(Z_\alpha\) and \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) do not share an identical factor would only exclude structural common vanishing, not approximate common smallness.

2. **Effective separation is missing.**  
   We need a polynomial lower bound:

   \[
   |Z_\alpha|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A},
   \]

   not merely nonzero.

3. **Exponential-polynomial recurrence remains.**  
   Even without common factors, two exponential sums along a one-parameter orbit may be simultaneously small unless actual arithmetic prevents it.

4. **The determinant is high-degree in AFE phases.**  
   A resultant would likely expand into subset-product frequencies, returning to the same cofactor/nonrecurrence objects already isolated.

Thus the resultant route collapses to an actual-orbit common-small-value nonrecurrence theorem.

---

## 6. Candidate named theorem

### Actual-Orbit Wronskian Incidence / Common-Small-Value Nonrecurrence

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible ordinary packet center and suppose

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Assume the canonical Wronskian is built from

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Then there exists \(A>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, in local common-small form,

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

throughout the admissible ordinary packet region.

Equivalently, in angle form, assuming the two parked norm inputs,

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]

This is the third ordinary-route named arithmetic input.

---

## 7. Relation to parked inputs

The ordinary route now consists of:

### Input 1: Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

### Input 2: Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

### Input 3: Actual-Orbit Wronskian Incidence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Together,

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

which is the Wronskian finite-jet anti-flatness input for ordinary Gate 1.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Common-small-value theorem: not proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-relaxed model: admits common smallness.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Resultant/Wronskian-of-Wronskians: no effective separation found.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Needed input: actual-orbit Wronskian incidence/nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s output is the final named theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-Orbit Wronskian Incidence / Common-Small-Value Nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

Agent 1 / A report: ordinary Gate 1 dependency stack. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Inputs 1--3 imply ordinary Gate 1, modulo canonical transfer and finite-jet-to-energy bookkeeping.}
}
\]

The ordinary branch now has a clean conditional theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence}
+
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence}
+
\text{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary finite-jet anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

The implication is structurally sound. The unproved pieces are precisely the three named actual-zeta arithmetic inputs plus the canonical transfer estimates needed to make sure the Wronskian is built from

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

rather than a model/proxy.

---

# 1. Ordinary-scale assumptions

Work in the ordinary packet regime:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

with safe jet depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

Let

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]

Ordinary Gate 1 is the normalized energy lower bound

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge
Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
}
\]

Equivalently, in physical variables,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

---

# 2. Wronskian setup at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero

Define rows

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

Let

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det\left(C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1}
\]

be the basis-normalized Wronskian.

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

expansion along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row gives

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
}
\]

Here

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and \(\mathbf M\) is the cofactor/Hodge-dual vector of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block.

---

# 3. The three named ordinary inputs

## Input 1: Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

This gives the \(Z_\alpha\)-row derivative lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_1}.
}
\]

Mechanism:

\[
\text{fixed-width cell mass}
\Rightarrow
\text{polylog-local }Z_\alpha\text{ amplitude}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A_1}.
\]

This input is parked as a named actual-orbit arithmetic theorem.

---

## Input 2: Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

This gives the cofactor lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

The natural averaged route is the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large sieve after resonance quotienting, but the pointwise statement is the actual input needed for the Wronskian route.

---

## Input 3: Wronskian Angle Nonalignment

This gives the angle lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf z',
\operatorname{span}\{q''_{\can}\text{-jet rows}\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'|.
}
\]

This is also parked as a named actual-orbit incidence theorem.

---

# 4. Inputs 1--3 imply a Wronskian lower bound

Combining Inputs 1--3 gives

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
=
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\]

\[
\ge
Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|
\]

\[
\ge
Q^{-A_3}Q^{-A_1}Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_W}
}
\]

for

\[
A_W=A_1+A_2+A_3.
\]

This is the ordinary Wronskian anti-degeneracy statement.

---

# 5. Wronskian lower bound implies finite-jet anti-design

The Wronskian determinant is a multilinear alternating functional of the \(Z_\alpha\)-row and the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows. If all normalized source-curvature jets were too small,

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\le Q^{-B_{\rm jet}}\lambda^3,
\]

then the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows would be too close to the source-flat design locus. Under the established row/basis conditioning bounds,

\[
\|C_\ell(\mathcal D)\|\le \exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

the determinant would satisfy

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\le Q^{-A_W-1}
\]

after choosing \(B_{\rm jet}\) large enough.

This contradicts the Wronskian lower bound.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_W}
\Rightarrow
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-B_{\rm jet}}\lambda^3.
}
\]

This is the ordinary finite-jet anti-design theorem.

---

# 6. Finite-jet anti-design implies ordinary Gate 1

Use the analytic-complexity package for the normalized canonical source curvature:

\[
\sup_{X^\ast}
|\partial_x^kF_\lambda(x)|
\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le R+1.
\]

Contrapositive:

If ordinary Gate 1 fails, then

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
<
Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

By local Sobolev/Cauchy/Bernstein/Remez-type propagation, small \(L^2\)-mass plus polynomial analytic complexity implies finite-jet flattening:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
<
Q^{-B'}\lambda^3
\]

on the relevant shrunken packet interval, after choosing \(B\) sufficiently large relative to \(B'\), \(R\), and the derivative-complexity constants.

But finite-jet anti-design gives

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-B_{\rm jet}}\lambda^3.
\]

Contradiction.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

This is ordinary Gate 1.

---

# 7. Dependency theorem

### Theorem: ordinary named inputs imply ordinary Gate 1

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Assume:

1. **Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence**

   \[
   Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
   \Rightarrow
   |\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_1}.
   \]

2. **Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence**

   \[
   Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
   \Rightarrow
   |\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
   \]

3. **Wronskian Angle Nonalignment**

   \[
   |\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
   \ge Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
   \]

4. **Canonical analytic-complexity package**

   \[
   \sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^kF_\lambda|
   \le Q^{C_k},
   \qquad 0\le k\le R+1.
   \]

5. **Basis/row conditioning**

   \[
   \|C_\ell(\mathcal D)\|,\ \|C_\ell(\mathcal D)^{-1}\|
   \le \exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
   \]

6. **Canonical transfer**

   The rows use

   \[
   q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
   \]

   with \(E_2\) and tails controlled through the derivative depth required by the Wronskian.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

That is ordinary Gate 1.

---

# 8. Hidden assumptions still needed

The implication above depends on the following technical assumptions beyond the three named inputs.

## A. Canonicality

The Wronskian must use

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

not:

\[
q''_{\source,R},
\]

not a zero-side proxy, not a prime-only toy model, and not a \(B_2\)-only diagnostic.

## B. \(E_2\) derivative control

Need enough control to transfer model rows to canonical rows. The expected derivative depth is approximately

\[
2R+1
\]

in normalized derivatives. A sufficient form is

\[
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-A_E}
\]

with \(A_E\) large compared with the determinant/cofactor Lipschitz losses.

## C. Row/basis conditioning

All basis-normalized operators must have losses at most

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

This is why the safe depth is

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

## D. Finite-jet-to-energy regularity

Need the analytic-complexity package:

\[
\sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^kF_\lambda|
\le Q^{C_k}
\]

through the finite order needed for the Sobolev/Cauchy/Remez propagation.

## E. Ordinary/singular separation

The proof only covers

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Deep singular packets

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

must be handled by the separate singular anti-design branch.

## F. \(Z_\alpha\)-zero admissibility

The \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) zero used in the Wronskian expansion must be the relevant ordinary off-line packet center, with all normalizations matching the row construction.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Inputs 1--3 imply ordinary Wronskian lower bound.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wronskian lower bound implies ordinary finite-jet anti-design.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-jet anti-design plus analytic complexity implies ordinary Gate 1.}
}
\]

So the ordinary dependency stack is now clean:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence}
+
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence}
+
\text{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment}
+
\text{canonical transfer}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:30:24)

_Thought for 4s_

Agent 1 / A report: Singular explicit-formula anti-design theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular Gate 1 reduces cleanly to a singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion.}
}
\]

Dominance proves singular Gate 1 unless the normalized singular packet realizes finite sine-moment cancellation:

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Pushing these moments through the explicit formula gives a prime-vector condition

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)-\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)-\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the required singular arithmetic input. I do not see a soft proof from local singular geometry alone; deterministic quadrature can still fake the sine-moment cancellation. The theorem must use actual zeta zero-prime compatibility.

---

# 1. Singular scaling

Work in the deep singular regime:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

Write

\[
c=\lambda,
\qquad
m=\gamma+cx.
\]

A singular local packet has the form

\[
q_{\rm sing}(m)=c^{-1}Q_{\rm sing}(x),
\]

so

\[
q_{\rm sing}'(m)=c^{-2}Q_{\rm sing}'(x),
\]

\[
q_{\rm sing}''(m)=c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x),
\]

and

\[
q_{\rm sing}^{(4)}(m)=c^{-5}Q_{\rm sing}^{(4)}(x).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\sim
c^{-5}\int_X|Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Since \(c\ll Q^{-1}(\log Q)^{-C}\) in the deep singular regime, the factor \(c^{-5}\) is enormous. Hence even a modest normalized lower bound for \(Q_{\rm sing}''\) proves Gate 1 strongly.

---

# 2. Singular dominance theorem

A clean dominance statement is:

### Singular dominance lemma

If

\[
\int_X |Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
c^{-5}Q^{-A}.
\]

Since

\[
|I_\rho|\asymp c|X|,
\]

this implies

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

for some \(B\), after weakening constants.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |Q_{\rm sing}''|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\text{singular Gate 1}.
}
\]

The only dangerous case is therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Exceptional singular anti-design condition

Use the normalized singular kernels

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

They satisfy

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

For a normalized singular packet aggregate

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)=\sum_j w_j K_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

the condition

\[
Q_{\rm sing}''(x)\approx0
\]

through depth \(R\) is equivalent to

\[
Q_{\rm sing}^{(r+2)}(0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

Using the kernel identity, this gives

\[
\boxed{
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

Here \(\mathcal B_k\) includes the canonical background, regularized tails, and any smooth/nonlocal terms after singular normalization.

This is the singular anti-design event.

---

# 4. Test functions recovering \(\sin(k\theta)\)

We want test functions \(h_k\) such that

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_k\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+\mathrm{Err}_k.
\]

A natural construction is to work in the harmonic/Poisson representation. Since

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\Im\frac{1}{x-e^{i\theta}}
\]

up to a harmless convention, the modes \(\sin(k\theta)\) can be recovered by testing against functions whose Cauchy transform extracts the \(k\)-th boundary harmonic.

One model choice is:

\[
h_k(x)=\operatorname{Im}\left[(x-i0)^{-k}\right]\chi_\sigma(x),
\]

or, more stably, use a smooth band-limited surrogate \(h_{k,\sigma}\) with a frequency cutoff \(\sigma\). Then

\[
\boxed{
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)
+
O(e^{-c\sigma})
+
O_{\sigma,k}(\text{tail cutoff}).
}
\]

The bandwidth \(\sigma\) must be at least polynomial in \(R\) if one wants uniform recovery for all

\[
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

A practical theorem should assume

\[
|\mathrm{Err}_k|\le Q^{-A}
\]

for all \(k\le R+3\).

---

# 5. Explicit formula translation

Let the zero-side statistic be

\[
\mathcal Z_k(\gamma,c)
=
\sum_\rho h_{k,c}(\gamma-\Im\rho),
\]

where \(h_{k,c}\) is the \(m\)-scale version of the normalized test function:

\[
h_{k,c}(t)=c^{-1}h_k(t/c).
\]

The explicit formula has schematic form

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z_k(\gamma,c)
=
\mathcal G_k(\gamma,c)
+
\mathcal T_k(\gamma,c)
+
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c).
}
\]

Here:

- \(\mathcal G_k\) is the gamma/background term;
- \(\mathcal T_k\) is the regularized tail / trivial / smoothing correction;
- \(\mathcal P_k\) is the prime-side statistic.

The prime statistic has the shape

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_k(c\log n)
}
\]

up to convention-dependent signs and gamma normalization.

Collecting the modes

\[
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

define

\[
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
=
(\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c))_{k=3}^{R+3},
\]

\[
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
=
(\mathcal G_k(\gamma,c))_{k=3}^{R+3},
\]

\[
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
=
(\mathcal T_k(\gamma,c))_{k=3}^{R+3}.
\]

Then the singular anti-design condition becomes

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right|_2
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Therefore the singular exclusion theorem is exactly the negation:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 6. Bandwidth and prime range

The Fourier factor is

\[
\widehat h_k(c\log n).
\]

If \(h_k\) is designed to recover \(\sin(k\theta)\), then its Fourier support must reach frequencies comparable to \(k\). Thus for

\[
k\le R+3,
\]

one expects meaningful prime contribution when

\[
c\log n\lesssim R^{C_0}
\]

for some fixed \(C_0\), often \(C_0=1\) in an ideal band-limited design and larger after smoothing.

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^{C_0}}{c}.
}
\]

In deep singular scale,

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

so

\[
\frac{1}{c}\gg Q(\log Q)^C.
\]

Thus the required prime range can extend well beyond the ordinary packet-frequency range

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

This is why the singular branch is genuinely separate from the ordinary Wronskian route.

---

# 7. Candidate theorem

### Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion

Let

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\qquad c=\lambda,
\qquad m=\gamma+cx.
\]

Let \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\). For each

\[
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

let \(h_{k,c}\) be a normalized singular test function satisfying

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_k\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O(Q^{-A})
\]

uniformly in the relevant packet geometry. Define the explicit-formula vectors

\[
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c),
\qquad
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c),
\qquad
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\]

as above.

Then the needed theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Under this theorem, singular anti-design is impossible. Therefore singular dominance gives Gate 1 in the deep singular regime.

---

# 8. What would prove the theorem?

The theorem would follow from an actual-prime vector nonrecurrence statement:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
2\Re
\sum_n
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_k(c\log n)
-
\mathcal G_k-\mathcal T_k
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is a long-prime analogue of the ordinary packet-frequency nonrecurrence inputs. It must use actual zeta arithmetic; deterministic local quadrature can defeat purely local zero-side arguments.

No standard soft estimate appears to force this vector away from zero. The theorem should therefore be carried as a named singular arithmetic input unless a new explicit-formula lower-bound mechanism is found.

---

# 9. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Singular dominance lemma: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Singular anti-design } \Longleftrightarrow
\text{finite sine-moment cancellation: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Explicit-formula translation to }\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R:
\text{ Green modulo test-function construction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prime-vector lower bound: open actual-zeta arithmetic input.}
}
\]

Thus the named singular input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion}
}
\]

with theorem statement

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the singular counterpart to the ordinary nonrecurrence inputs.
## User (2026-04-27 08:34:08)
