## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:34:27)

_Thought for 16s_

Agent 1 / A report: Gate 2 base-locus rigidity. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact interval base-locus rigidity is true: }
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\Rightarrow
u=q''_{\can}\equiv0.
}
\]

But the **pointwise** base-locus statement is false. At a single point,

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

does **not** force

\[
u=0.
\]

So Gate 2 cannot follow from pointwise algebra alone. It needs a propagation step: Gate 2 failure must first force approximate base-locus behavior on an interval or thick set, and then local ODE/unique-continuation rigidity can rule it out.

The correct Gate 2 architecture is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 mass}
+
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{thick approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
u\approx0,
}
\]

contradicting Gate 1.

---

# 1. Definitions

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The given normalized identities are

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\Gamma_G=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

---

# 2. Exact interval base-locus

Assume on an interval \(J\),

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0.
\]

Then

\[
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Also, since \(\Gamma_G\equiv0\),

\[
\Gamma_G''\equiv0.
\]

Therefore

\[
0=\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2.
\]

So on \(J\),

\[
q(q')^2\equiv0.
\]

There are two possibilities.

### Case 1: \(q\equiv0\) on an interval

Then

\[
q''\equiv0,
\]

so

\[
u=q''\equiv0.
\]

### Case 2: \(q\neq0\) on an open subinterval

Then

\[
(q')^2=0,
\]

so

\[
q'\equiv0.
\]

Hence \(q\) is constant on that subinterval, and therefore

\[
q''=0.
\]

Combining with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3
\]

gives

\[
0=6q-2q^3=2q(3-q^2).
\]

Thus

\[
q\in\{0,\pm\sqrt3\}.
\]

In all cases,

\[
u=q''=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\text{ on an interval}
\Rightarrow
u\equiv0.
}
\]

This is the exact base-locus rigidity theorem.

---

# 3. Pointwise base-locus is not rigid

At a single point \(m_\ast\), the equations

\[
\Gamma_G(m_\ast)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)=0
\]

do not force

\[
u(m_\ast)=0.
\]

Indeed,

\[
\Gamma_G(m_\ast)=0
\]

only gives

\[
u(m_\ast)=6q(m_\ast)-2q(m_\ast)^3.
\]

This may be nonzero. For example, if

\[
q(m_\ast)=1,
\]

then

\[
u(m_\ast)=4.
\]

The second condition is

\[
0=\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)
=
2q(m_\ast)(q'(m_\ast))^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''(m_\ast).
\]

This merely fixes

\[
\Gamma_G''(m_\ast)
=
12q(m_\ast)(q'(m_\ast))^2.
\]

It imposes a condition on higher jets, not directly on \(u(m_\ast)\). Therefore the pointwise system allows

\[
u(m_\ast)\neq0.
\]

So the desired rigidity must be an **interval/thick-set rigidity**, not a pointwise algebraic fact.

---

# 4. Approximate interval base-locus

Suppose on an interval \(J\),

\[
|\Gamma_G|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le\varepsilon,
\]

and derivatives are controlled:

\[
\sup_J |q^{(k)}|\le Q^{C_k}
\]

for \(k\) large enough.

From

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

we get

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon).
\]

From

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

if \(\Gamma_G\) is small not only in value but also propagated to second derivative,

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\le\varepsilon',
\]

then

\[
|q(q')^2|
\le
C(\varepsilon+\varepsilon').
\]

Hence, away from \(q=0\), one gets

\[
|q'|\ll (\varepsilon+\varepsilon')^{1/2}|q|^{-1/2}.
\]

Thus \(q\) is nearly constant on subintervals where \(|q|\) is bounded below. Substituting into

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon)
\]

then forces

\[
6q-2q^3\approx0,
\]

so

\[
q\approx0
\quad\text{or}\quad
q\approx\pm\sqrt3.
\]

In each case,

\[
q''\approx0,
\]

so

\[
u=q''\approx0.
\]

Thus the approximate interval theorem is plausible:

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|,\ |\Gamma_{G,2}|,\ |\Gamma_G''|\text{ small on }J
\Rightarrow
|u|\text{ small on }J.
}
\]

However, the formula for \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) contains \(\Gamma_G''\), so to use it one needs control or propagation of \(\Gamma_G\)-smallness from value-smallness to derivative-smallness.

That is exactly where Agent 2’s Remez/Bernstein propagation is needed.

---

# 5. Thick-set rigidity

Gate 2 failure would not initially give interval smallness. It gives weighted smallness:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Together with Gate 1,

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

one obtains a set \(E\subset I\) where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

but

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

On this set,

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0
\]

implies

\[
u\approx6q-2q^3.
\]

Since \(|u|\) is non-small on \(E\), this implies

\[
|6q-2q^3|\gtrsim Q^{-C_u}
\]

on much of \(E\).

But exact interval rigidity says that if the pair

\[
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

is small on an interval, then \(u\) must be small. Therefore, to derive a contradiction, one must upgrade the thick-set smallness to interval smallness.

This is not automatic. It requires a real-variable propagation lemma using the finite derivative-complexity package.

So the rigidity theorem should be stated conditionally:

\[
\boxed{
\text{thick approximate base-locus}
+
\text{Remez/Bernstein propagation}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
u\approx0.
}
\]

---

# 6. Candidate base-locus rigidity theorem

### Theorem: interval base-locus rigidity

Let \(J\) be an interval. Suppose

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le\varepsilon,
\]

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le\varepsilon,
\]

and the finite complexity package gives

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le\varepsilon'
\]

or equivalently gives enough propagation to control \(\Gamma_G''\). Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^C(\varepsilon+\varepsilon')^{c}
}
\]

on a slightly shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\), unless \(J\) is so small that derivative control is insufficient.

In particular, if \(\varepsilon,\varepsilon'\le Q^{-A}\) with \(A\) large enough, then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for some \(A'>0\).

This contradicts a Gate 1 thick-mass lower bound once propagated over enough intervals.

---

# 7. What still needs to be supplied

The exact base-locus rigidity is simple and true. The missing analytic bridge is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{smallness of }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ on a thick }u\text{-mass set}
\Rightarrow
\text{smallness on an interval, including derivative control.}
}
\]

This needs:

1. finite derivative complexity for \(q\) through at least the order needed to control \(\Gamma_G''\);
2. Remez/Bernstein propagation from thick sets;
3. a way to keep the set inside the region where \(|u|\) is not negligible;
4. quantitative constants compatible with \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\).

---

# 8. Countermodel warning

A pointwise countermodel exists:

Choose jets at \(m_\ast\) satisfying

\[
q(m_\ast)=1,\qquad q'(m_\ast)=0,
\]

\[
q''(m_\ast)=4.
\]

Then

\[
u(m_\ast)=4,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G(m_\ast)
=
4-6+2=0.
\]

Choose higher derivatives so that

\[
\Gamma_G''(m_\ast)=0.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)=0.
\]

So the base-locus equations at one point can coexist with nonzero \(u\). Therefore Gate 2 cannot be proved by pointwise sampling alone.

The required theorem must use interval/thick-set structure.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact interval base-locus rigidity: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pointwise base-locus rigidity: false.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Approximate thick-set-to-interval propagation: open, assigned to Agent 2.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 depends on propagation plus interval rigidity.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s output is:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\text{ on an interval}
\Rightarrow
u\equiv0,
}
\]

and the Gate 2 proof reduces to making this rigidity quantitative on intervals obtained from Gate 1 mass and Gate 2 failure.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:42:17)

I’ll focus this as Agent 1: derive what Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure actually gives, then isolate the precise propagation lemma needed to turn thick-set smallness into interval base-locus rigidity.

_Thought for 45s_

Agent 1 / A report: Gate 2 propagation / Remez–Bernstein theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure gives a polynomial-measure bad set, but not yet an interval.}
}
\]

The desired Gate 2 proof needs an additional real-variable propagation input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{polynomial-measure approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}.
}
\]

Without this, Agent 1’s interval rigidity theorem cannot be applied. A Remez/Bernstein route is plausible if the bad set is sufficiently **thick at a controlled scale**, but Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure alone gives only **global measure**, not scale-wise thickness. So the current missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 thick-set-to-interval propagation.}
}
\]

---

# 1. From Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure to a thick bad set

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
G^2=\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2.
\]

Assume a finite-complexity upper bound

\[
\sup_I |u|\le Q^{C_u}.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau^2=\frac12 Q^{-B}.
\]

Let

\[
E_u=\{m\in I: |u(m)|\ge \tau\}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I |u|^2
\le
\tau^2 |I|+Q^{2C_u}|E_u|,
\]

so

\[
|E_u|
\ge
\frac{Q^{-B}-\tau^2}{Q^{2C_u}}|I|
=
\frac12Q^{-B-2C_u}|I|.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|E_u|\ge Q^{-C_1}|I|.
}
\]

Now on \(E_u\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2=\frac12Q^{-B}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{E_u}G^2\,dm
\le
2Q^{B}\int_I |u|^2G^2\,dm
\le
2Q^{B-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
E=
\{m\in E_u:G(m)\le \sigma\}.
\]

By Markov, choosing

\[
\sigma^2=8Q^{B-A}|I|/|E_u|
\]

gives

\[
|E|\ge\frac12|E_u|.
\]

Using the lower bound for \(|E_u|\),

\[
\sigma^2
\le
Q^{-A+2B+2C_u+O(1)}.
\]

Thus, for \(A\) large enough,

\[
\boxed{
|E|\ge Q^{-C_1}|I|,
}
\]

and on \(E\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u'},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
}
\]

This part is solid.

---

# 2. Why this is not enough

Agent 1’s base-locus rigidity applies to an interval where

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are small, and where derivative control gives smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G''.
\]

The set \(E\) above has polynomial measure, but it may be dust-like. Positive measure alone does not imply any interval on which both \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) are uniformly small.

A counter-pattern is possible in real-variable terms:

- \(u\) is large on many small islands;
- \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are small on those islands;
- between islands, \(u\) is small or the anisotropy factors are large;
- total Gate 1 mass and Gate 2 failure both hold;
- no interval approximate base-locus appears.

Derivative bounds can rule out arbitrarily thin islands only if they are strong enough at the relevant scale. So the missing step is not measure extraction; it is **scale-thickness propagation**.

---

# 3. Required analytic-complexity package

The functions involved are

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

To propagate smallness and then invoke interval rigidity, one needs control of at least:

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ q''',\ q^{(4)}.
\]

Because

\[
\Gamma_G''=u''-6q''+12q(q')^2+12q^2q''
\]

involves derivatives up to

\[
q^{(4)}.
\]

For Remez/Bernstein propagation of those quantities, one likely needs a few more derivatives. A safe finite package is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6.
}
\]

A minimal package may be \(k\le4\), but \(k\le6\) is safer because differentiating \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) in propagation arguments can cost extra derivatives.

---

# 4. Propagation lemma needed

The clean missing lemma is:

### Gate 2 thick-set-to-interval propagation lemma

Let \(f_1=\Gamma_G\), \(f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}\), and suppose

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k f_i|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le k_0.
\]

Suppose there exists

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|
\]

such that

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Then there exists a subinterval \(J\subset I\) of length at least \(Q^{-C_J}|I|\) such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

and either

\[
\sup_J|u|\ge Q^{-C_u'}
\]

or \(u\)-mass remains nontrivial on \(J\).

This is not automatic from measure alone; it requires a Remez/Bernstein/Cartan-type theorem for the finite-complexity class.

---

# 5. How Remez could prove it

If \(E\) is not merely large but **relatively dense** at scale \(\ell\):

\[
|E\cap J|\ge \rho |J|
\]

for every subinterval \(J\subset I\) of length \(\ell\), with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

then a propagation theorem is plausible.

For analytic or polynomial-complexity functions \(f\), one expects:

\[
\sup_I |f|
\le
\left(\frac{C}{\rho}\right)^{N}
\sup_E |f|
+
\text{complexity error}.
\]

If the effective complexity \(N\) is fixed or grows only mildly, this is polynomially safe. If

\[
N\asymp R,
\]

then

\[
\left(\frac{C}{\rho}\right)^R
=
\exp(O(R\log Q))
=
\exp\!\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too large unless \(A\) is made correspondingly huge or the loss is improved. For Gate 2, because the functions are low-order expressions in \(q\), the effective complexity may be finite-order rather than \(R\)-order, but this must be justified.

So the theorem should either use:

\[
k_0=O(1)
\]

finite derivative control, or a relative-density propagation lemma with polynomial loss.

---

# 6. Control of \(\Gamma_G''\)

The interval rigidity needs smallness not only of

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

but effectively also of

\[
\Gamma_G''.
\]

There are two ways to get this.

### Route A: Cauchy/Remez propagation

If \(\Gamma_G\) is small on a real interval and has holomorphic extension with controlled complex bounds, then Cauchy estimates on a smaller interval give

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

after shrinking the interval and accepting polynomial losses.

### Route B: Include \(\Gamma_G''\) in the bad-set extraction

This is not directly available from Gate 2 failure, because Gate 2 weights only

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

So Route A is preferred.

Thus the propagation lemma must be strong enough to upgrade real smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) to derivative smallness on a subinterval. This again requires analytic/holomorphic complexity, not just \(C^0\) control.

---

# 7. Candidate Gate 2 theorem

### Conditional Gate 2 theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

2. Analytic complexity:

   \[
   \sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
   \qquad
   0\le k\le6,
   \]

   with holomorphic extension or a Remez class allowing thick-set propagation.

3. Thick-set propagation lemma:

   polynomial-measure smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) on the non-small \(u\)-set implies interval smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\Gamma_G''\).

4. Approximate interval base-locus rigidity:

   \[
   \sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A}
   \Rightarrow
   \sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^{-A'}.
   \]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A_G}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Set extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Positive-measure set alone: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need relative-density/Remez/Bernstein propagation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need derivative transfer to obtain }\Gamma_G''\text{ small.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Minimal derivative order: likely }k_0=4,\text{ safe }k_0=6.
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s output is the exact missing real-variable theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}
}
\]

which, together with interval base-locus rigidity, would prove Gate 2.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:46:51)

_Thought for 7s_

Agent 1 / A report: Gate 2 thick-set-to-interval propagation. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 propagation is not closed from measure information alone.}
}
\]

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure one can extract a polynomial-measure set

\[
E\subset I
\]

on which

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

That part is solid. But positive polynomial measure does **not** by itself give an interval on which \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are uniformly small. A dust-like set can evade interval rigidity unless one has an additional density/propagation principle.

So the missing theorem is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation.}
}
\]

A plausible version uses finite analytic complexity plus a relative-density hypothesis. Without that hypothesis, a counter-pattern remains possible.

---

# 1. Set extraction from Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
G^2=\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2.
\]

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2G^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume also a basic upper complexity bound

\[
\sup_I |u|\le Q^{C_u^{+}}.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau^2=\frac12Q^{-B}.
\]

Define

\[
E_u=\{m\in I:|u(m)|\ge\tau\}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_I |u|^2
\le
\tau^2|I|+Q^{2C_u^{+}}|E_u|.
\]

Thus

\[
|E_u|
\ge
\frac{Q^{-B}-\tau^2}{Q^{2C_u^{+}}}|I|
\ge
Q^{-C_1}|I|.
\]

On \(E_u\),

\[
|u|^2\ge \tau^2=\frac12Q^{-B}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{E_u}G^2\,dm
\le
2Q^B
\int_I |u|^2G^2\,dm
\le
2Q^{B-A}|I|.
\]

Now choose

\[
\sigma^2
=
4Q^{B-A}\frac{|I|}{|E_u|}.
\]

Since

\[
|E_u|\ge Q^{-C_1}|I|,
\]

we get

\[
\sigma^2\le Q^{-A+B+C_1+O(1)}.
\]

Let

\[
E=\{m\in E_u:G(m)\le \sigma\}.
\]

By Markov,

\[
|E|\ge \frac12|E_u|\ge Q^{-C_2}|I|.
\]

On \(E\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
}
\]

provided \(A\) is chosen sufficiently large.

So the extraction theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\exists E\subset I,\ |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\ |u|\ge Q^{-C},\
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Why positive measure is insufficient

Agent 1’s interval base-locus rigidity says:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\quad\text{on an interval}
\Rightarrow
u\equiv0.
\]

The extracted set \(E\) is not necessarily an interval. It may be distributed as many tiny components. The following obstruction remains possible at the level of real-variable analysis:

- \(u\) is large on many small islands;
- \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are small on those islands;
- between the islands, \(u\) is small or \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are large;
- \(E\) has polynomial measure;
- no subinterval \(J\) has uniformly small \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\).

So measure alone cannot invoke interval rigidity.

The necessary additional input is some form of scale-thickness:

\[
\boxed{
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C}|J|
}
\]

on many intervals \(J\) of controlled length, or an equivalent Remez/Cartan-type propagation theorem that turns polynomial measure plus finite complexity into interval control.

---

# 3. Required analytic-complexity package

The quantities are:

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
u=q'',
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

To control these functions and their propagation, a safe finite derivative package is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le6.
}
\]

The minimum may be \(k_0=4\), because

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

uses derivatives through \(q^{(4)}\). But if one differentiates \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) or applies Bernstein/Remez with derivative remainders, \(k_0=6\) is a safer theorem-level assumption.

Thus the current safe package is:

\[
\boxed{
k_0=6\text{ normalized derivatives.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Propagation lemma needed

The missing real-variable lemma should be stated as follows.

### Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k f_i|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le k_0,
\qquad i=1,2,
\]

with \(k_0\ge4\), preferably \(k_0=6\).

Suppose there exists

\[
E\subset I
\]

such that

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Then there exists a subinterval

\[
J\subset I,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

and, on a subinterval or subset of \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u'}.
\]

To apply approximate interval rigidity, one also needs either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A''}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\), or a direct estimate of

\[
q(q')^2
\]

from the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-equation.

---

# 5. Does derivative complexity plus measure force interval thickness?

Not in a trivial way.

If a \(C^k\)-bounded function is small on a set of positive measure, it need not be small on a macroscopic interval. It can oscillate between small and large values at a scale controlled by the derivative bounds.

Derivative bounds do impose a minimum island size: if

\[
|f|\le\varepsilon
\]

at a point and

\[
|f'|\le Q^C,
\]

then

\[
|f|\le 2\varepsilon
\]

on an interval of radius roughly

\[
\varepsilon Q^{-C}.
\]

But if

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

this interval may be extremely small. One obtains many tiny intervals, not necessarily a useful interval with enough \(u\)-mass.

Thus a simple derivative-bound argument is not enough unless the exponents are carefully balanced and the required interval for rigidity can be as small as a polynomial scale.

A Remez-type theorem may help if the function class has low effective complexity, not merely finite derivative bounds. For analytic functions with bounded complex growth, one can sometimes obtain:

\[
\sup_I |f|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N
\sup_E |f|,
\]

where \(N\) is an effective degree. If \(N=O(1)\), the loss is polynomial. If \(N\asymp R\), the loss may become

\[
\exp(O(R\log Q)),
\]

which is too large unless the initial smallness is chosen very strong.

So the viable propagation theorem likely needs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-order/low-complexity Remez, not high-degree }R\text{-Remez.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Control of \(\Gamma_G''\)

Approximate interval rigidity needs small

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2},
\quad\text{and effectively}\quad
\Gamma_G''.
\]

From

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

smallness of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone gives

\[
\Gamma_G''\approx 12q(q')^2.
\]

So it does **not** directly imply \(\Gamma_G''\) is small.

There are two routes.

## Route A: derivative propagation from \(\Gamma_G\)

If \(\Gamma_G\) is small on an interval and has controlled holomorphic extension, Cauchy estimates on a smaller interval can give

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

provided the complex radius is polynomially large relative to the interval scale.

This route requires complex analytic control.

## Route B: derive \(q(q')^2\)-smallness directly

If \(\Gamma_G\approx0\), then

\[
q''\approx6q-2q^3.
\]

If also \(\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0\), then

\[
2q(q')^2\approx \frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Without \(\Gamma_G''\)-control this is not useful. So Route B still needs derivative information, unless one can integrate the equation and use energy identities to control \(\Gamma_G''\) indirectly.

Thus Route A is cleaner.

---

# 7. Candidate conditional Gate 2 theorem

A complete conditional theorem is:

### Conditional Gate 2 theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

2. Analytic complexity:

   \[
   \sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
   \qquad
   0\le k\le6.
   \]

3. Gate 2 thick-set-to-interval propagation:

   Gate 2 failure implies an interval \(J\subset I\) such that

   \[
   \sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
   \]

   and \(u\) remains non-negligible on \(J\).

4. Derivative propagation:

   On a shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\),

   \[
   \sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
   \]

5. Approximate interval base-locus rigidity:

   \[
   \sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
   \Rightarrow
   \sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-A''}.
   \]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A_G}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 8. Final status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Set extraction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Positive measure }\not\Rightarrow\text{ interval: obstruction remains.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need Gate 2 thick-set-to-interval propagation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need derivative propagation to control }\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Safe derivative package: }0\le k\le6.
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s final output is the named missing theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}
}
\]

plus the auxiliary derivative-propagation requirement for \(\Gamma_G''\).

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:50:42)

_Thought for 6s_

Agent 1 / A report: Remez/Bernstein thick-set-to-interval theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Positive polynomial measure is not enough; a relative-density or finite-complexity Cartan/Remez input is needed.}
}
\]

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, we get a set

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\]

on \(E\). But this set can be dust-like. Derivative bounds alone give only very small neighborhoods around points of \(E\), not necessarily an interval large enough to run approximate base-locus rigidity.

So the missing theorem should be named precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation.}
}
\]

A plausible version is true under a **relative-density hypothesis** or a **Cartan/Remez finite-complexity hypothesis**, but it is not currently a consequence of positive measure alone.

---

## 1. Extracted bad set

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure give:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

\[
\int_I |u|^2(f_1^2+f_2^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assuming

\[
\sup_I |u|\le Q^{C_u^+},
\]

one extracts

\[
E\subset I
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_f}
}
\]

on \(E\), after choosing \(A\) sufficiently large.

This part is robust.

---

## 2. Positive measure is insufficient

A set \(E\) with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

need not contain any interval of comparable polynomial length. It may be a union of tiny islands.

Even if

\[
f_1,f_2
\]

are small on \(E\), they may become large between islands. Pointwise derivative bounds give local neighborhoods of smallness around points of \(E\), but the guaranteed radius is roughly

\[
\rho\sim \frac{Q^{-C_f}}{\sup|f_i'|}.
\]

If

\[
\sup|f_i'|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

then

\[
\rho\sim Q^{-C_f-C_1}.
\]

This is polynomially small, but it need not yield one interval where the pair

\[
(f_1,f_2)
\]

is small across a scale useful for base-locus rigidity unless the density of \(E\) is controlled at that scale.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{positive measure alone does not produce interval approximate base-locus.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Relative-density version

A clean sufficient hypothesis is:

There exists a scale

\[
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|
\]

and a density

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}
\]

such that for every subinterval \(J\subset I\) with \(|J|=\ell\),

\[
\boxed{
|E\cap J|\ge \rho |J|.
}
\]

Under this relative-density condition, a Remez-type theorem can propagate smallness.

A suitable theorem would be:

### Relative-density propagation theorem

Assume

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k f_i|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le k_0,
\qquad i=1,2.
\]

If

\[
|f_i|\le Q^{-A}
\]

on a relatively dense set \(E\), then there is an interval

\[
J\subset I,
\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J |f_1|+\sup_J|f_2|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

after shrinking exponents.

The derivative order required is at least enough to control oscillation of \(f_i\); for the later \(\Gamma_G''\) step, a safe package is

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6.
}
\]

---

## 4. Can relative density be extracted from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure?

Not from the integral information alone.

The set \(E\) can have polynomial total measure but be concentrated in a small portion of \(I\), or arranged as many small islands. Gate 1 only controls global \(u\)-mass; Gate 2 failure controls weighted average anisotropy. Neither prevents the bad set from being geometrically sparse.

A possible refinement is to first choose a subinterval \(I_0\subset I\) where the density of \(E\) is high by a dyadic density decomposition. This gives:

\[
|E\cap I_0|\ge Q^{-C}|I_0|.
\]

But it still does not guarantee relative density inside every smaller subinterval of \(I_0\).

So one of the following is needed:

1. a Cartan/Remez theorem using only total measure for the specific analytic class;
2. a density regularization lemma that finds a subinterval where \(E\) is relatively dense at the required scale;
3. an additional zero/oscillation-count bound for \(f_1,f_2\).

---

## 5. Finite-complexity Remez route

For polynomials of degree \(N\), Remez gives

\[
\sup_I |f|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N
\sup_E |f|.
\]

For analytic functions of finite exponential type or bounded zero count, analogous estimates exist.

If the effective complexity \(N\) is \(O(1)\), total measure

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

is enough, with polynomial loss.

If

\[
N\asymp R,
\]

the loss is

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too expensive unless the initial smallness from Gate 2 failure is made super-polynomially strong.

Thus the usable theorem must show that \(f_1,f_2\) belong to a finite-complexity class of **bounded or low effective degree** on the Gate 2 interval, not merely arbitrary analytic functions with \(R\)-scale complexity.

This is the key analytic issue.

---

## 6. Derivative order

The functions are:

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

\(f_1\) uses \(q\) through order \(2\). \(f_2\) uses

\[
q,\ q',\ \Gamma_G'',
\]

and hence \(q\) through order \(4\). If one differentiates \(f_2\) or uses derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\), one may need \(q\) through order \(6\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
k_0=4\text{ is minimal-looking; }k_0=6\text{ is safe.}
}
\]

I recommend stating Gate 2 propagation with the safe assumption:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6.
}
\]

---

## 7. Strongest theorem candidate

### Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume:

1. finite complexity:

   \[
   \sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
   \qquad 0\le k\le6;
   \]

2. extracted bad set:

   \[
   E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|;
   \]

3. non-small source:

   \[
   |u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E;
   \]

4. anisotropy smallness:

   \[
   |f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E;
   \]

5. either a relative-density condition for \(E\), or a finite-complexity Remez theorem for \(f_1,f_2\) with polynomial loss.

Then there exists

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

and \(u\) remains non-negligible on \(J\) or on a controlled subset of \(J\).

A derivative-propagation theorem must then supply

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A''}
\]

on a shrunken \(J'\), after which approximate interval rigidity gives \(u\approx0\), contradicting Gate 1 mass.

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Extraction of }E: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Positive measure alone: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need relative density or low-complexity Remez/Cartan theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Safe derivative package: }0\le k\le6.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 remains conditional on Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s final reduced theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}
}
\]

with an explicit density/Remez hypothesis.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:53:30)

_Thought for 6s_

Agent 1 / A report: relative-density extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global polynomial measure does not imply the needed relative density.}
}
\]

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure we get a set

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

But this does **not** force \(E\) to be relatively dense at any useful scale. A dust-like set can satisfy all of these measure conditions while containing no interval-scale region where \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are uniformly small.

Thus Gate 2 requires an additional input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

or, more explicitly, either a relative-density theorem for the extracted bad set, or a low-complexity Cartan/Remez theorem strong enough to convert total-measure smallness into interval smallness.

---

## 1. What global measure gives

The extraction step gives

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

A basic density argument says there exists some subinterval \(I_0\subset I\) with high average density:

\[
\frac{|E\cap I_0|}{|I_0|}\ge Q^{-C_E}.
\]

But this does **not** imply relative density on smaller intervals:

\[
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C}|J|
\]

for every \(J\subset I_0\) of a controlled length.

At best, global measure gives a density point in the measure-theoretic sense, but the scale of that density point may be arbitrarily small without additional regularity or complexity assumptions on \(E\).

---

## 2. Dust-like counterexample

Let \(I=[0,1]\). Fix

\[
\delta=Q^{-C_E}.
\]

Let \(E\) be a union of \(N\) tiny intervals:

\[
E=\bigcup_{j=1}^N [x_j,x_j+\ell],
\]

with

\[
N\ell=\delta.
\]

Choose the points \(x_j\) separated, and take \(\ell\) extremely small, e.g.

\[
\ell=Q^{-M}
\]

with \(M\) arbitrarily large.

Then

\[
|E|=\delta=Q^{-C_E}.
\]

But there is no lower relative-density bound at any scale larger than roughly \(\ell/\delta\). Large intervals may contain no \(E\), and intervals containing one component have density depending on the component scale.

Now define smooth functions \(f_1,f_2\) that are \(Q^{-A}\)-small on \(E\), but rise between the islands. With derivative bounds

\[
|f_i'|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

one only needs transition width

\[
\sim Q^{-A-C_1}
\]

around each island. If \(\ell\) is larger than this transition scale, the construction is compatible with derivative bounds.

Therefore, unless the derivative/complexity package prevents many such oscillatory islands, positive measure alone is not enough.

---

## 3. Does \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) help?

Only locally.

If

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

on \(E\), and

\[
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

then around each point of \(E\), \(u\) remains non-small on a radius

\[
\rho_u\asymp Q^{-C_u-C_1}.
\]

Similarly, if

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\]

and their derivatives are bounded by \(Q^{C_2}\), then they remain small on a radius

\[
\rho_\Gamma\asymp Q^{-C_\Gamma-C_2}.
\]

Thus each point in \(E\) gives a small interval of approximate base-locus. But the radius may be much smaller than what is needed for the interval-rigidity step unless exponents are arranged carefully.

So \(|u|\)-non-smallness plus derivative bounds gives local neighborhoods, but not automatically a usable interval of length

\[
Q^{-C}|I|
\]

with the right derivative smallness and mass retention.

---

## 4. A sufficient relative-density hypothesis

A strong enough hypothesis is:

There exist

\[
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|,
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

such that for every subinterval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|J|\ge \ell,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|E\cap J|\ge \rho |J|.
}
\]

Under this assumption, finite-complexity Remez/Cartan estimates can plausibly imply:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

on some controlled interval \(J'\), or possibly on all of a shrunken interval.

But this relative-density property does not follow from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure by measure theory alone.

---

## 5. Alternative sufficient hypotheses

Any of the following could replace explicit relative density.

### A. Bounded connected components

If \(E\) has at most \(Q^C\) connected components, then one component has length at least

\[
Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

That component is already an interval of approximate base-locus.

So a sufficient theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0(E)\le Q^C.
}
\]

But such a bound requires zero-count/oscillation control for the level sets of \(u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\).

### B. Cartan exceptional-set control

If the complement of the approximate base-locus has Cartan-type structure with bounded complexity, then positive measure of \(E\) may force an interval-like component.

This is essentially a complex-analytic version of bounded component count.

### C. Low effective complexity Remez

If \(f_1,f_2\) lie in a class with effective Remez degree \(N=O(1)\), then

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

is enough to propagate smallness with polynomial loss.

If \(N\asymp R\), the loss is too large:

\[
Q^{O(R)}=\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right).
\]

Thus the effective complexity must be genuinely low, not merely finite at the \(R\)-scale.

---

## 6. The sharp no-go

The following statement is false:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
+
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},\ 0\le k\le6
\Rightarrow
\exists J,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C'}|I|,
\ 
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

It is false unless the derivative exponents and smallness exponents are quantitatively tied so that transition layers cannot be too numerous or too thin. A generic \(C^6\)-bound permits many separated small islands.

So the theorem must include one of:

\[
\text{relative density},
\]

\[
\text{low Remez degree},
\]

\[
\text{bounded component count},
\]

\[
\text{Cartan exceptional-set control},
\]

or

\[
\text{stronger analytic continuation/growth control}.
\]

---

## 7. Final theorem candidate

### Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume:

\[
E\subset I,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume additionally one of:

1. \(E\) is relatively dense at scale \(\ell\ge Q^{-C}|I|\);
2. \(E\) has \(\le Q^C\) connected components;
3. \(f_1,f_2\) satisfy a low-complexity Remez/Cartan estimate with polynomial loss;
4. the approximate base-locus has Cartan exceptional-set control.

Then there exists an interval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

If derivative propagation also gives

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A''},
\]

then approximate interval rigidity implies

\[
u\approx0
\]

on \(J'\), contradicting retained Gate 1 mass.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global measure extraction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Relative density extraction from measure alone: false.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative bounds help locally but do not solve dust-like sets.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need extra density/Remez/Cartan/complexity input.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s final output is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

as the precise missing bridge from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure to interval base-locus rigidity.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:58:54)

_Thought for 5s_

Agent 1 / A report: relative-density / Cartan extraction. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure does not by itself give relative density.}
}
\]

It gives a polynomial-measure bad set

\[
E=\{|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},\ |\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}\},
\]

but this set can be dust-like. To pass from this set to interval base-locus rigidity, the proof needs an additional input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation.}
}
\]

The cleanest sufficient versions are either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{relative density of }E\text{ at polynomial scale,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{low-complexity Cartan/Remez control for }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

Derivative bounds help locally but do not, by themselves, rule out many separated small components.

---

## 1. What global measure gives

From the already-established extraction,

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

This implies there is at least one interval \(I_0\subset I\) with average density

\[
\frac{|E\cap I_0|}{|I_0|}\ge Q^{-C_E}.
\]

But it does **not** imply a scale-wise density statement such as

\[
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C}|J|
\]

for every subinterval \(J\subset I_0\) of length at least

\[
\ell\ge Q^{-C}|I_0|.
\]

A set can have large total measure but be distributed in small clusters separated by large gaps. Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure do not automatically exclude that geometry.

---

## 2. Dust-like counterexample

Let

\[
I=[0,1],
\qquad
|E|=Q^{-C_E}.
\]

Construct

\[
E=\bigcup_{j=1}^N [x_j,x_j+\delta],
\]

with

\[
N\delta=Q^{-C_E},
\]

and with the intervals separated by gaps much larger than \(\delta\).

Choose \(\delta\) polynomially small, for example

\[
\delta=Q^{-M}
\]

with \(M\) large but finite. This is compatible with finite derivative bounds if transitions occur over scale

\[
\delta_{\rm trans}\gtrsim Q^{-C_{\rm deriv}}.
\]

Define smooth functions \(u,f_1,f_2\), where

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

such that on \(E\),

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma},
\]

but outside narrow neighborhoods of \(E\), one or both \(f_i\) are large. With derivative bounds

\[
|f_i'|\le Q^C,
\]

this construction is possible if the components have width at least \(Q^{-C-C_\Gamma}\).

Hence positive measure plus finite derivative bounds still allows a bad set with no useful interval of uniform smallness.

So the following implication is false without more structure:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\Rightarrow
\exists J,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C'}|I|,\ 
\sup_J(|f_1|+|f_2|)\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

---

## 3. Does \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) help?

It helps only at a local scale.

If

\[
|u(x_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

then

\[
|u|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_u}
\]

on an interval of radius

\[
\rho_u\asymp Q^{-C_u-C_1}.
\]

Likewise, if

\[
|f_i(x_0)|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\]

and

\[
|f_i'|\le Q^{C_2},
\]

then

\[
|f_i|\le 2Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\]

on an interval of radius

\[
\rho_f\asymp Q^{-C_\Gamma-C_2}.
\]

Thus each point of \(E\) generates a small interval of approximate base-locus. But this radius may be much smaller than what is needed for interval rigidity and derivative propagation, and it does not produce relative density at larger scales.

---

## 4. Sufficient extra hypotheses

The following hypotheses would be enough.

### A. Relative density

There exist

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|
\]

such that every subinterval \(J\subset I\) with \(|J|\ge \ell\) satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|E\cap J|\ge \rho |J|.
}
\]

Then a Remez/Bernstein theorem can plausibly propagate smallness of \(f_1,f_2\) to a controlled interval.

### B. Bounded component count

If

\[
E
\]

has at most \(Q^C\) connected components, then one component has length at least

\[
Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

That component is already an interval of approximate base-locus.

### C. Cartan exceptional-set structure

If the complement of the approximate base-locus is covered by a controlled Cartan family of disks/intervals, then total measure lower bounds may force a nonexceptional interval.

### D. Low effective Remez complexity

If \(f_1,f_2\) belong to a class with effective Remez degree \(N=O(1)\), then total measure is enough:

\[
\sup_I|f_i|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N \sup_E|f_i|.
\]

With

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

and \(N=O(1)\), this gives polynomial loss. If \(N\asymp R\), the loss becomes

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too large unless the initial smallness is much stronger.

---

## 5. Can derivative bounds give component control?

A finite derivative bound

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

does not automatically bound the number of components of a level set by \(Q^{O(1)}\) unless one also has a lower separation principle for zeros of the relevant functions or a stronger analytic-complexity class.

For arbitrary \(C^6\)-bounded functions, many oscillations are possible at polynomial scales. To get component control, one would need one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-count control for }f_1,f_2,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{analytic continuation with bounded growth and Cartan estimates,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{ODE structure forcing low oscillation.}
}
\]

The ODE structure may help, but it is not yet formulated strongly enough to imply component bounds.

---

## 6. Clean density theorem needed

### Gate 2 Density Propagation Theorem

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume the extracted bad set

\[
E=\{|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},\ |f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_f}\}
\]

satisfies

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

Assume, in addition, one of:

1. \(E\) is relatively dense at scale \(\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|\);
2. \(E\) has at most \(Q^C\) connected components;
3. \(f_1,f_2\) satisfy a low-complexity Remez/Cartan theorem with polynomial loss.

Then there exists an interval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_J},
\]

and \(u\) remains non-small on \(J\) or on a controlled subset of \(J\).

This is the input needed before applying derivative propagation and interval rigidity.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Relative density does not follow from global measure alone.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative bounds give local neighborhoods, not global density.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need component-count, Cartan, or low-complexity Remez input.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 propagation remains conditional.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s reduced input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

as the precise bridge from the extracted bad set to an interval approximate base-locus.

Agent 1 / A report: final attempt on Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[

\text{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation is not proved from current assumptions.}
}
\]

The correct final status is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

should be carried as a named downstream input, unless a new low-complexity/Cartan theorem for \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) is proved.

The obstruction is precise: Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives a set \(E\) of polynomial measure where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A},
\]

but \(E\) can be dust-like. Positive measure and finite \(C^6\)-type derivative bounds do not force interval-scale smallness.

---

## 1. Desired theorem

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

The desired propagation theorem is:

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E
\]

imply that there is an interval

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\sup_J|f_1|+\sup_J|f_2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

This is what is needed to invoke derivative propagation and approximate interval rigidity.

---

## 2. Why current assumptions do not prove it

The current extraction gives only global measure:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

A positive-measure set can be a union of many tiny components:

\[
E=\bigcup_{\nu=1}^{N}[x_\nu,x_\nu+\delta_\nu],
\qquad
\sum_\nu\delta_\nu\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

No interval \(J\) of polynomial length need be contained in \(E\), and \(E\) need not be relatively dense on any useful scale.

Finite derivative bounds of the form

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

only imply local persistence near each point of \(E\). If

\[
|f_i(x_0)|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{and}\quad
|f_i'|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

then \(f_i\) remains small only on a radius roughly

\[
Q^{-A-C_1}.
\]

That does not force a macroscopic or even fixed polynomial-scale interval unless the distribution of \(E\) is controlled.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{positive measure + finite derivative bounds does not imply interval approximate base-locus.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Needed additional hypothesis

One of the following would close the step.

### A. Relative density

There exist

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|
\]

such that every subinterval \(J\subset I\) with \(|J|\ge\ell\) satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|E\cap J|\ge \rho |J|.
}
\]

Then Remez/Bernstein propagation can be applied on \(J\)-scale intervals.

### B. Bounded component count

If

\[
E
\]

has at most \(Q^C\) connected components, then some component has length at least

\[
Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

That component gives interval smallness directly.

### C. Low-complexity Remez/Cartan

If \(f_1,f_2\) satisfy a Remez inequality with effective degree \(N=O(1)\),

\[
\sup_I|f_i|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N
\sup_E|f_i|,
\]

then total measure suffices with polynomial loss.

If instead \(N\asymp R\), the loss becomes

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too expensive unless the initial smallness is much stronger than polynomial.

### D. Cartan exceptional-set control

If the bad complement has a controlled Cartan covering, then positive measure may force an interval avoiding the exceptional set.

This is a complex-analytic substitute for bounded component count.

---

## 4. Final named input

### Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
f_1=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume additionally a relative-density, bounded-component, low-Remez-degree, or Cartan-type hypothesis sufficient to prevent dust-like \(E\).

Then there exists

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Together with Gate 2 Derivative Propagation and approximate interval rigidity, this yields Gate 2.

---

## 5. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Set extraction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Positive measure alone: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[

\text{Finite }C^6\text{ bounds alone: insufficient unless tied to a stronger complexity theorem.}
}
\]

\[

\text{Needed input: relative density / bounded component count / low-complexity Remez / Cartan control.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s final answer is:

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:18:42)

_Thought for 5s_

Agent 1 / A report: D1 relative-density / Cartan extraction. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 is not proved from the current hypotheses. It should be named as a downstream input.}
}
\]

Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives a polynomial-measure set

\[
E\subset I
\]

where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

But this does **not** imply relative density, interval smallness, or bounded component count. Finite \(C^6\)-type derivative bounds give local persistence around points of \(E\), but they do not prevent a dust-like set with many separated components.

Thus the precise missing input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}.
}
\]

---

## 1. Starting point

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

From Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure, we have

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\]

on \(E\).

The desired conclusion is that there is an interval

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\sup_J |f_1|+\sup_J|f_2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

This does not follow from the stated data alone.

---

## 2. Global measure does not imply relative density

A set can satisfy

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|
\]

but fail every useful scale-wise density condition.

For example, take \(I=[0,1]\) and let

\[
E=\bigcup_{\nu=1}^{N}[x_\nu,x_\nu+\delta],
\]

with

\[
N\delta=Q^{-C_E}.
\]

By choosing the intervals widely separated and \(\delta\) very small, \(E\) has polynomial measure but no interval \(I_0\) on which every subinterval \(J\subset I_0\) of polynomial length satisfies

\[
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C}|J|.
\]

This is compatible with finite derivative bounds as long as transition regions around \(E\) are not thinner than the derivative scale.

Therefore the desired relative-density conclusion is false by measure theory alone.

---

## 3. Does \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) help?

Only locally.

If

\[
|u(x_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

then

\[
|u|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_u}
\]

on a radius

\[
\rho_u\asymp Q^{-C_u-C_1}.
\]

Similarly, if

\[
|f_i(x_0)|\le Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
|f_i'|\le Q^{C_2},
\]

then

\[
|f_i|\le 2Q^{-A}
\]

only on a radius

\[
\rho_f\asymp Q^{-A-C_2}.
\]

So derivative bounds thicken each point of \(E\) into a small interval. They do not force relative density or a large base-locus interval unless one also bounds the number of components or controls the distribution of those intervals.

---

## 4. Component-count route

A sufficient condition is:

\[
\#\pi_0(E)\le Q^{C_{\rm comp}}.
\]

Then some connected component of \(E\) has length at least

\[
\frac{|E|}{Q^{C_{\rm comp}}}\ge Q^{-C_E-C_{\rm comp}}|I|.
\]

This immediately yields an interval of approximate base-locus.

But current hypotheses do not provide

\[
\#\pi_0(E)\le Q^C.
\]

To get this, one would need zero-count or oscillation-count bounds for level sets of

\[
u,\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Finite \(C^6\)-bounds alone do not provide a sufficiently strong component-count theorem.

---

## 5. Cartan / low-complexity Remez route

A different sufficient condition is a Remez-type theorem for the class containing \(f_1,f_2\):

\[
\sup_I |f_i|
\le
\mathcal R(E,I)\sup_E |f_i|.
\]

For polynomial degree \(N\),

\[
\mathcal R(E,I)
\sim
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N.
\]

Since

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

this becomes

\[
\mathcal R(E,I)\le Q^{C_E N}.
\]

If

\[
N=O(1),
\]

the loss is polynomial and usable. If

\[
N\asymp R,
\]

then

\[
Q^{C_E R}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too large for a polynomial lower-bound architecture unless the smallness on \(E\) is made correspondingly stronger.

Thus a Remez/Cartan route needs one of:

\[
\boxed{N=O(1),}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{initial smallness stronger than polynomial,}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{a sharper Cartan theorem adapted to the ODE structure}.}
\]

Current inputs do not establish such a low-complexity theorem.

---

## 6. Weakest sufficient hypotheses for D1

Any one of the following would be enough.

### A. Relative-density hypothesis

There exist

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|
\]

such that every subinterval \(J\subset I\) with \(|J|\ge\ell\) obeys

\[
|E\cap J|\ge \rho |J|.
\]

### B. Bounded component count

\[
\#\pi_0(E)\le Q^{C_{\rm comp}}.
\]

### C. Zero-count / oscillation-count control

A bound of the form

\[
N_{\rm zeros}(f_1)+N_{\rm zeros}(f_2)\le Q^C
\]

or an analogous bound for threshold crossings.

### D. Low effective Remez degree

\[
\sup_I |f_i|
\le Q^C\sup_E|f_i|
\]

for \(i=1,2\).

### E. Cartan exceptional-set control

A complex-analytic statement saying the set where \(f_1,f_2\) are small cannot have polynomial measure without containing a controlled interval or forcing global smallness.

---

## 7. Final named theorem

### Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
f_1=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume additionally a relative-density, bounded-component, low-Remez-degree, or Cartan-type hypothesis sufficient to rule out dust-like \(E\).

Then there exists

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is D1.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Set extraction: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Relative density from global measure: false.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite derivative bounds alone: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need relative density, component control, low Remez degree, or Cartan control.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s output is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 remains a named input: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation.}
}

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:21:17)

_Thought for 7s_

Agent 1 / A report: final D1 theorem statement and no-go boundary. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 is a named downstream input, not currently proved.}
}
\]

The final form is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation.}
}
\]

It must upgrade a polynomial-measure approximate base-locus set

\[
E\subset I
\]

into an interval where

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are uniformly small. This does not follow from positive measure plus finite \(C^6\)-type derivative bounds. It requires one of: low effective Remez degree, relative density, Cartan/doubling control, bounded component count, or an equivalent structural theorem for \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\).

---

## 1. Final D1 theorem

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume set extraction has produced

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Then D1 should assert:

\[
\boxed{
\exists J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
}
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This implication is not valid from measure alone. The theorem must include an additional propagation hypothesis.

---

## 2. Acceptable additional hypotheses

Any of the following would be sufficient in principle.

### A. Low effective Remez degree

There is a Remez inequality for \(f_i\) with effective degree \(N=O(1)\):

\[
\sup_I |f_i|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N
\sup_E |f_i|.
\]

Since

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

this gives

\[
\sup_I |f_i|\le Q^{O(1)}\sup_E|f_i|.
\]

Choosing the initial smallness exponent \(A\) large enough gives interval smallness.

### B. Relative density plus low Remez degree

If there exist

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|I|
\]

such that every interval \(J\subset I\) with \(|J|\ge\ell\) satisfies

\[
|E\cap J|\ge\rho|J|,
\]

then Remez/Bernstein propagation can be localized.

### C. Cartan exceptional-set control

A complex-analytic statement of the form:

The set where

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\]

has controlled Cartan geometry, so if it has polynomial measure, it contains an interval-like component or forces global smallness.

### D. Bounded component count

If

\[
\#\pi_0(E)\le Q^{C_{\rm comp}},
\]

then some component has length

\[
\ge Q^{-C_E-C_{\rm comp}}|I|.
\]

That component gives the desired interval.

### E. Bounded doubling index

If \(f_1,f_2\) have polynomially bounded doubling index on \(I^\ast\), then smallness on a polynomial-measure set can be promoted with polynomial loss.

---

## 3. Dust-like countermodel with finite derivative bounds

The following model shows why finite \(C^6\)-type bounds alone are insufficient.

Let \(I=[0,1]\). Let

\[
E=\bigcup_{\nu=1}^{N}[x_\nu,x_\nu+\delta],
\]

with

\[
N\delta=Q^{-C_E}.
\]

Choose \(\delta=Q^{-M}\) and \(N=Q^{M-C_E}\), with \(M\) large but finite. Arrange the intervals to be separated.

Define smooth functions \(f_1,f_2\) such that

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\]

on \(E\), but \(f_1\) or \(f_2\) rises to size \(1\) between components. If the transition width is

\[
w\ge Q^{-C_{\rm der}},
\]

then derivatives through order \(6\) can be bounded by powers of \(Q\):

\[
\|f_i^{(k)}\|_\infty\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6.
\]

Thus \(E\) can have polynomial measure and the functions can be small on \(E\), while no polynomial-scale interval exists on which the functions are uniformly small.

This demonstrates:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite }C^6\text{ bounds alone do not prove D1.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Why generic \(N\asymp R\) Remez is too expensive

A Remez bound with degree \(N\) gives a loss roughly

\[
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N.
\]

Since

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

the loss is

\[
Q^{C_E N}.
\]

If

\[
N=O(1),
\]

this is polynomial and acceptable.

If

\[
N\asymp R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then the loss is

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(
\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}
\right)
\right).
\]

That is super-polynomial in \(Q\). It is incompatible with the fixed-polynomial lower-bound architecture unless the initial smallness on \(E\) is made super-polynomially strong, which Gate 2 failure does not naturally provide.

Thus D1 needs genuinely low effective complexity or a stronger density/Cartan mechanism.

---

## 5. Is low complexity plausible for \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\)?

The functions

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are finite-order differential-polynomial expressions in \(q\), but that does not automatically imply low Remez degree.

They may inherit high oscillatory complexity from the actual zeta phase. The finite-order algebraic form controls derivative order, not the number of oscillations or the doubling index.

So the statement

\[
N=O(1)
\]

is a real additional theorem. It might follow from a special ODE or ECT/Chebyshev structure, but no such structure has been established.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{low effective Remez complexity remains an open input.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Final named D1 input

### Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},\qquad
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad
f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Suppose

\[
E\subset I,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume, in addition, a propagation mechanism: low effective Remez degree, relative density, Cartan control, bounded component count, or bounded doubling index.

Then there exists

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is D1.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 proof from current assumptions: no.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dust-like countermodels survive finite }C^6\text{ bounds.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Generic }R\text{-degree Remez loss is too expensive.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 requires low-complexity/density/Cartan/doubling input.}
}
\]

So Agent 1’s final status is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation is a named downstream input.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:34:36)

_Thought for 7s_

Agent 1 / A report: final handoff for the ordinary Gate 1 stack. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3 + canonical transfer imply ordinary Gate 1.}
}
\]

The ordinary route is now a clean conditional theorem. It is not a proof of Gate 1, because O1–O3 are named open arithmetic inputs. But the internal implication chain is stable:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\text{finite-jet anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

The remaining work in this ordinary branch is no longer local Wronskian algebra; it is proving the named actual-zeta inputs.

---

## 1. Ordinary inputs

### O1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

At an admissible ordinary zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

O1 gives

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_1}.
}
\]

Here

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; numerically supported.}}
\]

---

### O2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

At the same zero,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]

Here \(\mathbf M\) is the cofactor vector of the canonical source-jet block built from

\[
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; reducible to zero-set spectral large sieve / pointwise cofactor nonrecurrence.}}
\]

---

### O3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment

O3 gives

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'|\,|\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Equivalent geometric form:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf z',
\operatorname{span}\{q''_{\can}\text{-jet rows}\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; final ordinary actual-orbit incidence theorem.}}
\]

---

## 2. O1–O3 imply Wronskian lower bound

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the normalized Wronskian expands as

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
}
\]

By O3,

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|
\ge
Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

By O1 and O2,

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge
Q^{-(A_1+A_2+A_3)}
=
Q^{-A_W}.
}
\]

This is the ordinary Wronskian anti-degeneracy conclusion.

---

## 3. Wronskian lower bound implies finite-jet anti-design

Let

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3 q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x),
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The Wronskian rows use

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad
0\le j\le R.
\]

If the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet were source-flat through depth \(R\), then the source rows would fall into the finite-design locus:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\le Q^{-B_{\rm jet}}\lambda^3.
\]

Under the row/basis conditioning package

\[
\|C_\ell(\mathcal D)\|,\ \|C_\ell^{-1}\|
\le \exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]

and finite derivative-complexity control, this would force

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\le Q^{-A_W-1},
\]

after choosing \(B_{\rm jet}\) sufficiently large.

This contradicts

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A_W}.
\]

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-B_{\rm jet}}\lambda^3.
}
\]

This is the ordinary finite-jet anti-design statement.

---

## 4. Finite-jet anti-design implies energy Gate 1

Ordinary Gate 1 is

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

In normalized variables,

\[
I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X,
\]

and

\[
q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x)=\lambda^{-3}F_\lambda(x).
\]

So

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
=
\lambda^{-5}\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

The normalized Gate 1 form is

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^6 |X|.
}
\]

Contrapositive:

If

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda|^2<Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|,
\]

then, using the analytic-complexity package

\[
\sup_{X^\ast}|\partial_x^kF_\lambda|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le R+1,
\]

local Sobolev/Cauchy/Remez propagation gives finite-jet flattening:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\le Q^{-B'}\lambda^3
\]

on a shrunken interval, after choosing \(B\) large relative to \(B'\) and the complexity constants.

This contradicts finite-jet anti-design.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |F_\lambda|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

---

## 5. Hidden assumptions and guardrails

### Canonical source

The proof must use

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
}
\]

It must not use a zero-side proxy, \(B_2\)-only diagnostic, prime-only toy, or truncated AFE model unless a transfer theorem is supplied.

---

### \(B_2\)

The finalized background term is

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(
\frac14+\frac{it}{2}
\right).
\]

This belongs in the canonical object. It is not a Gate 1 blocker by itself.

---

### \(E_2\) and tail transfer

Need derivative control sufficient for all rows and cofactors. The expected safe depth is

\[
\boxed{
k\le 2R+1
}
\]

in normalized derivatives for determinant/cofactor transfer, plus whatever is needed by the finite-jet-to-energy analytic package.

A typical sufficient condition is

\[
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-A_E},
\]

with \(A_E\) large compared with determinant Lipschitz losses.

---

### Basis conditioning

Need

\[
\|C_\ell(\mathcal D)\|,\ \|C_\ell(\mathcal D)^{-1}\|
\le \exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

This is why the safe depth remains

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

---

### Ordinary-scale regime

This proof covers

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

It does not cover deep singular packets

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

nor the mild transition unless a transition theorem \(T1\) is supplied.

---

### \(Z_\alpha\)-zero admissibility

The point \(m_0\) must be the admissible ordinary zero/center where the Wronskian expansion is valid:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

The chosen \(\alpha\), packet, and normalized derivative convention must match the row construction.

---

## 6. Final theorem

### Ordinary Gate 1 conditional theorem

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Assume canonicality, basis conditioning, analytic-complexity, and \(E_2\)/tail transfer.

Assume O1–O3:

\[
\text{Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence},
\]

\[
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence},
\]

\[
\text{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3 + canonical transfer}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## 7. Status table

| Ingredient | Status |
|---|---|
| Wronskian identity \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\) | structural |
| O1 Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence | named open input; numerically supported |
| O2 Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence | named open input |
| O3 Wronskian Angle Nonalignment | named open input |

| Wronskian lower bound \(\Rightarrow\) finite-jet anti-design | conditional on row/basis/canonical transfer |
| finite-jet anti-design \(\Rightarrow\) ordinary Gate 1 | conditional on analytic-complexity package |
| canonical \(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) | required guardrail |
| \(E_2\) transfer through derivative depth | open/technical |
| ordinary/singular transition | separate input |

Final classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary Gate 1 is conditionally reduced to O1--O3 plus canonical analytic transfer.}
}

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:39:33)

_Thought for 5s_

Agent 1 / A report: D1 low-complexity Remez / Cartan mechanism. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No D1 proof found. D1 remains a named input.}
}
\]

The obstruction is stable: \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) are finite-order differential-polynomial expressions in \(q\), but that does **not** imply low effective Remez degree, bounded doubling index, bounded component count, or Cartan control. Without one of those additional structures, a polynomial-measure set of smallness can remain dust-like and fail to yield interval smallness.

So the final D1 status is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

as an open downstream input.

---

## 1. Function class of \(F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\)

We have

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Thus \(\Gamma_G\) is a differential-polynomial in \(q\) through order \(2\), and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) uses \(q\) through order \(4\).

This gives a **finite-order algebraic structure**, but not by itself a low-complexity oscillation structure. In particular, from

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

one obtains finite derivative bounds for \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), but not a bound on the number of zero crossings or the doubling index of \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\).

---

## 2. No established low-dimensional ODE / ECT structure

A low-complexity Remez theorem would follow if \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) lay in a finite-dimensional Chebyshev or ECT system of dimension \(O(1)\), or satisfied a low-order linear ODE with controlled coefficients and nonoscillatory behavior.

The identities currently available are nonlinear:

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

These relate \(q\), \(q'\), \(q''\), and \(\Gamma_G''\), but they do not impose a closed low-dimensional linear system for \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\). They also do not rule out many oscillations of \(q\) or of the differential-polynomial expressions.

Therefore I do not see a valid route to

\[
N_{\rm Remez}=O(1)
\]

from the present identities alone.

---

## 3. Remez loss calculation

Assume a Remez-type estimate of the form

\[
\sup_I |F|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N
\sup_E |F|.
\]

From set extraction,

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

So the loss is

\[
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^N
\le Q^{C_E N+O(N)}.
\]

If

\[
N=O(1),
\]

this loss is polynomial and can be absorbed by taking the Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) larger.

If

\[
N\asymp R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then the loss is

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is super-polynomial in \(Q\), so it is not compatible with the fixed-polynomial lower-bound architecture unless the extracted smallness is super-polynomially strong. Gate 2 failure only naturally gives polynomial smallness after exponent choices.

Thus a generic high-degree Remez theorem is not enough.

---

## 4. Cartan / doubling alternative

A complex-analytic Cartan estimate could replace Remez if one can show that the set where

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\]

is small has controlled exceptional geometry.

A usable statement would be:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,\quad |F|\le Q^{-A}\text{ on }E
\]

implies either

\[
F
\]

is globally small on a controlled subinterval, or \(E\) lies in a Cartan exceptional set of small total measure.

But such a theorem requires a bound on the doubling index or zero count of \(F\). Finite \(C^6\)-type bounds do not provide that. A holomorphic tube bound plus growth control might, but the needed doubling estimate is not currently established.

So Cartan is a possible proof route, but it is not available from the present hypotheses.

---

## 5. Dust-like no-go boundary

Finite derivative bounds allow the following pattern.

Let \(E\) be a union of many small intervals whose total measure is \(Q^{-C}|I|\). Let \(F\) be very small on \(E\), but transition to \(O(1)\) between components over polynomially small transition layers. This can be arranged while preserving finite derivative bounds through order \(6\), provided the component widths and transition widths are chosen polynomially small enough.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
+
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},\ 0\le k\le6
}
\]

does not imply

\[
\boxed{
\exists J,\quad \sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is the precise no-go boundary.

---

## 6. Final named D1 input

### Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

Assume set extraction gives

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|F|\le Q^{-A}\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume in addition one of:

\[
\boxed{\text{low effective Remez degree }N=O(1),}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{bounded doubling index,}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Cartan exceptional-set control,}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{bounded component / zero-count control,}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{relative density at polynomial scale.}}
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is the exact D1 theorem needed before D2 and interval rigidity.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-order differential-polynomial structure: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite }C^6\text{ derivative bounds: insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Generic }N\asymp R\text{ Remez loss: too expensive.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 requires low-complexity / Cartan / doubling / density input.}
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 remains a named downstream open input.}
}
\]
