## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:49:04)

_Thought for 8s_

Agent 1 / A report: D1 targeted attack — low-complexity mechanism. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No low-complexity mechanism is currently available for }F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
}
\]

The identities

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

show that \(F\) is a finite-order differential-polynomial expression in \(q\). But finite differential order is not the same as low oscillatory complexity. In particular, it does not imply:

\[
N_{\rm eff}=O(1)
\]

for Remez, nor bounded zero count, nor bounded doubling index, nor an ECT/Chebyshev property.

So D1 remains a named input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}.
}
\]

---

# 1. Function class of \(F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\)

Let

\[
u=q''.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Expanding \(\Gamma_G''\),

\[
\Gamma_G''
=
q^{(4)}-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q''.
\]

Therefore

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2
-\frac16 q^{(4)}
+q''
-2q(q')^2
-q^2q''
\]

so the \(2q(q')^2\) terms cancel in this expanded convention, giving

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac16 q^{(4)}+(1-q^2)q''.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac16q^{(4)}+(1-q^2)u
}
\]

under the stated normalization.

This is useful: it shows \(F\) is a finite-order nonlinear differential expression in \(q\) through order \(4\). But it still does not impose low Remez complexity.

---

# 2. No closed low-order ODE for \(F\)

A low-complexity proof would need something like:

\[
F' = A(m)F
\]

or a finite-dimensional linear system

\[
\partial_m^kF+\sum_{j<k}a_j(m)\partial_m^jF=0
\]

with controlled coefficients and small \(k=O(1)\), or an ECT/Chebyshev structure bounding zeros.

The current identities do not give that.

They express \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) in terms of \(q\), \(q''\), and \(q^{(4)}\). They do not close the dynamics of \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\). Higher derivatives of \(F\) introduce higher derivatives of \(q\), and the system does not terminate without additional zeta-specific ODE structure.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite differential order } \not\Rightarrow \text{ finite-dimensional closed dynamics}.
}
\]

---

# 3. No ECT/Chebyshev property from current identities

An ECT/Chebyshev route would require that the relevant function family has uniformly bounded sign changes or that any nontrivial linear combination has controlled zeros.

But \(q\) is an actual zeta-derived phase/source function and can be highly oscillatory. The nonlinear forms

\[
q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
-\frac16q^{(4)}+(1-q^2)q''
\]

do not obviously form an ECT system. There is no monotonicity, positivity, sign-regularity, or variation-diminishing structure visible from these expressions.

Therefore no Chebyshev-style bounded-zero theorem follows.

---

# 4. Bounded zero-count / doubling index is not implied

A Cartan or doubling route would require a bound such as:

\[
N_F(I)\le Q^C
\]

for zeros or near-zeros of \(F\), or a doubling estimate

\[
\sup_{2J}|F|\le Q^C\sup_J|F|.
\]

Finite \(C^6\)-type bounds

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6,
\]

do not imply such a bound. One can construct \(C^6\)-bounded functions with many small oscillatory wells, at polynomially small scale, unless an independent oscillation-count or analytic-growth estimate is imposed.

Thus the key missing input is not derivative order; it is complexity control.

---

# 5. Remez loss if \(N_{\rm eff}\asymp R\)

A generic Remez inequality has the form

\[
\sup_I |F|
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^{N_{\rm eff}}
\sup_E |F|.
\]

From set extraction,

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|.
\]

Thus

\[
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^{N_{\rm eff}}
\le
Q^{O(N_{\rm eff})}.
\]

If

\[
N_{\rm eff}=O(1),
\]

the loss is polynomial and acceptable.

But if

\[
N_{\rm eff}\asymp R
\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then the loss is

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(
O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is super-polynomial and too large for the current fixed-polynomial Gate 2 architecture.

Therefore the D1 mechanism must prove genuinely low effective complexity, not merely finite \(R\)-scale complexity.

---

# 6. Sharp no-go boundary

The following implication is not justified:

\[
|F|\le Q^{-A}\text{ on }E,\quad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\quad
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},\ 0\le k\le6
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\exists J\subset I:\ \sup_J|F|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

A dust-like countermodel remains possible: \(F\) can be small on many polynomially thin components whose total measure is polynomial, while becoming large between them, without violating finite \(C^6\)-bounds.

To rule this out one needs at least one of:

\[
\boxed{\text{bounded component count}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{bounded zero count}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{bounded doubling index}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Cartan exceptional-set control}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{relative density at controlled scale}},
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{low effective Remez degree}}.
\]

None is currently proved from the identities for \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\).

---

# 7. Final D1 theorem statement

### Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

Assume Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure has produced

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and

\[
|F|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume additionally one of the following propagation structures:

1. \(F\) has low effective Remez degree \(N_{\rm eff}=O(1)\);
2. \(F\) has bounded doubling index \(Q^{O(1)}\);
3. the small-value set of \(F\) has Cartan exceptional-set control;
4. the bad set \(E\) has relative density at polynomial scale;
5. the level-set components of \(F\) are bounded by \(Q^{O(1)}\).

Then there exists

\[
J\subset I,\qquad |J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is the needed D1 input for Gate 2.

---

## Final classification

\boxed{
\text{No D1 proof candidate from current identities.}
}
\]

\boxed{
\text{Differential-polynomial structure alone is insufficient.}
}

\boxed{
\text{Finite }C^6\text{ bounds alone are insufficient.}
}

\boxed{
\text{Generic }N\asymp R\text{ Remez loss is too expensive.}

}

The key observation I’ll exploit is that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) simplifies after expanding \(\Gamma_G''\). That gives a more rigid pair:
\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=-\frac16q^{(4)}+(1-q^2)q''.
\]
This still may not close D1, but it gives a sharper attack surface than treating the two functions as generic.

There is a possible way to turn D1 from a named input into a conditional theorem: use **normalized packet bandwidth**, not only \(C^6\) bounds. In ordinary scale, AFE phases satisfy \(\lambda\log n=O(1)\), so the normalized local functions may have bounded exponential type.

_Thought for 2m 42s_

Agent 1 / A report: targeted D1 attack via packet-bandlimited Remez. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 may be provable if the canonical local packet satisfies a normalized bandlimited/Bernstein package.}
}
\]

This is the strongest new attack I see. The earlier no-go applies to generic \(C^6\)-bounded functions, but \(q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) are not generic if, after packet normalization, they are built from AFE phases with bounded normalized frequency

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n=O(1).
\]

Under that stronger packet-bandlimited hypothesis, a Remez/Logvinenko–Sereda type estimate gives polynomial loss, not \(Q^{O(R)}\), and D1 can be proved. Moreover, the same package gives D2 by Bernstein/Cauchy derivative control.

So the theorem to attack is now sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Packet-Bernstein/Remez Propagation}
\Rightarrow
\textbf{D1 + D2}.
}
\]

The remaining question is whether the full canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

satisfies that packet-bandlimited package with acceptable tail/error transfer.

---

# 1. Normalized packet formulation

Let

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda},
\qquad
q_\lambda(x)=q(m_0+\lambda x).
\]

In ordinary scale,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

For AFE packet frequencies,

\[
e^{-im\log n}
=
e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-ix\lambda\log n}.
\]

On the canonical main AFE range,

\[
\log n\lesssim Q,
\]

so

\[
\lambda\log n=O(1).
\]

Thus the normalized packet functions should have bounded exponential type, provided the tails and \(E_2\) are controlled.

This is the key distinction from the earlier \(C^6\)-only no-go.

---

# 2. Packet-Bernstein hypothesis

Assume on a normalized interval \(X\) of \(O(1)\)-length that

\[
q_\lambda=q_{\rm bl}+e,
\]

where \(q_{\rm bl}\) is entire or strip-holomorphic of exponential type

\[
\sigma\le C_0
\]

in the normalized variable \(x\), with

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(X)}|q_{\rm bl}|\le Q^{C_q},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}
\]

or, in the strongest form, on a fixed strip.

Assume the error satisfies, through the needed derivative order,

\[
\max_{0\le k\le 6}
\sup_X |\partial_x^k e|
\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

also decompose as

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,{\rm bl}}+e_G,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\Gamma_{G,2,{\rm bl}}+e_{G2},
\]

with exponential type

\[
\sigma_G,\sigma_{G2}\le C\sigma=O(1),
\]

because products of type-\(\sigma\) functions have type at most the sum of the types, and derivatives do not increase type.

So \(F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) has **effective Remez degree \(O(1)\)** under this packet-Bernstein package.

---

# 3. Remez theorem for bounded type

Use the following standard form.

### Packet Remez theorem

Let \(f\) be an entire or strip-holomorphic function of exponential type \(\sigma\), bounded by \(Q^C\) on the relevant tube. Let \(E\subset X\) with

\[
|E|\ge \delta |X|.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_X |f|
\le
\left(\frac{C}{\delta}\right)^{C(1+\sigma |X|)}
\sup_E |f|
+
\text{tube/tail error}.
}
\]

In our ordinary normalized packet,

\[
\sigma |X|=O(1),
\]

and

\[
\delta\ge Q^{-C_E}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\sup_X |f|\le Q^{C_R}\sup_E |f|+\text{error}
}
\]

with \(C_R=O(1)\), not \(O(R)\).

Apply this to

\[
f=\Gamma_G
\]

and

\[
f=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_X|\Gamma_G|+\sup_X|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A+C_R}+Q^{-A_e'}.
}
\]

Choosing \(A\) and \(A_e\) large gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_X|\Gamma_G|+\sup_X|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

This is exactly D1.

---

# 4. D2 follows by Bernstein/Cauchy

For entire functions of exponential type \(\sigma=O(1)\), Bernstein gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_X |\partial_x^2 f|
\le C\sigma^2\sup_X|f|
}
\]

after a harmless shrink of the interval, or with a polynomial tube-radius loss if only strip control is available.

Thus from

\[
\sup_X|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{X'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

This supplies the derivative control needed for approximate interval base-locus rigidity.

Therefore, under packet-bandlimited control,

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 and D2 merge into one propagation theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Gate 2 proof under Packet-Bernstein/Remez

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_X |u|^2\,dx\ge Q^{-B}|X|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_X |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dx
\le Q^{-A}|X|.
\]

Set extraction gives

\[
E\subset X,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|X|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Packet Remez gives

\[
\sup_X|\Gamma_G|+\sup_X|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma'}.
\]

Packet Bernstein gives

\[
\sup_{X'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma''}.
\]

Approximate interval base-locus rigidity gives

\[
\sup_{X''}|u|\le Q^{-C_u'}
\]

for \(C_u'\) arbitrarily large after choosing the original exponents large enough.

This contradicts the Gate 1 mass lower bound.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-Bernstein/Remez package}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 6. Why this avoids the previous no-go

The earlier obstruction was:

\[
N_{\rm eff}\asymp R
\Rightarrow
\text{Remez loss }Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right).
\]

The packet-bandlimited attack replaces that with

\[
N_{\rm eff}\asymp 1+\sigma |X|=O(1).
\]

Then the loss is only

\[
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So the dust-like set no-go for arbitrary \(C^6\)-bounded functions is still valid, but it does not apply if the function class has bounded exponential type in normalized packet coordinates.

---

# 7. Main caveat: canonical validity

This proof is only as good as the packet-bandlimited package for the **canonical** functions.

One must prove that the full canonical components satisfy it:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Required checks:

### Main/dual AFE support

Need normalized frequencies

\[
\lambda\log n=O(1)
\]

for all retained main and folded-dual packet terms.

### Background \(B_2\)

\(B_2\) is smooth/slowly varying on packet scale, hence compatible with bounded type or low-degree Taylor control.

### Tail and \(E_2\)

Need

\[
\max_{k\le 6}\sup_X|\partial_x^kE_2|\le Q^{-A_e}
\]

or an equivalent exponentially/super-polynomially small tail bound.

### Nonlinear closure

Need to verify that forming

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

does not amplify the residual error beyond \(Q^{-A}\). This requires polynomial bounds on \(q\) and its first six derivatives.

---

# 8. Final theorem candidate

### Packet-Bernstein Gate 2 Propagation Theorem

Let \(X\) be a normalized ordinary packet interval with

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Assume:

1. **Packet-bandlimited canonical representation**

   \[
   q=q_{\rm bl}+e
   \]

   with \(q_{\rm bl}\) of exponential type \(\sigma=O(1)\) in \(x\), and

   \[
   \max_{k\le6}\|\partial_x^ke\|_{L^\infty(X)}\le Q^{-A_e}.
   \]

2. **Polynomial amplitude bounds**

   \[
   \max_{k\le6}\|\partial_x^kq\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

3. **Gate 1**

   \[
   \int_X|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|X|.
   \]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_X |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dx
\ge Q^{-A}|X|.
}
\]

The proof is by contradiction:

\[
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{small }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ on polynomial-measure }E
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{Remez smallness on }X
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{ small by Bernstein}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
u\text{ small by interval rigidity}
\]

\[
\Rightarrow
\text{contradicts Gate 1.}
\]

---

# 9. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{New proof route found: packet-bandlimited Remez.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 is provable if normalized canonical packets have bounded exponential type.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D2 follows from the same package by Bernstein/Cauchy.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main remaining task: prove canonical packet-bandlimited/tail-transfer package.}
}
\]

So I would replace the old D1/D2 split with a sharper target:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet-Bernstein/Remez Package}
}
\]

and then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical Packet-Bernstein/Remez Package}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:57:08)

I need to correct the most optimistic part of the previous attack: “bounded exponential type” alone is not automatically enough for a positive-measure Remez theorem. For Paley–Wiener-type classes, relative density or a finite-term/finite-dimensional structure is usually the decisive condition.

_Thought for 35s_

## Continued Agent 1 / A attack: D1 via packet Bernstein/Remez, corrected

I need to refine the previous route. The promising idea was:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
x_n=\lambda\log n=O(1),
\]

so locally the canonical packet should behave like a bounded-frequency object in normalized \(x\)-coordinates. If true in a strong enough sense, D1 follows.

But the naive claim

\[
\text{bounded exponential type alone}
\Rightarrow
\text{positive-measure Remez with polynomial loss}
\]

is too optimistic unless the precise Remez/Cartan class is controlled. For general bandlimited or exponential-type functions, **relative density** or an appropriate **Nazarov/Cartan/Remez theorem with growth control** is needed. Plain \(C^6\)-bounds are still insufficient.

So the refined attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove a canonical packet Bernstein--Remez theorem for }
F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
}
\]

If that theorem holds, D1 and D2 both follow.

---

# 1. Normalized packet representation

Let

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

A retained AFE term has phase

\[
e^{-im\log n}
=
e^{-im_0\log n}
e^{-ix\lambda\log n}.
\]

On ordinary packet-frequency support,

\[
\log n\lesssim Q,
\]

so

\[
\lambda\log n=O(1).
\]

Thus a model packet has the form

\[
q_{\rm model}(x)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal N}
a_n(x)e^{-i\omega_n x}
+
\sum_{n\in\mathcal N^-}
b_n(x)e^{+i\omega_n^-x}
+
B_{\rm sm}(x),
\]

with

\[
|\omega_n|,\ |\omega_n^-|\le \sigma_0=O(1),
\]

and slowly varying amplitudes

\[
\partial_x^k a_n,\ \partial_x^k b_n,\ \partial_x^kB_{\rm sm}
\]

polynomially bounded, ideally negligible for \(k\le6\).

If the amplitudes are frozen over \(x=O(1)\), this is a bounded-frequency exponential sum. Products and derivatives then preserve bounded type:

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

has type \(\le3\sigma_0\), and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

has type \(\le3\sigma_0\) as well.

So the key candidate package is:

\[
\boxed{
F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\text{ lies in a bounded-type, polynomial-growth class in }x.
}
\]

---

# 2. The exact propagation theorem needed

A usable theorem is:

### Canonical packet Remez theorem

Let \(f\) be a canonical packet function on a normalized interval \(X\), with bounded packet type

\[
\sigma X=O(1),
\]

and polynomial growth in a complex strip or Bernstein space:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(X)}|f|\le Q^C,
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

If

\[
E\subset X,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|X|,
\]

and

\[
|f|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{X'}|f|\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(X'\subset X\), after choosing \(A\) sufficiently large.

For D1, we need this for

\[
f=\Gamma_G
\]

and

\[
f=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This is stronger and more precise than “finite \(C^6\)-bounds.” It is a genuine packet Remez/Cartan theorem.

---

# 3. Why finite-term Turán is not enough

A finite exponential-sum Turán lemma often has loss depending on the number of terms:

\[
\sup_X |f|
\le
\left(\frac{C|X|}{|E|}\right)^{N-1}
\sup_E|f|.
\]

Here \(N\) may be the number of AFE terms, which is enormous. That loss is useless.

So the proof must not depend on the raw number of frequencies. It must depend on **bandwidth / type**, not cardinality.

That means the needed theorem is closer to a Paley–Wiener / Logvinenko–Sereda / Cartan-style estimate than a finite-term Turán estimate.

---

# 4. Positive measure versus relative density

There is still a subtlety.

Many bandlimited uncertainty theorems require **relative density**, not merely positive measure. D1 gives only

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

So the packet Remez theorem must be of a type that handles arbitrary measurable \(E\) of positive measure, with loss depending on \(|E|\), or else D1 still needs a relative-density input.

The required theorem is therefore one of:

### Option A: arbitrary-measure packet Remez

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\Rightarrow
\sup_{I}|f|\le Q^C\sup_E|f|
\]

for bounded-type canonical packets.

### Option B: relative-density extraction plus Logvinenko–Sereda

First prove \(E\) is relatively dense at some polynomial scale from zeta/canonical structure; then apply a thick-set theorem.

### Option C: Cartan exceptional-set geometry

Show the small-value set of \(F\) cannot have polynomial measure in dust form unless \(F\) is globally small.

Among these, Option A is the cleanest but strongest. Option C may be more realistic for holomorphic packet functions.

---

# 5. D2 follows if the packet theorem gives complex or Bernstein control

Suppose D1 gives

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

D2 asks for

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

If D1 output is only real-axis \(C^0\)-smallness, this does not follow.

But if the packet theorem gives either:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad \rho\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then Cauchy gives

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
\rho^{-2}Q^{-A}
\le
Q^{-A+2C}.
\]

Or, if the class satisfies a Bernstein inequality,

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
C\sigma^2\sup_J|\Gamma_G|
\]

with \(\sigma=O(1)\), then

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Thus D1 and D2 can merge into:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet Bernstein--Remez Propagation}.
}
\]

This is better than treating D1 and D2 separately.

---

# 6. Gate 2 theorem under packet Bernstein–Remez

Assume the following package.

### Packet Bernstein–Remez package

For

\[
F=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

if

\[
|F|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E\subset I,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

then there exists \(J\subset I\), \(|J|\ge Q^{-C'}|I|\), such that

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A'}
\]

with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Then:

1. Cauchy/Bernstein gives

   \[
   \sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A''}.
   \]

2. Approximate interval rigidity gives

   \[
   \sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-A'''}.
   \]

3. But Gate 1 + set extraction retained nontrivial \(u\)-mass on the bad set. With the propagation interval chosen from that set, this contradicts

   \[
   |u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
   \]

   on a controlled subset.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet Bernstein--Remez package}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. What must now be proved

The attack reduces D1/D2 to four concrete canonical analytic checks.

## Check 1: bounded normalized frequency

Show the canonical packet representation for \(q\), \(u\), \(\Gamma_G\), and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) uses only normalized frequencies

\[
|\lambda\log n|\le C
\]

after tails are controlled.

## Check 2: amplitude variation

Show the AFE/gamma/cutoff amplitudes are either:

\[
\text{slowly varying with polynomial derivative bounds}
\]

or absorbable into the same Bernstein/Remez class.

## Check 3: nonlinear closure

Show products and derivatives used to form

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

preserve the packet Bernstein/Remez class with only polynomial losses.

## Check 4: canonical tail transfer

Show

\[
q_{\can}-q_{\rm packet}
\]

and its derivatives through \(k\le6\) are small enough:

\[
\max_{k\le6}\|\partial_x^k(q_{\can}-q_{\rm packet})\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

This includes \(B_2\), main/dual AFE, and \(E_2\).

---

# 8. Remaining obstruction

The main unresolved mathematical point is whether there exists a Remez/Cartan inequality for the canonical packet class with loss depending on bandwidth/type rather than number of AFE terms.

If yes, D1/D2 become provable.

If no, D1 remains a named input.

So the next exact theorem should be:

### Canonical Packet Bernstein–Remez Theorem

Let \(f\) be any function generated from the ordinary canonical packet class by finitely many derivatives and products up to the operations defining \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\). Suppose

\[
|f|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E\subset I,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then there exists a subinterval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|f|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

with \(\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}\).

This theorem would close both D1 and D2.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Generic finite }C^6\text{ control is insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{But ordinary packet frequency localization may provide the missing low complexity.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1/D2 reduce to a Canonical Packet Bernstein--Remez theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{This is now the sharpest attack target for Gate 2.}
}
\]

I would now replace separate D1 and D2 by the single sharper input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet Bernstein--Remez Propagation}
}
\]

and try to prove it directly for the ordinary canonical packet class.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:02:37)

The attack can be sharpened: instead of a vague “Remez” claim, use a **spectral inequality for bandlimited functions on an interval**. If the canonical packet really lies in a Paley–Wiener-type class of normalized bandwidth \(O(1)\), then arbitrary positive-measure \(E\) is enough; relative density is not needed locally.

_Thought for 26s_

## Continued Agent 1 / A attack: D1/D2 via local spectral inequalities

The previous “packet-bandlimited Remez” route can be made sharper. The right tool is not generic Remez for finite sums. It is a **local spectral inequality for bandlimited functions**:

\[
\|f\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
\left(\frac{C|I|}{|E|}\right)^{C(1+\sigma |I|)}
\|f\|_{L^2(E)}
\]

for functions with Fourier support in \([-\sigma,\sigma]\), on an interval \(I\), with measurable \(E\subset I\).

This is exactly the kind of result that avoids the earlier \(Q^{O(R)}\) loss. If the normalized canonical packet has bandwidth

\[
\sigma |I|=O(1),
\]

then

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

only costs

\[
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So D1 and D2 can be proved from a sharper input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Local Bandlimit Package}
}
\]

for

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This is now the best attack target.

---

# 1. Local spectral inequality

Let \(I\subset\mathbb R\) be an interval, \(E\subset I\), and

\[
|E|\ge \delta |I|.
\]

Let \(f\) be bandlimited:

\[
\operatorname{supp}\widehat f\subset[-\sigma,\sigma].
\]

Then a local Logvinenko–Sereda / Nazarov-type spectral inequality gives

\[
\boxed{
\|f\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
\left(\frac{C}{\delta}\right)^{C(1+\sigma |I|)}
\|f\|_{L^2(E)}.
}
\]

If

\[
\sigma |I|=O(1)
\]

and

\[
\delta\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\|f\|_{L^2(I)}\le Q^{C'}\|f\|_{L^2(E)}.
}
\]

This works for arbitrary measurable \(E\), not only relatively dense \(E\), because the interval \(I\) is bounded. Relative density is needed for global whole-line control, but a local interval spectral inequality can use only \(|E|/|I|\).

This is the key improvement.

---

# 2. Apply to D1

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, we already have

\[
E\subset I,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Assume

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are locally bandlimited in normalized coordinates, with bandwidth

\[
\sigma=O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(E)}+\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(E)}
\le
Q^{-A}|E|^{1/2}.
\]

The spectral inequality gives

\[
\|\Gamma_G\|_{L^2(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}\|_{L^2(I)}
\le
Q^{-A+C}|I|^{1/2}.
\]

For a bandlimited function,

\[
\|f\|_{L^\infty(I')}
\le
C_\sigma |I|^{-1/2}\|f\|_{L^2(I)}
\]

on a slightly shrunken interval \(I'\subset I\). Hence

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I'}|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_{I'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le
Q^{-A'}
}
\]

after choosing \(A\) large.

This proves D1 under local bandlimitedness.

---

# 3. D2 follows from Bernstein

For bandlimited \(f\),

\[
\operatorname{supp}\widehat f\subset[-\sigma,\sigma],
\]

Bernstein gives

\[
\|f^{(k)}\|_{L^\infty}
\le
\sigma^k\|f\|_{L^\infty}.
\]

Taking

\[
f=\Gamma_G,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I''}|\Gamma_G''|
\le
C\sigma^2 \sup_{I'}|\Gamma_G|
\le
Q^{-A''}.
}
\]

Thus D2 follows automatically.

So the combined statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local bandlimit for }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\Rightarrow
\text{D1 + D2}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Check local bandlimit for the ordinary packet

In normalized coordinates

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

a main AFE term has phase

\[
e^{-im\log n}
=
e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-ix\lambda\log n}.
\]

For ordinary packet-frequency support,

\[
\log n\lesssim Q.
\]

Thus

\[
|\lambda\log n|\lesssim 1.
\]

The folded dual branch has the same property after folding.

So the model packet

\[
q_{\rm packet}(x)
=
\sum_n a_n e^{-i\omega_nx}
+
\sum_n b_n e^{+i\omega_n^-x}
+
B_{\rm sm}(x)
\]

has

\[
|\omega_n|,\ |\omega_n^-|\le \sigma_0=O(1).
\]

If amplitudes are frozen or sufficiently slowly varying, then \(q_{\rm packet}\) is bandlimited to bounded frequency up to controlled error.

Then:

\[
q',
q'',
q^{(4)}
\]

are still bandlimited with the same bandwidth, and nonlinear products satisfy bandwidth addition:

\[
q^3:\quad \sigma\le3\sigma_0,
\]

\[
q^2q'':\quad \sigma\le3\sigma_0.
\]

Using the simplified identity

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac16q^{(4)}+(1-q^2)q'',
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ have normalized bandwidth }O(1)
}
\]

for the model packet.

This is precisely what D1 needs.

---

# 5. The canonical obstruction

The proof is not complete until this model statement is transferred to the full canonical object:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The needed canonical package is:

### Canonical Local Bandlimit Package

On each ordinary packet interval, write

\[
q=q_{\rm bl}+e,
\]

where

\[
q_{\rm bl}
\]

is a bounded-bandwidth normalized packet function, and

\[
e
\]

satisfies

\[
\max_{0\le k\le6}
\|\partial_x^ke\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

In addition,

\[
q_{\rm bl},\Gamma_{G,{\rm bl}},\Gamma_{G,2,{\rm bl}}
\]

must satisfy polynomial amplitude bounds.

Then the spectral inequality applies to the bandlimited part, and the error \(e\) is absorbed.

This package is now the exact theorem to prove.

---

# 6. Why this is plausible

The ordinary packet regime is exactly the regime where normalized frequencies are bounded:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

So, unlike the generic \(C^6\) setting, the actual canonical packet has a reason to be low-complexity in the normalized coordinate.

This avoids the dust-set counterexample. The counterexample uses arbitrary \(C^6\) oscillatory bumps; it is not bandlimited to \(\sigma=O(1)\).

For a genuinely bandlimited function, a polynomial-measure small set does force global smallness on a bounded interval with polynomial loss.

---

# 7. What must be verified

The remaining technical checks are precise.

## Check A: AFE truncation

Show all retained main and folded-dual terms satisfy

\[
|\lambda\log n|\le C.
\]

Terms with larger normalized frequency must be included in the error and shown derivative-small through order \(6\).

## Check B: amplitude variation

AFE weights, gamma factors, conductors, and cutoffs depend on \(m\). Need to show their \(x\)-derivatives through order \(6\) are polynomially bounded and do not introduce high normalized frequencies.

A slowly varying amplitude times a bandlimited phase is not strictly bandlimited. One can either:

1. absorb amplitude derivatives into an “almost-bandlimited” spectral inequality; or  
2. approximate amplitudes by low-degree Taylor polynomials on \(I\), producing a finite sum of derivatives of bandlimited functions.

The latter should be acceptable if the degree is \(O(1)\).

## Check C: nonlinear closure

Need to show that forming

\[
q^3,\qquad q^2q'',
\qquad q^{(4)}
\]

preserves the bandlimit class up to bounded bandwidth and polynomial coefficient growth.

## Check D: canonical error

Need

\[
\max_{0\le k\le6}
\|\partial_x^k(q_{\can}-q_{\rm bl})\|_\infty
\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

This is the main tail-transfer estimate.

---

# 8. Combined theorem

### Canonical Packet Bandlimit Propagation Theorem

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

On a normalized packet interval \(I\), suppose

\[
q=q_{\rm bl}+e,
\]

where \(q_{\rm bl}\) is built from normalized frequencies

\[
|\omega|\le\sigma_0=O(1)
\]

with controlled slowly varying amplitudes, and

\[
\max_{k\le6}\|\partial_x^ke\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

Then, if

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

there exists a shrunken interval \(I'\subset I\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I'}|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_{I'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|
+
\sup_{I'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Therefore, by approximate interval rigidity,

\[
u\approx0
\]

on \(I'\).

Combined with the Gate 1 lower bound, this proves Gate 2.

---

# 9. Updated status

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1/D2 can be attacked through local spectral inequalities.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The key is not generic Remez, but packet bandlimitedness.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The main remaining task is canonical local bandlimit/tail transfer.}
}
\]

So the old split:

\[
D1=\text{Density/Remez},\qquad D2=\text{Derivative Propagation}
\]

can be replaced by a sharper single target:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet Bandlimit Propagation}
}
\]

and the implication is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical Packet Bandlimit Propagation}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Read. This is the most useful update in several rounds: the downstream layer has sharpened in two directions. 

## Gate 2 update

The best new route is no longer generic D1/D2. It is:

[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Source Oscillation / Component-Count Bound}
}
]

for:

[
u=q''_{\can}.
]

Target:

[
#\pi_0{|u|\ge Q^{-C}}\le Q^C.
]

If this holds, then Gate 1 gives a mass-bearing component of ({|u|\ge Q^{-C}}). Gate 2 failure then forces (\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}) to be small on most of that component. Gap-density / finite-difference interpolation gives (\Gamma_G'')-smallness, and interval rigidity forces (u\approx0), contradicting the component’s (u)-mass.

So D1/D2 can be replaced by a sharper target:

[
\boxed{
\text{Source oscillation bound}
+
\text{weighted gap-density extraction}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
]

This looks more concrete than the earlier generic Remez/Cartan formulation, especially if (u) is effectively bandlimited in ordinary normalized coordinates.

## (q_0)-wall update

The most concrete new D3 route is **wall escape**, not necessarily finding a row that survives exactly at (q_0=0).

If:

[
q_0(m_0)\approx0,\qquad u(m_0)=q_0''(m_0)\not\approx0,
]

then Taylor expansion implies (q_0) becomes polynomially nonzero at a nearby point, provided (q_0''') and (u') are controlled. Then D4 can apply at that nearby non-wall point.

New target:

[
\boxed{
\textbf{(q_0)-Wall Escape Sampling Theorem}
}
]

[
q_0\approx0,\ u\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\text{ nearby}: |q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C},
\ |u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C},
\ \text{Gate 2 mass still live}.
]

This may be easier than finding a source-robust row, assuming downstream row conversion only needs a row lower bound somewhere in the packet interval, not exactly at the original sampled point.

## Row algebra update

D3/D4 can also be unified as a finite algebra problem:

[
\boxed{
\textbf{(q_0)-Adic Row-Pencil Nonvanishing}
}
]

or, more sharply, an ideal-generation statement at the wall.

At (q_0=0),

[
\Gamma_G\equiv u,
]

and:

[
\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv u-\frac16u''.
]

Let:

[
\eta=u-\frac16u'',\qquad W=(u,\eta).
]

The wall Gate 2 condition becomes:

[
|u|^2|W|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
]

The desired finite algebra certificate is:

[
(u,\eta)^N\subset (R_1,\ldots,R_s)\bmod(q_0),
]

with polynomially bounded coefficients. If true, the wall branch closes. If false for projected/raw/ambient/correction rows, D3 really needs a new invariant.

Do **not** run another broad strategy round. The next useful agent round should be targeted at one of these concrete tasks:

1. Prove the **Gate 2 source oscillation/component-count bound** for (u=q''_{\can}).
2. Prove the **wall-escape sampling theorem** and check whether nearby sampling is admissible.
3. Execute the **(q_0)-adic row residue / ideal-generation audit** for (A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}).
4. Formalize D4 as the **matrix-leading theorem**:
   [
   \mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,\qquad
   \sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
   ]

The strongest near-term path appears to be:

[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2: source oscillation bound}
\quad+\quad
\text{wall: escape sampling or row-pencil audit}.
}

Agent 1 / A report: Gate 2 source oscillation / component-count theorem. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{A source component-count theorem is plausible under a canonical packet-Cartwright/bandlimit package.}
}
\]

The target is:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

This does **not** follow from finite \(C^6\)-bounds alone. It can be attacked if, in ordinary normalized coordinates, \(u\) belongs to a bounded-exponential-type / Cartwright / Paley–Wiener-like class with polynomial growth and controlled canonical tails.

So the sharp theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet-Cartwright Source Oscillation Bound}
\Rightarrow
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is stronger and more concrete than the older generic D1 Remez formulation.

---

# 1. Normalized ordinary coordinate

Work in ordinary scale:

\[
m=m_0+\lambda t,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

An AFE phase satisfies

\[
e^{-im\log n}
=
e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-it\lambda\log n}.
\]

On ordinary packet-frequency support,

\[
\log n\lesssim Q,
\]

so normalized frequencies satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\xi_n=\lambda\log n=O(1).
}
\]

Thus the retained main and folded-dual packets are low-frequency in \(t\).

---

# 2. Candidate canonical packet class

Write

\[
u(t)=q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda t).
\]

The useful package is:

\[
\boxed{
u=u_{\rm pkt}+e,
}
\]

where \(u_{\rm pkt}\) is a real-valued Cartwright / Paley–Wiener type function in \(t\) with exponential type

\[
\sigma=O(1),
\]

and polynomial growth

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|u_{\rm pkt}|\le Q^C
\]

on a normalized complex tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I),
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The error should satisfy at least

\[
\max_{k\le 6}\|\partial_t^k e\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

For the source oscillation bound itself, a stronger holomorphic/tube tail bound is better than merely \(C^6\).

---

# 3. Component-count theorem under packet-Cartwright control

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Consider

\[
U_\tau=\{t\in I:|u(t)|\ge \tau\}.
\]

If \(u\) is real-valued, each component of \(U_\tau\) has boundary points where

\[
u(t)=\tau
\quad\text{or}\quad
u(t)=-\tau.
\]

Equivalently, boundary points are zeros of

\[
F_\tau(t)=u(t)^2-\tau^2.
\]

If \(u\) has exponential type \(O(1)\), then \(F_\tau\) has exponential type \(O(1)\). A Cartwright/Jensen zero-count bound for \(F_\tau\) gives

\[
N_I(F_\tau)
\le
C\bigl(1+\sigma |I|+\log(M_\tau/m_\tau)\bigr),
\]

where

\[
M_\tau=\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|F_\tau|
\]

and \(m_\tau\) is a non-tiny reference size, for example a maximum on a slightly smaller interval or an \(L^2\)-normalized quantity.

Under polynomial growth and a dyadic choice of \(\tau\) avoiding pathological plateau levels, this gives

\[
N_I(F_\tau)\le Q^C.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0(U_\tau)\le N_I(F_\tau)+1\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the desired source component-count theorem.

---

# 4. Plateau caveat and dyadic threshold choice

There is one technical caveat. If

\[
F_\tau=u^2-\tau^2
\]

is tiny throughout \(I\), then Jensen cannot use a good lower reference value. But in that case

\[
|u|\approx\tau
\]

on most of \(I\), so \(U_\tau\) is not highly oscillatory at that threshold. To avoid threshold pathologies, choose \(\tau\) dyadically.

From Gate 1,

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Pick

\[
\tau\in\{Q^{-C_0},2Q^{-C_0},4Q^{-C_0},\ldots\}
\]

so that the level \(\tau\) is not a prolonged plateau level and \(U_\tau\) still carries polynomial \(u\)-mass. A standard layer-cake/dyadic argument should provide such a \(\tau\).

Thus the theorem should be stated for a chosen noncritical dyadic threshold:

\[
\boxed{
\exists \tau=Q^{-C_\tau}\text{ with }U_\tau\text{ mass-bearing and }\#\pi_0(U_\tau)\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 5. Canonical components

The key canonical question is whether

\[
u=q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

satisfies the packet-Cartwright package.

## \(P_2,D_2\)

The main and folded-dual packet terms are built from phases with

\[
|\lambda\log n|=O(1)
\]

on ordinary support. These are compatible with type \(O(1)\).

## \(B_2\)

The background

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
\]

is smooth and slowly varying on packet scale. It should be treated as a low-frequency or low-degree analytic term, hence compatible with the same Cartwright package.

## \(E_2\)

The error/tail must be controlled in a complex tube or at least through enough derivatives. For component counting, tube control is preferable:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|E_2|\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

If only real \(C^6\)-control is available, that is not enough for Cartwright zero counting.

So the main missing canonical input is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary canonical packet admits a tube-controlled bounded-type approximation.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Component bound implies a route to Gate 2

Assume

\[
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge \tau\}\le Q^C
\]

for a mass-bearing threshold \(\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}\).

Let

\[
U_\tau=\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

By Gate 1 and dyadic thresholding, choose \(\tau\) such that

\[
\int_{U_\tau}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

If \(U_\tau\) has at most \(Q^C\) components, some component \(J_0\) satisfies

\[
\int_{J_0}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

Since \(|u|\ge\tau\) on \(J_0\), this gives

\[
|J_0|\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

If Gate 2 fails, then on most of this same component,

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\]

is small. Because \(J_0\) is an interval, finite-difference or interpolation stencils can be chosen inside it to propagate smallness to interval control. Then approximate interval rigidity applies.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source component count}
+
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}.
}
\]

This is exactly the missing D1 mechanism.

---

# 7. What is proved and what remains

## Proved/reduced

Under canonical packet-Cartwright control:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C
}
\]

is a plausible theorem via zero-count bounds for

\[
u^2-\tau^2.
\]

This would give the component needed for Gate 2 propagation.

## Still open

The canonical packet-Cartwright package itself:

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}
\text{ has bounded normalized type and polynomial tube growth on ordinary packets.}
}
\]

This is stronger than finite \(C^6\)-control and must be proved from the canonical AFE/tail decomposition.

---

# 8. Final theorem candidate

### Gate 2 Source Oscillation Bound

Assume ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Suppose on each normalized ordinary packet interval \(I\), the canonical source

\[
u=q''_{\can}
\]

has a decomposition

\[
u=u_{\rm pkt}+e
\]

where \(u_{\rm pkt}\) is real-valued of exponential type \(O(1)\), has polynomial tube growth, and \(e\) is \(Q^{-A}\)-small in the same tube.

Then for every polynomial threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

outside a finite exceptional dyadic set,

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{t\in I:|u(t)|\ge\tau\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Consequently, Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure yields an interval approximate base-locus, and together with derivative propagation and interval rigidity proves Gate 2.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Component-count theorem is plausible under packet-Cartwright control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite }C^6\text{ bounds alone remain insufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main missing input: canonical packet tube/bandlimit control for }u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

So the sharp new target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet-Cartwright Source Oscillation Bound}
}
\]

which would replace the older abstract D1 density/Remez input and materially advance Gate 2.

_Thought for 16s_

Agent 1 / A continued attack: source oscillation / component-count route. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The source component-count route is viable if }u=q''_{\can}
\text{ has a local Cartwright/Paley--Wiener representation with polynomial growth.}
}
\]

The key theorem is no longer a vague Remez statement. It can be made as a concrete zero-count/component-count lemma:

\[
\boxed{
u \text{ of exponential type }O(1)
\quad+\quad
\|u\|_{\infty,\text{tube}}\le Q^C
\quad+\quad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\Rightarrow
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge\tau\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

More sharply, under good Cartwright bounds the number of threshold components should be only \(O(\log Q)\) or \(Q^{o(1)}\), but \(Q^C\) is all Gate 2 needs.

So the target becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet-Cartwright Source Oscillation Bound}.
}
\]

If this is proved for \(u=q''_{\can}\), then Gate 2 has a plausible path:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{component count}
+
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{mass-bearing interval approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
u\approx0,
\]

contradiction.

---

## 1. Component count from threshold zeros

Let

\[
U_\tau=\{t\in I:|u(t)|\ge\tau\},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

If \(u\) is real-valued on \(I\), then every bounded component of \(U_\tau\) has boundary points where

\[
u(t)=\tau
\quad\text{or}\quad
u(t)=-\tau.
\]

Equivalently, boundary points are zeros of

\[
F_\tau(t)=u(t)^2-\tau^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\#\pi_0(U_\tau)
\le
1+N_I(F_\tau),
\]

where \(N_I(F_\tau)\) is the number of real zeros of \(F_\tau\) in \(I\).

Thus it suffices to bound real zeros of

\[
u^2-\tau^2.
\]

---

## 2. Cartwright/Jensen zero count

Assume \(u\) extends holomorphically to a complex tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I)=\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,I)\le\rho\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

and satisfies exponential-type / tube growth

\[
|u(z)|\le Q^{C_u}e^{\sigma|\Im z|},
\qquad
\sigma=O(1).
\]

Then

\[
F_\tau(z)=u(z)^2-\tau^2
\]

has type \(O(1)\) and growth

\[
|F_\tau(z)|\le Q^{C_F}.
\]

If \(F_\tau\) is not identically tiny, Jensen/Cartan gives a zero-count estimate of the form

\[
N_I(F_\tau)
\le
C\left(1+\sigma |I|+\log\frac{M}{m}\right),
\]

where

\[
M=\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|F_\tau|,
\]

and \(m\) is a nonzero reference value, such as \(\sup_{I'}|F_\tau|\) on a smaller interval.

With

\[
M\le Q^{C_F},
\qquad
m\ge Q^{-C_m},
\]

one gets

\[
N_I(F_\tau)\le Q^C.
\]

In fact the natural estimate is closer to

\[
N_I(F_\tau)\ll \log Q
\]

when \(\sigma |I|=O(1)\), but \(Q^C\) is enough.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

## 3. Handling bad threshold levels

There is a nuisance case where

\[
u^2-\tau^2
\]

is very small on a large part of \(I\), so the reference lower bound \(m\) is weak.

This can be handled by choosing \(\tau\) dyadically. From Gate 1,

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

By layer cake, there exists a dyadic threshold

\[
\tau=2^jQ^{-C_0}
\]

such that:

1. \(U_\tau=\{|u|\ge\tau\}\) carries polynomial \(u\)-mass:

   \[
   \int_{U_\tau}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|;
   \]

2. \(\tau\) is not an exceptional plateau threshold for \(u\).

For such a noncritical dyadic \(\tau\), \(u^2-\tau^2\) has a usable reference lower bound, and the zero-count argument applies.

So the component theorem should be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\exists \tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\text{ carrying polynomial }u\text{-mass such that }
\#\pi_0(U_\tau)\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is exactly what Gate 2 propagation needs.

---

## 4. Component count implies Gate 2 interval extraction

Assume Gate 1 and choose \(\tau\) as above. Then

\[
\int_{U_\tau}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

If

\[
\#\pi_0(U_\tau)\le Q^C,
\]

then some connected component \(J_0\subset U_\tau\) satisfies

\[
\int_{J_0}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

Since

\[
|u|\ge\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\quad\text{on }J_0,
\]

this gives

\[
|J_0|\ge Q^{-C''}|I|.
\]

If Gate 2 fails, then

\[
\int_{J_0}|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\]

is small for at least one such mass-bearing component after pigeonholing. Since \(|u|\ge\tau\) on \(J_0\), it follows that

\[
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\]

is small on most of \(J_0\).

Now \(J_0\) is an actual interval, not a dust set. This is the improvement over the earlier D1 setting. On \(J_0\), one can use finite-difference, interpolation, or local spectral inequalities to upgrade high-measure smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) to interval smallness.

Then D2 / derivative propagation supplies \(\Gamma_G''\)-smallness, and approximate interval rigidity gives \(u\approx0\) on a shrunken subinterval, contradicting \(|u|\ge\tau\) on \(J_0\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source component count}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2 propagation}.
}
\]

---

## 5. Canonical packet-Cartwright package needed

The real remaining work is proving the component-count hypothesis for the canonical source

\[
u=q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The needed package is:

### Canonical Packet-Cartwright Package

On an ordinary normalized packet interval

\[
m=m_0+\lambda t,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

write

\[
u(t)=u_{\rm pkt}(t)+e(t),
\]

where:

1. \(u_{\rm pkt}\) is holomorphic in a tube \(\mathcal T_\rho(I)\), \(\rho\ge Q^{-C}\);

2. \(u_{\rm pkt}\) has exponential type

   \[
   \sigma=O(1)
   \]

   in the normalized variable \(t\);

3. \(u_{\rm pkt}\) has polynomial tube growth

   \[
   \sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|u_{\rm pkt}|\le Q^C;
   \]

4. the canonical error satisfies

   \[
   \sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I)}|e|\le Q^{-A_e}
   \]

   or at least real derivative control strong enough not to create extra threshold components.

If this holds, then

\[
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C.
\]

---

## 6. Why ordinary packets plausibly satisfy this

For the main AFE terms,

\[
e^{-im\log n}
=
e^{-im_0\log n}e^{-it\lambda\log n}.
\]

On ordinary support,

\[
\log n\lesssim Q,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so

\[
|\lambda\log n|\lesssim1.
\]

Thus the oscillatory packet is of normalized type \(O(1)\). Folded dual terms behave similarly.

The background \(B_2\) is smooth/slowly varying on packet scale, and should have very low local type.

The only delicate part is canonical tail/error control:

\[
E_2
\]

and any AFE truncation residual must not introduce high-frequency threshold oscillations of size comparable to \(\tau\).

So the decisive canonical task is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{control high normalized frequencies in }u=q''_{\can}
\text{ below the polynomial threshold }Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

## 7. Potential obstruction: long tails

If the canonical \(E_2\) or regularized tail contains non-negligible contributions with

\[
\lambda\log n\gg1,
\]

then the component-count theorem may fail: high-frequency tails could create many threshold components even if their \(L^2\) mass is small.

Therefore the transfer must be in a norm that controls threshold topology, not only energy.

A safe condition is

\[
\|E_2\|_{C^1(I)}\le Q^{-A_e}
\]

with \(A_e\) large relative to the threshold \(\tau\), or stronger tube-smallness.

If only

\[
\|E_2\|_{L^2}
\]

is small, that is not enough to preserve component count.

---

## 8. Refined theorem

### Gate 2 Source Oscillation Theorem

Assume ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Assume the canonical source has a packet-Cartwright decomposition

\[
u=u_{\rm pkt}+e
\]

with normalized type \(O(1)\), polynomial tube growth, and

\[
\|e\|_{C^1(I)}\le Q^{-A_e}.
\]

Then there exists a dyadic threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

such that:

1. \(U_\tau=\{|u|\ge\tau\}\) carries polynomial source mass:

   \[
   \int_{U_\tau}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|;
   \]

2. \(U_\tau\) has polynomially many components:

   \[
   \boxed{
   \#\pi_0(U_\tau)\le Q^C.
   }
   \]

Consequently, Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure produces a mass-bearing interval approximate base-locus. With derivative propagation and interval rigidity, Gate 2 follows.

---

## 9. What to attack next

The next concrete proof task is no longer generic D1. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet-Cartwright Decomposition for }u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Specifically:

1. prove normalized type \(O(1)\) for the retained main+dual packet source;
2. prove polynomial tube growth;
3. prove high-frequency tail \(C^1\) or tube-smallness below the selected threshold;
4. show \(B_2\) is harmless;
5. verify the same decomposition survives the exact canonical regularization.

If that is done, the component-count theorem follows, and Gate 2 becomes substantially closer.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{New route: source component count via Cartwright threshold zeros.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{This avoids the dust-set obstruction by controlling components of }|u|\ge\tau.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main missing input: canonical packet-Cartwright/tail-topology control.}
}
\]

So the sharpened Gate 2 target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Packet-Cartwright Source Oscillation Bound}
}
\]

rather than the older generic D1 Remez propagation.

_Thought for 29s_

Agent 1 / A report: Gate 2 two-threshold interval extraction. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The two-threshold extraction step is provable under polynomial Lipschitz bounds.}
}
\]

Precisely, Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives a point where \(u\) is polynomially non-small and the anisotropy factor is polynomially small. Polynomial Lipschitz bounds then thicken that point into a polynomial-length interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

on which

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

So the old dust-set obstruction can be bypassed **if** we use pointwise Lipschitz thickening rather than trying to extract relative density from the whole bad set.

The required analytic input is now much simpler:

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\qquad
\|\Gamma_G'\|_\infty+\|\Gamma_{G,2}'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

This is a finite-complexity/Lipschitz package, weaker than full Remez/Cartan propagation.

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
F_{\rm aniso}
=
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume the polynomial Lipschitz bounds

\[
|u'(m)|\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G'(m)|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'(m)|
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Since

\[
|F_{\rm aniso}(x)-F_{\rm aniso}(y)|
\le
|\Gamma_G(x)-\Gamma_G(y)|
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}(x)-\Gamma_{G,2}(y)|,
\]

this gives

\[
|F_{\rm aniso}'|\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}
\]

in the Lipschitz sense.

---

# 2. Source threshold

Set

\[
M=Q^{-B}.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=\frac14 Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Then

\[
(2\tau)^2=\frac14 Q^{-B}.
\]

Let

\[
H=\{m\in I:|u(m)|\ge 2\tau\}.
\]

On the complement \(I\setminus H\),

\[
|u|^2<4\tau^2=\frac14Q^{-B}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{I\setminus H}|u|^2\,dm
\le
\frac14Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

By Gate 1,

\[
\int_H|u|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac34 Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

So the high-source set carries polynomial \(u\)-mass.

---

# 3. Small anisotropy point

By Gate 2 failure,

\[
\int_H |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Hence the weighted average of \(F_{\rm aniso}^2\) on \(H\) obeys

\[
\frac{
\int_H |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
}{
\int_H |u|^2\,dm
}
\le
\frac{Q^{-A}|I|}{\frac34Q^{-B}|I|}
\le
C Q^{-A+B}.
\]

Thus there exists

\[
m_\ast\in H
\]

such that

\[
F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

At the same point,

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge 2\tau
=
\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

So we have found a point with

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-B/2-O(1)}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G(m_\ast)|+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{-(A-B)/2+O(1)}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Lipschitz thickening to an interval

Define

\[
r_u
=
c\,Q^{-B/2-C_u}|I|,
\]

and

\[
r_F
=
c\,Q^{-(A-B)/2-C_F}|I|,
\]

with \(c>0\) sufficiently small.

Let

\[
r=\min(r_u,r_F).
\]

Take a one-sided or two-sided interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

containing \(m_\ast\) with

\[
|J|\ge r.
\]

If \(m_\ast\) is within \(r\) of the boundary of \(I\), choose the available one-sided interval. This only changes constants.

For \(m\in J\),

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}|m-m_\ast|
\le
c Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Choosing \(c\) small,

\[
|u(m)|\ge \tau\ge Q^{-B/2-O(1)}.
\]

Similarly,

\[
|F_{\rm aniso}(m)-F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}|m-m_\ast|
\le
c Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

So

\[
F_{\rm aniso}(m)
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

Thus on \(J\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A_1},
}
\]

with

\[
C_1=B/2+O(1),
\]

and

\[
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F).
\]

The interval length satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge
Q^{-C_J}|I|,
}
\]

where

\[
C_J=
\max\left(B/2+C_u,\ (A-B)/2+C_F\right)+O(1).
\]

This is polynomial length for fixed exponents.

---

# 5. Choice of exponents

If the integral-rigidity lemma requires

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_{\rm rig}},
\]

then choose the Gate 2 failure exponent \(A\) so that

\[
\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)\ge A_{\rm rig}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
A\ge B+2A_{\rm rig}+O(C_F).
\]

Then the extraction gives the required anisotropy smallness on the interval \(J\).

The price is that the interval length shrinks polynomially:

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|.
\]

That is acceptable for the local rigidity argument as long as the derivative and correction estimates are valid on polynomial subintervals.

---

# 6. Boundary cases

If \(m_\ast\) lies near the boundary of \(I\), choose one of

\[
[m_\ast,m_\ast+r]\cap I,
\qquad
[m_\ast-r,m_\ast]\cap I
\]

with length at least \(r/2\). The same estimates hold.

If the downstream interval-rigidity lemma requires a centered interval with room to shrink, first work inside a slightly shrunken interval

\[
I^{\circ}\subset I
\]

and use a boundary-layer estimate. If all high-source mass lies in the boundary layer, one may choose a one-sided rigidity version or enlarge the parent packet. This is a technical boundary issue, not a conceptual obstruction.

---

# 7. Theorem statement

### Two-threshold interval extraction theorem

Assume:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

and polynomial Lipschitz bounds

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|\Gamma_G'\|_\infty+\|\Gamma_{G,2}'\|_\infty
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then there exists an interval \(J\subset I\) satisfying

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

Here one may take

\[
C_1=B/2+O(1),
\]

\[
A_1=(A-B)/2-O(C_F),
\]

and

\[
C_J=
\max(B/2+C_u,\ (A-B)/2+C_F)+O(1).
\]

---

# 8. Consequence for Gate 2

This theorem replaces the older, more difficult D1 density/Remez problem.

The Gate 2 proof now needs:

1. two-threshold extraction, proved above under Lipschitz bounds;
2. the integral-rigidity lemma on \(J\):

   \[
   \sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le \varepsilon
   \Rightarrow
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|;
   \]

3. contradiction with

   \[
   |u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
   \quad\text{on }J'.
   \]

So the new Gate 2 route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure + polynomial Lipschitz}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}.
}
\]

This avoids dust-set and Remez/Cartan issues entirely.

---

# 9. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Two-threshold extraction: proved under polynomial Lipschitz bounds.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No generic Remez or relative-density input is needed for this step.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining Gate 2 task: prove the integral-rigidity lemma.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 1’s output is the extraction theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\exists J:
|u|\ge Q^{-C},\quad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\text{ on }J.
}
\]

under polynomial Lipschitz/complexity assumptions.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:35:46)

I’ll continue by attacking the integral-rigidity lemma directly. The aim is to replace the old D1/D2 machinery with: extraction gives an interval; integral rigidity turns small \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) on that interval into small \(u=q''\).

_Thought for 38s_

Agent 1 / A continued attack: Gate 2 integral-rigidity lemma. Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Gate 2 integral-rigidity lemma looks provable by cutoff energy estimates.}
}
\]

Assume on an interval \(J\):

\[
|g|+|h|\le \varepsilon,
\qquad
g:=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
h:=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Then, on a shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\), one should get

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|,
\qquad
u=q''.
}
\]

This is exactly the rigidity estimate needed after the two-threshold extraction step. The proof is not merely formal; it has a concrete energy route. The remaining work is to verify cutoff/boundary terms under the exact normalized derivative convention.

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

so

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Therefore it is enough to show

\[
\int_{J'} |F(q)|^2
\]

is small, since

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon.
\]

The difficulty is controlling \(F(q)\) without assuming \(g''\) is small. The second equation

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

lets us control a weighted kinetic term after integrating by parts, using only \(g\)-smallness rather than \(g''\)-smallness.

---

# 2. Kinetic control away from \(q=0\)

Choose a smooth sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) such that:

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)
\quad\text{for } |q|\ge2\delta,
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0
\quad\text{for } |q|\le\delta,
\]

with

\[
|s_\delta'|\lesssim\delta^{-1},
\qquad
|s_\delta''|\lesssim\delta^{-2}.
\]

Let \(\phi\) be a cutoff supported in \(J\), equal to \(1\) on \(J'\), with polynomially controlled derivatives.

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q)
\]

and integrate. The main term is

\[
2\int \phi |q|(q')^2
\]

on the region \(|q|\ge2\delta\). Hence

\[
2\int \phi |q|(q')^2
\le
\int |\phi h|
+
\frac16\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''\right|
+
\text{transition terms}.
\]

Integrating the \(g''\)-term by parts twice gives

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g\,(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Since

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

and the cutoff derivatives cost powers of \(\delta^{-1}\) and polynomial derivative bounds for \(q\), we get schematically

\[
\left|\int g\,(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}} |q|(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

In particular, on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
\boxed{
\int (q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-4}|J|.
}
\]

The exact power of \(\delta\) is not important; the target exponent \(2/5\) comes from the favorable \(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\) balance. A worse polynomial power still gives some positive exponent.

---

# 3. Potential control for \(F(q)\)

Now test

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi \chi_\delta(q)F(q),
\]

where \(\chi_\delta(q)=0\) on \(|q|\le2\delta\) and \(\chi_\delta(q)=1\) on \(|q|\ge3\delta\).

Then

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is

\[
O(Q^C\varepsilon |J|).
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int (\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'
+
\text{boundary}.
\]

The derivative expands into terms involving

\[
F'(q)(q')^2,
\qquad
\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\qquad
\phi' \chi_\delta F(q)q'.
\]

All are controlled by the kinetic estimate above and the polynomial bounds for \(q,F,F'\), with cutoff losses in powers of \(\delta^{-1}\).

Thus one obtains

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}} |F(q)|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

Again the exponent \(-3\) is a schematic safe target; exact cutoff bookkeeping may produce \(-4\) or another fixed power, but still yields a positive rigidity exponent.

---

# 4. Small-\(q\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3=O(\delta).
\]

Therefore

\[
|u|=|F(q)+g|
\le
C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}} |u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Optimize \(\delta\)

Combining the two regions:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2/5},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
=
\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J|.
}
\]

This is the desired integral rigidity estimate.

---

# 6. Gate 2 consequence

From the two-threshold extraction step, Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le\varepsilon
\]

on \(J\).

Then on a shrunken \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2 |J'|.
\]

But the rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Choose the Gate 2 failure exponent so that

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}<\frac12\tau^2.
\]

Contradiction.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction + integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Remaining technical checks

The proof requires:

1. **Normalized derivative convention audit**  
   Ensure all primes and double primes in

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
   \]

   are the same normalized derivative.

2. **Cutoff boundary terms**  
   Choose \(J'\Subset J\) and \(\phi\) with polynomial derivative cost.

3. **Polynomial amplitude bounds**  
   Need

   \[
   |q|,\ |q'|,\ |q''|,\ |q'''|
   \le Q^C
   \]

   on \(J\), probably through \(q^{(4)}\) for clean bookkeeping.

4. **Transition region \(\delta\le |q|\le3\delta\)**  
   The cutoff derivative terms must be bounded without losing more than a fixed power of \(\delta^{-1}\).

5. **Boundary case \(q\) changes sign often**  
   The sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) is designed to handle this; no monotonicity of \(q\) is needed.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral rigidity proof candidate: strong.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No }\Gamma_G''\text{-smallness hypothesis is needed separately.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D2 is absorbed by the integration-by-parts argument.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 now reduces mainly to two-threshold extraction + cutoff bookkeeping.}
}
\]

So the downstream Gate 2 route should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{two-threshold interval}
\Rightarrow
\text{integral rigidity contradiction}.
}
\]

This is substantially stronger than the earlier D1/D2 named-input formulation.

A precise version is:

where

\qquad

So the downstream Gate 2 route becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 1. Rigidity lemma statement

Let \(J'\Subset J\) be intervals, and assume normalized derivative conventions. Suppose on \(J\),

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
|h|\le\varepsilon,
\]

with polynomial complexity bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |q''|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

The exponent \(2/5\) is not sacred; what matters is a positive power of \(\varepsilon\). But \(2/5\) comes from the clean balance

\[
\delta^2
\sim
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

---

# 2. Basic equations

Set

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
g=q''-F(q),
\]

so

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Also,

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

The plan is:

1. use \(h\) to control \((q')^2\) away from \(q=0\);
2. use \(q''=F(q)+g\) to control \(F(q)^2\);
3. use \(|q|\ll1\) to control the small-\(q\) region.

---

# 3. Weighted kinetic estimate

Choose a smooth cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) with:

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)
\quad\text{for }|q|\ge2\delta,
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0
\quad\text{for }|q|\le\delta,
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1},
\qquad
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

Let \(\phi\) be a smooth cutoff supported in \(J\), with

\[
\phi\equiv1\quad\text{on }J',
\]

and derivatives bounded by polynomial powers of \(|J|^{-1}\), absorbed into \(Q^C\).

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q)
\]

and integrate:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi q s_\delta(q)(q')^2
-
\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

The main term satisfies

\[
q s_\delta(q)\ge c|q|
\quad\text{on }|q|\ge2\delta.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}} |q|(q')^2
\le
C\int |\phi h|
+
C\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''\right|.
\]

Now integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g\,(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Since

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi\left(s_\delta''(q)(q')^2+s_\delta'(q)q''\right),
\]

the polynomial derivative bounds imply

\[
\left|\int g\,(\phi s_\delta(q))''\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J|.
\]

Also,

\[
\int |\phi h|\le \varepsilon |J|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}} |q|(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J|.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}} (q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

This is the key kinetic bound.

---

# 4. Control of \(F(q)^2\) away from \(q=0\)

Choose another cutoff \(\chi_\delta(q)\) with:

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad\text{for }|q|\le2\delta,
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad\text{for }|q|\ge3\delta,
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

we have

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int (\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

The derivative expands into terms involving:

\[
\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q',
\]

\[
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2.
\]

On the support of \(\chi_\delta\) and \(\chi_\delta'\),

\[
|q|\ge2\delta.
\]

Thus the kinetic estimate controls the \(q'\)-terms. In particular,

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

The \(\phi'\)-term is handled by Cauchy–Schwarz and absorbed with a small multiple of

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
\]

plus the same kinetic error.

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}} |F(q)|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

This is the potential-energy bound.

---

# 5. Small-\(q\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3=O(\delta).
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

and

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

we get

\[
|q''|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}} |q''|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Combine and optimize

On \(|q|\ge3\delta\),

\[
q''=F(q)+g,
\]

so

\[
|q''|^2\le2|F(q)|^2+2\varepsilon^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'} |q''|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2/5},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
=
\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |q''|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J|.
}
\]

Since

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

this proves the integral-rigidity estimate:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 7. Gate 2 contradiction

From the two-threshold extraction theorem, Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives an interval \(J\) such that

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le\varepsilon
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

On a shrunken interval \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
\]

But the integral-rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Choose the Gate 2 failure exponent so that

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}<\frac12\tau^2.
\]

Contradiction.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction + integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. Remaining technical audits

This proof still needs formal verification of:

1. **Exact normalized derivative convention**

   The identity

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
   \]

   must use the same derivative convention as the integral estimates.

2. **Cutoff bookkeeping**

   The estimates for \(s_\delta,\chi_\delta,\phi\) must be written with exact constants and all boundary terms.

3. **Polynomial derivative bounds**

   Need

   \[
   |q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
   \]

   on \(J\). This should follow from canonical local analytic complexity.

4. **Interval shrinkage**

   Need \(J'\Subset J\) with length still polynomially comparable to \(J\).

5. **Vector anisotropy**

   Since

   \[
   |g|+|h|\le\sqrt2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2},
   \]

   the scalar assumption follows from the extraction.

These are technical, not conceptual.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral rigidity lemma: strong proof candidate.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D2 is absorbed; no separate }\Gamma_G''\text{-smallness hypothesis needed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 reduces to two-threshold extraction + cutoff energy estimates.}
}
\]

So the downstream state improves to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + polynomial Lipschitz/complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}
}
\]

provided the cutoff proof is formalized under the canonical derivative convention.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:44:14)

_Thought for 9s_

Agent 1 / A report: two-threshold extraction with exponent bookkeeping. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Two-threshold extraction is a valid local theorem under polynomial Lipschitz bounds.}
}
\]

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, one can extract an actual interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

such that

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

throughout \(J\). This avoids the older dust-set/Remez obstruction: the argument finds a single good point by weighted averaging and then thickens it using Lipschitz control.

---

# 1. Assumptions

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

and define

\[
F_{\rm aniso}
=
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume polynomial Lipschitz bounds:

\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|\Gamma_G'\|_{L^\infty(I)}
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}'\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\|F_{\rm aniso}'\|_{L^\infty(I)}
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}
\]

in the Lipschitz sense, because

\[
|F_{\rm aniso}(x)-F_{\rm aniso}(y)|
\le
|\Gamma_G(x)-\Gamma_G(y)|
+
|\Gamma_{G,2}(x)-\Gamma_{G,2}(y)|.
\]

---

# 2. Source threshold

Choose

\[
\tau=\frac14 Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Then

\[
(2\tau)^2
=
\frac14Q^{-B}.
\]

Define the high-source set

\[
H=\{m\in I: |u(m)|\ge2\tau\}.
\]

On \(I\setminus H\),

\[
|u|^2<4\tau^2=\frac14Q^{-B}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{I\setminus H}|u|^2\,dm
\le
\frac14Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

By Gate 1,

\[
\int_H |u|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac34Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

So \(H\) carries a fixed polynomial fraction of the Gate 1 source mass.

---

# 3. Find a high-source, low-anisotropy point

From Gate 2 failure,

\[
\int_H |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
\le
Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Divide by the source mass on \(H\):

\[
\frac{
\int_H |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm
}{
\int_H |u|^2\,dm
}
\le
\frac{Q^{-A}|I|}
{\frac34Q^{-B}|I|}
\le
2Q^{-(A-B)}
\]

after absorbing harmless constants.

Therefore there exists

\[
m_\ast\in H
\]

such that

\[
F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)^2
\le
2Q^{-(A-B)}.
\]

Hence

\[
F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

At the same point,

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge2\tau
=
\frac12Q^{-B/2}.
\]

So the pointwise extraction gives:

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_\ast)|\ge \frac12Q^{-B/2},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G(m_\ast)|+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)|
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Lipschitz thickening

Define

\[
r_u
=
c\,Q^{-B/2-C_u}|I|,
\]

and

\[
r_F
=
c\,Q^{-(A-B)/2-C_F}|I|,
\]

where \(c>0\) is a sufficiently small absolute constant.

Let

\[
r=\min(r_u,r_F).
\]

Choose an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

containing \(m_\ast\), one-sided if necessary, with

\[
|J|\ge r/2.
\]

For \(m\in J\),

\[
|u(m)-u(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1}|m-m_\ast|
\le
cQ^{-B/2}.
\]

Taking \(c\) small enough,

\[
|u(m)|
\ge
\frac14Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

with

\[
C_1=B/2+O(1).
\]

Similarly,

\[
|F_{\rm aniso}(m)-F_{\rm aniso}(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}|m-m_\ast|
\le
cQ^{-(A-B)/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
F_{\rm aniso}(m)
\le
C Q^{-(A-B)/2}
\]

on \(J\). Hence

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-A_1}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

where

\[
A_1
=
\frac{A-B}{2}-O(1)
\]

after absorbing the Lipschitz and constant losses into the chosen \(A\). More explicitly, if tracking \(C_F\) through the interval length,

\[
A_1
=
\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1).
\]

The interval length satisfies

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
C_J
=
\max\left(
B/2+C_u,\ (A-B)/2+C_F
\right)+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 5. Boundary cases

If \(m_\ast\) lies within distance \(r\) of \(\partial I\), choose the longer of the available one-sided intervals

\[
[m_\ast-r,m_\ast]\cap I,
\qquad
[m_\ast,m_\ast+r]\cap I.
\]

This gives

\[
|J|\ge r/2
\]

unless \(I\) itself has already been reduced to a smaller boundary packet. All estimates above are one-sided and remain valid.

If the later integral-rigidity lemma requires

\[
J'\Subset J,
\]

take \(J'\) to be the middle half of \(J\). Then

\[
|J'|\asymp |J|
\]

and all lower/upper bounds persist on \(J'\).

---

# 6. Exponent hierarchy for integral rigidity

Suppose the integral-rigidity lemma gives:

\[
\sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le \varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Here

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

So the rigidity upper bound is

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R-\frac{2A_1}{5}}|J'|.
\]

But extraction gives

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J',
\]

so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-2C_1}|J'|.
\]

For contradiction, require

\[
C_R-\frac{2A_1}{5}
<
-2C_1.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\frac{2A_1}{5}
>
2C_1+C_R.
\]

Using

\[
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1),
\]

this becomes

\[
\frac{A-B}{5}
>
2C_1+C_R+O(C_F)+O(1).
\]

Since

\[
C_1=B/2+O(1),
\]

a sufficient condition is

\[
\boxed{
A
\ge
B+5(2C_1+C_R+C_F+C_0)
}
\]

for a large absolute bookkeeping constant \(C_0\). In simpler terms:

\[
\boxed{
A\gg B+C_u+C_F+C_R
}
\]

is enough.

---

# 7. Final extraction theorem

### Two-threshold interval extraction theorem

Assume:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

and

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|\Gamma_G'\|_\infty+\|\Gamma_{G,2}'\|_\infty
\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then there exists an interval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
\boxed{
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|
}
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge Q^{-C_1}
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

One can take

\[
C_1=B/2+O(1),
\]

\[
A_1=\frac{A-B}{2}-O(C_F)-O(1),
\]

\[
C_J=\max(B/2+C_u,\ (A-B)/2+C_F)+O(1).
\]

If \(A\) is large enough relative to \(B,C_u,C_F\) and the integral-rigidity loss \(C_R\), this interval contradicts the rigidity lemma.

---

# 8. Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Two-threshold extraction: proved under polynomial Lipschitz bounds.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No Remez/Cartan or relative-density input is needed for this extraction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining Gate 2 task: formalize the integral-rigidity cutoff estimates.}
}
\]

Thus the Gate 2 proof route is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{two-threshold interval}
\Rightarrow
\text{integral-rigidity contradiction}.
}
\]
