## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:50:42)

_Thought for 9s_

Agent 1 / A report: canonical derivative and Lipschitz bounds audit. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The needed Lipschitz/cutoff bounds reduce to a finite canonical derivative package through order }7.
}
\]

For the Gate 2 extraction and integral-rigidity route, the safe derivative package is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 7.
}
\]

Order \(6\) is enough for the integral-rigidity lemma itself, but the two-threshold extraction needs a Lipschitz bound for

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and \(h'\) contains \(g'''\), hence \(q^{(5)}\). Depending on the exact normalized conventions and whether \(q\) or \(u=q''\) is the primitive row variable, order \(5\) may suffice locally; order \(7\) is safer for canonical transfer, projection/gauge errors, and derivative losses through \(E_2\).

So the clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical derivative control through }k\le7
\Rightarrow
\text{all local bounds needed for G2-A, G2-B, and D3a.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Derivative convention

Use the normalized packet derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

On normalized coordinate

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda},
\]

this is simply

\[
\mathcal D=\partial_x.
\]

All derivatives below should be interpreted in this normalized sense unless otherwise stated.

Let

\[
q=q(x),
\qquad
u=q''=\mathcal D^2q.
\]

Then

\[
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

The exact coefficients are convention-sensitive, but the derivative-order accounting is not.

---

## 2. Derivatives needed for G2-A extraction

G2-A uses Lipschitz bounds for

\[
u,\qquad g,\qquad h.
\]

### \(u'\)

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

we have

\[
u'=q'''.
\]

So

\[
\|u'\|_\infty
\]

requires

\[
q^{(3)}.
\]

### \(g'\)

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

Therefore

\[
g'=q'''-6q'+6q^2q'.
\]

So

\[
\|g'\|_\infty
\]

requires

\[
q^{(3)}
\]

plus bounds on \(q,q'\).

### \(h'\)

First compute derivative order.

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Then

\[
h'=2q'(q')^2+4qq'q''-\frac16g'''.
\]

Now \(g'''\) uses \(q^{(5)}\), because \(g=q''+\text{lower}\). Thus

\[
\|h'\|_\infty
\]

requires

\[
q^{(5)}
\]

plus lower derivative bounds.

So the minimal derivative order for G2-A is:

\[
\boxed{k_0=5.}
\]

---

## 3. Derivatives needed for G2-B integral rigidity

G2-B uses:

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
\]

on the cutoff support.

The terms are:

- \(q,q'\) appear in \(2q(q')^2\);
- \(q''=u\) appears in \(g\);
- \(q'''\) appears in differentiating cutoffs and kinetic terms;
- \(q^{(4)}\) appears inside \(g''\) and in bounds for \(h\).

The integration-by-parts proof moves derivatives from \(g''\) onto cutoff functions. Since

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
\]

uses \(q''\) and \((q')^2\), not higher derivatives, that part is mild. But controlling \(h\), \(g\), and their smoothness in the surrounding extraction already wants more.

For the lemma itself, a safe requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},\qquad 0\le k\le4.
}
\]

For combined G2-A + G2-B, use:

\[
\boxed{
0\le k\le5.
}
\]

---

## 4. Why \(k\le7\) is safer canonically

Even if local algebra only needs \(k\le5\), canonical transfer from

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

often costs extra derivative margin.

Reasons:

1. **Projection/gauge derivatives** may introduce one or two more normalized derivatives.

2. **Tail truncation estimates** are usually more stable if stated with slack.

3. **Row-conversion and D4** involve \(A_7,A_9,H,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), and correction terms may contain derivatives just above the leading symbolic order.

4. If one differentiates \(h\) again while controlling thickening or row mobility, one encounters \(q^{(6)}\).

Thus the robust canonical theorem should ask for:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This is not because the leading proof uses all seven derivatives, but because it makes the canonical transfer guardrail stable.

---

## 5. Canonical decomposition transfer

We need the derivative package for the canonical source

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Equivalently, in terms of \(q\), we need \(q\) and its normalized derivatives through \(7\). Since \(q''=q''_{\can}\), this means controlling \(q''_{\can}\) through normalized order \(5\):

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

For the canonical decomposition:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

we require:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j B_2|\le Q^{C_j},
\]

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j P_2|\le Q^{C_j},
\]

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j D_2|\le Q^{C_j},
\]

and

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j E_2|\le Q^{C_j}
\]

for

\[
0\le j\le5.
\]

For perturbative transfer, \(E_2\) may need the stronger smallness

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E},
\qquad
0\le j\le5,
\]

if \(E_2\) is not intended to be part of the main canonical object. If \(E_2\) is retained canonically, polynomial boundedness is enough for Gate 2 extraction/rigidity, but later row transfer may need smallness.

---

## 6. Bounds for \(g,h\) in terms of \(q\)

Assume

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le5.
\]

Then

\[
|u'|=|q'''|\le Q^{C_3}.
\]

Also,

\[
|g'|
=
|q'''-6q'+6q^2q'|
\le Q^{C_g}.
\]

For \(h'\),

\[
h'=2(q')^3+4qq'q''-\frac16g'''.
\]

Expanding \(g'''\) gives terms involving

\[
q^{(5)},\ q^{(3)},\ q'',\ q',\ q.
\]

So

\[
|h'|\le Q^{C_h}.
\]

Converting to interval scaling gives

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}
\]

after absorbing the normalized length convention. If \(I\) is normalized to length \(O(1)\), the \(|I|^{-1}\) factor is harmless; in physical coordinates it comes from \(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\).

---

## 7. Theorem statement

### Canonical derivative package for downstream Gate 2

Let \(I^\ast\) be a fixed enlargement of the packet interval \(I\). Suppose

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
\]

Then:

1. G2-A Lipschitz bounds hold:

   \[
   \|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
   \]

   \[
   \|\Gamma_G'\|_\infty+\|\Gamma_{G,2}'\|_\infty
   \le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1}.
   \]

2. G2-B cutoff bounds hold:

   \[
   |q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|
   \le Q^C.
   \]

3. D3a wall-escape bounds hold if additionally

   \[
   |u'|=\|q'''\|_\infty\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
   \]

4. D4 row-conversion derivative/correction estimates have the derivative slack needed for projection/gauge bookkeeping.

If \(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\), it suffices to prove polynomial normalized derivative bounds for each canonical component through the induced order.

---

## 8. Missing transfer estimate

The only missing part is not local algebra; it is canonical analytic complexity:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2)|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5,
}
\]

or, equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This is plausible from the canonical AFE/gamma/tail framework, but it must be stated explicitly.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative order needed locally: }k\le5.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Safe canonical package: }k\le7\text{ for }q,\text{ or }j\le5\text{ for }q''_{\can}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Under that package, all Lipschitz/cutoff bounds for G2-A, G2-B, D3a follow.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining task: prove canonical derivative bounds for }B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:52:24)

I’ll attack the transfer estimate as a canonical analytic-complexity theorem. The first issue is avoiding a false proof by absolute values: AFE coefficient \(\ell^1\)-bounds can be enormous, so the estimate must use standard zeta/log-derivative bounds, smoothing, or \(L^2\)-to-\(L^\infty\) control, not naive summation.

_Thought for 35s_

## Attack: canonical transfer estimate for downstream derivative bounds

We need to prove the local analytic-complexity package:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},\qquad 0\le k\le 7,
}
\]

or equivalently, since

\[
u=q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2 q
\]

in normalized coordinates,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

This is the “missing transfer estimate” from canonical decomposition

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

to the local bounds needed for:

\[
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction},
\quad
\text{G2-B integral rigidity},
\quad
\text{D3a wall escape}.
\]

Source context: 

---

# 1. First warning: naive AFE \(\ell^1\)-bounds are too large

For the prime/main branch one has a schematic packet

\[
P_2(t)\sim
\sum_n a_n(t)e^{-it\log n}.
\]

Differentiating \(j\) times with

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_t
\]

gives phase factors

\[
(\lambda\log n)^j.
\]

In ordinary scale,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
\log n\lesssim Q,
\]

so

\[
|\lambda\log n|^j\lesssim 1
\]

for fixed \(j\).

That part is fine.

But bounding the sum by

\[
\sum_n |a_n|
\]

is generally much too crude. For AFE-length \(n\le e^{Q/2}\), absolute values can produce exponential-in-\(Q\) bounds. We need one of:

1. a direct log-derivative/zeta analytic bound;
2. a smoothed \(L^2\to L^\infty\) Dirichlet-polynomial bound;
3. a zero-avoiding contour / Borel–Carathéodory argument;
4. a packet model plus canonical tail transfer.

The cleanest route is the zero-avoiding analytic-complexity route.

---

# 2. Correct theorem target

### Ordinary canonical derivative transfer theorem

Let \(I^\ast\) be the enlarged ordinary packet interval and suppose

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Assume \(I^\ast\) is ordinary, meaning the relevant analytic continuations stay a polynomial normalized distance away from singularities/zeros:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_{\zeta})
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

for a normalized complex tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{t+is:t\in I^\ast,\ |s|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Assume also standard polynomial growth on the boundary:

\[
|\zeta(s)|+|\zeta'(s)|+\cdots+|\zeta^{(K)}(s)|
\le Q^{C_K}
\]

after the relevant completed/gamma normalization, for \(K\) large enough.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad
0\le j\le5.
}
\]

This is the exact transfer estimate downstream needs.

---

# 3. Why zero-avoidance is necessary

Without a zero-avoidance or regularization hypothesis, the estimate is false.

The log-derivative side can have poles near zeros. If a zeta zero lies within distance

\[
\ll \lambda Q^{-C}
\]

of the packet, derivatives of \(q''_{\can}\) can blow like powers of the inverse distance. That is precisely the singular mechanism.

So the theorem must be split:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packet: zero-avoiding derivative transfer;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular packet: handled by singular explicit-formula branch.}
}
\]

Trying to prove uniform polynomial derivative bounds across both regimes would incorrectly erase the singular branch.

---

# 4. Component estimates

## 4.1 Background \(B_2\)

The canonical background is

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

Asymptotically,

\[
B_2(t)=O(t^{-2}),
\]

and more generally

\[
\partial_t^j B_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal D^jB_2(t)
=
\lambda^j\partial_t^jB_2(t)
=
O_j(\lambda^jt^{-2-j}).
\]

Since \(t\sim e^Q\) and \(\lambda Q\asymp1\),

\[
|\mathcal D^jB_2(t)|\le e^{-2Q}Q^{-j} \ll Q^{-A}
\]

for every fixed \(A\), at large \(Q\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ is harmless for derivative transfer.}
}
\]

It must remain in the canonical object, but it is not a derivative-bound obstruction.

---

## 4.2 Main and dual AFE packets \(P_2,D_2\)

Write schematically:

\[
P_2(t)
=
\sum_n a_n(t)e^{-it\log n},
\]

\[
D_2(t)
=
e^{i\Theta(t)}
\sum_n b_n(t)e^{+it\log n},
\]

with smooth AFE weights.

When applying \(\mathcal D^j\), terms split into:

\[
\mathcal D^j(a_n(t)e^{-it\log n})
=
\sum_{r=0}^j
\binom jr
(\mathcal D^{j-r}a_n(t))
(-i\lambda\log n)^r
e^{-it\log n}.
\]

On ordinary support,

\[
|\lambda\log n|\le C.
\]

The coefficient derivatives are mild because conductor and gamma parameters vary on height scale \(t\), not packet scale \(\lambda\):

\[
\mathcal D\log N(t)
=
\lambda\partial_t\log N(t)
=
O(\lambda/t)
\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Similarly, normalized gamma-factor derivatives are polynomially bounded or smaller.

Thus, at the formal-symbol level,

\[
\mathcal D^jP_2
\]

and

\[
\mathcal D^jD_2
\]

are packet sums with the same normalized frequency support and polynomially modified coefficients.

The missing part is not differentiation; it is bounding the packet sums themselves.

---

# 5. Two proof routes for \(P_2,D_2\)

## Route A: analytic log-derivative bound

If \(q''_{\can}\) is a completed log-derivative / phase-curvature expression, then on a zero-avoiding tube one can use Cauchy estimates:

Assume

\[
|q''_{\can}(z)|\le Q^{C_0}
\quad\text{on }\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast).
\]

Then for \(0\le j\le5\),

\[
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(t)|
\le
j!\rho^{-j}Q^{C_0}
\le Q^{C_0+jC_\rho+O(1)}.
\]

This gives the desired bound.

So it is enough to prove:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)}
|q''_{\can}(z)|
\le Q^{C_0}.
}
\]

This follows from zero-avoidance plus standard logarithmic derivative estimates:

\[
\frac{\zeta'}{\zeta}(s)
=
\sum_\rho \frac1{s-\rho}
+
O(\log t),
\]

and higher derivatives give

\[
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^k\frac{\zeta'}{\zeta}(s)
=
O_k\left(\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-k-1}+\log^{k+2}t\right).
\]

If

\[
\operatorname{dist}(s,\rho)\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0}
\]

and \(\lambda\asymp Q^{-1}\), then

\[
|s-\rho|^{-1}\le Q^{C_0+1}.
\]

A local zero-count bound gives only polynomially many zeros in the relevant unit window, so the sum is polynomial in \(Q\).

Thus Route A reduces transfer to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-avoidance + local zero-count}
\Rightarrow
\text{polynomial log-derivative bounds}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest route.

---

## Route B: packet AFE \(L^2\to L^\infty\)

Use a smoothed packet estimate:

\[
P_2(t)=\sum_n a_n e^{-it\log n}W(n/N).
\]

On a packet interval \(I^\ast\), the normalized frequencies satisfy \(|\lambda\log n|\le C\). If one has

\[
\int_{I^{\ast\ast}}|P_2(t)|^2dt\le Q^C|I^{\ast\ast}|,
\]

and polynomial Bernstein control

\[
\|\mathcal DP_2\|_\infty\le Q^C\|P_2\|_\infty
\]

or a local spectral inequality, then

\[
\|P_2\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
\]

This avoids zero-avoidance but requires a strong packet \(L^2\) estimate and local bandlimit control.

This route is less direct than Route A.

---

# 6. \(E_2\) transfer

For downstream bounds, \(E_2\) may be treated in either of two ways.

## Inclusive canonical treatment

If \(E_2\) is part of the canonical object, then we only need polynomial derivative bounds:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

This suffices for G2-A/G2-B Lipschitz and cutoff estimates.

## Perturbative model transfer

If proving a theorem first for

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2
\]

and then transferring to

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

we need smallness:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

For Gate 2 derivative bounds, inclusive treatment is enough. For model-to-canonical replacement, smallness is required.

Given the paper’s current emphasis on canonical objects, I recommend the inclusive version for downstream Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
E_2\text{ included, polynomially controlled.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final transfer theorem

### Ordinary canonical analytic-complexity transfer

Assume:

1. Ordinary separation:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
   \ge \lambda Q^{-C_0},
   \qquad
   \rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
   \]

2. Local zero-count:

   \[
   N_\zeta(\mathcal T_1(I^\ast))\le Q^{C_N}.
   \]

3. Completed gamma/background derivatives are standard.

4. The canonical decomposition

   \[
   q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
   \]

   is valid in the tube and \(E_2\) is polynomially controlled through normalized derivative order \(5\).

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad
0\le j\le5.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|
\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This proves the derivative/Lipschitz package needed for G2-A, G2-B, and D3a.

---

# 8. Consequence for downstream

From this transfer theorem:

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|
\le Q^{C}|I|^{-1},
\]

and

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|
\le Q^C
\]

all follow.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-avoidance + canonical analytic complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{all local derivative bounds required for Gate 2 and wall escape.}
}
\]

---

# 9. What remains open

The transfer estimate is now reduced to two precise inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-avoidance / zero-separation in the packet tube;}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical }E_2\text{ polynomial derivative control through }j\le5.
}
\]

If ordinary packets are defined to exclude deep singular proximity, the first is part of ordinary/singular separation. If not, it must be added explicitly.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ derivative transfer: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
P_2,D_2\text{ derivative differentiation: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
P_2,D_2\text{ sup bounds: need zero-avoidance/log-derivative or packet }L^2\to L^\infty.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_2\text{ transfer: needs polynomial derivative control through }j\le5.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Missing transfer estimate is now a precise ordinary analytic-complexity theorem.}
}
\]

The strongest target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Ordinary Canonical Analytic-Complexity Transfer}
}
\]

stated above.

I’ll continue by trying to prove the “Ordinary Canonical Analytic-Complexity Transfer” from the canonical object itself, not from prime-side absolute sums. The key is to use meromorphic/zero-distance control for the full \(q''_{\can}\), then treat AFE pieces only as canonical representations.

_Thought for 15s_

## Continued attack: Ordinary Canonical Analytic-Complexity Transfer

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The transfer estimate is provable if “ordinary” includes polynomial zero-distance in a complex packet tube.}
}
\]

The clean route is not to bound \(P_2,D_2\) termwise. The clean route is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}
\text{ is the boundary value of a meromorphic canonical curvature;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packet}
=
\text{packet tube stays polynomially far from its poles/zeros;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cauchy/log-derivative estimates}
\Rightarrow
\sup |\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j}.
}
\]

So the missing transfer estimate can be converted into a precise ordinary/singular separation axiom:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

If that separation holds, derivative transfer is Green. If it fails, the packet belongs to the singular/near-zero branch and must be handled by the singular explicit-formula route.

---

# 1. Correct object: the full canonical curvature

We should not try to prove

\[
|P_2|,\ |D_2|
\]

separately by absolute convergence. That is too crude.

Instead, work with the full canonical source

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
}
\]

The prime/dual decomposition is a representation. The analytic-complexity bound should be proved for the full object.

The desired estimate is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

Equivalently, since \(q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|
\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

---

# 2. Ordinary packet tube

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_t,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Let \(I^\ast\) be the real packet interval, and let

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{z=t+is:t\in I^\ast,\ |s|\le \rho\lambda\}.
\]

Take

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Define ordinary tube separation:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

This is the exact point where the ordinary route separates from the singular route. If a zero enters this tube at distance smaller than \(\lambda Q^{-C_0}\), one should not expect polynomial derivative bounds for the canonical log-curvature. That is a near-zero/singular packet.

---

# 3. Meromorphic derivative estimate

Assume \(q''_{\can}\) is represented as a meromorphic canonical curvature with poles only at zeta zeros and controlled gamma/background terms. Schematically, near height \(t\),

\[
q''_{\can}(z)
=
B_2(z)
+
\sum_{\rho}
\mathcal K(z-\rho)
+
\text{regular terms},
\]

where the kernel and its derivatives obey estimates of the form

\[
|\partial_z^j \mathcal K(z-\rho)|
\le
C_j |z-\rho|^{-j-\kappa}
\]

for some fixed \(\kappa\), depending on the exact curvature normalization.

If

\[
|z-\rho|\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

then each nearby zero contributes at most

\[
(\lambda Q^{-C_0})^{-j-\kappa}
=
\lambda^{-j-\kappa}Q^{C(j+\kappa)}.
\]

Applying the normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D^j=\lambda^j\partial_z^j
\]

gives

\[
\lambda^j|z-\rho|^{-j-\kappa}
\le
\lambda^{-\kappa}Q^{C(j+\kappa)}.
\]

Since

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

this is polynomial in \(Q\).

A local zero-count bound in the relevant tube/window gives at most \(Q^C\) relevant zeros. Far zeros contribute by summable tails or standard logarithmic-derivative estimates.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{\mathcal T_{\rho/2}(I^\ast)}
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

This is the core proof.

---

# 4. Cauchy formulation

There is an even cleaner Cauchy version.

Assume a zeroth-order bound on the tube:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)}
|q''_{\can}(z)|
\le Q^{C_0}.
}
\]

Then Cauchy gives, for \(z\in \mathcal T_{\rho/2}(I^\ast)\),

\[
|\partial_z^j q''_{\can}(z)|
\le
j!(\rho\lambda)^{-j}Q^{C_0}.
\]

Multiplying by \(\lambda^j\),

\[
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(z)|
\le
j!\rho^{-j}Q^{C_0}.
\]

Since

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(z)|
\le Q^{C_0+jC_\rho+O(1)}.
}
\]

Thus it is enough to prove the tube sup bound

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)}|q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_0}.
\]

That bound follows from ordinary zero-distance plus standard meromorphic/log-derivative estimates.

So the transfer theorem can be stated compactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-distance}+\text{tube growth}
\Rightarrow
\text{normalized derivative bounds}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Background \(B_2\)

For the background term,

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]

the asymptotic polygamma estimates give

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal D^jB_2(t)=\lambda^jO_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

At height \(t\sim e^Q\), and \(\lambda\asymp Q^{-1}\),

\[
|\mathcal D^jB_2(t)|\ll e^{-2Q}Q^{-j}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ is automatically polynomially bounded, in fact tiny.}
}
\]

No obstruction here.

---

# 6. Prime/dual AFE pieces

For \(P_2,D_2\), the derivative operation itself is harmless in ordinary scale:

\[
\mathcal D^j e^{-it\log n}
=
(-i\lambda\log n)^j e^{-it\log n}.
\]

On ordinary support,

\[
|\lambda\log n|\le C.
\]

Smooth weight derivatives are also harmless because conductor variation is slow on the packet scale:

\[
\mathcal D\log N(t)
=
\lambda \partial_t\log N(t)
=
O(\lambda/t)
\ll Q^{-A}
\]

for large \(t\).

But supremum bounds should come from the **full canonical meromorphic function**, not from

\[
\sum |a_n|.
\]

So the AFE pieces are fine for representation and canonical bookkeeping, but not the primary proof of the derivative bound.

---

# 7. \(E_2\) control

There are two possible policies.

## Inclusive policy

Treat

\[
E_2
\]

as part of the canonical object. Then the meromorphic/tube bound is applied to

\[
q''_{\can}
\]

directly. No separate smallness of \(E_2\) is needed for Gate 2 local derivative bounds.

This is preferable.

## Perturbative policy

If one proves estimates for a model

\[
q''_{\model}=B_2+P_2+D_2
\]

and then transfers to

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\model}+E_2,
\]

then one needs

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E},
\qquad
0\le j\le5.
\]

This is stronger and not necessary for the downstream local bounds if the full canonical object is used throughout.

Recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use inclusive canonical policy for Gate 2.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Formal theorem

### Ordinary Canonical Analytic-Complexity Transfer

Let \(I^\ast\) be an ordinary packet interval with

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Assume there is a complex tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

such that:

1. **ordinary zero-distance**

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
   \ge \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

2. **canonical tube growth**

   \[
   \sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)}
   |q''_{\can}(z)|
   \le Q^{C_1};
   \]

3. **canonical decomposition fidelity**

   \[
   q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
   \]

   holds in the tube, with no proxy substitutions.

Then for \(0\le j\le5\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j}.
}
\]

Equivalently, for \(0\le k\le7\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|
\le Q^{C_k}.
}
\]

Consequently, the Lipschitz and cutoff bounds needed for G2-A, G2-B, and D3a hold.

---

# 9. What still needs proof

The only nontrivial remaining analytic-complexity input is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)}
|q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_1}.
}
\]

This can be proved from ordinary zero-distance plus standard log-derivative/explicit-formula bounds if the canonical curvature is indeed a fixed finite derivative of the completed log object.

If the paper has already established such ordinary zero-distance or singular separation, then this transfer estimate is essentially Green.

If not, then the missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Ordinary zero-distance/tube growth lemma for }q''_{\can}.
}
\]

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{B}_2\text{ derivative bounds: Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE derivative factors: Green in ordinary scale.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Supremum bounds: use full canonical meromorphic/tube estimates, not AFE }\ell^1.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main remaining assumption: ordinary zero-distance + tube growth for }q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Thus the missing transfer estimate is attacked successfully up to a precise ordinary/singular separation lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary tube avoids zeros polynomially}
\Rightarrow
\sup|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j}.
}

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:57:22)

_Thought for 14s_

Continuing Agent 1 / A attack: ordinary zero-distance/tube-growth transfer. Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The missing transfer estimate reduces to a standard meromorphic log-derivative bound plus local zero count.}
}
\]

More precisely, if the ordinary packet tube stays polynomially far from zeros,

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge \delta,
\qquad
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0},
\]

then finite normalized derivatives of the canonical curvature satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

So the downstream Gate 2 derivative package is Green **inside the ordinary zero-separated regime**. The remaining bookkeeping is to make the canonical formula for \(q''_{\can}\) explicitly meromorphic and to define “ordinary” as polynomial tube separation from zeros.

---

# 1. Abstract meromorphic lemma

Let \(F(s)\) be a completed zeta-type function whose logarithmic derivative has simple poles at zeros \(\rho\):

\[
\frac{F'}{F}(s)=\sum_\rho \frac{1}{s-\rho}+\text{regular/gamma terms},
\]

with the sum interpreted in the usual symmetrized/log-derivative sense.

Let \(K_r(s)\) be any fixed finite derivative:

\[
K_r(s)=\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r\frac{F'}{F}(s).
\]

Then

\[
K_r(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho \frac{1}{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\text{regular/gamma terms}.
\]

Assume \(s\) lies in a tube \(\mathcal T\) satisfying

\[
\operatorname{dist}(s,\mathcal Z_F)\ge \delta.
\]

Then for fixed \(r\),

\[
\boxed{
|K_r(s)|\le Q^{C_r}
}
\]

provided

\[
\delta\ge Q^{-C_\delta}
\]

and the local zero count in unit windows is polynomial in \(Q\). For zeta at height \(t\sim e^Q\), this local zero count is \(O(Q)\) on unit windows, hence polynomial.

---

# 2. Proof by dyadic zero annuli

Fix \(s\in\mathcal T\). Split zeros into annuli around \(s\):

\[
A_0=\{\rho:\delta\le |s-\rho|\le 2\delta\},
\]

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta<|s-\rho|\le2^{\nu+1}\delta\},
\qquad \nu\ge0.
\]

For zeros in \(A_\nu\),

\[
|s-\rho|^{-r-1}\le (2^\nu\delta)^{-r-1}.
\]

A crude local zero-count bound gives

\[
\#\{\rho:|s-\rho|\le R\}\le Q^C(1+R)
\]

for \(R\le Q^C\), and far zeros contribute by the standard convergent/symmetrized log-derivative tail.

Therefore,

\[
\sum_{\rho}|s-\rho|^{-r-1}
\le
\sum_{\nu\le C\log Q}
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-r-1}
+
Q^C.
\]

The worst contribution is from the first annulus:

\[
\ll Q^C\delta^{-r-1}.
\]

Since

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0},
\]

we get

\[
\delta^{-r-1}\asymp Q^{(1+C_0)(r+1)}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
|K_r(s)|\le Q^{C_r}.
}
\]

This proves polynomial tube growth for fixed log-derivative order.

---

# 3. Normalized derivative conversion

The downstream estimates use

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_t,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1}.
\]

Suppose

\[
q''_{\can}(t)
\]

is a fixed finite linear combination of completed log-derivative derivatives and gamma/background terms. Then

\[
\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}
=
\lambda^j\partial_t^j q''_{\can}.
\]

If \(\partial_t^j q''_{\can}\) is controlled by a fixed higher log-derivative order \(K_{r+j}\), then from the meromorphic lemma,

\[
|\partial_t^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_{r+j}}.
\]

Multiplying by

\[
\lambda^j\le1
\]

only improves the estimate. Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

Equivalently, since \(u=q''_{\can}\),

\[
\boxed{
|u|+|\mathcal D u|+\cdots+|\mathcal D^5u|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is enough for the two-threshold extraction and the integral-rigidity cutoff estimates.

---

# 4. Background term \(B_2\)

The background is

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

Polygamma asymptotics give

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

At \(t\sim e^Q\),

\[
|\mathcal D^jB_2|
=
|\lambda^j\partial_t^jB_2|
\ll
Q^{-j}e^{-(2+j)Q}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ and all required normalized derivatives are negligible, hence polynomially bounded.}
}
\]

Thus \(B_2\) is canonical but not dangerous for transfer.

---

# 5. Main/dual AFE pieces

For the AFE representation,

\[
P_2(t)=\sum_n a_n(t)e^{-it\log n},
\]

\[
D_2(t)=e^{i\Theta(t)}\sum_n b_n(t)e^{+it\log n}.
\]

In ordinary scale,

\[
|\lambda\log n|\lesssim1
\]

on the packet-frequency support. Therefore normalized derivatives of the oscillatory factors are harmless:

\[
\mathcal D^j e^{\mp it\log n}
=
(\mp i\lambda\log n)^j e^{\mp it\log n}
=
O_j(1)e^{\mp it\log n}.
\]

Amplitudes are also slowly varying on packet scale:

\[
\mathcal D\log N(t)
=
\lambda\partial_t\log N(t)
=
O(\lambda/t)
\ll Q^{-A}
\]

for any fixed \(A\) at large height.

But again, the correct supremum proof is not termwise \(\ell^1\). It is the meromorphic/tube proof for the full canonical object. The AFE decomposition is bookkeeping; the log-derivative/tube bound supplies the actual \(L^\infty\) control.

---

# 6. Ordinary versus singular separation

The transfer theorem must be explicitly conditional on ordinary zero-distance.

If

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
<
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

then the log-derivative poles can produce large derivatives, and the packet is not ordinary. This is exactly the singular or near-singular regime.

So define:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packet}
:=
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packet}
\Rightarrow
\text{canonical analytic-complexity transfer}.
}
\]

If this fails, route to singular analysis.

---

# 7. Transfer theorem

### Ordinary Zero-Separated Analytic-Complexity Transfer

Let \(I^\ast\) be a normalized ordinary packet interval with

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Let

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{t+is:t\in I^\ast,\ |s|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Assume:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Assume \(q''_{\can}\) is the full canonical meromorphic curvature associated to the completed object, with poles only at the relevant zeros and standard gamma/background terms. Then for every fixed \(j\le5\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
|\mathcal D^jq''_{\can}|
\le
Q^{C_j}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

Consequences:

\[
|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

and

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
\]

Thus all local derivative assumptions for G2-A, G2-B, and wall escape follow.

---

# 8. Remaining exact checks

The proof requires the paper to state or verify:

1. **Meromorphic representation**  
   \(q''_{\can}\) must be identified with a fixed finite derivative/combination of completed log derivatives and gamma terms.

2. **Pole set**  
   The only dangerous poles in the packet tube are zeta zeros or the relevant \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, plus controlled trivial/gamma singularities far away.

3. **Local zero count**  
   Need a polynomial bound on zeros in unit or polynomial windows:

   \[
   N(t+1)-N(t-1)\ll Q.
   \]

4. **Tube zero-distance**  
   Ordinary packets must explicitly satisfy

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
   \ge\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
   \]

5. **Canonical inclusion of \(E_2\)**  
   Either \(E_2\) is included in the meromorphic canonical object, or if it is a truncation error, one needs

   \[
   \sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E}
   \]

   through \(j\le5\).

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transfer estimate is Green under ordinary zero-separated tube hypothesis.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The proof uses meromorphic log-derivative bounds, not AFE absolute sums.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If zero-distance fails, the packet is singular/transition, not ordinary.}
}
\]

Thus the downstream local derivative package is reduced to the following clean input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Ordinary Zero-Separated Analytic-Complexity Transfer}
}
\]

and this is likely provable with standard zeta zero-count/log-derivative machinery once the canonical meromorphic formula for \(q''_{\can}\) is fixed.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:58:33)

I’ll sharpen the transfer proof into a standard lemma: derivative bounds for \(q''_{\can}\) follow from a zero-free tube plus a local zero-count estimate for the relevant completed log derivative. The aim is to make this plug-and-play for Gate 2.

_Thought for 26s_

Continuing Agent 1 / A attack: make the transfer estimate a standard zero-free-tube lemma. Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The canonical derivative transfer is essentially provable by a zero-free-tube log-derivative lemma.}
}
\]

A clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},\ 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

This is exactly the analytic-complexity package needed for G2-A, G2-B, and wall escape. The proof should use the completed meromorphic object and standard logarithmic-derivative estimates, not AFE absolute-value sums.

---

# 1. Standard log-derivative lemma

Let

\[
s=\sigma+it,\qquad t\asymp T,\qquad Q=\log T.
\]

Let

\[
L(s)=\frac{\xi'}{\xi}(s)
\]

or the relevant completed log derivative. For fixed \(k\ge0\), standard partial-fraction estimates give a bound of the form

\[
\boxed{
L^{(k)}(s)
\ll_k
Q^{k+2}
+
\sum_{\rho:\ |t-\gamma|\le1}
\frac{1}{|s-\rho|^{k+1}}
}
\]

inside a fixed vertical strip, with gamma/trivial-zero terms included in the \(Q^{k+2}\)-type background.

Assume a zero-free tube:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(s,\mathcal Z_\zeta)\ge \delta.
\]

Then every local zero contributes at most \(\delta^{-(k+1)}\), and the number of zeros in \(|t-\gamma|\le1\) is

\[
O(Q).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(k)}(s)|
\ll_k
Q^{C_k}\delta^{-(k+1)}
}
\]

or simply

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(k)}(s)|\le Q^{C_k}
}
\]

whenever

\[
\delta\ge Q^{-C_\delta}.
\]

In our ordinary packet,

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so

\[
\delta\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

Hence

\[
\delta^{-(k+1)}\asymp Q^{(1+C_0)(k+1)},
\]

which is polynomial.

Thus the completed log-derivative and any fixed finite number of its derivatives are polynomially bounded throughout the ordinary zero-separated tube.

---

# 2. Transfer to \(q''_{\can}\)

The canonical curvature \(q''_{\can}\) should be expressible as a fixed finite combination of:

\[
L(s),\quad L'(s),\quad L''(s),\quad \ldots,\quad L^{(m)}(s),
\]

plus explicit gamma/background terms, possibly with real/imaginary parts and smooth bounded coefficients. The exact formula must be pinned down in the canonical definitions, but the analytic estimate is stable for any fixed \(m\).

If

\[
q''_{\can}(t)=\mathcal F\bigl(L,L',\ldots,L^{(m)},\text{gamma terms}\bigr),
\]

where \(\mathcal F\) is a fixed algebraic/differential expression of bounded degree, then the log-derivative lemma gives

\[
\boxed{
|q''_{\can}(z)|\le Q^{C}
}
\]

on the tube.

Moreover, differentiating \(q''_{\can}\) \(j\) times only requires finitely more \(L^{(k)}\)’s, with \(k\le m+j\). For \(j\le5\), this remains fixed order, hence polynomially bounded.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|\partial_t^j q''_{\can}(z)|\le Q^{C_j}
}
\]

on the tube.

Since

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_t,
\qquad
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

we have

\[
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(z)|
=
\lambda^j|\partial_t^j q''_{\can}(z)|
\le Q^{C_j}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

Equivalently, if \(u=q''_{\can}\) and \(u=\mathcal D^2q\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

---

# 3. Dyadic annulus proof, avoiding hidden convergence issues

To avoid relying on a vague partial-fraction statement, one can prove the local part directly.

For \(s\in\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)\), split zeros into annuli:

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le 2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Local zero count gives

\[
\#A_\nu\le Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)
\]

for \(\nu\) up to polynomial range. Then

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(k+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(k+1)}.
\]

Summing \(\nu\) gives a bound dominated by the first few annuli:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\rho:\ |t-\gamma|\le Q^C}
|s-\rho|^{-(k+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(k+1)}.
}
\]

Far zeros are handled by the standard symmetrized log-derivative expansion and contribute \(Q^C\) for fixed \(k\).

Thus the zero-distance hypothesis is exactly what prevents blow-up.

---

# 4. Background \(B_2\)

For

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]

polygamma asymptotics give

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

At

\[
t\asymp e^Q,
\qquad
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

\[
|\mathcal D^jB_2(t)|
=
|\lambda^j\partial_t^jB_2(t)|
\ll
Q^{-j}e^{-(2+j)Q}.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ is harmless for all downstream derivative bounds.}
}
\]

It remains part of the canonical source, but it is not a transfer obstacle.

---

# 5. AFE components \(P_2,D_2,E_2\)

The AFE decomposition

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

should be treated as a canonical representation, not as the proof of the \(L^\infty\) bound.

For \(P_2,D_2\), normalized differentiation is symbolically safe because

\[
\mathcal D^j e^{\mp it\log n}
=
(\mp i\lambda\log n)^j e^{\mp it\log n},
\]

and on ordinary support

\[
|\lambda\log n|\lesssim1.
\]

The issue is bounding the sums. That is better obtained from the full meromorphic object.

For \(E_2\), there are two choices:

### Inclusive canonical treatment

If \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical object, no separate smallness is needed for Gate 2 derivative bounds. The full meromorphic estimate applies to \(q''_{\can}\).

### Truncation-transfer treatment

If \(E_2\) is a truncation remainder between a model and the canonical object, then one needs

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E},
\qquad
0\le j\le5.
\]

For downstream Gate 2, the inclusive treatment is cleaner.

---

# 6. Ordinary packet definition

The transfer theorem suggests the following clean definition.

### Ordinary zero-separated packet

A packet \(I^\ast\) is ordinary if:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and there is a tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

On such packets,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

If this distance condition fails, the packet is near a zero on the packet scale and belongs to the singular/transition analysis rather than the ordinary Gate 2 local transfer.

---

# 7. Connection to downstream lemmas

Once the derivative transfer holds:

## G2-A extraction

We get

\[
|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

and

\[
|g'|+|h'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Thus two-threshold extraction is valid.

## G2-B integral rigidity

We get

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
\]

Thus all cutoff terms in the integral-rigidity proof are controlled.

## Wall escape

We get

\[
|u'|=|q'''|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Thus first-exit wall escape is valid with polynomial exponents.

So the transfer theorem supplies exactly the local analytic package needed downstream.

---

# 8. Final theorem

### Ordinary Zero-Separated Analytic-Complexity Transfer

Assume:

1. \(\lambda Q\asymp1\);

2. \(I^\ast\) has a complex tube

   \[
   \mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\qquad \rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho};
   \]

3. the tube is polynomially zero-separated:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\zeta)
   \ge \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

4. \(q''_{\can}\) is represented by the full canonical meromorphic curvature, with standard gamma/background terms and no proxy substitution.

Then for \(0\le j\le5\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j}.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This proves the analytic complexity assumptions used by two-threshold extraction, integral rigidity, and wall escape.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transfer estimate is provable under ordinary zero-separated tube definition.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If zero-distance fails, route to singular/transition branch.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No AFE }\ell^1\text{ bound is needed or desired.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining task: state canonical meromorphic formula for }q''_{\can}\text{ and the ordinary zero-separated packet definition.}
}

Continuing Agent 1 / A attack: canonical meromorphic formula and ordinary zero-separated transfer. Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The derivative-transfer estimate can be made theorem-level if }q''_{\can}
\text{ is tied explicitly to a completed log-derivative.}
}
\]

The cleanest formulation is an **abstract completed-log-derivative transfer lemma**:

\[
q''_{\can}(t)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{r_0}
a_r(t)\,\Re/\Im\left[
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r
\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\right]_{s=1/2+it}
+
\text{regular gamma/background terms},
\]

with fixed \(r_0\). Then polynomial zero-separation in a complex packet tube gives

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
\]

This supplies every local derivative bound needed for:

\[
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction},
\]

\[
\text{G2-B integral rigidity},
\]

\[
\text{D3a wall escape}.
\]

The remaining thing to pin down is not a new analytic idea; it is a **canonical-definition audit**: show the paper’s \(q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) is indeed the boundary value / AFE representation of such a completed meromorphic object.

---

# 1. Abstract canonical transfer lemma

Let \(\Xi(s)\) be the completed object whose critical-line phase/source curvature defines \(q''_{\can}\). Suppose

\[
q''_{\can}(t)
=
\mathcal L(t)
+
\mathcal R(t),
\]

where \(\mathcal R\) is regular and satisfies polynomial normalized derivative bounds, and

\[
\mathcal L(t)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{r_0}
a_r(t)
\mathcal P_r(1/2+it),
\]

with fixed \(r_0\), polynomially bounded coefficients \(a_r\), and

\[
\mathcal P_r(s)
=
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r
\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]

or a real/imaginary part thereof.

Assume ordinary packet scale:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_t.
\]

Let \(I^\ast\) be the packet interval and define a tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{t+iy:t\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Assume polynomial zero separation:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\delta,
\qquad
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Then for every fixed \(j\le5\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(t)|
\le Q^{C_j}.
}
\]

This is the transfer theorem needed downstream.

---

# 2. Proof of the abstract lemma

For

\[
\mathcal P_r(s)
=
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r
\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s),
\]

the completed partial fraction formula gives

\[
\mathcal P_r(s)
=
(-1)^r r!
\sum_{\rho}
\frac{1}{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\mathcal G_r(s),
\]

where \(\mathcal G_r\) contains gamma/background and normalizing terms.

Inside the standard vertical strip, \(\mathcal G_r\) is polynomially controlled in \(Q=\log t\) for fixed \(r\):

\[
|\mathcal G_r(s)|\le Q^{C_r}.
\]

For the zero sum, use dyadic annuli around \(s\):

\[
A_\nu
=
\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Local zero counting gives

\[
\#\{\rho:|s-\rho|\le R\}\le Q^{C}(1+R)
\]

for the required polynomial \(R\)-range. Hence

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}
|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Summing over \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:

\[
\sum_{\rho}
|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Since

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}
\asymp Q^{-1-C_0},
\]

we get

\[
\delta^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^{(1+C_0)(r+1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
|\mathcal P_r(s)|\le Q^{C_r}.
\]

Now differentiate \(j\le5\) times in \(t\). This merely increases \(r\) by at most \(j\), so the same bound holds for a fixed larger order:

\[
|\partial_t^j \mathcal P_r(1/2+it)|
\le Q^{C_{r,j}}.
\]

Multiplying by

\[
\lambda^j\le1
\]

gives

\[
|\mathcal D^j \mathcal P_r(1/2+it)|
\le Q^{C_{r,j}}.
\]

The coefficients \(a_r(t)\) are smooth/gamma/conductor factors with polynomial normalized derivatives, so Leibniz only costs more polynomial powers. Therefore

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j}.
\]

That proves the abstract transfer lemma.

---

# 3. What exactly must be audited canonically

The proof above becomes valid once the canonical source is written in one of the following equivalent forms.

## Form A: completed meromorphic form

Show

\[
q''_{\can}(t)
\]

is a fixed finite combination of completed logarithmic derivative derivatives:

\[
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\quad
(r\le r_0),
\]

plus regular gamma/background terms.

This is the cleanest.

## Form B: exact explicit-formula form

Show

\[
q''_{\can}(t)
=
B_2(t)
+
\sum_\rho K(t-\gamma)
+
\text{regularized tail},
\]

where

\[
K^{(j)}(x)
\ll_j |x|^{-j-\kappa}
\]

near zero and has controlled decay/tail. Then the same zero-distance proof applies.

## Form C: canonical AFE plus exact remainder

Show

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

equals the same completed meromorphic object in the tube, not merely on the real line. Then the meromorphic proof controls the full sum.

Of these, Form A is best for proof; Form C is best for consistency with existing paper notation.

---

# 4. Why this avoids all AFE absolute-sum problems

The bad route was:

\[
|P_2(t)|
\le
\sum_n |a_n|.
\]

That can be exponentially large and useless.

The correct route is:

\[
P_2+D_2+B_2+E_2
=
q''_{\can}
=
\text{completed meromorphic curvature}.
\]

Then zero-distance controls the full value with cancellations already included. The AFE decomposition is only a representation; it is not the analytic-complexity proof.

So the transfer theorem should explicitly say:

\[
\boxed{
\text{do not prove this by AFE }\ell^1\text{ estimates.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Ordinary/singular classification becomes exact

This transfer proof suggests a clean definition.

## Ordinary zero-separated packet

\[
I^\ast\text{ is ordinary if}
\]

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\sup|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|\le Q^{C_j}.
\]

## Near-singular packet

If

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
<
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

then the packet is not covered by the ordinary derivative transfer. It belongs to singular/transition analysis.

This is important: the derivative-transfer theorem is not a global smoothness claim. It is exactly the analytic marker separating ordinary and singular behavior.

---

# 6. Connection to Gate 2

From the transfer theorem, we get the bounds used in the downstream proof.

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Then

\[
\|u'\|_\infty
=
\|\mathcal Dq''_{\can}\|_\infty
\le Q^C.
\]

Also

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Using

\[
\sup|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^C,\qquad k\le7,
\]

we get

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Therefore G2-A is valid.

For G2-B, we need

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C,
\]

which is also included.

For D3a wall escape, we need

\[
|u'|=|q'''|\le Q^C.
\]

Also included.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated transfer}
\Rightarrow
\text{all local derivative assumptions for downstream Gate 2 and wall escape.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Remaining possible issue: \(q\) itself versus \(q''\)

The theorem directly bounds

\[
q''_{\can}=u
\]

and its derivatives. But G2-B also uses

\[
q,\quad q'.
\]

If \(q\) is a primitive of \(q''_{\can}\), bounds on \(q''\) do not automatically bound \(q,q'\) without constants of integration.

So the canonical definition of \(q\) must also include a normalization or direct meromorphic formula.

We need one of:

1. direct polynomial bounds for \(q,q'\) from their own canonical definitions;

2. normalization of \(q,q'\) on the packet plus integration of \(q''\);

3. rewriting all identities in terms of \(q_0,q_0',u\) with separate polynomial bounds for \(q_0,q_0'\).

This is a real bookkeeping point.

The downstream package should assume explicitly:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},\qquad0\le k\le7.
}
\]

Then note that this follows from the completed meromorphic formula for \(q\), not merely from \(q''\).

If only \(q''\) is meromorphic-controlled, add separate primitive bounds:

\[
|q|+|q'|\le Q^C.
\]

---

# 8. Final theorem with primitive bounds

### Ordinary Zero-Separated Canonical Complexity

Assume the canonical functions \(q,q',q''_{\can}\) arise from the completed meromorphic object and the packet tube is polynomially zero-separated:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty+\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^C,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the exact local analytic-complexity package needed downstream.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transfer estimate is provable under ordinary zero-separated tube condition.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need explicit canonical meromorphic formula for }q\text{, not only }q''.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE termwise absolute estimates should be avoided.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If tube zero-distance fails, route to singular/transition branch.}
}
\]

Thus the next proof step is finite and concrete:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Audit canonical definitions of }q,q',q''_{\can}
\text{ as completed meromorphic log-derivative objects.}
}
\]

Once that audit is done, the derivative-transfer estimate is essentially closed for ordinary packets.

## Continued Agent 1 / A attack: primitive bounds and final transfer closure

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The ordinary derivative-transfer package closes if one adds a primitive-normalization clause for }q,q'.
}
\]

The prior transfer proof gives polynomial bounds for

\[
u=q''_{\can}
\]

and its normalized derivatives:

\[
\mathcal D^j u,\qquad 0\le j\le5.
\]

But Gate 2 identities also use

\[
q,\qquad q'.
\]

So the missing final detail is not analytic complexity of \(u\); it is controlling the two constants of integration. This can be handled in either of two ways:

\[
\boxed{
\text{direct meromorphic formulas for }q,q',
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{basepoint normalization }|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C.
}
\]

With either one, the full local package follows.

---

# 1. Normalized primitive transfer

Work in normalized coordinate

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal D=\partial_x.
\]

Assume the zero-separated tube transfer gives

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_x^j u|\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad
0\le j\le5,
\]

where

\[
u=q''.
\]

Let \(I^\ast\) have normalized length \(O(Q^C)\), and in the ordinary local packet case usually \(O(1)\).

If at one basepoint \(x_0\in I^\ast\),

\[
|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^{C_0},
\]

then for \(x\in I^\ast\),

\[
q'(x)=q'(x_0)+\int_{x_0}^{x}u(y)\,dy,
\]

so

\[
|q'(x)|\le Q^{C_0}+|I^\ast|\sup_{I^\ast}|u|
\le Q^{C'}.
\]

Similarly,

\[
q(x)=q(x_0)+(x-x_0)q'(x_0)+\int_{x_0}^{x}(x-y)u(y)\,dy,
\]

so

\[
|q(x)|\le Q^{C'}.
\]

Then higher derivatives follow from \(u\):

\[
q''=u,\quad q'''=u',\quad q^{(4)}=u'',\quad \ldots
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_x^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

So primitive control reduces to one polynomial basepoint bound.

---

# 2. Where basepoint bounds can come from

There are three possible sources.

## A. Direct canonical definition

If \(q\) is itself a canonical phase/log-derivative quantity, then the same zero-separated meromorphic argument applies directly:

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ldots,q^{(7)}
\]

are fixed finite combinations of completed log-derivative derivatives and gamma/background terms.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k}
}
\]

follows immediately from ordinary zero-distance.

This is the cleanest route.

## B. Normalization / admissibility

If \(q\) is a normalized local variable in the geometric model, then ordinary admissibility should include

\[
|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C.
\]

Then primitive integration closes the estimate.

## C. Local energy plus zero-separated phase control

If \(q\) is not directly meromorphic but its derivatives are, one can still choose a packet center normalization. Without such a normalization, \(q\) could be shifted by large affine terms without changing \(q''\). Since Gate 2 contains \(q\) itself, this ambiguity must be fixed somewhere.

Therefore the proof must explicitly state one of A or B.

---

# 3. Gate 2 local complexity theorem

The downstream local analytic package should be stated as:

### Ordinary local complexity theorem

Let \(I^\ast\) be an ordinary zero-separated packet with

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Assume the tube zero-distance condition

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Assume also either:

\[
q\text{ has a direct completed-meromorphic formula,}
\]

or

\[
|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C
\quad\text{at one point }x_0\in I^\ast.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty
+
\|\Gamma_G'\|_\infty
+
\|\Gamma_{G,2}'\|_\infty
\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This supplies all local derivative assumptions for:

\[
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction},
\]

\[
\text{G2-B integral rigidity},
\]

\[
\text{D3a wall escape}.
\]

---

# 4. Check \(g,h\) derivative bounds explicitly

Recall

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
g'=q'''-6q'+6q^2q'.
\]

Under

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q'''|\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
|g'|\le Q^C.
\]

Next,

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

For \(h'\),

\[
h'=2(q')^3+4qq'q''-\frac16g'''.
\]

Since \(g''' \) involves \(q^{(5)}\) plus polynomial lower-order terms, it is enough to have

\[
\sup|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^C,\qquad k\le5.
\]

The safer \(k\le7\) package covers all projection/gauge and row-conversion slack.

Thus the local Lipschitz constants are polynomial.

---

# 5. Does zero-distance control \(q,q'\) directly?

If

\[
q
\]

is a phase or logarithmic derivative primitive of the completed object, the direct meromorphic formula likely has the form

\[
q(t)
=
\sum_{r\le r_0}a_r(t)\Re/\Im\left[\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)\right]
+
\text{gamma/background}.
\]

Then the zero-distance proof gives \(q\) and every derivative directly.

If instead \(q\) is a local coordinate obtained by integrating \(q''_{\can}\), then the basepoint condition is unavoidable.

So the canonical audit must answer:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }q\text{ directly canonical, or only a primitive of }q''_{\can}?
}
\]

If direct: zero-distance closes all bounds.

If primitive: add basepoint normalization.

---

# 6. Ordinary/singular interaction

If the zero-distance condition fails,

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
<
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

then derivatives of \(q''_{\can}\) can be large:

\[
|u^{(j)}|\sim \operatorname{dist}^{-j-\kappa}.
\]

This is not a defect. It is exactly why the singular branch exists.

So the transfer theorem should be tied explicitly to ordinary coverage:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated packets satisfy local complexity;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{near-zero packets route to singular/transition branch.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final closed downstream implication

With the local complexity theorem in place:

## G2-A

Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure gives \(m_\ast\), and Lipschitz thickening gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A}
\]

on \(J\).

## G2-B

Integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C Q^{-2A/5}|J'|.
\]

But

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\text{on }J'
\]

gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction for \(A\) large.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + ordinary local complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This is a significant downstream simplification.

---

# 8. Remaining formal tasks

The attack now leaves a finite checklist:

1. **Canonical formula audit**
   
   Identify \(q,q',q''_{\can}\) as completed meromorphic objects or specify primitive normalization.

2. **Zero-distance definition**
   
   Define ordinary packets by polynomial zero-separation in a tube.

3. **Log-derivative bound citation/proof**
   
   State the partial-fraction/local-zero-count lemma.

4. **Primitive normalization**
   
   If needed, state

   \[
   |q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C.
   \]

5. **Integral-rigidity cutoff proof**
   
   Formalize the energy estimates with all cutoff losses.

Once these are written, Gate 2 is no longer a named mysterious input; it is a conditional local theorem under ordinary zero-separated complexity.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative transfer: essentially closed under ordinary zero-distance plus primitive normalization.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2: reduced to formal cutoff proof + local complexity theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Key audit: canonical status of }q\text{ itself.}
}
\]

The most precise theorem now is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Ordinary Zero-Separated Local Complexity}
+
\textbf{Integral Rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\textbf{Gate 2}.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:02:29)

I’ll now try to remove the last loose assumption: separate primitive bounds for \(q,q'\). The key is that on the extracted interval \(g\) is small and \(u=q''\) is polynomially bounded, so \(F(q)=6q-2q^3\) is polynomially bounded; this already forces \(q\) to be polynomially bounded.

_Thought for 26s_

## Continued Agent 1 / A attack: removing unnecessary primitive assumptions

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Separate primitive bounds for }q,q'\text{ may not be needed for Gate 2 itself.}
}
\]

For the Gate 2 argument, the strongest local package can be reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
|u|+|u'|+|g'|+|h'|\le Q^C
}
\]

for extraction, plus

\[
\boxed{
|u|\le Q^C
}
\]

on the interval where integral rigidity is applied. Once \(g\) is small on that interval, the identity

\[
u=F(q)+g,\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

forces \(q\) to be polynomially bounded. The integral-rigidity proof can then control \(q'\) through the \(h\)-equation rather than assuming \(|q'|\le Q^C\) a priori.

So the prior primitive-normalization requirement can be weakened:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For Gate 2, it is enough to transfer canonical bounds for }u,g,h
\text{ and their first derivatives, not all primitives.}
}
\]

A direct canonical formula for \(q\) is still useful for row conversion and bookkeeping, but it may not be necessary for the Gate 2 analytic bridge.

---

# 1. What extraction really needs

The two-threshold extraction step only needs Lipschitz bounds for:

\[
u,
\qquad
g=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

That is,

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\|g'\|_\infty+\|h'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

It does **not** need independent bounds for \(q\) or \(q'\).

Therefore, for extraction, the transfer estimate can be stated directly as:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
\left(
|u|+|\mathcal D u|+|g|+|\mathcal D g|+|h|+|\mathcal D h|
\right)
\le Q^C.
}
\]

If \(u,g,h\) are canonical meromorphic/log-derivative quantities, ordinary zero-separated tube bounds give this directly.

---

# 2. Bound \(q\) from \(u\) and \(g\) on the rigidity interval

On the interval \(J\) produced by extraction, we have

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

and canonical transfer gives

\[
|u|\le Q^C.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

we get

\[
|F(q)|\le |u|+|g|\le Q^C.
\]

For large \(|q|\),

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\asymp |q|^3.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|q|\le Q^C
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

This removes the need for a primitive bound for \(q\) in the Gate 2 rigidity step.

---

# 3. Avoid assuming \(|q'|\le Q^C\)

The integral-rigidity proof initially seemed to need a polynomial bound for \(q'\). But one can structure the kinetic estimate so that \(q'\) is controlled by the equation

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

itself.

Recall the kinetic multiplier:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
=
2\int \phi q s_\delta(q)(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

After integrating by parts,

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expanding,

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The apparently dangerous term is

\[
\varepsilon\int \phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2.
\]

But \(s_\delta''\) is supported where

\[
\delta\le |q|\le 2\delta.
\]

There,

\[
(q')^2
\le
\delta^{-1}|q|(q')^2.
\]

Since

\[
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2},
\]

this term is bounded by

\[
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\int_{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta}
\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

This is a small multiple of the kinetic quantity if

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\ll1.
\]

With the later choice

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5},
\]

we have

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{2/5}\ll1.
\]

So this term can be absorbed into the left-hand side.

The \(s_\delta'(q)q''\) term is supported in the same transition region. There,

\[
|q|\lesssim\delta,
\]

and

\[
q''=F(q)+g=O(\delta+\varepsilon).
\]

Thus

\[
\varepsilon\int \phi |s_\delta'(q)q''|
\le
C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}(\delta+\varepsilon)|J|
\le
C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

The term involving

\[
\phi' s_\delta'(q)q'
\]

is handled by Cauchy–Schwarz and absorbed using the kinetic term plus a polynomial cutoff cost.

Therefore the kinetic estimate can be obtained without an independent \(|q'|\) bound.

---

# 4. Refined kinetic estimate

Let

\[
K_\delta
=
\int \phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

Then the multiplier estimate gives

\[
K_\delta
\le
C\varepsilon |J|
+
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}K_\delta
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}(\delta+\varepsilon)|J|
+
\text{cutoff-boundary terms}.
\]

For

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5},
\]

the coefficient

\[
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
=
C\varepsilon^{2/5}
\]

is small. Absorb it:

\[
\boxed{
K_\delta
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

Then on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
(q')^2\le (2\delta)^{-1}|q|(q')^2,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|.
}
\]

This is even better than the earlier schematic \(\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\), provided the boundary terms are handled carefully. If boundary terms force extra \(\delta^{-2}\), we still have the safe bound

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

Either bound gives a positive rigidity exponent.

---

# 5. Potential estimate without a \(q'\) a priori bound

The potential estimate tests

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q).
\]

After integration by parts, terms include:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'.
\]

Here:

- \(F'(q)=6-6q^2\), polynomially bounded because \(|q|\le Q^C\);
- on the support of \(\chi_\delta'\), \(|q|\sim\delta\), so \(F(q)=O(\delta)\), while \(|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}\), hence \(\chi_\delta'F(q)=O(1)\);
- the \(q'\)-terms are controlled by the kinetic estimate.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{|q|\ge3\delta}\phi |F(q)|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M}|J|
}
\]

for some fixed \(M\). The earlier \(M=3\) is plausible; even \(M=5\) would be acceptable, giving exponent \(2/(M+2)\) after optimization.

So the proof does not require an independent \(q'\)-bound. It only needs:

\[
|q|\le Q^C,
\]

which follows from \(|u|+|g|\le Q^C\).

---

# 6. General exponent if cutoff loss is \(\delta^{-M}\)

Suppose the final bound is

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(\delta^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-M}\right)|J|.
\]

Optimize with

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/(M+2)}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2/(M+2)},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-M}=\varepsilon^{2/(M+2)}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/(M+2)}|J|.
}
\]

Any fixed \(M\) gives a positive power of \(\varepsilon\), enough for Gate 2.

Thus exact \(\delta^{-3}\) bookkeeping is not essential. What matters is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cutoff losses are finite polynomial powers of }\delta^{-1}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Weaker local complexity theorem

The Gate 2 proof can now use the following weaker package.

### Minimal Gate 2 local complexity

On the ordinary interval \(J\), assume:

\[
|u|+|g|+|h|+|u'|+|g'|+|h'|\le Q^C.
\]

Then:

1. G2-A extraction works.

2. Integral rigidity works because:
   - \(|q|\le Q^C\) follows from \(u=F(q)+g\);
   - \(q'\) is controlled in energy by the \(h\)-equation;
   - no pointwise \(q'\)-bound is necessary.

This is weaker than requiring

\[
|q|+|q'|+\cdots+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
\]

a priori.

That is a meaningful improvement.

---

# 8. Transfer estimate now only needs \(u,g,h\)

The ordinary meromorphic transfer should target:

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
g=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and their first normalized derivatives.

If these are canonical meromorphic quantities with ordinary zero-separated tube control, then

\[
|u|+|u'|+|g|+|g'|+|h|+|h'|\le Q^C
\]

follows from the same log-derivative lemma.

This avoids needing to bound the primitive \(q'\) directly.

One still needs \(q\) in

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

but on the rigidity interval,

\[
|q|\le Q^C
\]

is forced by

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

So primitive \(q\) control is local, not global.

---

# 9. Updated Gate 2 theorem

### Gate 2 from minimal local complexity

Assume:

1. Gate 1;

2. if Gate 2 fails, two-threshold extraction gives \(J\) with

   \[
   |u|\ge Q^{-C},
   \qquad
   |g|+|h|\le\varepsilon;
   \]

3. local complexity:

   \[
   |u|+|g|+|h|+|u'|+|g'|+|h'|\le Q^C
   \]

   on \(J\);

4. normalized identities:

   \[
   g=u-6q+2q^3,
   \qquad
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
   \]

Then cutoff energy estimates imply

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|
\]

for some fixed \(c>0\). For \(\varepsilon\) small enough, this contradicts

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on \(J'\). Hence Gate 2 holds.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Primitive }q'\text{ bounds are probably unnecessary for Gate 2.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need only canonical bounds for }u,g,h\text{ and their first derivatives.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }h\text{-equation supplies energy control of }q'.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral rigidity survives any fixed cutoff-loss exponent.}
}
\]

This is a real simplification of the transfer estimate and Gate 2 proof.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:09:29)

_Thought for 17s_

## Continued Agent 1 / A attack: strengthening the integral-rigidity proof

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The integral-rigidity lemma can be proved more cleanly using a }q\text{-multiplier rather than a sign multiplier.}
}
\]

The previous proof used a smoothed sign cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) to get a positive term

\[
|q|(q')^2.
\]

That works but creates technical transition terms involving \(s_\delta'\) and \(s_\delta''\). A cleaner route is to multiply the \(h\)-equation by \(q\)-weighted cutoffs. This gives direct control of

\[
q^2(q')^2,
\]

which is exactly what is needed away from \(q=0\), because on \(|q|\ge\delta\),

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2.
\]

This avoids sign-cutoff singularities and makes the proof more robust.

---

# 1. Equations

Work in normalized coordinates. Let

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Assume on an interval \(J\)

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon.
\]

Let \(J'\Subset J\). The target is

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^c |J'|
}
\]

for some fixed \(c>0\). The previous expected value was \(c=2/5\); the cleaner proof may give a different positive exponent. Any fixed \(c>0\) is enough for Gate 2.

---

# 2. Use a \(q\)-multiplier for kinetic energy

Choose a cutoff \(\phi\in C_c^\infty(J)\), with

\[
0\le \phi\le1,
\qquad
\phi\equiv1\text{ on }J',
\]

and with polynomial derivative bounds.

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi q
\]

and integrate:

\[
\int \phi qh
=
2\int \phi q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi qg''.
\]

Integrate the \(g''\)-term by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi qg''
=
\int g(\phi q)''.
\]

Now

\[
(\phi q)''
=
\phi''q+2\phi'q'+\phi q''.
\]

Hence

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le
\varepsilon\int
\left(
|\phi''q|+2|\phi'q'|+\phi |q''|
\right).
\]

The \(q\) term is polynomially bounded once \(u\) and \(g\) are polynomially bounded, because

\[
F(q)=u-g
\]

and \(F(q)=6q-2q^3\) grows cubically. Thus

\[
|q|\le Q^C.
\]

The \(q''\) term is

\[
q''=u=F(q)+g,
\]

so it is also polynomially bounded.

The \(q'\)-term can be controlled by Cauchy–Schwarz using the kinetic quantity itself. On the support of \(\phi'\), choose \(\phi=\psi^2\), so

\[
|\phi'|^2\le C Q^C\phi.
\]

Then

\[
\varepsilon\int |\phi' q'|
\le
\varepsilon
\left(\int \phi q^2(q')^2\right)^{1/2}
\left(\int \frac{|\phi'|^2}{\phi q^2}\right)^{1/2}.
\]

This has a problem near \(q=0\). To avoid it, localize away from small \(q\). That is exactly what we need.

---

# 3. Localized \(q\)-multiplier

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) satisfy

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad (|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

with

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1},
\qquad
|\chi_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

Multiply \(h\) by

\[
\phi\,\chi_\delta(q)\,q.
\]

Then

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta qh
=
2\int \phi\chi_\delta q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi\chi_\delta q g''.
\]

After two integrations by parts,

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta q g''
=
\int g(\phi\chi_\delta(q)q)''.
\]

The derivatives of \(\chi_\delta(q)q\) cost powers of \(\delta^{-1}\), but crucially they are supported where

\[
\delta\le |q|\le2\delta.
\]

On that transition region,

\[
|q|\asymp \delta,
\]

and therefore terms with \((q')^2\) are still controlled by the same weighted kinetic quantity

\[
K_\delta
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta q^2(q')^2,
\]

up to fixed powers of \(\delta^{-1}\).

The result is an estimate of the form

\[
K_\delta
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M_1}K_\delta
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M_2}|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^\alpha
\]

with \(\alpha>0\) small enough that

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M_1}\ll1.
\]

Then absorb the \(K_\delta\)-term:

\[
\boxed{
K_\delta
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M}|J|
}
\]

for some fixed \(M\).

Consequently, on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M-2}|J|.
}
\]

This is the kinetic bound needed for the next step.

---

# 4. Potential estimate

Now use

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Let \(\theta_\delta(q)\) be another cutoff with

\[
\theta_\delta=0\quad (|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\theta_\delta=1\quad (|q|\ge3\delta).
\]

Test against

\[
\phi\,\theta_\delta(q)\,F(q).
\]

Then

\[
\int \phi\theta_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\theta_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\theta_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is \(O(Q^C\varepsilon |J|)\). For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\theta_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\theta_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

The derivative expands into

\[
\phi'\theta_\delta F(q)q',
\]

\[
\phi\theta_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
\phi\theta_\delta F'(q)(q')^2.
\]

On the support of \(\theta_\delta\) and \(\theta_\delta'\), we have \(|q|\ge2\delta\), so the kinetic estimate controls the \((q')^2\)-terms.

For the \(\phi'Fq'\) term, use Cauchy–Schwarz and absorb a small portion of the left-hand side:

\[
\left|\int\phi'\theta_\delta Fq'\right|
\le
\eta\int\phi\theta_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta\int\frac{|\phi'|^2}{\phi}\theta_\delta(q')^2.
\]

The last term is controlled by the kinetic bound.

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M'}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Small-\(q\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3=O(\delta).
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

we have

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Optimize

Combining large and small \(q\) regions:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-M'}
\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/(M'+2)}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2
=
\varepsilon^{2/(M'+2)}
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-M'}
=
\varepsilon^{2/(M'+2)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{c}|J'|,
}
\]

where

\[
c=\frac{2}{M'+2}>0.
\]

So even if the precise cutoff bookkeeping worsens the exponent from \(2/5\), Gate 2 still follows.

This robustness is important.

---

# 7. Consequence for Gate 2

The two-threshold extraction gives an interval \(J\) where

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon.
\]

Then on \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
\]

Integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|.
\]

Choose the Gate 2 failure exponent so that

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^c<\frac12\tau^2.
\]

Contradiction.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + two-threshold extraction + integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 8. What remains to formalize

The proof now needs exact cutoff bookkeeping, but the conceptual structure is robust. The remaining tasks are:

1. specify \(\phi,\chi_\delta,\theta_\delta\) with derivative bounds;

2. write the exact estimate for

   \[
   (\phi\chi_\delta(q)q)'';
   \]

3. show all transition terms are bounded by

   \[
   Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M}(1+K_\delta)
   \]

   with fixed \(M\);

4. absorb the \(K_\delta\)-term by choosing \(\delta=\varepsilon^\alpha\);

5. prove the potential estimate with Cauchy–Schwarz absorption;

6. track the interval shrinkage \(J'\Subset J\).

None of these appears conceptually blocking.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral rigidity is robust: exact exponent may vary, but any }c>0\text{ suffices.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{A }q\text{-multiplier avoids sign-cutoff complications.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No independent }q'\text{ pointwise bound is necessary.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 now reduces to local cutoff bookkeeping plus derivative-complexity transfer.}
}
\]

This is a substantial downstream simplification.
