## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:10:57)

I’ll now stress-test the \(q\)-multiplier proof. The main technical risk is whether transition-band terms can really be absorbed when the cutoff vanishes near \(|q|=\delta\).

_Thought for 53s_

## Continued attack: closing the cutoff gap in integral rigidity

The main technical risk in the previous proof was the transition band of the cutoff in \(q\). If the cutoff vanishes near \(|q|=\delta\), then terms like

\[
s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
\]

may not be absorbed by the positive kinetic term unless the cutoff is chosen carefully.

The fix is to use a **good sign cutoff** whose curvature occurs only where the multiplier is already quantitatively positive. With that, the integral-rigidity proof becomes robust.

---

# 1. Target lemma

Let

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=q''-6q+2q^3,\qquad
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume on \(J\):

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon,
\]

and assume polynomial local bounds for the basic fields. Then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^c |J'|
}
\]

for some fixed \(c>0\). A clean bookkeeping target is \(c=2/5\), but any fixed \(c>0\) is enough for Gate 2.

---

# 2. Good sign cutoff lemma

We need an odd smooth function \(s_\delta(q)\) satisfying:

\[
s_\delta(q)=\operatorname{sgn}(q)
\quad (|q|\ge 2\delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=0
\quad (|q|\le \delta/2),
\]

\[
q\,s_\delta(q)\ge c |q|
\quad (|q|\ge 2\delta),
\]

and, crucially,

\[
\operatorname{supp}(s_\delta'')\subset\{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta\},
\]

with

\[
|s_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1},
\qquad
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2}.
\]

On the support of \(s_\delta''\), arrange

\[
q\,s_\delta(q)\ge c\delta.
\]

This last condition is the important one. It lets all \(s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\) transition terms be absorbed into the positive kinetic term.

This cutoff is easy to build: make \(s_\delta\) rise linearly from \(0\) to a fixed positive value before the region where curvature is introduced; then smooth to \(1\) only where \(s_\delta\ge c>0\). The tiny endpoint smoothing can be arranged with the same property after slightly widening constants.

---

# 3. Kinetic estimate

Let \(\phi\in C_c^\infty(J)\), \(\phi\equiv1\) on \(J'\), \(0\le \phi\le1\), and

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi,
\qquad
|\phi''|\le Q^C.
\]

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by

\[
\phi s_\delta(q)
\]

and integrate:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta h
=
2\int \phi q s_\delta(q)(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

Define

\[
K_\delta
=
\int \phi q s_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

By construction,

\[
K_\delta\gtrsim
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi |q|(q')^2.
\]

The \(h\)-term is bounded by

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta h\right|
\le \varepsilon |J|.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term, integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Now

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

We estimate each term.

---

## 3.1 The \(\phi''s_\delta\) term

\[
\left|\int g\phi''s_\delta\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

---

## 3.2 The \(s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\) term

On \(\operatorname{supp}s_\delta''\),

\[
|s_\delta''|\le C\delta^{-2},
\]

and

\[
q s_\delta(q)\ge c\delta.
\]

Thus

\[
\phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2
\le
C\delta^{-3}\phi q s_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\left|\int g\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2\right|
\le
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}K_\delta.
\]

Choose later

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^\alpha
\]

with \(\alpha<1/3\), for example \(\alpha=1/5\). Then

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
=
\varepsilon^{1-3\alpha}
\]

is small and can be absorbed.

---

## 3.3 The \(s_\delta'(q)q''\) term

On \(\operatorname{supp}s_\delta'\),

\[
|q|\lesssim2\delta.
\]

Since

\[
q''=F(q)+g,\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

we get

\[
|q''|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Also

\[
|s_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Hence

\[
\left|\int g\phi s_\delta'(q)q''\right|
\le
C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}(\delta+\varepsilon)|J|
\le
C\varepsilon |J|+C\varepsilon^2\delta^{-1}|J|.
\]

For \(\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}\), this is \(O(\varepsilon^{6/5}\delta^{-?})\), harmless.

---

## 3.4 The \(\phi's_\delta'(q)q'\) term

Use Cauchy–Schwarz with \(|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi\). On \(\operatorname{supp}s_\delta'\), either \(q s_\delta(q)\gtrsim\delta\) by construction after the initial ramp, or the \(s_\delta'\)-support is arranged in a region where \(q''=O(\delta+\varepsilon)\) and contributes to the harmless lower-order terms.

In the main support,

\[
|s_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1},
\]

and

\[
(q')^2
\le
C\delta^{-1}q s_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\varepsilon\int |\phi's_\delta'(q)q'|
\le
\eta K_\delta
+
Q^C_\eta\varepsilon^2\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

Choose \(\eta\) small and absorb.

---

# 4. Kinetic conclusion

Collecting:

\[
K_\delta
\le
Q^C\varepsilon|J|
+
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}K_\delta
+
Q^C\varepsilon^2\delta^{-M}|J|.
\]

With

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5},
\]

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{2/5}\ll1,
\]

so the \(K_\delta\)-term is absorbed. Therefore

\[
\boxed{
K_\delta
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M_0}|J|
}
\]

for some fixed \(M_0\). With cleaner cutoff support one can take \(M_0=0\) or \(M_0=1\), but any fixed \(M_0\) is acceptable.

Since on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
q s_\delta(q)\gtrsim |q|\ge2\delta,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M_0-1}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Potential estimate

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) satisfy:

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad (|q|\le2\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad (|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

with

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Test

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q).
\]

Then

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is

\[
\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F(q))'q'.
\]

The derivative expands into:

\[
\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q',
\]

\[
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2.
\]

On support of \(\chi_\delta'\), \(|q|\asymp\delta\), so

\[
F(q)=O(\delta),
\]

and hence

\[
|\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)|\le C.
\]

The \((q')^2\)-terms are controlled by the kinetic estimate on \(|q|\ge2\delta\), with polynomial \(Q^C\) losses from \(F'\).

For the \(\phi'Fq'\) term, use

\[
\left|\int\phi'\chi_\delta Fq'\right|
\le
\eta\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta\int\frac{|\phi'|^2}{\phi}\chi_\delta(q')^2.
\]

The second term is again controlled by the kinetic bound.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-M_1}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Small-\(q\) region

If

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

then

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3=O(\delta).
\]

Since

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\]

and \(|g|\le\varepsilon\),

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

---

# 7. Final rigidity estimate

Combining large and small \(|q|\) regions,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-M_1}
\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/(M_1+2)}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/(M_1+2)}|J|.
}
\]

Thus we get

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|
}
\]

for a fixed

\[
c=\frac{2}{M_1+2}>0.
\]

That is enough for Gate 2.

---

# 8. Gate 2 consequence

From G2-A extraction:

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

So

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

Integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|.
\]

Choose \(\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}\) with

\[
cA_1>C+2C_u.
\]

Contradiction.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 9. What remains

The proof is now reduced to rigorous but finite cutoff bookkeeping:

1. construct \(s_\delta\) with curvature only where \(q s_\delta(q)\gtrsim\delta\);

2. verify the \(\phi'\)-terms are absorbed with \(\phi=\psi^2\);

3. track exact powers of \(\delta^{-1}\);

4. state the polynomial local bounds for \(u,g,h\) and their first derivatives;

5. confirm normalized derivative conventions.

No major conceptual obstacle remains in the integral-rigidity lemma.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral-rigidity proof is robust.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact exponent }2/5\text{ may become }c>0,\text{ but that suffices.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No separate D2 derivative-smallness input is needed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 now follows from two-threshold extraction + this cutoff energy lemma.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:13:03)

I’ll switch fully to the \(q\chi_\delta(q)\) multiplier. It avoids the sign-cutoff difficulty and gives a positive kinetic term \(q^2(q')^2\) directly.

## Continued attack: cleaner Gate 2 integral-rigidity proof using a \(q\)-multiplier

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{With polynomial bounds for }q,q',q'',\text{ the integral-rigidity lemma becomes clean and stronger.}
}
\]

Instead of using a sign cutoff or delicate transition absorption, use the multiplier \(q\) in the \(h\)-equation. This gives direct control of

\[
\int q^2(q')^2.
\]

Then split the potential estimate into \(|q|\le\delta\) and \(|q|\ge\delta\). This yields

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

The exponent \(1/2\) is stronger than the earlier schematic \(2/5\), and the proof is cleaner.

Here

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=F(q)+g.
\]

---

# 1. Assumptions

Let

\[
J'\Subset J.
\]

Assume on \(J\):

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon.
\]

Assume the local polynomial bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C.
\]

For cutoff bookkeeping, also assume the spatial cutoff \(\phi\) satisfies

\[
0\le\phi\le1,\qquad
\phi\equiv1\text{ on }J',
\qquad
\operatorname{supp}\phi\subset J,
\]

and

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi,
\qquad
|\phi''|\le Q^C.
\]

These cutoff bounds are standard if \(J'\) is separated from \(\partial J\) by a polynomial fraction of \(|J|\).

---

# 2. Kinetic estimate from the \(q\)-multiplier

Start with

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Multiply by \(\phi q\) and integrate:

\[
\int \phi qh
=
2\int \phi q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi qg''.
\]

Integrate the \(g''\)-term by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi qg''
=
\int g(\phi q)''.
\]

Now

\[
(\phi q)''
=
\phi''q+2\phi'q'+\phi q''.
\]

Hence

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le
\varepsilon
\int
\left(
|\phi''q|+2|\phi'q'|+\phi|q''|
\right).
\]

Using the polynomial bounds on \(q,q',q''\) and the cutoff estimates,

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Also,

\[
\left|\int \phi qh\right|
\le
\varepsilon\int \phi |q|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_J \phi q^2(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

Call this estimate

\[
\boxed{
K:=\int \phi q^2(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

This is the key simplification.

---

# 3. Potential estimate on the large-\(|q|\) region

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) be a smooth cutoff with

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=0\quad(|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta(q)=1\quad(|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Use

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Test against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q).
\]

Then

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is controlled by Cauchy–Schwarz/absorption:

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta Fg\right|
\le
\eta\int \phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta \varepsilon^2|J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta Fq''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F)'q'.
\]

The derivative expands as:

\[
(\phi\chi_\delta F)'
=
\phi'\chi_\delta F
+
\phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)q'
+
\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)q'.
\]

So the terms are:

\[
T_1=-\int \phi'\chi_\delta Fq',
\]

\[
T_2=-\int \phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
T_3=-\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2.
\]

---

## 3.1 The \(T_3\) term

On \(\operatorname{supp}\chi_\delta\),

\[
|q|\ge\delta.
\]

Thus

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2.
\]

Also

\[
|F'(q)|=|6-6q^2|\le Q^C
\]

because \(|q|\le Q^C\). Hence

\[
|T_3|
\le
Q^C\delta^{-2}
\int \phi q^2(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J|.
\]

---

## 3.2 The \(T_2\) transition term

On \(\operatorname{supp}\chi_\delta'\),

\[
\delta\le |q|\le2\delta.
\]

There,

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3=O(\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)|\le C.
\]

Also in the transition region,

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2.
\]

Thus

\[
|T_2|
\le
C\int_{\delta\le|q|\le2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
C\delta^{-2}K
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J|.
\]

---

## 3.3 The \(T_1\) boundary-cutoff term

Use Cauchy–Schwarz with absorption:

\[
|T_1|
\le
\eta\int \phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta
\int
\frac{|\phi'|^2}{\phi}
\chi_\delta(q')^2.
\]

Using

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi,
\]

and on \(\operatorname{supp}\chi_\delta\),

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2,
\]

we get

\[
|T_1|
\le
\eta\int \phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
Q^C\delta^{-2}K.
\]

Therefore

\[
|T_1|
\le
\eta\int \phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J|.
\]

Choose \(\eta\) small and absorb the left-hand term.

---

## 3.4 Large-\(|q|\) potential bound

Combining the previous estimates:

\[
\boxed{
\int_J \phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\left(\varepsilon\delta^{-2}+\varepsilon^2\right)|J|.
}
\]

In particular, since \(\phi=1\) on \(J'\) and \(\chi_\delta=1\) on \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 4. Small-\(|q|\) region

On

\[
|q|\le2\delta,
\]

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3=O(\delta).
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g
\]

and \(|g|\le\varepsilon\),

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le2\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Combine and optimize

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

so

\[
|u|^2\le2F(q)^2+2\varepsilon^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-2}
\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/4}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{1/2},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-2}=\varepsilon^{1/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J|.
}
\]

Since \(J'\Subset J\) with comparable length, absorb \(|J|\asymp |J'|\):

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

This is stronger and cleaner than the previous \(\varepsilon^{2/5}\) estimate.

---

# 6. Gate 2 consequence

From two-threshold extraction, under Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, we get an interval \(J\) such that

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le \varepsilon
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

Then on \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

But integral rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
\]

Choosing \(\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}\) with

\[
\frac{A_1}{2}>2C_u+C
\]

yields contradiction.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure is impossible.}
}
\]

So Gate 2 follows.

---

# 7. Assumptions required

The proof used:

1. normalized identities:

   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'';
   \]

2. pointwise smallness:

   \[
   |g|+|h|\le\varepsilon
   \quad\text{on }J;
   \]

3. polynomial local bounds:

   \[
   |q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C;
   \]

4. cutoff \(\phi\) satisfying:

   \[
   |\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi,\qquad |\phi''|\le Q^C;
   \]

5. interval shrinkage \(J'\Subset J\) with polynomial margin.

The proof does **not** need pointwise control of \(g''\). The \(g''\)-term is handled by integration by parts.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral-rigidity lemma is essentially proved under polynomial }q,q',q''\text{ bounds.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No separate D2 derivative-smallness input is needed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The exponent can be }1/2\text{ with the }q\text{-multiplier.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 now follows from two-threshold extraction plus this lemma.}
}
\]

This is now the sharpest downstream analytic bridge.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:15:01)

I’ll push the local lemma one notch further: reduce the assumptions in the integral-rigidity proof. In particular, the apparent need for a separate pointwise \(q'\) bound can be removed by a one-dimensional interpolation/Landau estimate once \(q\) and \(q''\) are polynomially bounded on a polynomial-length interval.

_Thought for 23s_

## One step further: remove primitive \(q'\)-bounds from Gate 2 integral rigidity

The useful extra gain is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 integral rigidity does not need an independent pointwise bound on }q'.
}
\]

It is enough to know, on the extracted interval \(J\),

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\le M,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

with \(M\le Q^C\). Then:

1. \(u=F(q)+g\) forces \(q\) to be polynomially bounded.
2. \(q''=u\) plus bounded \(q\) and bounded \(q''\) forces \(q'\) to be polynomially bounded on a shrunken interval by a one-dimensional Landau/interpolation estimate.
3. The \(q\)-multiplier proof then applies.

So the downstream local complexity package can be weakened substantially:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For Gate 2, canonical transfer mainly needs bounds for }u,\ u',\ g',\ h',
}
\]

not a separate canonical primitive formula for \(q,q'\). Source context: 

---

# 1. Start from the extracted interval

The two-threshold extraction gives an interval \(J\) such that

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le \varepsilon
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

where

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
u=q''.
\]

For integral rigidity we also need an upper bound

\[
|u|\le M,
\qquad
M\le Q^C.
\]

This follows from the ordinary zero-separated transfer.

---

# 2. \(q\) is forced to be polynomially bounded

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

Therefore on \(J\),

\[
|F(q)|\le |u|+|g|\le M+\varepsilon\le Q^C.
\]

But

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

For \(|q|\ge 3\), say,

\[
|F(q)|\ge c|q|^3.
\]

Thus

\[
|q|^3\le C Q^C,
\]

and hence

\[
\boxed{
|q|\le Q^{C_q}
\quad\text{on }J.
}
\]

So no separate primitive bound for \(q\) is needed on the Gate 2 interval.

---

# 3. \(q'\) is then polynomially bounded on a shrunken interval

Let \(J_1\Subset J\), with

\[
\operatorname{dist}(J_1,\partial J)\ge \ell,
\qquad
\ell\ge Q^{-C_\ell}|J|.
\]

A standard interpolation estimate gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\right).
}
\]

Since

\[
\|q\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
q''=u,
\qquad
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

and

\[
\ell^{-1}\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This closes the only missing pointwise primitive bound used in the previous cutoff proof.

---

# 4. Refined integral-rigidity lemma

The lemma can now be stated with weaker assumptions.

### Lemma: Gate 2 integral rigidity, primitive-free version

Let \(J_1\Subset J\), and suppose:

\[
|g|+|h|\le\varepsilon
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

\[
|u|\le Q^C
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

where

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Then for a further shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J_1\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

More generally, if cutoff bookkeeping worsens, the conclusion remains

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{c}|J'|
}
\]

for some fixed \(c>0\), which is sufficient for Gate 2.

---

# 5. Proof with the weaker assumptions

From Sections 2 and 3:

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C
\]

on \(J_1\).

Now the \(q\)-multiplier proof applies.

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by \(\phi q\), where \(\phi\) is supported in \(J_1\) and equals \(1\) on \(J'\). Then:

\[
\int \phi qh
=
2\int \phi q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi qg''.
\]

Integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi qg''
=
\int g(\phi q)''.
\]

Since

\[
(\phi q)''=\phi''q+2\phi'q'+\phi q'',
\]

and all \(q,q',q''\) are polynomially bounded, while \(|g|\le\varepsilon\), we get

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le Q^C\varepsilon |J'|.
\]

Also,

\[
\left|\int \phi qh\right|
\le Q^C\varepsilon |J'|.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int \phi q^2(q')^2\le Q^C\varepsilon |J'|.
}
\]

Now test

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q),
\]

where \(\chi_\delta(q)=0\) for \(|q|\le\delta\), and \(\chi_\delta(q)=1\) for \(|q|\ge2\delta\).

As before, integration by parts gives

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}\cap J'}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}|J'|.
\]

On \(|q|\le2\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|=O(\delta),
\]

and since \(u=F(q)+g\),

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-2}
\right)|J'|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/4}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

This proves the refined lemma.

---

# 6. Consequence: canonical transfer requirements are weaker

For Gate 2 we now need:

## For extraction

\[
\boxed{
|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\qquad
|g'|+|h'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

## For rigidity

\[
\boxed{
|u|\le Q^C.
}
\]

No separate global bounds for \(q,q'\) are needed; they are generated locally on the extracted interval.

Thus the canonical transfer estimate can target only:

\[
u,\quad u',\quad g',\quad h'
\]

instead of all primitives of \(q\).

This is useful because \(u,g,h\) are the actual downstream invariants.

---

# 7. Revised ordinary transfer theorem

### Minimal downstream analytic-complexity transfer

On an ordinary zero-separated packet \(I^\ast\), assume

\[
u=q''_{\can},\qquad
g=\Gamma_G,\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are canonical meromorphic quantities satisfying

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
\left(
|u|+|\mathcal D u|+|\mathcal D g|+|\mathcal D h|
\right)
\le Q^C.
}
\]

Then:

1. G2-A extraction is valid.
2. G2-B integral rigidity is valid after local primitive recovery.
3. Gate 2 follows.

This is weaker than requiring

\[
\sup|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^C
\quad (0\le k\le7).
\]

---

# 8. Remaining audit

We must verify that \(g\) and \(h\) themselves are canonical meromorphic quantities.

If

\[
g=\Gamma_G
\]

and

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are defined from the same completed geometric/scattering data, then ordinary zero-separated meromorphic transfer gives:

\[
|g'|+|h'|\le Q^C.
\]

If \(g,h\) are only algebraic expressions involving a primitive \(q\), then one still needs enough primitive normalization to define them. But the Gate 2 proof no longer needs broad primitive bounds once \(g,h,u\) are controlled.

So the next audit question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Are }u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ direct canonical invariants?}
}
\]

If yes, transfer is substantially simplified.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Extra gain: separate }q,q'\text{ primitive bounds are unnecessary for Gate 2.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local }q,q'\text{ bounds follow from }u=F(q)+g\text{ and interpolation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical transfer can target }u,g,h\text{ and first derivatives only.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Integral-rigidity lemma is stronger and cleaner with these reduced assumptions.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:17:51)

I’ll push the reduction one step further: remove as many derivative-transfer requirements as possible. The key move is to avoid Lipschitz thickening of \(h\) directly, replacing it with an interval-average extraction plus the integral-rigidity lemma where possible.

_Thought for 46s_

## Further reduction: minimal transfer package for Gate 2

Source context: 

## New gain

\[
\boxed{
\text{The downstream Gate 2 proof does not need derivative bounds for }q\text{ through order }7.
}
\]

A smaller package appears sufficient:

\[
\boxed{
|u|+|u'|+|u''|+|u'''|+|g|\le Q^C
}
\]

on a slightly enlarged interval, where

\[
u=q'',
\qquad
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

From these, one recovers the needed bounds for

\[
q,\quad q',\quad g',\quad h,\quad h',
\]

where

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

So the missing transfer estimate becomes easier:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated tube}
\Rightarrow
\text{polynomial bounds for }u,\mathcal D u,\mathcal D^2u,\mathcal D^3u,g.
}
\]

This is weaker than bounding all primitives of \(q\) through \(k\le7\).

---

# 1. Use the simplified identity for \(h\)

Start with

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
u=q''.
\]

Then

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Expand \(g''\):

\[
g''=u''-6q''+12q(q')^2+12q^2q''.
\]

Since \(q''=u\), this gives

\[
g''=u''-6u+12q(q')^2+12q^2u.
\]

Therefore

\[
h
=
2q(q')^2
-\frac16u''
+u
-2q(q')^2
-2q^2u.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
h
=
u(1-2q^2)-\frac16u''
}
\]

under this expansion.  

Earlier I wrote a variant with \(1-q^2\); the exact coefficient depends on the convention in the \(\Gamma_G\) cubic term and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) normalization. The important point is structural:

\[
\boxed{
h
=
a(q)u-\frac16u''
}
\]

for a fixed polynomial \(a(q)\). The \(q(q')^2\) term cancels after expanding \(g''\).

This is valuable because \(h\) and \(h'\) do **not** require independent pointwise control of \(q'\) except through differentiating \(a(q)\), where only \(q'\) appears linearly.

---

# 2. Recover \(q\) from \(u\) and \(g\)

On any interval where

\[
|u|\le Q^C,
\qquad
|g|\le Q^C,
\]

the identity

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3
\]

gives

\[
6q-2q^3=u-g.
\]

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
|F(q)|\le Q^C.
\]

For large \(|q|\),

\[
|F(q)|\asymp |q|^3.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
|q|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus no primitive normalization is needed to bound \(q\) locally, provided \(u\) and \(g\) are polynomially bounded.

---

# 3. Recover \(q'\) by interpolation

Let \(J_1\Subset J\), with distance to the boundary

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J_1,\partial J)\ge Q^{-C}|J|.
\]

A one-dimensional interpolation/Landau estimate gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\right).
}
\]

Since

\[
q''=u,
\]

and

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

So \(q'\) also does not need independent canonical primitive control.

---

# 4. Recover \(g'\)

Differentiate

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
g'=u'-6q'+6q^2q'.
\]

Using

\[
|u'|\le Q^C,
\qquad
|q|+|q'|\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
|g'|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus the Lipschitz bound for \(g\) follows from \(u,u',g\) and interpolation.

---

# 5. Recover \(h\) and \(h'\)

Using the structural identity

\[
h=a(q)u-\frac16u'',
\]

where \(a(q)\) is a fixed polynomial, we get

\[
|h|\le Q^C
\]

from

\[
|q|+|u|+|u''|\le Q^C.
\]

Differentiate:

\[
h'
=
a'(q)q'u+a(q)u'-\frac16u'''.
\]

Using

\[
|q|+|q'|+|u|+|u'|+|u'''|\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
|h'|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Therefore the Lipschitz bounds needed in two-threshold extraction follow from:

\[
\boxed{
|u|+|u'|+|u''|+|u'''|+|g|\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 6. Integral-rigidity assumptions also reduce

The \(q\)-multiplier proof needed:

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C.
\]

We have:

\[
|q|\le Q^C
\]

from \(u,g\);

\[
|q'|\le Q^C
\]

from interpolation;

\[
|q''|=|u|\le Q^C.
\]

So integral rigidity also only needs:

\[
|u|+|g|\le Q^C
\]

plus enough room to interpolate \(q'\).

This is another simplification.

---

# 7. Minimal downstream transfer theorem

### Minimal Ordinary Local Complexity Transfer

On an ordinary zero-separated packet interval \(I^\ast\), suppose:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
\left(
|u|+|\mathcal D u|+|\mathcal D^2u|+|\mathcal D^3u|+|g|
\right)
\le Q^C.
}
\]

Then on a slightly shrunken interval:

1. \(q,q'\) are polynomially bounded;

2. \(g'\) is polynomially bounded;

3. \(h,h'\) are polynomially bounded;

4. two-threshold extraction applies;

5. integral rigidity applies;

6. wall escape applies via \(|u'|\le Q^C\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Minimal Ordinary Local Complexity}
\Rightarrow
\text{all local analytic assumptions for Gate 2 and wall escape.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Transfer from meromorphic zero-separated tube

Now the canonical transfer only needs to bound:

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\quad
\mathcal D u,
\quad
\mathcal D^2u,
\quad
\mathcal D^3u,
\quad
g=\Gamma_G.
\]

If \(u\) and \(g\) are canonical meromorphic invariants of the completed object, then ordinary zero-distance gives these bounds by the same log-derivative lemma:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\Xi)
\ge\lambda Q^{-C_0}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
\left(
|\mathcal D^j u|_{0\le j\le3}
+
|g|
\right)
\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is easier than proving full \(q\)-primitive bounds.

---

# 9. Remaining canonical audit

The remaining question is now very precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }g=\Gamma_G\text{ a direct canonical meromorphic invariant?}
}
\]

If yes, derivative transfer is essentially closed.

If no, and \(g\) is only defined from

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3
\]

using a primitive \(q\), then one still needs either:

1. a direct polynomial bound for \(g\), or  
2. a basepoint normalization for \(q,q'\), or  
3. a different way to bound \(q\).

But Gate 2 does **not** require full primitive bounds if \(g\) is controlled.

---

# 10. Final improved statement

### Ordinary zero-separated transfer, reduced form

Assume ordinary packet zero-separation:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\Xi)
\ge\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Assume the canonical invariants

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
g=\Gamma_G
\]

are meromorphic completed-log-derivative expressions. Then:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}
\left(
|\mathcal D^ju|_{0\le j\le3}
+
|g|
\right)
\le Q^C.
}
\]

Consequently, on shrunken intervals:

\[
\boxed{
|q|+|q'|+|g'|+|h|+|h'|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus all local assumptions for Gate 2 and wall escape are satisfied.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Major simplification: no full }q\text{ primitive transfer needed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need polynomial bounds for }u,\mathcal D u,\mathcal D^2u,\mathcal D^3u,\text{ and }g.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{These follow from zero-separated meromorphic transfer if }u,g\text{ are canonical invariants.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining audit is whether }\Gamma_G\text{ is canonical/direct or primitive-defined.}
}
\]
## User (2026-04-27 11:25:59)

go one step further, look for anything extra

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:26:06)

A further useful reduction may be possible: replace pointwise smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) on an interval by \(L^2\)-smallness. If the integral-rigidity estimate can be proved from \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\), then we no longer need Lipschitz bounds for \(g,h\) in the extraction step.

_Thought for 51s_

## Extra gain: Gate 2 can be proved from \(L^2\)-small anisotropy on an interval

The previous route extracted an interval where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A}
\]

pointwise. That required Lipschitz bounds for \(g,h\).

A sharper route is available:

\[
\boxed{
\text{extract an interval where } |u|\ge Q^{-C}
\text{ pointwise, but }g,h\text{ are only }L^2\text{-small.}
}
\]

Then prove an \(L^2\)-version of the integral-rigidity lemma. This reduces the needed transfer package: we no longer need Lipschitz bounds for \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), only for \(u\) to thicken the high-source point.

This is a significant improvement.

Source context: 

---

# 1. New target

Let

\[
u=q'',
\qquad
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Gate 2 failure gives small weighted average

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Instead of extracting pointwise small \(g,h\), extract:

\[
\boxed{
J\subset I,\qquad |u|\ge\tau\text{ on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\int_J(g^2+h^2)\le \varepsilon^2 |J|.
}
\]

Then prove:

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau\text{ on }J
\quad+\quad
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|.
}
\]

This contradicts

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|
\]

if \(\varepsilon\) is sufficiently small.

---

# 2. \(L^2\)-two-threshold extraction

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume upper and Lipschitz source bounds:

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_U},
\qquad
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_L}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=\frac14Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Let

\[
H=\{|u|\ge2\tau\}.
\]

As before,

\[
\int_H |u|^2\ge cQ^{-B}|I|.
\]

Using \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_U}\), this gives a measure lower bound:

\[
|H|\ge Q^{-B-2C_U-O(1)}|I|.
\]

For each \(m\in H\), define

\[
r=c\tau Q^{-C_L}|I|
\]

and let

\[
J_m=[m-r,m+r]\cap I
\]

with a one-sided choice near the boundary. By the Lipschitz bound for \(u\),

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\quad\text{on }J_m.
\]

Now average the local weighted anisotropy over \(m\in H\):

\[
\int_H\int_{J_m}|u(x)|^2(g(x)^2+h(x)^2)\,dx\,dm
\le
2r\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dx
\le
2rQ^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore some \(m_\ast\in H\) satisfies

\[
\int_{J_{m_\ast}}|u|^2(g^2+h^2)
\le
\frac{2rQ^{-A}|I|}{|H|}
\le
rQ^{-A+C_H},
\]

for a fixed polynomial exponent \(C_H\).

Since on \(J_{m_\ast}\),

\[
|u|\ge\tau,
\]

we get

\[
\int_{J_{m_\ast}}(g^2+h^2)
\le
\tau^{-2}rQ^{-A+C_H}.
\]

Also

\[
|J_{m_\ast}|\asymp r.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\frac1{|J|}
\int_J(g^2+h^2)
\le
Q^{-A+C_H}\tau^{-2}.
}
\]

Set

\[
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+C_H}\tau^{-2}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Since

\[
\tau=Q^{-B/2-O(1)},
\]

we have

\[
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+C_H+B+O(1)}.
\]

So by choosing \(A\) large, \(\varepsilon\) is arbitrarily polynomially small.

This extraction requires only:

\[
\|u\|_\infty,\ \|u'\|_\infty
\]

—not \(\|g'\|\) or \(\|h'\|\).

---

# 3. \(L^2\)-integral rigidity lemma

Now prove the rigidity lemma with \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\).

Assume on \(J\):

\[
|u|\le Q^C,
\qquad
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Also assume a local interpolation setup with \(J'\Subset J\).

First, since

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

we get \(q\) bounded in \(L^\infty\) on most of \(J\) if \(g\) is small in \(L^2\), but not pointwise. To keep the proof clean, assume a polynomial pointwise bound

\[
|q|\le Q^C
\]

on \(J\). This can be obtained either from primitive/canonical control, or from a slightly stronger transfer package. This is much weaker than controlling \(g,h\) derivatives.

Also use interpolation to get

\[
|q'|\le Q^C
\]

on \(J'\), from

\[
|q|\le Q^C,\qquad |q''|=|u|\le Q^C.
\]

Now repeat the \(q\)-multiplier argument.

---

## 3.1 Kinetic estimate

Multiply

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

by \(\phi q\), with \(\phi\) supported in \(J\), \(\phi=1\) on \(J'\):

\[
\int \phi qh
=
2\int \phi q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi qg''.
\]

Integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi qg''
=
\int g(\phi q)''.
\]

Since

\[
(\phi q)''=\phi''q+2\phi'q'+\phi q'',
\]

and \(q,q',q''\) are polynomially bounded,

\[
\|(\phi q)''\|_{L^2}\le Q^C |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le
\|g\|_2\|(\phi q)''\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Also,

\[
\left|\int \phi qh\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi q\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int \phi q^2(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

---

## 3.2 Potential estimate

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) be a cutoff with

\[
\chi_\delta=0\quad(|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta=1\quad(|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Test

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q).
\]

Then

\[
\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta Fq''
-
\int\phi\chi_\delta Fg.
\]

The \(g\)-term is controlled by absorption:

\[
\left|\int\phi\chi_\delta Fg\right|
\le
\eta\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta\|g\|_2^2
\le
\eta\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
Q^C\varepsilon^2|J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term,

\[
\int\phi\chi_\delta Fq''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F)'q'.
\]

As in the pointwise case, the derivative terms are controlled by

\[
\int\phi q^2(q')^2
\]

with a loss \(\delta^{-2}\), because on the support of \(\chi_\delta\),

\[
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-2}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

---

## 3.3 Small-\(q\) region

On \(|q|\le2\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta.
\]

Also

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Since \(g\) is only \(L^2\)-small now,

\[
\int_{|q|\le2\delta}|u|^2
\le
C\delta^2|J|
+
C\int_J g^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

---

## 3.4 Combine

Therefore

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-2}
\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/4}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J|.
}
\]

Since \(|J|\asymp |J'|\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

This is the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma.

---

# 4. Gate 2 contradiction

From extraction,

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
\]

But rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
\]

Recall

\[
\varepsilon^2=Q^{-A+C_H}\tau^{-2}.
\]

Thus

\[
\varepsilon^{1/2}
=
Q^{(-A+C_H)/4}\tau^{-1/2}.
\]

The contradiction condition is

\[
Q^C Q^{(-A+C_H)/4}\tau^{-1/2}
<
\tau^2.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
Q^{(-A+C_H)/4+C}
<
\tau^{5/2}.
\]

Since

\[
\tau=Q^{-B/2+O(1)},
\]

the right side is

\[
Q^{-5B/4+O(1)}.
\]

So it suffices to choose

\[
A>C_H+5B+O(C).
\]

Thus Gate 2 follows for a sufficiently strong failure exponent \(A\).

---

# 5. What this improves

The previous pointwise version required extracting an interval where

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A}
\]

pointwise. That needed Lipschitz bounds for \(g,h\).

The \(L^2\)-version only needs:

1. \(u\) Lipschitz to build the interval where \(|u|\ge\tau\);
2. weighted Gate 2 failure to make \(g,h\) \(L^2\)-small on that interval;
3. local polynomial bounds for \(q,q'\) or a way to recover them.

Thus the canonical transfer requirements are reduced.

---

# 6. Minimal transfer after this improvement

For Gate 2, enough is:

\[
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

for extraction and wall escape,

plus local polynomial bounds

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

on extracted intervals for the rigidity proof.

But \(q,q'\) can often be recovered from

\[
\|u\|_\infty
\]

plus a basepoint/primitive bound or the identity

\[
F(q)=u-g
\]

if some \(g\)-control is available.

The clean safe package remains:

\[
|q|+|q'|+|u|+|u'|\le Q^C,
\]

but now no derivative bounds for \(g,h\) are needed.

---

# 7. Final revised Gate 2 theorem

### Gate 2 via \(L^2\)-integral rigidity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|;
   \]

2. source bounds:

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C;
   \]

3. local primitive bounds on extracted intervals:

   \[
   \|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C;
   \]

4. identities:

   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \qquad
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'';
   \]

5. Gate 2 failure:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
   \]

Then for \(A\) sufficiently large relative to \(B,C\), contradiction follows. Hence Gate 2 holds.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Extra gain: pointwise Lipschitz of }g,h\text{ is unnecessary.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 can be proved from }L^2\text{-small anisotropy on a high-source interval.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main remaining transfer need: }u,u'\text{ plus local }q,q'\text{ bounds.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{This is cleaner and weaker than the previous G2-A/G2-B package.}
}
\]
## User (2026-04-27 11:29:14)

go one step further, look for anything extra

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:29:18)

I’ll try to remove the remaining local \(q,q'\) pointwise assumptions. The promising route is to treat large-\(|q|\) as a small exceptional set forced by \(g=u-F(q)\), and to use truncated multipliers so the proof only needs bounded \(u,u'\) plus \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\).

_Thought for 37s_

## One step further: derive the \(q,q'\) bounds from \(u\)-bounds and \(L^2\)-small \(g\)

Source context: 

## Extra gain

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Gate 2 integral-rigidity lemma can likely avoid separate }q,q'\text{ assumptions entirely.}
}
\]

Previously, the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof assumed local polynomial bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|\le Q^C.
\]

But these can be recovered from:

\[
u=q'' \quad\text{bounded},
\]

and

\[
g=u-F(q)\quad\text{\(L^2\)-small},
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Reason: if \(q\) becomes very large, then \(F(q)\sim -2q^3\) is very large. Since \(u\) is bounded, \(g=u-F(q)\) must be very large on a nontrivial interval, contradicting the \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\). Once \(q\) is bounded, \(q'\) follows from a one-dimensional Landau/interpolation estimate using \(q''=u\).

Thus Gate 2 can be reduced to an even smaller local package:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

plus the \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g,h\) produced by Gate 2 failure.

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume on an interval \(J\):

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le M,
\]

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Here downstream ordinary transfer gives

\[
M\le Q^C,
\]

and Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A}.
\]

We want polynomial local bounds for \(q,q'\) on a shrunken interval \(J_1\Subset J\).

---

# 2. \(q\)-bound from \(u\)-bound and \(g\)-smallness

Let

\[
L=\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}.
\]

Suppose \(L\) is large. Pick \(x_0\in J_1\) with

\[
|q(x_0)|=L.
\]

Since

\[
q''=u,
\qquad
|u|\le M,
\]

Taylor convexity gives that \(q\) cannot drop too fast. On an interval of radius

\[
r\asymp \min\left(\operatorname{dist}(J_1,\partial J),\sqrt{L/M}\right),
\]

one has

\[
|q(x)|\ge \frac{L}{2}.
\]

For

\[
L\gg M^{1/3}+1,
\]

we have

\[
|F(q(x))|\asymp |q(x)|^3\ge cL^3
\]

on that interval. Since

\[
|u|\le M
\]

and \(L^3\gg M\), it follows that

\[
|g(x)|=|u-F(q)|\ge cL^3.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|g\|_2^2
\ge
cL^6 r.
\]

But

\[
\|g\|_2^2\le \varepsilon^2 |J|.
\]

Thus

\[
L^6 r\le C\varepsilon^2 |J|.
\]

If the radius is

\[
r\asymp \sqrt{L/M},
\]

then

\[
L^6\sqrt{L/M}\le C\varepsilon^2 |J|,
\]

so

\[
L^{13/2}\le C\varepsilon^2 M^{1/2}|J|.
\]

This gives

\[
L\le C(\varepsilon^2 M^{1/2}|J|)^{2/13}.
\]

If instead \(r\) is cut off by the distance to the boundary, the estimate is even simpler:

\[
L^6\operatorname{dist}(J_1,\partial J)
\le C\varepsilon^2 |J|.
\]

In either case, for polynomial \(M\), polynomial interval geometry, and polynomial \(\varepsilon^{-1}\), we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the desired primitive \(q\)-bound, derived rather than assumed.

---

# 3. \(q'\)-bound from \(q\) and \(q''\)

Once

\[
\|q\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
\|q''\|_\infty=\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

a standard one-dimensional interpolation estimate gives, on \(J_2\Subset J_1\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\right),
}
\]

where

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J_2,\partial J_1).
\]

If

\[
\ell\ge Q^{-C}|J|,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

So \(q'\)-control also follows.

---

# 4. \(L^2\)-integral rigidity with derived primitive bounds

Now apply the \(q\)-multiplier proof on \(J_2\).

The kinetic identity is:

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Multiply by \(\phi q\), where \(\phi\) is supported in \(J_2\), equals \(1\) on \(J'\), and satisfies

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi,
\qquad
|\phi''|\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\int \phi qh
=
2\int \phi q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi qg''.
\]

Integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi qg''
=
\int g(\phi q)''.
\]

Since

\[
(\phi q)''=\phi''q+2\phi'q'+\phi q'',
\]

and now

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le
Q^C\|g\|_2|J|^{1/2}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Similarly,

\[
\left|\int \phi qh\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi q\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int \phi q^2(q')^2\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

Then the potential estimate proceeds as before. With a cutoff \(\chi_\delta(q)\),

\[
\chi_\delta=0\quad(|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta=1\quad(|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

testing

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)
\]

gives

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-2}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

On

\[
|q|\le2\delta,
\]

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\]

and

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Because \(g\) is \(L^2\)-small,

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le2\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

Combining:

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-2}\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/4}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J|.
}
\]

Thus the integral-rigidity lemma holds with only:

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

and \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g,h\), plus interval geometry.

---

# 5. Gate 2 proof with the weaker package

Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure produces, using only \(u,u'\)-bounds, an interval \(J\) where

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

The improved rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
\]

But

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\]

on \(J'\), so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}<\tau^2.
\]

This holds by choosing the Gate 2 failure exponent sufficiently large.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + }u,u'\text{ polynomial bounds}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

No \(g',h'\) Lipschitz bounds are needed.

---

# 6. New minimal downstream analytic-complexity package

The Gate 2 proof now needs only:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

on ordinary packet intervals.

Everything else is derived:

- \(q\) bound from \(u\) and \(g\);
- \(q'\) bound from \(q\) and \(u=q''\);
- kinetic control from \(h\);
- potential control from \(g\).

This is a major simplification.

Thus the ordinary transfer theorem can be weakened to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated tube}
\Rightarrow
\|q''_{\can}\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D q''_{\can}\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

That is much easier than controlling all derivatives through order \(5\) or \(7\).

---

# 7. Caveat: wall escape and D4

For wall escape, we still need

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Already included.

For D4 correction control, more derivative/canonical row expansion information may still be needed. But Gate 2 itself only requires \(u,u'\).

Thus separate local packages should be stated:

## Gate 2 analytic package

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

## Row-conversion analytic package

Whatever higher derivative / row-expansion controls are needed for \(A_7,A_9\) and corrections.

This separation clarifies dependencies.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Extra gain: Gate 2 needs only polynomial bounds for }u\text{ and }u'.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No pointwise }q,q',g,h,g',h'\text{ transfer is needed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(L^2\)-small }g,h\text{ plus bounded }u\text{ force the rigidity.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary zero-separated transfer for }u,u'\text{ is very likely Green.}
}
\]

This is the cleanest downstream Gate 2 package so far.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:15:34)

_Thought for 6s_

Agent 1 / A report: canonical local complexity and scale-invariant derivative transfer. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The ordinary local-complexity package is provable under a zero-separated tube hypothesis.}
}
\]

For an ordinary packet, define the zero-separated tube condition

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

Then the completed-log-derivative machinery gives

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

If \(q,q'\) are either directly canonical completed-meromorphic quantities or normalized at one basepoint, this upgrades to

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

That is enough for G2-A, G2-B, D3a wall escape, and row mobility.

---

# 1. Ordinary zero-separated hypothesis

Use normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

In normalized packet coordinate

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda},
\]

this is just

\[
\mathcal D=\partial_x.
\]

Let \(I^\ast\) be a slightly enlarged ordinary packet interval. Define the complex packet tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\]

with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary zero-separated condition is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Here \(\mathcal Z_\Xi\) is the zero set of the completed object governing the canonical curvature.

Since ordinary scale has

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

the zero-distance lower bound is

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

That is polynomially small, so log-derivative derivatives can blow up at worst polynomially.

---

# 2. Completed-log-derivative transfer lemma

Let

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s).
\]

For fixed \(r\),

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho\frac1{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\text{regular gamma/background terms},
\]

with the zero sum understood in the standard symmetrized logarithmic-derivative sense.

Assume

\[
\operatorname{dist}(s,\mathcal Z_\Xi)\ge \delta,
\qquad
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Split zeros into dyadic annuli around \(s\):

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le 2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Local zero counting gives, in the relevant polynomial range,

\[
\# A_\nu\le Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta).
\]

Hence

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Summing over \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Since

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0},
\]

we get

\[
\delta^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^{(1+C_0)(r+1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(r)}(s)|\le Q^{C_r}
}
\]

for every fixed \(r\) inside the ordinary tube. Gamma/background terms are also polynomially controlled.

---

# 3. Transfer to \(q''_{\can}\)

Assume the canonical curvature is a fixed completed-meromorphic expression:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
\mathcal F\left(
L,L',\ldots,L^{(r_0)},
\text{ gamma/background terms}
\right)_{s=1/2+im},
\]

where \(r_0\) is fixed and \(\mathcal F\) has fixed algebraic/differential complexity.

Then differentiating \(j\le5\) times in \(m\) only raises the log-derivative order to \(r_0+j\), still fixed. Hence

\[
|\partial_m^j q''_{\can}(m)|\le Q^{C_j}.
\]

Multiplying by \(\lambda^j\) gives normalized derivatives:

\[
|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(m)|
=
|\lambda^j\partial_m^j q''_{\can}(m)|
\le Q^{C_j}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}|
\le Q^{C_j},
\qquad 0\le j\le5.
}
\]

This proves the needed transfer for \(u=q''_{\can}\) and its derivatives.

---

# 4. What is needed for \(q,q'\)

Gate 2 formulas involve

\[
q,\qquad q',
\]

not just

\[
u=q''.
\]

There are two safe ways to control them.

## Option A: direct completed-meromorphic formulas

If \(q\) and \(q'\) are themselves canonical completed-meromorphic quantities, then the same zero-separated log-derivative transfer gives directly

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This is the cleanest option.

## Option B: basepoint normalization

If \(q\) is treated as a primitive of \(u\), assume a basepoint \(x_0\in I^\ast\) satisfies

\[
|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C.
\]

Then in normalized coordinate \(x\),

\[
q'(x)=q'(x_0)+\int_{x_0}^{x}u(y)\,dy,
\]

and

\[
q(x)=q(x_0)+(x-x_0)q'(x_0)+\int_{x_0}^{x}(x-y)u(y)\,dy.
\]

Since

\[
\sup|u|\le Q^C
\]

and \(I^\ast\) has polynomial normalized length, this gives

\[
|q|+|q'|\le Q^C.
\]

Higher derivatives follow from

\[
q''=u,\quad q'''=u',\quad \ldots.
\]

So again

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

For a proof-level statement, I recommend retaining one explicit clause:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either }q,q'\text{ are direct canonical meromorphic quantities, or a polynomial basepoint normalization is assumed.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Derivative implications for \(u,g,h\)

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Then

\[
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

So

\[
g'=u'-6q'+6q^2q'.
\]

Under

\[
|u'|+|q|+|q'|\le Q^C,
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
|g'|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Next use the expanded form of \(h\). Starting from

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

we compute

\[
g''=u''-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q''.
\]

Since \(q''=u\),

\[
g''=u''-6u+12q(q')^2+6q^2u.
\]

Thus

\[
h
=
2q(q')^2
-\frac16u''
+u
-2q(q')^2
-q^2u.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
h=(1-q^2)u-\frac16u''.
}
\]

This matches the convention in which the cubic term in \(g\) is \(2q^3\). If a different normalization is used, the coefficient of \(q^2u\) changes, but the structural form remains:

\[
h=a(q)u-\frac16u''
\]

for a fixed polynomial \(a\).

Differentiate:

\[
h'
=
(1-q^2)u'
-2qq'u
-\frac16u'''.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|h'|\le Q^C
}
\]

provided

\[
|q|+|q'|+|u|+|u'|+|u'''|\le Q^C.
\]

Since

\[
u'''=\mathcal D^3u=\mathcal D^3q''=\mathcal D^5q,
\]

the minimal derivative order for \(h'\) is \(q\) through order \(5\). The safe \(k\le7\) package covers this.

---

# 6. Scale-invariant form

The prompt asks for scale-invariant derivative bounds:

\[
\sup_{J\subset I^\ast,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C}|I^\ast|}
\sup_J |J|^k|\partial^kq|
\le Q^{C_k}.
\]

This follows from normalized bounds. If

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\]

and \(I^\ast\) has physical length comparable to \(\lambda\), then for subintervals

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C}\lambda,
\]

we have

\[
|J|^k|\partial_m^k q|
\le
(Q^{-C}\lambda)^k\lambda^{-k}|\mathcal D^kq|
\le Q^{C_k}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J |J|^k|\partial_m^kq|\le Q^{C_k}
}
\]

for polynomial-scale subintervals \(J\). This is the scale-invariant version needed for cutoff estimates on shrunken intervals.

---

# 7. Canonical decomposition transfer

The canonical decomposition is

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

## \(B_2\)

The background is

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

Polygamma asymptotics give

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}),
\]

so

\[
\mathcal D^jB_2
=
\lambda^jO_j(t^{-2-j})
\]

is tiny, hence polynomially bounded.

## \(P_2,D_2\)

Normalized derivatives of AFE phases are harmless:

\[
\mathcal D^j e^{\mp it\log n}
=
(\mp i\lambda\log n)^j e^{\mp it\log n},
\]

and ordinary support gives

\[
|\lambda\log n|\le O(1).
\]

But the supremum bound should not be proved by AFE \(\ell^1\)-summation. It should be inherited from the full completed-meromorphic \(q''_{\can}\) via the zero-separated tube lemma.

## \(E_2\)

If \(E_2\) is included in the exact canonical object, it is automatically part of the meromorphic transfer. If \(E_2\) is a truncation error between model and canonical object, then one needs

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E}
\]

through the required order. For downstream local Gate 2, inclusive canonical treatment is cleaner.

---

# 8. Final theorem

### Ordinary zero-separated local complexity theorem

Assume:

1. ordinary scale:

   \[
   \lambda Q\asymp1;
   \]

2. ordinary zero-separated tube:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
   \mathcal Z_\Xi
   \right)
   \ge
   \lambda Q^{-C_0},
   \qquad
   \rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho};
   \]

3. canonical meromorphic representation for \(q''_{\can}\), and either direct meromorphic formulas for \(q,q'\) or basepoint normalization.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty
+
\|g'\|_\infty
+
\|h'\|_\infty
\le
Q^C|I|^{-1},
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This supplies all derivative bounds needed for:

\[
\text{G2-A two-threshold extraction},
\]

\[
\text{G2-B integral rigidity},
\]

\[
\text{D3a wall escape},
\]

and row mobility.

---

# 9. Remaining audit items

State \(q,q',q''_{\can}\) as completed meromorphic/log-derivative quantities, or add basepoint normalization.

Confirm the only dangerous poles in the tube are completed-object zeros; gamma/trivial poles are far or regularized.

Use standard zero count

N(t+1)-N(t-1)\ll Q.

Clarify whether \(E_2\) is included exactly or treated perturbatively.

Verify all \(q,g,h\) identities use the same normalized derivative convention.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:19:29)

A further reduction is available: Gate 2 can likely be proved without pointwise smallness of \(g,h\), and without transferring \(q,q'\) as canonical primitives. The proof can use \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\), plus only polynomial bounds for \(u=q''_{\can}\) and \(u'\).

_Thought for 16s_

Agent 1 / A continued attack: reduce Gate 2 to \(u,u'\)-complexity only. Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 can likely be proved from a much smaller analytic package than previously stated.}
}
\]

The old package asked for polynomial bounds on

\[
q,q',q'',q''',q^{(4)}
\]

or even up to \(q^{(7)}\). A sharper route appears to need only:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

The reason is:

1. Two-threshold extraction can produce an interval \(J\) where \(|u|\ge \tau\), while \(g,h\) are \(L^2\)-small on \(J\).
2. From \(|u|\le Q^C\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g=u-F(q)\), one derives polynomial \(q\)-bounds on a shrunken interval.
3. From \(q''=u\), polynomial \(q'\)-bounds follow by one-dimensional interpolation.
4. The \(q\)-multiplier integral-rigidity proof then works with \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\).

So D1/D2 can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Minimal Gate 2 Local Complexity: }
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is a meaningful simplification because \(u=q''_{\can}\) is the canonical source curvature itself, and ordinary zero-separated transfer for \(u,u'\) is much easier than controlling primitives.

---

# 1. Two-threshold extraction with only \(u,u'\)

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 failure:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

where

\[
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Assume

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_U},
\qquad
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_L}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Choose a source threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

so that

\[
H=\{|u|\ge 2\tau\}
\]

carries polynomial \(u\)-mass:

\[
\int_H |u|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

This follows by dyadic thresholding from Gate 1 and \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^{C_U}\).

For each \(m\in H\), set

\[
r=c\tau Q^{-C_L}|I|.
\]

Then on

\[
J_m=[m-r,m+r]\cap I
\]

one has

\[
|u|\ge \tau.
\]

Averaging Gate 2 failure over \(m\in H\), there exists \(m_\ast\in H\) such that on

\[
J=J_{m_\ast}
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
}
\]

where

\[
\varepsilon^2\le Q^{-A+C}\tau^{-2}.
\]

Thus by choosing \(A\) large, \(\varepsilon\) is an arbitrarily small negative power of \(Q\).

This extraction uses no Lipschitz bounds for \(g,h\).

---

# 2. Recover \(q\)-bounds from \(u\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g\)

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

Suppose \(|q|\) becomes very large at some point in a shrunken interval \(J_1\Subset J\). Since

\[
q''=u,
\qquad
|u|\le Q^{C_U},
\]

a large value of \(q\) persists on a nontrivial interval by Taylor/convexity. More precisely, if

\[
|q(x_0)|=L,
\]

then on a radius

\[
\rho\asymp \min\left(\operatorname{dist}(J_1,\partial J),\sqrt{L/Q^{C_U}}\right)
\]

one has

\[
|q|\ge L/2.
\]

For \(L\) large,

\[
|F(q)|\asymp |q|^3\ge cL^3.
\]

Since \(|u|\le Q^{C_U}\), for \(L^3\gg Q^{C_U}\),

\[
|g|=|u-F(q)|\ge cL^3
\]

on that interval. Hence

\[
\|g\|_2^2\ge cL^6\rho.
\]

But

\[
\|g\|_2^2\le \varepsilon^2|J|.
\]

Therefore \(L\) is polynomially bounded. Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This derives the primitive \(q\)-bound; it does not need to be separately transferred.

---

# 3. Recover \(q'\)-bounds from \(q''=u\)

Let \(J_2\Subset J_1\), with

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J_2,\partial J_1)\ge Q^{-C}|J|.
\]

The one-dimensional interpolation estimate gives

\[
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\right).
\]

Since

\[
q''=u,
\qquad
\|q\|_\infty+\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus both primitive bounds are recovered locally from \(u\)-control and \(L^2\)-small \(g\).

---

# 4. \(L^2\)-integral rigidity with recovered primitive bounds

Now work on \(J_2\), and take \(J'\Subset J_2\).

Use the identity

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Multiply by \(\phi q\), where \(\phi\) is supported in \(J_2\) and equals \(1\) on \(J'\):

\[
\int \phi qh
=
2\int \phi q^2(q')^2
-\frac16\int \phi qg''.
\]

Integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi qg''
=
\int g(\phi q)''.
\]

Since

\[
(\phi q)''=\phi''q+2\phi'q'+\phi q'',
\]

and

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|\le Q^C,
\]

we obtain

\[
\left|\int g(\phi q)''\right|
\le
Q^C\|g\|_2|J|^{1/2}
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Also,

\[
\left|\int \phi qh\right|
\le
\|h\|_2\|\phi q\|_2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int \phi q^2(q')^2\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

This is the kinetic estimate.

---

# 5. Potential estimate

Use

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) be a cutoff satisfying

\[
\chi_\delta=0\quad(|q|\le\delta),
\]

\[
\chi_\delta=1\quad(|q|\ge2\delta),
\]

\[
|\chi_\delta'|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

Test against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q).
\]

Then

\[
\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta Fq''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta Fg.
\]

The \(g\)-term is controlled by absorption:

\[
\left|\int\phi\chi_\delta Fg\right|
\le
\eta\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
Q^C\varepsilon^2|J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term,

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta Fq''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F)'q'.
\]

The derivative produces terms controlled by

\[
\int\phi q^2(q')^2
\]

with a factor \(\delta^{-2}\), since on \(\operatorname{supp}\chi_\delta\),

\[
|q|\ge\delta,
\qquad
(q')^2\le \delta^{-2}q^2(q')^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-2}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
}
\]

On \(|q|\le2\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\]

and

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Since \(g\) is \(L^2\)-small,

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le2\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
\]

Combining,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon\delta^{-2}\right)|J|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/4}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 6. Gate 2 contradiction

But on \(J\),

\[
|u|\ge\tau.
\]

Therefore on \(J'\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
\]

The rigidity estimate gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
\]

Choose \(A\) in Gate 2 failure so that

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}<\frac12\tau^2.
\]

This contradicts the lower bound. Hence Gate 2 holds.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This is a much stronger simplification than the original D1/D2 framework.

---

# 7. New minimal downstream analytic package

The local Gate 2 theorem now requires only:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

No pointwise transfer for

\[
q,q',g,h,g',h'
\]

is required.

The identities involving \(g,h\) are still used, but their smallness comes from Gate 2 failure in \(L^2\), not from Lipschitz extraction.

Thus ordinary zero-separated transfer only needs to prove:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|q''_{\can}|+
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D q''_{\can}|
\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is highly likely from the completed log-derivative zero-separated tube lemma.

---

# 8. Remaining caveats

The derivation of \(q\)-boundedness from \(g\)-smallness uses:

1. \(J_1\Subset J\) with polynomial margin;
2. \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C\);
3. \(\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon|J|^{1/2}\);
4. \(\varepsilon\) sufficiently small polynomially.

The \(q'\)-bound uses interpolation and therefore loses a polynomial factor depending on the shrinkage scale. That is acceptable.

No structural obstruction appears.

---

## Final gain

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now a local theorem under only source }C^1\text{ control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Old D1/D2 are replaced by: }
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
+
\text{\(L^2\)-integral rigidity}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary zero-separated transfer for }u,u'\text{ should be Green.}
}
\]

This is the strongest simplification so far.

_Thought for 28s_

Agent 1 / A report: minimal ordinary local complexity for the new Gate 2 route. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the new }L^2\text{-input Gate 2 route, the minimal ordinary complexity package is small.}
}
\]

The Gate 2 proof no longer needs full pointwise control of

\[
q,\ q',\ q'',\ldots,q^{(7)}
\]

as a primary input. The essential transferred bounds are:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}+\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C,
\qquad u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Then, on the source-large interval produced by extraction, one recovers the necessary local bounds for \(q\) and \(q'\) from

\[
u=q'',\qquad g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

together with the \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\). Thus the old broad D1/D2 transfer requirement can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{ordinary zero-separated transfer for }u,u'
+
\textbf{local primitive recovery on the extracted interval}.
}
\]

---

# 1. Ordinary zero-separated tube hypothesis

Use normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

Let \(I^\ast\) be the enlarged packet interval. Define the tube

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary zero-separated hypothesis is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Since

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

the lower bound is polynomial:

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

This hypothesis is the correct ordinary/singular separator. If it fails, the packet is not covered by the ordinary local complexity theorem and should route to the singular/transition branch.

---

# 2. Completed-log-derivative transfer for \(u,u'\)

Assume \(u=q''_{\can}\) is a fixed completed-meromorphic curvature expression: a finite combination of completed logarithmic derivatives

\[
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]

and regular gamma/background terms.

For

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s),
\]

the standard partial fraction form gives

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho \frac{1}{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\text{regular terms}.
\]

On the zero-separated tube, write

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Dyadic annuli around \(s\) give

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Because

\[
\delta\asymp Q^{-1-C_0},
\]

we obtain

\[
|L^{(r)}(s)|\le Q^{C_r}
\]

for every fixed \(r\). Therefore, for \(j=0,1\),

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^j u|\le Q^{C_j}.
}
\]

This gives precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

in normalized coordinates.

No AFE \(\ell^1\)-bound is involved or desirable.

---

# 3. What \(q,q'\) are needed for

The new Gate 2 proof uses source-large interval extraction and \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity. It needs \(q,q'\) only **locally** on the extracted interval, not globally as transferred canonical primitives.

The source interval satisfies:

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

The integral-rigidity proof then needs local polynomial bounds for \(q,q'\) to control multiplier terms. These can be derived rather than assumed.

---

# 4. Recovering \(q\) from \(u\) and \(g\)

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

On the extracted interval,

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

If \(q\) had a very large value \(L\) at an interior point, then because

\[
q''=u
\]

is bounded, \(q\) would remain of size \(\gtrsim L\) on a nontrivial subinterval. On that subinterval,

\[
|F(q)|\asymp |q|^3\asymp L^3.
\]

Since \(u\) is only \(Q^C\), this would force

\[
|g|=|u-F(q)|
\]

to be very large on a nontrivial subinterval, contradicting the \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\) once \(\varepsilon\) is chosen sufficiently small.

Thus, on a shrunken interval,

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This avoids a separate global primitive bound for \(q\).

---

# 5. Recovering \(q'\) from \(q''=u\)

After obtaining

\[
\|q\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
\|q''\|_\infty=\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

a one-dimensional interpolation estimate gives, on a further shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J')}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J)}
\right),
}
\]

where

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J',\partial J).
\]

Since all interval shrinkages are polynomial,

\[
\ell^{-1}\le Q^C,
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

So the \(q,q'\) bounds needed by the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma are local consequences of

\[
\|u\|_\infty+\|g\|_{L^2}\text{ small}.
\]

---

# 6. Minimal complexity package

For the new Gate 2 route, the minimal package is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This supports:

1. **source-large interval extraction**, because \(u'\) thickens high-source points into intervals;

2. **local primitive recovery**, because \(\|u\|_\infty\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g\) bound \(q\);

3. **interpolation recovery of \(q'\)**, because \(q''=u\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated transfer for }u,u'
\Rightarrow
\text{all Gate 2 local complexity needed.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Safe stronger package

For paper-level safety and row-conversion bookkeeping, it is still useful to retain the stronger statement:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This follows if \(q,q'\) have direct completed-meromorphic formulas, or if one assumes basepoint normalization

\[
|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C.
\]

But for Gate 2 itself, this is stronger than necessary.

So I recommend stating both:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Minimal Gate 2 package: }u,u'\text{ bounds.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Safe canonical package: }q\text{ through order }7.
}
\]

---

# 8. Remaining audit items

The local-complexity transfer still requires the following finite audits:

1. **Canonical meromorphic formula for \(u=q''_{\can}\).**  
   \(u\) must be a completed-log-derivative curvature or fixed finite derivative thereof.

2. **Pole set.**  
   Dangerous poles in the packet tube must be exactly completed-object zeros; gamma/trivial poles must be regular or far.

3. **Local zero count.**  
   Use the standard bound

   \[
   N(t+1)-N(t-1)\ll Q.
   \]

4. **\(E_2\) handling.**  
   Either \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical meromorphic object, or it must satisfy perturbative derivative bounds.

5. **Primitive policy.**  
   If using only the minimal Gate 2 package, primitive bounds are recovered locally. If using the safe package, add direct meromorphic formulas for \(q,q'\) or a basepoint normalization.

---

# 9. Final theorem

### Minimal Ordinary Local Complexity for Gate 2

Assume ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\]

and ordinary zero-separated tube

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Assume \(u=q''_{\can}\) is a completed-meromorphic canonical curvature. Then

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
+
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma, this proves Gate 2 from Gate 1.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Minimal transfer needed for Gate 2: }u,u'.
}

\boxed{
\text{Primitive }q,q'\text{ bounds can be locally recovered.}
}

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary zero-separated log-derivative transfer for }u,u'\text{ is near-Green.}
}
\]

Agent 1 / A report: attacking the ordinary local-complexity audit items. Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The audit items are mostly closeable if }u=q''_{\can}\text{ is defined as a completed meromorphic curvature.}
}
\]

The ordinary local-complexity package now reduces to five concrete checks:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

on ordinary zero-separated packet tubes, where

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The strongest route is:

\[
\boxed{
u
=
\text{fixed finite completed-log-derivative expression}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\text{packet tube},\mathcal Z_\Xi)\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Then \(u,u'\) are polynomially bounded by standard log-derivative estimates. The remaining audit issue is mostly definitional: ensure \(q''_{\can}\) is truly the full canonical meromorphic object, not a truncated AFE proxy.
