# Audit 1 — Canonical meromorphic formula for \(u=q''_{\can}\)

## Target

We need a theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
u(t)=q''_{\can}(t)
=
\mathcal U\left(
\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi},
\left(\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}\right)',
\ldots,
\left(\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}\right)^{(r_0)};
\text{ gamma/background}
\right)_{s=1/2+it}
}
\]

where \(r_0\) is fixed and \(\mathcal U\) has fixed algebraic/differential complexity.

Then ordinary zero-separation gives:

\[
\boxed{
|u|+|\mathcal D u|\le Q^C.
}
\]

## Attack

The canonical decomposition currently used is:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

To make the audit proof-level, this must be tied to the completed meromorphic object:

\[
\boxed{
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
=
q''_{\Xi,\can}
}
\]

where \(q''_{\Xi,\can}\) is obtained from the completed object \(\Xi\), not just from a real-line AFE approximation.

So the necessary canonical statement is:

### Canonical identity

There exists a completed object \(\Xi(s)\) such that, on the real line and in the packet tube,

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}(t)
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi](1/2+it)
}
\]

for a fixed operator \(\mathfrak C_2\) made from finitely many derivatives of \(\Xi'/\Xi\) and regular gamma terms.

Then the AFE formula

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

is just a representation of that same canonical object.

## Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Closeable by definition audit.}
}
\]

If \(q''_{\can}\) is explicitly defined as the completed meromorphic curvature, this item is Green.

If \(q''_{\can}\) is defined only through truncated AFE pieces, then one must separately prove that the truncation plus \(E_2\) equals the completed meromorphic object to the required accuracy.

---

# Audit 2 — Pole set

## Target

We need:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The only dangerous poles of }u=q''_{\can}
\text{ in the packet tube are zeros of }\Xi.
}
\]

Gamma/trivial poles must either be outside the tube or already included in regular background terms.

## Attack

The completed log derivative has poles where

\[
\Xi(s)=0.
\]

If

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s),
\]

then

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
\]

has poles at the zeros of \(\Xi\), with order \(r+1\). Therefore every fixed finite expression in \(L,L',\ldots,L^{(r_0)}\) has poles only at \(\mathcal Z_\Xi\), unless extra denominators are introduced.

So we need to confirm:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]
\text{ uses no denominators other than powers implicit in }\Xi'/\Xi.
}
\]

No factors like

\[
\frac1{q_0},\quad \frac1u,\quad \frac1{\Gamma_G},\quad \frac1{\Gamma_{G,2}}
\]

may appear in the canonical curvature definition.

For gamma terms:

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

The polygamma poles occur at nonpositive integers of the argument

\[
\frac14+\frac{it}{2},
\]

which are far from high critical-line packet tubes around \(t\asymp e^Q\). Hence \(B_2\) is holomorphic and tiny there.

## Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Green if canonical operators are denominator-free except for }\Xi'/\Xi.
}
\]

This should be an explicit guardrail: no projected or normalized row expression with \(1/q_0\)-type denominators may be used in \(q''_{\can}\).

---

# Audit 3 — Local zero count

## Target

For \(t\asymp T\), \(Q=\log T\), need a polynomial local zero-count bound:

\[
\boxed{
N_\Xi(t+R)-N_\Xi(t-R)\le Q^C(1+R)
}
\]

for \(R\) in the polynomial/tube range used in the log-derivative annulus argument.

For ordinary zeta-type objects, one expects the sharper bound:

\[
N(t+1)-N(t-1)\ll Q.
\]

## Attack

Use standard zero-counting for the completed zeta object:

\[
N(T+1)-N(T-1)=O(\log T)=O(Q).
\]

For wider polynomial windows,

\[
N(T+R)-N(T-R)\ll RQ+Q
\]

for \(R\ge1\), so in the notation used in the annulus proof:

\[
\#\{\rho:|s-\rho|\le R\}\le Q^C(1+R).
\]

Then with zero-distance

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0},
\]

the log-derivative derivative estimate becomes:

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^{C_r}.
\]

Thus for fixed \(r\),

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\left(\frac{d}{ds}\right)^r
\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\right|
\le Q^{C_r}.
}
\]

## Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Green for classical completed zeta; state as a cited standard zero-count lemma.}
}
\]

No new RH-level input is needed here.

---

# Audit 4 — \(E_2\): inclusive versus perturbative

## Target

Clarify whether

\[
E_2
\]

is part of the exact canonical object or a truncation/model error.

## Attack

There are two consistent policies.

### Policy A: inclusive canonical policy

Define

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}:=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then the derivative transfer is applied to the full object \(q''_{\can}\). Under this policy, no separate smallness estimate for \(E_2\) is needed for Gate 2. We only need the completed meromorphic formula and zero-separated tube estimate.

This is preferable for downstream Gate 2.

### Policy B: model-plus-error policy

If one proves estimates for

\[
q''_{\model}:=B_2+P_2+D_2
\]

and transfers to

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\model}+E_2,
\]

then one needs:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E},
\qquad 0\le j\le1
}
\]

for the minimal Gate 2 package \((u,u')\), and stronger bounds through higher \(j\) if using the old safe \(q^{(0..7)}\) package or D4 corrections.

For current Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
j\le1\text{ is enough for }u,u'.
}
\]

For D4 / row conversion, the needed order depends on row expansion corrections and may be higher.

## Recommendation

Use Policy A for Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
E_2\text{ is included in the canonical object.}
}
\]

Then handle D4 row residuals separately, where exact correction estimates are genuinely needed.

## Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2: closeable via inclusive policy.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4: still needs correction-specific }E_2\text{ audit.}
}
\]

---

# Audit 5 — Primitive policy for \(q,q'\)

## Target

Decide whether we must prove global bounds for

\[
q,\ q'
\]

or can recover them locally.

## Attack

For the new \(L^2\)-input Gate 2 proof, we do **not** need global primitive transfer.

The proof only needs local \(q,q'\) bounds on the extracted source interval. These can be derived as follows.

Gate 2 failure plus extraction gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Also ordinary transfer gives

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

If \(q\) became too large on a shrunken interval, then \(F(q)\sim-2q^3\) would be too large on a nontrivial interval because

\[
q''=u
\]

is bounded. Then

\[
g=u-F(q)
\]

would have large \(L^2\)-norm, contradicting \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\).

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

locally.

Then interpolation gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_\infty
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_\infty+\ell\|q''\|_\infty
\right)
\le Q^C
}
\]

on a further shrunken interval.

Thus primitive \(q,q'\) bounds are locally recovered.

## Status

\[
\boxed{
\text{For Gate 2, primitive transfer is unnecessary.}
}
\]

However, for D4 row algebra, \(q_0\) appears explicitly in

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
\]

and wall escape uses \(q_0''=u\). There, we still need \(q_0\) as a defined canonical scalar, but not necessarily a global meromorphic transfer estimate beyond local \(u,u'\) and the actual value of \(q_0\).

---

# Final minimal Gate 2 transfer theorem

### Ordinary Minimal Gate 2 Transfer

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\]

and ordinary zero-separated tube:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Assume \(u=q''_{\can}\) is the full canonical completed meromorphic curvature. Then

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
+
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is enough for:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + }L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Primitive \(q,q'\) bounds are recovered locally on the extracted interval.

---

# Final audit status table

| Audit item | Status | Remaining action |
|---|---:|---|
| Canonical meromorphic formula for \(u=q''_{\can}\) | Closeable | Define \(q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) explicitly |
| Pole set | Green if denominator-free | Confirm no \(1/q_0,1/u,1/\Gamma\) in canonical curvature |
| Local zero count | Green | Cite/prove \(N(T+1)-N(T-1)\ll\log T\) |
| \(E_2\) | Gate 2 green under inclusive policy | For D4, audit correction-specific \(E_2\) residuals |
| Primitive \(q,q'\) | Not needed for Gate 2 transfer | Recover locally from \(u\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g\) |
| Ordinary/singular split | Essential | If zero-distance fails, route to singular/transition |

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 transfer reduces to ordinary zero-separated bounds for }u,u'.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{This is likely Green once }q''_{\can}\text{ is explicitly completed-meromorphic.}

The next highest-value target is therefore the \(L^2\)-input integral-rigidity proof, not further transfer estimates.

## Extra step: primitive recovery via \(L^2\)-potential control

Source context: 

## New gain

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Gate 2 proof can avoid separate assumptions on }q,q'.
}
\]

The missing piece was: in the \(L^2\)-input integral-rigidity proof, we used local polynomial bounds for

\[
q,\qquad q'.
\]

These can be **derived** from:

\[
u=q''\ \text{bounded},
\]

and

\[
g=u-F(q)\ \text{\(L^2\)-small},
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

The clean mechanism is a one-dimensional Gagliardo–Nirenberg/interpolation estimate.

So the Gate 2 local analytic package reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I)}+\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
}
\]

plus Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure. This is a substantial simplification.

---

# 1. \(L^2\)-control of \(F(q)\)

On the extracted source interval \(J\), Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Also ordinary local complexity gives

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le M,
\qquad M\le Q^C.
\]

Since

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}+\|g\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
(M+\varepsilon)|J|^{1/2}.
\]

Now

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

For all real \(q\),

\[
|q|^3\le C\bigl(|F(q)|+1\bigr).
\]

Hence

\[
|q|^6\le C\bigl(|F(q)|^2+1\bigr).
\]

Integrating:

\[
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}^6
\le
C\left(\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}^2+|J|\right)
\le
Q^C |J|.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C |J|^{1/6}.
}
\]

This gives polynomial \(L^6\)-control of \(q\), without any primitive assumption.

---

# 2. \(L^\infty\)-control of \(q\) from \(q''=u\)

Use the one-dimensional Gagliardo–Nirenberg estimate on \(J_1\Subset J\):

\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\le
C\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J)}^{1/13}
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}^{12/13}
+
C|J|^{-1/6}\|q\|_{L^6(J)}.
\]

The exponent \(1/13\) is the standard scaling exponent for interpolating \(L^\infty\) from \(W^{2,\infty}\) and \(L^6\) in one dimension.

Since

\[
q''=u,\qquad
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

and

\[
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/6},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

So \(q\) is polynomially bounded locally.

---

# 3. \(L^\infty\)-control of \(q'\)

Use a standard Landau/interpolation inequality on \(J_2\Subset J_1\):

\[
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\right),
\]

where

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J_2,\partial J_1).
\]

The extracted interval has polynomial length, and we choose the shrinkage so that

\[
\ell^{-1}\le Q^C |I|^{-1}.
\]

Since

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus both primitive bounds required by the multiplier proof are derived.

---

# 4. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity now has minimal assumptions

We can restate the lemma as:

### Minimal \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

Assume on \(J\):

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

with

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Then on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
}
\]

The proof is:

1. \(L^2\)-small \(g\) plus bounded \(u\) gives \(q\in L^6\).
2. \(q''=u\in L^\infty\) gives \(q\in L^\infty\).
3. Interpolation gives \(q'\in L^\infty\).
4. The \(q\)-multiplier proof gives kinetic control:

   \[
   \int \phi q^2(q')^2\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
   \]

5. Testing \(q''=F(q)+g\) against \(\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)\) yields

   \[
   \int_{|q|\ge2\delta}F(q)^2
   \le Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-2}+\varepsilon^2)|J|.
   \]

6. On \(|q|\le2\delta\),

   \[
   |F(q)|\le C\delta.
   \]

7. Optimizing with

   \[
   \delta=\varepsilon^{1/4}
   \]

   gives

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
   \]

This is stronger than the earlier \(\varepsilon^{2/5}\) target.

---

# 5. Gate 2 now needs only \(u,u'\) transfer

The source-large interval extraction needs:

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

The rigidity lemma needs:

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Thus, for Gate 2, the only canonical analytic-complexity transfer required is:

\[
\boxed{
\|q''_{\can}\|_\infty
+
\|\mathcal D q''_{\can}\|_\infty
\le Q^C.
}
\]

Under ordinary zero-separated tube hypotheses, this follows from the completed log-derivative lemma for the canonical curvature \(u=q''_{\can}\).

So the broad old package

\[
\sup|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^C,\quad 0\le k\le7
\]

is no longer a Gate 2 requirement. It remains useful for D4 row algebra and general safety, but Gate 2 itself needs much less.

---

# 6. Final Gate 2 theorem, simplified

### Gate 2 theorem from minimal source complexity

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|;
   \]

2. ordinary source complexity:

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C;
   \]

3. Gate 2 failure:

   \[
   \int_I|u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
   \]

Then source-large interval extraction gives \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-T}
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

The minimal \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
\]

But

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\]

on \(J'\), so

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge\tau^2|J'|.
\]

For \(A\) sufficiently large, these contradict. Therefore Gate 2 holds.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Extra gain: }q,q'\text{ bounds are derived, not assumed.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 requires only }u,u'\text{ canonical transfer.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(L^2\)-input rigidity exponent improves to }1/2\text{ under this route.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary zero-separated transfer for }u=q''_{\can}\text{ and }\mathcal D u
\text{ is now the only Gate 2 analytic-complexity input.}
}
\]

This is the sharpest simplification so far.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:38:26)

I’ll try to remove the \(u'\) requirement too. The question is whether Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure can produce a source-mass interval with \(L^2\)-small anisotropy without first thickening a point by Lipschitz control.

_Thought for 37s_

## Further attack: can we remove the \(u'\) requirement?

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the current proof route, }u'\text{-control is genuinely needed, or must be replaced by a component/oscillation bound.}
}
\]

The Gate 2 simplification reached:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

A natural next question is whether \(\|u'\|_\infty\) can be removed, leaving only

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

I do **not** think so for the current extraction method. Without \(u'\)-control, Gate 1 mass may concentrate on dust-like high-source sets. Gate 2 failure then gives \(g,h\)-smallness only on those dust-like sets, not on an interval. The \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma needs an interval.

So the sharp minimal package is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

or, alternatively,

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C
+
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge\tau\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

The \(u'\)-bound is the cheaper route.

---

# 1. Why \(u'\) was used

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

To use \(L^2\)-input rigidity, we need an interval \(J\) with:

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

The \(u'\)-bound creates this \(J\). If \(m_\ast\) satisfies

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge2\tau,
\]

and

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

then on a radius

\[
r\asymp \tau Q^{-C_u}|I|,
\]

we get

\[
|u|\ge\tau.
\]

That is the entire point of \(u'\)-control.

---

# 2. Why \(u\)-boundedness alone is insufficient

Assume only

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

Then Gate 1 implies the set

\[
H_\tau=\{|u|\ge \tau\}
\]

has polynomial measure for a suitable \(\tau\), but it does not imply \(H_\tau\) contains a polynomial-length interval.

One can have

\[
H_\tau
=
\bigcup_{\nu=1}^N I_\nu
\]

with many very small components whose total measure is polynomially large. On each \(I_\nu\), \(u\) is large and \(g,h\) are small; outside these islands, \(u\) is small or \(g,h\) are large. This is compatible with

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

and

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

But no component \(I_\nu\) need have a useful length unless one has:

\[
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

or

\[
\#\pi_0(H_\tau)\le Q^C.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty\text{ alone cannot produce the source interval.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Equivalent alternatives to \(u'\)-control

There are two viable substitutes.

## Alternative A: source component-count bound

If for a mass-bearing threshold \(\tau\),

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge\tau\}\le Q^C,
}
\]

then Gate 1 gives a source-mass component \(J\) of polynomial length. On that component,

\[
|u|\ge\tau.
\]

Then Gate 2 failure gives \(L^2\)-small \(g,h\) on at least one such component by pigeonholing.

This was the “source oscillation/component-count” route.

## Alternative B: quantitative persistence from \(u'\)

If

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
}
\]

then every high-source point thickens to a polynomial interval. This is simpler and follows from the ordinary zero-separated transfer for \(u,u'\).

Thus the minimal extraction input is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either }u'\text{-control or a source component-count theorem.}
}
\]

Since \(u'\)-control is near-Green from the meromorphic transfer, it is preferable.

---

# 4. Can weighted rigidity avoid the interval?

Could we prove Gate 2 directly from

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\ll1
\]

without extracting an interval?

A possible weighted rigidity theorem would be:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\qquad
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\int_I |u|^2\le Q^{-B'}|I|,
\]

a contradiction.

But the known integral-rigidity proof uses integration by parts on

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and needs to control unweighted terms like

\[
\int g(\phi q)''
\]

or at least terms weighted by a smooth cutoff. The Gate 2 failure gives smallness of \(g,h\) only where \(|u|^2\) is large. If one inserts a weight depending on \(u\), integration by parts creates derivatives of \(u\), \(u'\), and likely higher derivatives. So weighted rigidity does not eliminate complexity; it likely reintroduces derivative assumptions in a harder form.

Therefore the source-interval route is cleaner.

---

# 5. Refined minimal Gate 2 theorem

### Minimal source-interval Gate 2 theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|;
   \]

2. source control:

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty |I|\le Q^C;
   \]

3. identities:

   \[
   g=u-6q+2q^3,
   \qquad
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'';
   \]

4. \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity:

   if \(J\) is an interval with \(|u|\ge\tau\) and

   \[
   \|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
   \le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
   \]

   then

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/2}|J'|.
   \]

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

for some sufficiently large \(A\).

The only canonical analytic-complexity input is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 6. Ordinary zero-separated transfer is enough

Under ordinary zero-separated tube control,

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

and with \(u=q''_{\can}\) a completed meromorphic curvature, the log-derivative lemma gives:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

In physical variables, this is

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\lambda\|\partial_m u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

So

\[
\|\partial_m u\|_\infty\le Q^C\lambda^{-1}.
\]

Since \(|I|\asymp\lambda\) in ordinary normalized packets,

\[
\|\partial_m u\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Thus the extraction \(u'\)-control follows.

---

# 7. What remains after this reduction

The downstream proof obligations are now highly concrete:

1. **Ordinary zero-separated transfer for \(u,u'\)**  
   Near-Green via completed log-derivative estimates.

2. **Source interval extraction**  
   Proven from Gate 1, Gate 2 failure, and \(u'\)-control.

3. **\(L^2\)-input integral rigidity**  
   Needs formal cutoff proof, but conceptually strong.

4. **D3a wall escape**  
   Needs \(u'\)-control, already included.

5. **D4 row conversion**  
   Finite row-symbol/correction audit.

This is a substantially simpler downstream package than the original D1/D2/D3/D4 architecture.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cannot remove }u'\text{ without replacing it by component-count/oscillation control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(u'\)-control is minimal and near-Green.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 analytic complexity now reduces to }u,u'\text{ only.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next highest-value task remains the formal }L^2\text{-input integral-rigidity proof.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:58:42)

_Thought for 24s_

Agent 1 / A report: minimal canonical local complexity for the new Gate 2 route. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the new }L^2\text{-input Gate 2 route, the minimal canonical transfer is essentially }u,u'\text{ only.}
}
\]

The active Gate 2 route no longer needs broad pointwise control of

\[
q,q',q'',\ldots,q^{(7)}
\]

as a primary transfer input. It needs:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}+\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C,
\qquad u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

The primitive quantities \(q,q'\) needed inside the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof can either be supplied by a safe canonical package, or recovered locally on the source interval from:

\[
u=q'',\qquad g=u-6q+2q^3,
\qquad \|g\|_{L^2(J)}\ll |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Thus the best current local-complexity statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary zero-separated tube}
\Rightarrow
\|q''_{\can}\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D q''_{\can}\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

A stronger \(q^{(0..7)}\) package remains useful for D4/row bookkeeping, but Gate 2 itself appears to need much less.

---

# 1. Ordinary zero-separated tube hypothesis

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

For an enlarged ordinary packet interval \(I^\ast\), define

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary zero-separated hypothesis should be:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Because

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

this is polynomial separation:

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

If this fails, the packet is not ordinary and should be routed to the singular/transition branch.

---

# 2. Completed-log-derivative transfer for \(u,u'\)

Assume

\[
u=q''_{\can}
\]

is the full canonical completed-meromorphic curvature:

\[
u(t)=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]

where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is a fixed finite expression in completed logarithmic derivatives of \(\Xi\) and regular gamma/background terms.

Let

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s).
\]

For fixed \(r\),

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_{\rho}
\frac{1}{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\text{regular terms}.
\]

On the zero-separated tube, set

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Dyadic annuli around \(s\) give

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^{C_r}.
\]

Therefore every fixed completed log-derivative order is polynomially bounded in the ordinary tube.

Since \(u\) is a fixed finite expression in those derivatives,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|u|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Differentiating \(u\) once in \(m\) only raises the completed-log-derivative order by one. Hence

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D u|
=
\sup_{I^\ast}|\lambda\partial_m u|
\le Q^C.
}
\]

This proves the minimal source-complexity transfer needed for the new Gate 2 extraction:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

No AFE \(\ell^1\)-bound should be used.

---

# 3. Canonical definition requirement

The above proof requires:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

That is, the AFE expression must be the canonical representation of the completed meromorphic curvature, not a standalone truncated proxy.

If \(u\) is only defined as a finite AFE truncation, the log-derivative proof does not apply directly. Then one would need perturbative error estimates:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^jE_2|\le Q^{-A_E}
\]

for the derivative orders used. For Gate 2 minimal complexity, \(j\le1\) is enough for \(u,u'\). D4 may require more.

Recommended policy:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the inclusive canonical policy for Gate 2: }E_2\text{ is part of }q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Then no separate \(E_2\)-smallness is needed for the Gate 2 transfer estimate.

---

# 4. Pole-set audit

The completed curvature operator \(\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) must introduce no dangerous denominators except those inherent in

\[
\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}.
\]

The dangerous pole set should be exactly:

\[
\mathcal Z_\Xi.
\]

Gamma/trivial poles are either far from high critical-line packet tubes or are regularized into the background. In particular, \(q''_{\can}\) must not contain denominators such as:

\[
\frac1{q_0},
\qquad
\frac1u,
\qquad
\frac1{\Gamma_G},
\qquad
\frac1{\Gamma_{G,2}}.
\]

If such denominators appear, the zero-separated zeta-tube hypothesis does not control them. Those denominators belong to projected row-conversion algebra, not to the canonical source curvature.

So the pole-set guardrail is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}\text{ must be denominator-free except through completed log derivatives.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Primitive strategy for \(q,q'\)

The \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity lemma uses \(q\) and \(q'\), but the new route does not require global transfer bounds for them.

There are three possible policies.

## Option A — Direct canonical formulas

If \(q,q'\) are also direct completed-meromorphic quantities, then ordinary zero-separated transfer gives:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k}
\]

for the required finite orders. This is the safest paper-level formulation.

## Option B — Basepoint normalization

If \(q\) is only a primitive of \(u=q''\), assume

\[
|q(m_b)|+|\mathcal D q(m_b)|\le Q^C
\]

at one point \(m_b\in I^\ast\). Then integrate \(u\) to get polynomial \(q,q'\) bounds on \(I^\ast\).

## Option C — Local recovery on the extracted source interval

For Gate 2 itself, this is enough.

On the source interval \(J\), Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
g=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Since \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C\), this gives \(L^2\)-control of

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Because

\[
|q|^6\ll |F(q)|^2+1,
\]

we get

\[
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/6}.
\]

With \(q''=u\in L^\infty\), one-dimensional interpolation gives, on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}+\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J')}\le Q^C.
\]

Thus primitive bounds are recovered locally.

For the Gate 2 proof, Option C is sufficient. For D4 row bookkeeping, Option A or B may still be preferable.

---

# 6. Minimal derivative package by module

## Gate 2 source extraction

Needs:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This follows from ordinary zero-separated transfer for \(u,u'\).

## \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

Needs local \(q,q',q''\) bounds. These are obtained from:

\[
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

plus \(L^2\)-small \(g\), as above.

## Wall escape

Needs:

\[
\boxed{
\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

Already included.

## Row mobility

Needs derivative bounds for the row vector:

\[
\|\mathbf A_N'\|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

This is not implied by the minimal Gate 2 package. It belongs to the D4/row-conversion analytic audit.

---

# 7. Safe stronger package

For broad bookkeeping, one may still state:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad
0\le k\le7.
}
\]

This follows if \(q,q'\) have direct completed-meromorphic formulas or basepoint normalization. It automatically covers:

- G2-A source extraction;
- G2-B integral rigidity;
- D3a wall escape;
- many row-mobility estimates.

But it is stronger than the current Gate 2 proof requires.

---

# 8. Theorem: minimal ordinary local complexity

### Minimal ordinary local complexity for Gate 2

Assume:

1. ordinary scale:

   \[
   \lambda Q\asymp1;
   \]

2. ordinary zero-separated tube:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
   \mathcal Z_\Xi
   \right)
   \ge
   \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

3. \(u=q''_{\can}\) is the full completed-meromorphic canonical curvature:

   \[
   u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
   \]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with local primitive recovery from \(L^2\)-small \(g\), this provides all local complexity needed for Gate 2.

---

# 9. Status table

| Item | Status | Notes |
|---|---:|---|
| Zero-separated transfer for \(u,u'\) | Near-Green | Standard completed log-derivative bound |
| Canonical formula \(u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) | Finite audit | Must define \(q''_{\can}\) as full meromorphic object |
| Pole set | Near-Green | No denominators besides \(\Xi'/\Xi\) |
| Local zero count | Green | Standard \(N(T+1)-N(T-1)\ll \log T\) |
| \(E_2\) policy | Closeable | Inclusive for Gate 2; perturbative for model transfer/D4 |
| Primitive \(q,q'\) for Gate 2 | Near-Green | Recover locally from \(u\) and \(L^2\)-small \(g\) |
| Safe \(q^{(0..7)}\) package | Stronger fallback | Useful for D4 and bookkeeping |
| Row mobility derivative bounds | Separate D4 audit | Not covered by minimal Gate 2 package |

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:00:36)

I’ll tighten the “local primitive recovery” step into a scale-invariant lemma. This is the last piece needed to justify that Gate 2 only needs canonical transfer for \(u=q''_{\can}\) and \(u'\), rather than global primitive bounds for \(q,q'\).

_Thought for 17s_

## Continued attack: scale-invariant primitive recovery for Gate 2

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Primitive recovery can be made scale-invariant and proof-level.}
}
\]

On the source-large interval \(J\), it is enough to know:

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le M,
\qquad
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=u-F(q),\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then on a shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}+\ell\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J')}
\le Q^C
}
\]

for polynomial \(M,\varepsilon^{-1},\ell^{-1}\), where

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J',\partial J).
\]

Thus Gate 2 does **not** need a global canonical primitive transfer for \(q,q'\). Local primitive bounds are forced by the equations and \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\).

---

# 1. Scale-invariant primitive recovery lemma

Let \(J\) be an interval of length \(L\), and let \(J'\Subset J\) with

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J',\partial J)>0.
\]

Assume

\[
q''=u,
\]

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Assume

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le M,
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon L^{1/2}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}
\le
C\left[
M^{1/13}
\left(M+\varepsilon+1\right)^{12/13}
+
\left(M+\varepsilon+1\right)
\right]
}
\]

up to polynomial powers of \(L/\ell\) after scaling.

In the downstream regime,

\[
M\le Q^C,\qquad \varepsilon^{-1}\le Q^C,\qquad L/\ell\le Q^C,
\]

this gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Then the interpolation estimate

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J'')}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J')}
\right)
}
\]

for \(J''\Subset J'\) yields

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J'')}\le Q^C.
}
\]

---

# 2. Proof of the \(q\)-bound

From

\[
g=u-F(q),
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}+\|g\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
(M+\varepsilon)L^{1/2}.
\]

The cubic polynomial

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3
\]

satisfies the pointwise algebraic inequality

\[
\boxed{
|q|^6\le C\left(|F(q)|^2+1\right).
}
\]

Indeed, for \(|q|\gg1\), \(|F(q)|\asymp |q|^3\), and for bounded \(|q|\), the constant term covers the estimate.

Integrating gives

\[
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}^6
\le
C\left(
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}^2+L
\right)
\le
C(M+\varepsilon+1)^2L.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}
\le
C(M+\varepsilon+1)^{1/3}L^{1/6}.
}
\]

This is enough for an \(L^\infty\)-bound once \(q''\) is bounded.

---

# 3. Gagliardo–Nirenberg interpolation

Rescale \(J\) to unit length. In one dimension,

\[
\|Q\|_{L^\infty}
\le
C\|Q''\|_{L^\infty}^{1/13}
\|Q\|_{L^6}^{12/13}
+
C\|Q\|_{L^6}
\]

on a shrunken interval.

Applying this to

\[
Q(y)=q(a+Ly)
\]

gives, after scaling,

\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}
\le
Q^C
\]

whenever

\[
\|q''\|_\infty=\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

\[
L^{-1/6}\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C,
\]

and \(J'\) is polynomially separated from \(\partial J\).

Since both hypotheses are satisfied, we get

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}\le Q^C.
}
\]

The exact exponent \(1/13\) is not important. Any one-dimensional interpolation estimate giving \(L^\infty\) from \(L^6\) and \(W^{2,\infty}\) is sufficient.

---

# 4. Recover \(q'\)

Once

\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}\le Q^C
\]

and

\[
\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J')}\le Q^C,
\]

the standard Landau estimate gives for \(J''\Subset J'\):

\[
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J'')}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J')}
\right),
\]

where

\[
\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J'',\partial J').
\]

If

\[
\ell^{-1}\le Q^C |I|^{-1}
\]

in physical units, or \(\ell^{-1}\le Q^C\) in normalized units, then

\[
\boxed{
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J'')}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This recovers the last primitive bound needed for the \(q\chi_\delta(q)\)-multiplier proof.

---

# 5. Consequence for \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

The \(L^2\)-input integral-rigidity lemma can now be stated with minimal assumptions:

### Minimal \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma

Assume on \(J\):

\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\]

where

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Then, on a polynomially shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|
}
\]

or at least

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{c}|J'|
}
\]

for some absolute \(c>0\), depending on the finalized cutoff bookkeeping.

No separate assumptions on global \(q,q'\) are needed.

---

# 6. Why this is enough for Gate 2

The new Gate 2 proof uses:

1. Gate 1:

   \[
   \int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

2. Source bound and derivative:

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty|I|\le Q^C.
   \]

3. Gate 2 failure:

   \[
   \int_I|u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
   \]

4. Source-large interval extraction produces \(J\) with

   \[
   |u|\ge \tau
   \]

   and

   \[
   \|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
   \le
   \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
   \]

5. Minimal \(L^2\)-rigidity gives

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{c}|J'|.
   \]

6. But source largeness gives

   \[
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
   \]

For \(A\) large enough, contradiction.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\|u\|_\infty+\|u'\|_\infty\le Q^C
+
L^2\text{-rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Updated canonical transfer requirement

The only canonical transfer needed for Gate 2 is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Under ordinary zero-separated tube hypotheses, this follows from the completed log-derivative estimate for the canonical curvature.

Primitive \(q,q'\) are recovered locally and do not need independent global transfer for Gate 2.

This is the cleanest minimal analytic package so far.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Primitive recovery can be formalized by }L^6 + W^{2,\infty}\text{ interpolation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 needs canonical transfer for }u,u'\text{ only.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No global }q,q'\text{ primitive bounds are required for Gate 2.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining main proof task is the }L^2\text{-input integral-rigidity cutoff proof.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:45:03)

_Thought for 9s_

Agent 1 / A report: canonical real-normal-form and \(u,u'\) transfer. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 canonical package closes modulo one explicit definition audit: }u=q''_{\can}\text{ must be the full completed meromorphic curvature.}
}
\]

Under the ordinary zero-separated tube condition,

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

the standard completed-log-derivative estimate gives

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}+\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
\le Q^C,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

This supplies the analytic input needed for source thickening and wall escape. The remaining real-normal-form requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R
}
\]

on the critical line. This is Green if \(q\) is built from a real completed critical-line scalar such as \(\Xi(t)=\xi(1/2+it)\) or a Hardy-normalized equivalent, and not from a one-sided complex AFE branch.

---

# 1. Completed real scalar

For the Riemann xi-function,

\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s),
\]

one has the functional equation

\[
\xi(s)=\xi(1-s)
\]

and Schwarz symmetry

\[
\overline{\xi(s)}=\xi(\overline{s}).
\]

On the critical line \(s=1/2+it\),

\[
\overline{\xi(1/2+it)}
=
\xi(1/2-it)
=
\xi(1-(1/2+it))
=
\xi(1/2+it).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(t):=\xi(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R
\qquad(t\in\mathbb R).
}
\]

If the paper uses a Hardy-normalized scalar \(Z(t)\), the same real-line conclusion holds by construction:

\[
\boxed{
Z(t)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

Thus a real scalar normal form is available, provided \(q\) is defined from this real completed critical-line scalar or an equivalent real gauge.

---

# 2. Ordinary zero-separated tube

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

For an enlarged ordinary packet \(I^\ast\), define

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary hypothesis is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Since

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

this distance is polynomial:

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

If this condition fails, the packet is not ordinary; it belongs to the singular/transition branch.

---

# 3. Completed-log-derivative transfer for \(u,u'\)

Assume

\[
u=q''_{\can}
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi](1/2+im),
\]

where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is a fixed finite completed-meromorphic curvature operator formed from

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]

and finitely many derivatives \(L^{(r)}(s)\), plus regular gamma/background terms.

For fixed \(r\),

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho \frac{1}{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\text{regular terms}.
\]

Set

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

On the ordinary tube, every zero satisfies

\[
|s-\rho|\ge\delta.
\]

Split zeros into dyadic annuli

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le 2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Using the local zero-count bound

\[
N_\Xi(t+R)-N_\Xi(t-R)\ll Q^C(1+R),
\]

we get

\[
\# A_\nu\ll Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta).
\]

Hence

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\ll
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Summing over \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\ll Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Since

\[
\delta^{-1}\asymp Q^{1+C_0},
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(r)}(s)|\le Q^{C_r}
}
\]

for every fixed \(r\).

Because \(u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) is a fixed finite expression in these objects,

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Also,

\[
\mathcal D u=\lambda \partial_m u
\]

only raises the completed-log-derivative order by one and multiplies by \(\lambda\le 1\). Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the minimal analytic-complexity transfer needed for the current Gate 2 route.

---

# 4. Pole-set audit

The proof above is valid only if \(q''_{\can}\) is denominator-free except through completed logarithmic derivatives.

Allowed poles:

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(s)=0.
}
\]

Allowed regular terms:

\[
\boxed{
\text{gamma/background/polygamma terms, conductor factors, fixed smooth coefficients.}
}
\]

Forbidden denominators in \(q''_{\can}\):

\[
\boxed{
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Such denominators may appear in projected row algebra, but they cannot appear in the canonical curvature \(q''_{\can}\). If they do, ordinary zero-separation from \(\mathcal Z_\Xi\) does not control them.

Gamma/trivial poles are harmless at high critical-line packet height: for

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]

polygamma poles are far from \(t\asymp e^Q\), and

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

So \(B_2\) and its normalized derivatives are polynomially bounded, in fact tiny.

---

# 5. Real normal form

If

\[
q=q(t)
\]

is defined from the real completed critical-line scalar \(\Xi(t)\) or Hardy-normalized \(Z(t)\), and the coordinate chart is real, then

\[
\boxed{
q(t)\in\mathbb R
}
\]

for real \(t\). Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
u(t)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

Then

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

is real, and

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

is also real.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

If \(q\) is chart-dependent, the theorem must be stated chartwise:

### Real chart condition

On the chart used for Gate 2,

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
\]

the identities

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

hold with normalized real derivatives, and all chart denominators are bounded below by \(Q^{-C}\).

If a chart denominator can vanish, the real-normal-form proof is not valid there; either switch charts or treat that region separately.

---

# 6. Primitive policy

For the current Gate 2 proof, global primitive transfer for \(q,q'\) is not strictly necessary.

The minimal route is:

1. Use ordinary transfer to get

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

2. From Gate 2 failure on the extracted source interval \(J\), get

   \[
   \|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
   \]

3. Since

   \[
   g=u-F(q),
   \qquad
   F(q)=6q-2q^3,
   \]

   we have

   \[
   F(q)=u-g.
   \]

4. Use

   \[
   |q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2)
   \]

   to get

   \[
   \|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C |J|^{1/6}.
   \]

5. Since

   \[
   q''=u,\qquad \|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
   \]

   one-dimensional interpolation gives local

   \[
   \|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty\le Q^C
   \]

   on \(J'\Subset J\).

So for Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
\text{primitive bounds are locally recovered.}
}
\]

However, for a safe paper-level theorem and for D4 row algebra, one may instead assume either:

\[
\boxed{
q,q'\text{ have direct completed-meromorphic formulas,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
|q(m_b)|+|q'(m_b)|\le Q^C
}
\]

at one basepoint.

---

# 7. \(E_2\) policy

Use the inclusive canonical policy for Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical curvature. The zero-separated meromorphic transfer applies to the full \(q''_{\can}\), and no separate \(E_2\)-smallness is needed for Gate 2.

If instead \(E_2\) is a truncation error between a model and the canonical object, then the minimal Gate 2 transfer requires

\[
\boxed{
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}.
}
\]

For D4, higher \(E_2\)-derivative residuals may still need audit.

---

# 8. Final theorem package

### Gate 2 canonical package

Assume:

1. real completed scalar:

   \[
   \Xi(t)=\xi(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R
   \]

   or equivalent Hardy real scalar;

2. ordinary zero-separated tube:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
   \mathcal Z_\Xi
   \right)
   \ge
   \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

3. canonical curvature definition:

   \[
   u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]
   \]

   with no forbidden denominators;

4. real chart:

   \[
   q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
   \]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with local primitive recovery, this supplies the analytic package for the \(L^2\)-input Gate 2 proof.

---

# 9. Final status table

| Audit item | Verdict | Exact blocker if not closed |
|---|---:|---|
| \(\Xi(t)\in\mathbb R\) | Green for completed \(\xi\) / Hardy scalar | Need actual scalar definition |
| Ordinary tube condition | Green as definition | If false, route to singular/transition |
| \(u,u'\) transfer | Green under completed meromorphic \(u\) | Need \(u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) |
| Pole set | Green if denominator-free | Forbidden denominators in \(q''_{\can}\) |

| Primitive \(q,q'\) policy | Gate 2: recover locally | D4 may need safe stronger bounds |

---

## Continued attack: real normal form and completed-log derivative closure

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The real-normal-form audit closes if }q\text{ is built from a real completed critical-line scalar, not from a one-sided AFE branch.}
}
\]

The correct canonical package is:

\[
\boxed{
Y(t):=\xi(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R
\quad\text{or}\quad
Y(t):=Z(t)\in\mathbb R,
}
\]

and all Gate 2 variables are real differential expressions in \(Y\), or in a real coordinate derived from \(Y\), on zero-free ordinary intervals. Then

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R
}
\]

and the \(L^2\)-input rigidity proof is valid.

The remaining blocker is precise and finite:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Confirm that the paper’s }q,\ q''_{\can},\ \Gamma_G,\ \Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ are defined in this real completed gauge.}
}
\]

If they are instead defined from \(P_2\), \(D_2\), or another one-sided complex branch, the present Gate 2 real-rigidity proof does not apply without an additional Hermitian reformulation.

---

# 1. Realness of the completed critical-line scalar

For the Riemann xi-function,

\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s),
\]

we have

\[
\xi(s)=\xi(1-s)
\]

and

\[
\overline{\xi(s)}=\xi(\overline{s}).
\]

For

\[
s=\frac12+it,
\]

\[
\overline{\xi(1/2+it)}
=
\xi(1/2-it)
=
\xi(1-(1/2+it))
=
\xi(1/2+it).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(t):=\xi(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R
\qquad(t\in\mathbb R).
}
\]

Likewise, Hardy’s \(Z(t)\) is real by definition. Thus either choice supplies a real scalar on the critical line.

---

# 2. Real log-derivative hierarchy on zero-free intervals

On an ordinary interval avoiding zeros, let

\[
Y(t)=\Xi(t)
\]

or

\[
Y(t)=Z(t),
\]

with

\[
Y(t)\neq0.
\]

Then \(Y\) is real-valued on the real line. On any connected zero-free component, choose a real logarithm of \(|Y|\) and define

\[
\ell(t):=\frac{d}{dt}\log |Y(t)|
=
\frac{Y'(t)}{Y(t)}.
\]

Since \(Y,Y'\in\mathbb R\),

\[
\boxed{
\ell(t)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

Moreover,

\[
\ell^{(k)}(t)
=
\frac{d^k}{dt^k}\frac{Y'(t)}{Y(t)}
\]

is real for every \(k\) on the zero-free interval.

Thus any expression

\[
\mathcal P\bigl(\ell,\ell',\ldots,\ell^{(r)}\bigr)
\]

with real coefficients is real.

So if

\[
q,\ u=q''_{\can},\ g=\Gamma_G,\ h=\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are real differential-polynomial expressions in this hierarchy, then

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

This is the exact real-normal-form condition.

---

# 3. Relation to completed log derivative in \(s\)

Let

\[
L(s)=\frac{\xi'}{\xi}(s).
\]

Along the critical line,

\[
Y(t)=\xi(1/2+it).
\]

Then

\[
\frac{d}{dt}\log Y(t)
=
i\,L(1/2+it).
\]

Since \(Y(t)\in\mathbb R\) on zero-free intervals, the quantity

\[
iL(1/2+it)
\]

is real.

More generally,

\[
\frac{d^k}{dt^k}\frac{d}{dt}\log Y(t)
=
i^{k+1}L^{(k)}(1/2+it),
\]

and this is real on real \(t\) away from zeros.

So the same completed log-derivative transfer estimates apply, but the real variables should be expressed as the real critical-line combinations

\[
\boxed{
i^{k+1}L^{(k)}(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

This avoids ambiguity about taking real or imaginary parts.

---

# 4. Canonical curvature \(u=q''_{\can}\)

For Gate 2, the minimum needed canonical transfer is:

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This closes if

\[
u=q''_{\can}
\]

is a fixed real differential expression in the completed hierarchy:

\[
\boxed{
u(t)
=
\mathcal U
\left(
iL,\ i^2L',\ \ldots,\ i^{r+1}L^{(r)}
\right)_{s=1/2+it}
+
\text{regular gamma/background}.
}
\]

Here \(r\) is fixed and \(\mathcal U\) has real coefficients.

Then:

1. \(u(t)\in\mathbb R\) on real \(t\);
2. \(u\) is meromorphic off the line with poles only at zeros of \(\xi\);
3. ordinary zero-separated tube estimates give

   \[
   \|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
   \]

So the \(u,u'\) part of the Gate 2 analytic package is closed.

---

# 5. Real form of \(g,h\)

The real-rigidity proof uses the identities:

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

If \(q\in\mathbb R\), then

\[
q',q'',g,g'',h\in\mathbb R.
\]

Hence the kinetic term in the \(h\)-identity is genuinely positive:

\[
2q(q')^2\cdot q\chi_\delta(q)
=
2q^2\chi_\delta(q)(q')^2\ge0.
\]

This positivity is the core reason the \(L^2\)-input rigidity proof works. It fails for a generic complex \(q\), since

\[
q^2(q')^2
\]

has no fixed sign or Hermitian positivity.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{real normal form is not cosmetic; it is structurally necessary.}
}
\]

---

# 6. One-sided AFE branches are not enough

The components

\[
P_2,\qquad D_2
\]

are generally complex oscillatory branches. Individually, they do not supply a real scalar source.

The real canonical source must be the full symmetric/completed object:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
}
\]

with main and dual branches combined in the correct completed real gauge.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Gate 2 real-rigidity proof cannot be applied to }P_2\text{ or }D_2\text{ alone.}
}
\]

Any proof using a one-sided branch must be rewritten in a complex Hermitian form, which is a different theorem.

---

# 7. Chart-dependent \(q\)

If \(q\) is not directly

\[
\ell(t)=Y'/Y
\]

but a local chart coordinate or normalized source variable, the necessary chart condition is:

\[
\boxed{
q=\Psi(\ell,\ell',\ldots,\ell^{(r)})
}
\]

with \(\Psi\) real-valued on real inputs and no uncontrolled denominators on the chart.

If \(\Psi\) has denominators, the chart must satisfy a polynomial lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
|\operatorname{denominator}_\Psi|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the packet interval. Otherwise the real-normal-form variables may blow up independently of the zero-separated tube.

So the chartwise version is:

### Real chart normal form

On a chart where all denominators are polynomially bounded below,

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
\]

the identities

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

hold with real normalized derivatives.

This is enough for the Gate 2 rigidity proof.

---

# 8. Minimal canonical audit checklist

To close the real-normal-form audit, verify exactly:

1. **Completed scalar**  
   The proof uses \(Y(t)=\xi(1/2+it)\), \(Z(t)\), or an explicitly real equivalent.

2. **Real source coordinate**  
   \(q\) is real-valued on real \(t\), either directly or in a real chart.

3. **Canonical curvature**  
   \(u=q''_{\can}\) is the second normalized derivative of that real \(q\), or the canonical expression agreeing with it.

4. **Gate 2 identities**  
   The identities

   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
   \]

   hold in the same derivative convention.

5. **No forbidden denominators**  
   \(q''_{\can}\) has no denominators except those in the completed log derivative. Chart denominators, if any, are bounded below.

6. **Full canonical object**  
   \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) equals the full real canonical \(u\). It is not a one-sided proxy.

If all six hold, the canonical real Gate 2 package is closed.

---

# 9. Final theorem

### Real canonical Gate 2 normal form

Assume:

1. \(Y(t)\) is a real completed critical-line scalar;
2. \(q\) is a real chart coordinate built from \(Y\) with denominator lower bounds;
3. \(u=q''_{\can}=q''\) is the full canonical curvature;
4. \(g,h\) satisfy

   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'';
   \]

5. the ordinary packet tube is polynomially zero-separated from zeros of \(Y\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with the \(L^2\)-input integral-rigidity lemma, this proves Gate 2 from Gate 1.

---

## Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Real normal form: Green for completed }\xi/Z\text{ gauge.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{One-sided AFE branches: not admissible for the real rigidity proof.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Chart denominators must be audited if }q\text{ is not direct.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remaining blocker: confirm the paper’s }q,q''_{\can},\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\text{ are exactly in this real canonical gauge.}
}
\]

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Gate 2 canonical package closes modulo one finite definition audit.}
}
\]

If

\[
u=q''_{\can}
\]

is the full completed meromorphic curvature associated to a real critical-line scalar \(\Xi(t)\), and the packet is ordinary zero-separated, then

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
+

\le Q^C.

\[

also closes if \(q\) is defined in a real completed gauge, not from a one-sided AFE branch.

# 1. Real completed critical-line scalar

Let

\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s).
\]

Then

\[
\xi(s)=\xi(1-s),
\qquad
\overline{\xi(s)}=\xi(\overline{s}).
\]

For

\[
s=\frac12+it,
\]

\[
\overline{\xi(1/2+it)}
=
\xi(1/2-it)
=
\xi(1-(1/2+it))
=
\xi(1/2+it).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(t):=\xi(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R
\quad (t\in\mathbb R).
}
\]

The same applies to a Hardy-normalized scalar \(Z(t)\), if that is the paper’s real critical-line scalar.

Thus a real scalar gauge exists.

---

# 2. Real normal form

Assume \(q\) is a real chart coordinate built from \(\Xi(t)\), \(Z(t)\), or their real logarithmic derivative hierarchy on a zero-free interval. Then

\[
q(t)\in\mathbb R.
\]

If

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

then

\[
u(t)\in\mathbb R.
\]

Therefore

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

is real, and

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''
\]

is real.

So

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

This is structurally necessary: the rigidity proof uses the nonnegative term

\[
2q^2\chi_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

If \(q\) is complex, that positivity disappears.

Therefore the real-normal-form audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 must use the full real completed canonical object, not a one-sided AFE branch.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Ordinary zero-separated tube

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Let \(I^\ast\) be an enlarged ordinary packet interval. Define

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary zero-separated hypothesis is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Since

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

this lower bound is polynomial:

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

If this condition fails, the packet is singular/transition, not ordinary.

---

# 4. Completed-log-derivative transfer

Let

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s).
\]

For fixed \(r\),

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho \frac1{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\mathcal G_r(s),
\]

where \(\mathcal G_r\) denotes regular gamma/background terms.

On the ordinary tube set

\[
\delta:=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Then

\[
|s-\rho|\ge\delta
\]

for every zero \(\rho\).

Split zeros into dyadic annuli

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Using local zero count,

\[
\# A_\nu\le Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta),
\]

so

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Summing over \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Because

\[
\delta^{-1}\asymp Q^{1+C_0},
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(r)}(s)|\le Q^{C_r}
}
\]

for every fixed \(r\).

---

# 5. Transfer for \(u=q''_{\can}\)

Assume the canonical curvature is a fixed completed-meromorphic expression

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi](1/2+im),
}
\]

where \(\mathfrak C_2\) uses only finitely many \(L^{(r)}\)’s and regular gamma/background terms.

Then the previous estimate gives

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Moreover,

\[
\mathcal D u=\lambda\partial_m u
\]

only raises the completed-log-derivative order by one and multiplies by \(\lambda\le1\). Hence

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the minimal analytic-complexity package needed for source thickening in the current Gate 2 route.

---

# 6. Pole-set audit

The transfer proof is valid if \(q''_{\can}\) has no uncontrolled denominators.

Allowed:

\[
\boxed{
\Xi'/\Xi,\quad L^{(r)},\quad \text{regular gamma/background terms}.
}
\]

Forbidden inside \(q''_{\can}\):

\[
\boxed{
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Such denominators may occur in row-projection algebra, but not in the canonical source curvature.

For the background term,

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]

polygamma poles are far from high critical-line packet tubes, and

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}),
\]

so \(B_2\) is harmless.

---

# 7. \(E_2\) policy

Use the inclusive canonical policy for Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical object, and no separate \(E_2\)-smallness is needed for the Gate 2 \(u,u'\) transfer.

If instead \(E_2\) is a truncation/model error, the minimal Gate 2 transfer needs

\[
\boxed{
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}.
}
\]

D4 may still require higher-order \(E_2\)-residual audits.

---

# 8. Primitive \(q,q'\) policy

For the \(L^2\)-input rigidity proof there are two admissible policies.

## Safe policy

Assume direct real canonical formulas for \(q,q'\), or basepoint normalization:

\[
\boxed{
|q(m_b)|+|\mathcal Dq(m_b)|\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with \(u=q''\), this gives \(q,q'\) bounds on \(I^\ast\).

## Minimal Gate 2 policy

Recover \(q,q'\) locally on the extracted source interval.

Given

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le\varepsilon |J|^{1/2},
\quad
\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

we get

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

Since

\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2),
\]

we get

\[
q\in L^6(J)
\]

with polynomial norm. Since

\[
q''=u\in L^\infty(J),
\]

one-dimensional interpolation gives

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J')}+\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J')}\le Q^C
}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(J'\Subset J\).

Thus primitive \(q,q'\) bounds are locally recoverable for Gate 2.

---

# 9. Final theorem package

### Canonical Gate 2 package

Assume:

1. \(Y(t)=\Xi(t)\) or \(Z(t)\) is real on the critical line;

2. \(q\) is a real chart coordinate, so

   \[
   q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R;
   \]

3. the ordinary packet tube is zero-separated:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
   \mathcal Z_\Xi
   \right)
   \ge
   \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

4. the canonical curvature is the full completed meromorphic object:

   \[
   u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi];
   \]

5. \(q''_{\can}\) has no forbidden denominators.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

Together with local primitive recovery, this supplies the analytic package for the \(L^2\)-input Gate 2 proof.

---

# 10. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 canonical package is near-Green.}
}

The only exact blockers are finite definition checks:

## Continued attack: close the definition audit as a finite compatibility test

Source context: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The canonical transfer for }u,u'\text{ is effectively closed; the remaining definition audit is a finite compatibility test for }q,g,h.
}
\]

The remaining issue is **not** analytic complexity. It is whether the paper’s variables satisfy the exact real scalar identities:

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

If yes, Gate 2 has the local real-variable package it needs. If no, the current rigidity proof is being applied to the wrong variables.

So the audit should be reduced to a finite checklist:

\[
\boxed{
\text{real scalar }q
\quad+\quad
u=q''
\quad+\quad
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
\quad+\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

---

# 1. Separate analytic transfer from coordinate compatibility

There are two logically distinct issues.

## A. Analytic transfer

This is now near-Green:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}
\]

implies

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This follows from completed log-derivative estimates if

\[
u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]
\]

is a fixed completed meromorphic curvature.

## B. Coordinate compatibility

This is the remaining finite audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does this canonical }u\text{ equal }q''\text{ for the same real }q\text{ used in }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}?
}
\]

The \(L^2\)-rigidity proof needs this identity. It cannot use an unrelated canonical curvature \(u\).

---

# 2. Minimal compatibility theorem

The local Gate 2 proof only needs the following.

### Compatibility package

On each ordinary packet interval \(I\), there exists a real \(C^4\) scalar \(q\) such that:

\[
\boxed{
u=q''
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
}
\]

Furthermore,

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

Then the Gate 2 real-rigidity proof applies.

This package does **not** require a global formula for \(q\). It does not require \(q\) to be a log derivative globally. It only requires the local real scalar identities to be exact in the normalized derivative convention.

---

# 3. If \(q\) is only defined up to affine ambiguity

Suppose \(u=q''_{\can}\) is known, but \(q\) is a primitive:

\[
q''=u.
\]

Then \(q\) is defined up to

\[
q\mapsto q+am+b.
\]

The identity

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

fixes this ambiguity. Indeed, if \(\Gamma_G\) is canonical, then \(q\) must solve

\[
2q^3-6q+(u-\Gamma_G)=0
\]

pointwise.

Thus \(q\) cannot be an arbitrary primitive. It must be the branch of the cubic relation compatible with

\[
q''=u.
\]

This gives a useful audit test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Check that the }q\text{ used in the paper satisfies both the cubic relation and }q''=u.
}
\]

If both hold, affine ambiguity is gone.

If only \(q''=u\) holds, Gate 2 variables are underdetermined.

If only the cubic relation holds, the second-derivative dynamics may fail.

---

# 4. Consistency equation for \(q\)

Combining

\[
q''=u
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

gives the forced ODE

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Gamma_G.
}
\]

Thus the definition audit can be restated as:

\[
\boxed{
q\text{ solves }q''=6q-2q^3+\Gamma_G.
}
\]

This is useful because it only involves \(q\) and \(\Gamma_G\). Then \(u\) is automatically

\[
u=q''.
\]

The second identity is:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

So the entire Gate 2 definition audit is exactly two equations:

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Gamma_G,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

If these are present in the paper, the real-variable Gate 2 proof is legitimate.

---

# 5. Realness audit

The scalar \(q\) must be real-valued.

There are three acceptable cases.

## Case A: \(q\) is directly defined from a real completed scalar

For example, from

\[
\Xi(t)=\xi(1/2+it)\in\mathbb R
\]

or Hardy \(Z(t)\in\mathbb R\).

Then

\[
q\in\mathbb R
\]

is immediate if the defining formula has real coefficients and denominator signs are controlled.

## Case B: \(q\) is a real chart coordinate

Then the chart must be stated with real input/output:

\[
q=\Psi(Y,Y',\ldots,Y^{(r)}),
\qquad
Y(t)\in\mathbb R,
\]

where

\[
\Psi:\mathbb R^{r+1}\to\mathbb R.
\]

Any denominator in \(\Psi\) must satisfy

\[
|\operatorname{denominator}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on the chart.

## Case C: \(q\) is selected as a real solution branch of the cubic/ODE system

Then one must prove branch continuity and realness on \(I\).

This is acceptable but requires a branch-selection lemma.

---

# 6. Denominator audit

The Gate 2 canonical source \(u=q''_{\can}\) must be denominator-free except through the completed log derivative. But the **chart** defining \(q\) may have denominators.

If chart denominators exist, they do not invalidate the proof as long as:

\[
\boxed{
|\text{chart denominator}|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the interval.

If a chart denominator can vanish, then either:

1. switch to another real chart;
2. exclude the chart-singular region by a separate argument;
3. or rewrite Gate 2 in chart-free variables.

Thus the definition audit should include:

\[
\boxed{
\text{List all denominators in }q,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

Forbidden in \(u=q''_{\can}\):

\[
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
\]

Allowed in chart definition only if bounded below.

---

# 7. Canonical \(E_2\) audit

For Gate 2, use the inclusive identity:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then \(E_2\) is part of the exact object and no separate smallness is needed for \(u,u'\).

But if the paper treats \(E_2\) as a truncation remainder, then the audit must prove:

\[
\boxed{
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}
}
\]

for Gate 2 minimal transfer.

The audit question is binary:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }E_2\text{ exact-canonical or perturbative?}
}
\]

For downstream Gate 2, exact-canonical is strongly preferable.

---

# 8. Final finite audit list

To close the Gate 2 canonical definition package, verify the following six items.

## Item 1 — Real scalar

\[
Y(t)=\Xi(t)\text{ or }Z(t)\in\mathbb R.
\]

## Item 2 — Real \(q\)

\[
q(t)\in\mathbb R
\]

in the chosen chart.

## Item 3 — Curvature identity

\[
u=q''_{\can}=q''.
\]

## Item 4 — First anisotropy identity

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
\]

## Item 5 — Second anisotropy identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

## Item 6 — Canonical meromorphic source

\[
q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]
\]

with no forbidden denominators and ordinary zero-separated transfer:

\[
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

If all six are true, the Gate 2 canonical package is closed.

---

# 9. What we can conclude now

Without the actual definitions in front of us, I cannot certify Items 2–5 as facts. But the audit is now finite and exact.

The downstream Gate 2 proof no longer depends on broad Remez/Cartan/nonrecurrence inputs. It depends on:

\[
\boxed{
\text{these five/six definition equalities}
}
\]

and the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma.

This is a major reduction.

---

}

## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:00:59)

_Thought for 8s_

Agent 1 / A report: canonical real-normal-form and \((u,u')\) transfer. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The analytic transfer for }u,u'\text{ closes under the ordinary zero-separated tube hypothesis.}
}
\]

The remaining non-analytic issue is a **finite definition audit**:

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,\qquad
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

If the paper’s \(q\) is the same real completed-gauge scalar used in \(u=q''_{\can}\), then the Gate 2 canonical package is closed. If \(q\) is a one-sided AFE branch or an unrelated primitive, the current real-rigidity proof does not apply.

---

# 1. Real completed scalar

Let

\[
\Xi(t)=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]

where

\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s).
\]

Since

\[
\xi(s)=\xi(1-s),
\qquad
\overline{\xi(s)}=\xi(\overline{s}),
\]

we have for real \(t\),

\[
\overline{\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)}
=
\xi\!\left(\frac12-it\right)
=
\xi\!\left(1-\left(\frac12+it\right)\right)
=
\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(t)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

A Hardy-normalized scalar \(Z(t)\) is also admissible, provided all downstream quantities are defined from that same real scalar gauge.

---

# 2. Ordinary zero-separated tube

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

For an enlarged packet \(I^\ast\), define

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary zero-separated hypothesis is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Since \(\lambda\asymp Q^{-1}\), the separation scale is polynomial:

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

If this fails, the packet is not ordinary and must be routed to singular/transition analysis.

---

# 3. Transfer for \(u=q''_{\can}\) and \(\mathcal D u\)

Assume

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\!\left(\frac12+im\right),
}
\]

where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is a fixed finite completed-meromorphic curvature operator built from

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]

and finitely many derivatives \(L^{(r)}(s)\), plus regular gamma/background terms.

For fixed \(r\),

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho\frac1{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\mathcal G_r(s),
\]

where \(\mathcal G_r\) contains regular gamma/background terms.

Set

\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

On the ordinary tube,

\[
|s-\rho|\ge \delta
\]

for every zero \(\rho\). Split zeros into dyadic annuli:

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Using standard local zero-counting,

\[
\#A_\nu\le Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta).
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Summing in \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^{C_r}.
\]

Therefore, for each fixed \(r\),

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(r)}(s)|\le Q^{C_r}.
}
\]

Since \(u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) has fixed finite complexity,

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Also,

\[
\mathcal D u=\lambda\partial_m u
\]

only raises the completed-log-derivative order by one and multiplies by \(\lambda\le1\). Hence

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the minimal canonical transfer needed for the current Gate 2 proof.

---

# 4. Pole-set audit

The transfer proof is valid only if \(q''_{\can}\) has no uncontrolled denominators.

Allowed inside \(q''_{\can}\):

\[
\boxed{
\Xi'/\Xi,\quad L^{(r)},\quad \text{regular gamma/background terms}.
}
\]

Forbidden inside \(q''_{\can}\):

\[
\boxed{
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Such denominators may appear later in row-projection or quotient algebra, but not in the canonical curvature.

For

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]

polygamma poles are far from high critical-line packet tubes, and

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

So \(B_2\) is regular and harmless.

---

# 5. \(E_2\) policy

For Gate 2, the clean policy is inclusive:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical object, and no separate \(E_2\)-smallness is needed for the \(u,u'\) transfer.

If instead \(E_2\) is a perturbative truncation error, Gate 2 minimally needs

\[
\boxed{
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}.
}
\]

D4 may require higher-order \(E_2\)-residual audits.

---

# 6. Real normal form for \(q,u,g,h\)

The real-rigidity proof requires

\[
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
\]

This is valid if \(q\) is defined from the real scalar \(\Xi(t)\) or Hardy \(Z(t)\) by a real chart:

\[
q=\Psi(Y,Y',\ldots,Y^{(r)}),
\qquad
Y(t)\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
\Psi:\mathbb R^{r+1}\to\mathbb R.
\]

If \(\Psi\) has denominators, require

\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{\rm chart}|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the packet.

Then

\[
q(t)\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
u=q''\in\mathbb R,
\]

and

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3\in\mathbb R,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\in\mathbb R.
\]

If \(q\) is instead a one-sided AFE branch, then \(q\) is generally complex and the positive kinetic term in the rigidity proof fails. The current Gate 2 proof is then not valid without a separate Hermitian reformulation.

---

# 7. Compatibility identities

The finite definition audit consists of exactly these equalities, in the same normalized derivative convention:

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=q''.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Gamma_G,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

If either identity is approximate, define residuals

\[
r_G=\Gamma_G-(q''-6q+2q^3),
\]

\[
r_{G,2}=
\Gamma_{G,2}
-
\left(2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right).
\]

Then the \(L^2\)-rigidity lemma requires

\[
\boxed{
\|r_G\|_{L^2(J)}+\|r_{G,2}\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

For the clean theorem, the identities should be exact.

---

# 8. Primitive policy

For Gate 2, global primitive transfer for \(q,q'\) is not strictly necessary.

Safe option:

\[
\boxed{
|q(m_b)|+|\mathcal Dq(m_b)|\le Q^C
}
\]

at one basepoint, or direct completed-meromorphic formulas for \(q,q'\).

Minimal option:

On the source interval \(J\), Gate 2 failure gives

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

Since

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

and \(\|u\|_\infty\le Q^C\), we get \(F(q)\in L^2\), hence

\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2)
\]

gives \(q\in L^6\). With \(q''=u\in L^\infty\), one-dimensional interpolation gives local \(q,q'\) bounds on \(J'\Subset J\).

Thus primitive bounds are locally recoverable for Gate 2.

---

# 9. Final theorem package

### Gate 2 canonical package

Assume:

1. \(Y(t)=\Xi(t)\) or Hardy \(Z(t)\) is real on the critical line;

2. \(q\) is a real chart coordinate with denominator lower bound if needed;

3. \(u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) is the full completed meromorphic curvature;

4. ordinary zero-separated tube:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
   \mathcal Z_\Xi
   \right)
   \ge
   \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

5. compatibility identities:

   \[
   u=q'',
   \]

   \[
   \Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   \Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
   \]

Then

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This supplies the canonical analytic package required by the \(L^2\)-input Gate 2 theorem.

---

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic transfer for }u,u'\text{ is closed under ordinary zero-separated tube and completed-meromorphic }u.
}
\]

\boxed{
\text{Remaining audit is finite: confirm real gauge and the three compatibility identities.}
}
\]

\[

}

## Audit item 1 — Real critical-line scalar

This item is mathematically Green if the paper uses the completed \(\xi\)-function or Hardy \(Z\)-function.

For

\[
\Xi(t):=\xi(1/2+it),
\]

we have

\[
\overline{\xi(1/2+it)}
=
\xi(1/2-it)
=
\xi(1-(1/2+it))
=
\xi(1/2+it),
\]

so

\[
\boxed{\Xi(t)\in\mathbb R.}
\]

Thus a real scalar gauge exists.

**Audit status:** Green for completed \(\xi\) or Hardy \(Z\).  
**Blocker if not:** if \(q\) is built from raw \(\zeta(1/2+it)\), \(P_2\), or \(D_2\) alone, then \(q\) is generally complex and the real rigidity proof does not apply. The uploaded handoff explicitly warns that the real-rigidity proof needs the full canonical real object, not a one-sided AFE branch. 

---

## Audit item 2 — \(u=q''_{\can}=q''\)

The Gate 2 proof needs the same scalar \(q\) to satisfy

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=q''.
}
\]

This is not optional: the rigidity lemma uses both

\[
u=q''
\]

and

\[
u=F(q)+g.
\]

If \(q''_{\can}\) is a separate curvature not literally equal to the second normalized derivative of the same \(q\), the proof is not valid.

**Audit status:** not certified from the handoff.  
**Exact blocker:** locate the paper’s definition of \(q\) and verify, in the same normalized derivative convention, that

\[

\]

\[

\]

must satisfy

\[
\|r_u\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\]

or a stronger pointwise version on the rigidity interval.

---

The proof requires

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[

\]

This identity is repeatedly stated in the downstream handoff and is the bridge between \(u\)-mass and the scalar potential \(F(q)=6q-2q^3\). 

**Audit status:** accepted as a stated downstream identity, but not independently certified against the paper’s definitions.

If the actual paper definition differs, compute

\[

If \(r_G\) is not small or not structured, Gate 2 is blocked.

\]

is a fixed completed meromorphic curvature with poles only at zeros of \(\Xi\).

The proof is standard: write \(L=\Xi'/\Xi\), use partial fractions for \(L^{(r)}\), split zeros into dyadic annuli, and use local zero counting. If

\[
\operatorname{dist}\left(1/2+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),\mathcal Z_\Xi\right)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]

then each fixed log-derivative order is polynomially bounded; applying \(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_t\) preserves polynomial bounds.

**Audit status:** near-Green if \(q''_{\can}\) is the completed meromorphic curvature.  
**Exact blocker:** confirm the definition

\[

\]

The handoff explicitly says \(q''_{\can}\) must be the full canonical object and that one-sided \(P_2\) or \(D_2\) alone is not acceptable.

For the zero-separated transfer to apply, \(q''_{\can}\) may use

\]

but it must not contain uncontrolled denominators such as

\[
\Xi(t)=\xi(1/2+it),
\quad
Z(t),
\quad
\text{or a real chart built from them.}
\]

Not acceptable:

\[
P_2\text{-only},\quad D_2\text{-only},\quad \text{one-sided AFE branch.}
\]

## Check 2 — Curvature identity

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=q''.
}
\]

This must use the same normalized derivative convention as the Gate 2 identities.

## Check 3 — First anisotropy identity

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
}
\]

If not exact, compute

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(q''-6q+2q^3).
\]

Need

\[
\|r_G\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

## Check 4 — Second anisotropy identity

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

If not exact, compute

\[
r_{G,2}:=\Gamma_{G,2}
-\left(2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right).
\]

Need

\[
\|r_{G,2}\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

## Check 5 — Completed meromorphic curvature

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Equivalently, the expression

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

must be an exact representation of the completed canonical curvature, not just a real-line truncated AFE approximation.

## Check 6 — No forbidden denominators

Inside \(q''_{\can}\), there must be no denominators:

\[
\boxed{
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Such denominators belong, if anywhere, to row-projection algebra, not to the canonical source curvature.

---

# 4. \(E_2\) policy

For Gate 2, use the inclusive policy if possible:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then no separate \(E_2\)-smallness is needed for Gate 2.

If \(E_2\) is perturbative rather than exact-canonical, Gate 2 needs only:

\[
\boxed{
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}.
}
\]

Higher \(E_2\)-derivatives remain a D4 / Wronskian-transfer issue, not a minimal Gate 2 issue.

---
