_Thought for 2m 33s_

Agent 1 / A report: canonical real-normal-form and \((u,u')\) transfer. Source prompt: 

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The analytic transfer for }u,u'\text{ is closed under the ordinary zero-separated tube hypothesis.}
}
\]

The remaining blocker is finite and definitional:

\[
\boxed{
q\text{ must be the same real completed-gauge scalar for which }u=q''_{\can}=q''.
}
\]

If the draft applies the canonical convention

\[
q=q_\zeta=\Phi_\zeta',
\qquad
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta''',
\]

then the Gate 2 canonical package closes. The existing repair notes explicitly propose this convention and warn not to confuse \(q''_{\can}\) with the affine-subtracted complement curvature \(q''_{\source,R}=(G^{\new})''\). turn71file0

---

# 1. Real completed scalar

Let

\[
\Xi(t):=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right),
\]

where

\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s).
\]

The completed function satisfies

\[
\xi(s)=\xi(1-s),
\qquad
\overline{\xi(s)}=\xi(\overline{s}).
\]

Thus, for \(t\in\mathbb R\),

\[
\overline{\Xi(t)}
=
\overline{\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)}
=
\xi\!\left(\frac12-it\right)
=
\xi\!\left(1-\left(\frac12+it\right)\right)
=
\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)
=
\Xi(t).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\Xi(t)\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

A Hardy-normalized scalar \(Z(t)\) is also acceptable, provided the paper’s \(q\), \(u\), \(\Gamma_G\), and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) are all defined in that same real gauge.

---

# 2. Ordinary zero-separated tube

Use

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

For an enlarged ordinary packet interval \(I^\ast\), define

\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le\rho\lambda\},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}.
\]

The ordinary zero-separated hypothesis is

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Since

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

this is polynomial separation:

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_0}\asymp Q^{-1-C_0}.
\]

If this condition fails, the packet is not ordinary; it must be routed to the singular/transition branch.

---

# 3. Completed-log-derivative transfer for \(u,u'\)

Assume the canonical source curvature is the full completed meromorphic object

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\!\left(\frac12+im\right),
}
\]

where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is a fixed finite expression in the completed logarithmic derivative

\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]

and finitely many derivatives \(L^{(r)}(s)\), plus regular gamma/background terms.

For fixed \(r\),

\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho \frac1{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\mathcal G_r(s),
\]

where \(\mathcal G_r\) is regular in the ordinary packet tube.

Set

\[
\delta:=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

By ordinary separation,

\[
|s-\rho|\ge\delta
\]

for all zeros \(\rho\) in the tube.

Split zeros into annuli

\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le2^{\nu+1}\delta\}.
\]

Using the standard local zero count

\[
\#A_\nu\le Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta),
\]

we get

\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Summing in \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:

\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}.
\]

Since

\[
\delta^{-1}\asymp Q^{1+C_0},
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
|L^{(r)}(s)|\le Q^{C_r}
}
\]

for every fixed \(r\).

Because \(u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) has fixed finite complexity,

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Also

\[
\mathcal D u=\lambda\partial_m u
\]

only raises the completed-log-derivative order by one and multiplies by \(\lambda\le1\). Hence

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
}
\]

So the minimal Gate 2 transfer is

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This proof must be made from the completed meromorphic object. It must not use termwise AFE \(\ell^1\)-bounds.

---

# 4. Pole-set audit

The transfer above is valid only if \(q''_{\can}\) has no uncontrolled denominators.

Allowed inside \(q''_{\can}\):

\[
\boxed{
\Xi'/\Xi,\quad L^{(r)},\quad \text{regular gamma/background terms}.
}
\]

Forbidden inside \(q''_{\can}\):

\[
\boxed{
1/q,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Such denominators may occur later in row projection or quotient algebra, but not in the canonical curvature itself.

For

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]

the polygamma poles are far from high critical-line ordinary packet tubes, and

\[
\partial_t^jB_2(t)=O_j(t^{-2-j}).
\]

So \(B_2\) is regular and harmless for this transfer.

---

# 5. \(E_2\) policy

For Gate 2, the clean policy is inclusive:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
}
\]

Then \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical object, and no separate \(E_2\)-smallness is needed for the \(u,u'\) transfer.

If the draft treats \(E_2\) as a truncation/model error instead, then Gate 2 minimally requires

\[
\boxed{
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}.
}
\]

Higher \(E_2\)-derivative estimates may still be needed for D4, but not for minimal Gate 2.

---

# 6. Real normal form

The \(L^2\)-input rigidity proof requires positivity of the kinetic term

\[
2q^2\chi_\delta(q)(q')^2.
\]

So it requires

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

This holds if \(q\) is a real chart coordinate built from a real completed scalar \(Y(t)\), such as

\[
Y(t)=\Xi(t)
\quad\text{or}\quad
Y(t)=Z(t),
\]

by a real map

\[
q=\Psi(Y,Y',\ldots,Y^{(r)}),
\qquad
\Psi:\mathbb R^{r+1}\to\mathbb R.
\]

If \(\Psi\) has denominators, the chart must satisfy

\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{\rm chart}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Then \(q\in\mathbb R\), and if

\[
u=q'',
\]

we also get \(u\in\mathbb R\). Consequently,

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3\in\mathbb R,
\]

and

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''\in\mathbb R.
\]

If \(q\) is a one-sided AFE branch, this real normal form fails. A separate complex/Hermitian rigidity theorem would then be needed.

---

# 7. Compatibility identities

The finite definition audit consists of the following identities, in the same normalized derivative convention:

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=q''.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
q''=6q-2q^3+\Gamma_G,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]

If the actual definitions produce residuals

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(q''-6q+2q^3),
\]

\[
r_{G,2}:=
\Gamma_{G,2}-
\left(2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right),
\]

then the rigidity proof requires

\[
\boxed{
\|r_G\|_{L^2(J)}+\|r_{G,2}\|_{L^2(J)}
\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
}
\]

The repair notes explicitly propose the canonical convention

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''
\]

and define the Gram anisotropy functionals with the full actual-zeta jets

\[
q_0=q_\zeta(m),\qquad
q''=q''_{\can}(m),\qquad
q^{(4)}=(q_\zeta)^{(4)}(m).
\]

Under that convention, the compatibility package is exactly what Gate 2 needs. 

---

# 8. Primitive policy

For the safe Gate 2 theorem, assume

\[
\boxed{
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
}
\]

on the rigidity interval.

For the sharper minimal theorem, recover \(q,q'\) locally.

From

\[
g=u-F(q),
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]

we have

\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]

Since

\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2),
\]

\(F(q)\in L^2\) implies

\[
q\in L^6.
\]

With

\[
q''=u\in L^\infty,
\]

one-dimensional interpolation gives

\[
q,q'\in L^\infty
\]

on a shrunken interval.

Thus global primitive transfer is not necessary for Gate 2, but it is a safe simplifying assumption.

---

# 9. Final theorem package

### Ordinary real-canonical Gate 2 package

Assume:

1. \(Y(t)=\Xi(t)\) or \(Z(t)\) is real on the critical line;

2. \(q\) is a real chart coordinate with denominator lower bound if needed;

3. the ordinary tube is zero-separated:

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
   \mathcal Z_\Xi
   \right)
   \ge
   \lambda Q^{-C_0};
   \]

4. the canonical curvature is the full completed meromorphic object:

   \[
   u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi];
   \]

5. the compatibility identities hold:

   \[
   u=q'',
   \]

   \[
   \Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
   \]

   \[
   \Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
   \]

Then

\[
\boxed{
q,u,g,h\in\mathbb R,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D u\|_\infty\le Q^C.
}
\]

This is the canonical analytic package needed for the \(L^2\)-input Gate 2 theorem.

---

## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:36:57)

_Thought for 12s_

```latex
\begin{definition}[Actual-zeta real phase and canonical Gate--2 anisotropy]
Fix an ordinary smooth packet and let \(\mathcal D\) denote the normalized packet derivative. Let
\[
\Phi_\zeta
\]
be the real completed critical-line phase/scalar used in the local phase kernel. Define
\[
q_\zeta:=\mathcal D\Phi_\zeta
\]
or, in ordinary prime notation,
\[
q_\zeta:=\Phi_\zeta'.
\]
Define the canonical source curvature by
\[
q''_{\can}:=\mathcal D^2 q_\zeta=\mathcal D^3\Phi_\zeta.
\]
On ordinary smooth zero-separated packets,
\[
q_\zeta,\qquad q''_{\can},\qquad \Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]
are real-valued. If a critical-line zero lies in the unregularized packet interval, the packet is routed to the singular/transition branch, or else the corresponding regularized phase convention is used.

Define the canonical Gate--2 anisotropy quantities by
\[
\Gamma_G
:=
q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
:=
(1-q_\zeta^2)q''_{\can}
-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Equivalent differentiated form of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)]
With the definitions above,
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
From
\[
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3
\]
and
\[
q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q_\zeta,
\]
we compute
\[
\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G
=
\mathcal D^2q''_{\can}
-6\mathcal D^2q_\zeta
+\mathcal D^2(2q_\zeta^3).
\]
Since
\[
\mathcal D^2q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^4q_\zeta,
\qquad
\mathcal D^2q_\zeta=q''_{\can},
\]
and
\[
\mathcal D^2(2q_\zeta^3)
=
12q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
+
6q_\zeta^2q''_{\can},
\]
we get
\[
\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G
=
\mathcal D^4q_\zeta
-6q''_{\can}
+
12q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
+
6q_\zeta^2q''_{\can}.
\]
Therefore
\[
2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G
=
2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta
+q''_{\can}
-2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
-q_\zeta^2q''_{\can}.
\]
The \(2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2\) terms cancel, leaving
\[
2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2
-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G
=
(1-q_\zeta^2)q''_{\can}
-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta
=
\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]
\end{proof}
```

## Edit 1 — Add ordinary zero-separated transfer theorem

**Where:** In Section `Downstream local closure package: Gate 2, wall escape, and carrier rows`, immediately after:

```latex
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{\(L^2\)}{L2}-input real rigidity}
```

and before:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[\(L^2\)-input real rigidity; safe primitive-bounded form]
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Ordinary zero-separated source packet]
\label{def:ordinary-zero-separated-source-packet}
Let \(I^\ast\) be an enlarged ordinary packet interval and let
\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,\qquad \lambda Q\asymp 1.
\]
For \(\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}\), write
\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\}.
\]
We say that \(I^\ast\) is ordinary zero-separated if
\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]
If this condition fails, the packet is not treated by the ordinary Gate--2 local
argument; it is routed to the singular/transition branch, or else a regularized
phase convention must be used.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Ordinary zero-separated source-complexity transfer]
\label{lem:ordinary-zero-separated-source-complexity-transfer}
Assume \(I^\ast\) is ordinary zero-separated in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:ordinary-zero-separated-source-packet}.  Assume also that
the canonical source curvature is the full completed meromorphic curvature
\[
u=q''_{\can}=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\left(\frac12+im\right),
\]
where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is a fixed finite expression in the completed logarithmic
derivative
\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]
and finitely many derivatives \(L^{(r)}(s)\), together with regular
gamma/background terms and no denominators other than those implicit in
\(L=\Xi'/\Xi\).  Then
\[
\boxed{
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
+
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}
\le Q^C.
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For fixed \(r\), the completed logarithmic derivative has the standard local
partial-fraction form
\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_\rho\frac1{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\mathcal G_r(s),
\]
where \(\mathcal G_r\) denotes the regular gamma/background contribution.
Set
\[
\delta=\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]
On the ordinary tube, \(|s-\rho|\ge\delta\).  Splitting the zeros into dyadic
annuli
\[
A_\nu=\{\rho:2^\nu\delta\le |s-\rho|\le2^{\nu+1}\delta\},
\]
and using the local zero-count estimate
\[
\#A_\nu\le Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta),
\]
gives
\[
\sum_{\rho\in A_\nu}|s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C(1+2^\nu\delta)(2^\nu\delta)^{-(r+1)}.
\]
Summing over \(\nu\), the first annuli dominate:
\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le
Q^C\delta^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^{C_r}.
\]
Thus every fixed \(L^{(r)}(s)\) entering \(\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) is polynomially
bounded on the tube.  Since \(u=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) has fixed finite
complexity,
\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
\]
Applying \(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\) only raises the required
completed-log-derivative order by one and multiplies by \(\lambda\le1\), so
\[
\|\mathcal D u\|_{L^\infty(I^\ast)}\le Q^C.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Canonical and denominator guardrails]
\label{rem:canonical-denominator-guardrails-gate-two}
For Gate~2 the inclusive canonical convention is
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2=\mathfrak C_2[\Xi].
\]
Thus \(E_2\) is part of the exact canonical object and no separate
\(E_2\)-smallness is needed for the minimal \(u,u'\) transfer.  If instead
\(E_2\) is used as a perturbative truncation error, the minimal Gate--2
transfer requires
\[
\|E_2\|_\infty+\|\mathcal D E_2\|_\infty\le Q^{-A_E}.
\]
The canonical curvature \(q''_{\can}\) may contain \(\Xi'/\Xi\), its fixed
derivatives, and regular gamma/background terms.  It must not contain
denominators such as
\[
1/q,\qquad 1/u,\qquad 1/\Gamma_G,\qquad
1/\Gamma_{G,2},\qquad 1/|\Gamma|.
\]
Those denominators, if present, belong to later row-projection algebra, not to
the canonical source curvature used in Gate~2.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The current draft uses the \(u'\)-bound in the Gate 2 theorem, but does not yet include the clean theorem showing where it comes from. This insertion closes the ordinary analytic-complexity transfer under the ordinary zero-separated tube hypothesis.

---

## Edit 2 — Add a finite real/canonical compatibility lemma

**Where:** Immediately after Lemma `\ref{lem:ordinary-zero-separated-source-complexity-transfer}` from Edit 1, before the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Real-canonical Gate--2 compatibility]
\label{lem:real-canonical-gate-two-compatibility}
Assume the actual-zeta local variables are in the real completed gauge of
Definition~\ref{def:canonical-actual-zeta-phase-curvature}.  Thus
\[
q=q_\zeta,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q_\zeta,
\]
and the canonical anisotropies are
\[
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=(1-q_\zeta^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta.
\]
Then, on ordinary smooth zero-separated packets,
\[
q,\quad u,\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]
are real-valued and, with \(g=\Gamma_G\), \(h=\Gamma_{G,2}\),
\[
u=q'',
\]
\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]
and
\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The real-valuedness follows from the real completed critical-line gauge.  The
first two identities are the definitions.  For the final identity, apply
Lemma~\ref{lem:differentiated-form-second-gate-two-anisotropy} after suppressing
the \(\zeta\)-subscript:
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(\mathcal Dq)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]
In ordinary local prime notation this is
\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Residual version of the compatibility package]
\label{rem:gate-two-compatibility-residuals}
If a later convention uses approximate instead of exact definitions, define
\[
r_u:=q''_{\can}-q'',
\]
\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(q''-6q+2q^3),
\]
and
\[
r_{G,2}:=
\Gamma_{G,2}
-\left(2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right).
\]
The \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma remains applicable provided these residuals are
\(L^2\)-small on the source interval at the same scale as \(g,h\).  In the main
canonical convention used here these residuals are zero.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** Your draft already contains the definitions and the differentiated identity near the front. This lemma packages them exactly where the downstream proof uses them, preventing future confusion between \(q''_{\can}\), \(q''_{\source,R}\), and one-sided AFE/proxy quantities.

## Edit 4 — Add optional primitive-recovery strengthening

**Where:** Replace the current remark:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Primitive-free strengthening not used]
...
\end{remark}
```

with the following stronger but still disciplined version:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Primitive recovery from \(L^2\)-small \(g\)]
\label{rem:primitive-recovery-from-l2-small-g}
The main proof uses the safe local bound
\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]
inside Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe}.  This assumption can often
be recovered locally from the source bound and \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\).
Indeed, since
\[
g=u-F(q),\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]
one has
\[
F(q)=u-g.
\]
The algebraic inequality
\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2)
\]
implies that \(F(q)\in L^2(J)\) gives \(q\in L^6(J)\).  If \(q''=u\in
L^\infty(J)\), then the one-dimensional interpolation estimate gives, on a
shrunken interval \(J_1\Subset J\),
\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C,
\]
and then the Landau estimate gives, on \(J_2\Subset J_1\),
\[
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\right)
\le Q^C,
\]
for polynomial shrinkage scale \(\ell\).  Thus the safe primitive bounds are not
a separate actual-zeta arithmetic input; they are either assumed for clarity or
recovered locally from the canonical identities and \(L^2\)-smallness of \(g\).
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This captures a real improvement from the conversation while keeping the safe proof as the mainline.

---

## Edit 5 — Add a row mobility lemma

**Where:** In Section `Gauge-locked wall escape and row energy`, immediately after Theorem `\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}` and before the proof, or immediately after its proof before Remark `\ref{rem:d3-replaced-by-wall-escape-plus-d4}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Row mobility from a point sample to row energy]
\label{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}
Let \(\mathbf A_N:I\to \mathcal H_N\) be the downstream row vector, in the
row norm used for the final row-energy statement.  Assume
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]
for some \(m_\ast\in I\), and
\[
\|\mathbf A_N'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]
Then there exists a one-sided or two-sided subinterval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with
\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]
such that
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\qquad (m\in J_\ast).
\]
Consequently
\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Take
\[
r=cQ^{-C_A-C_D}|I|
\]
with \(c>0\) sufficiently small and choose the available one-sided or two-sided
interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) of length comparable to \(r\) containing
\(m_\ast\).  For \(m\in J_\ast\),
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)-\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}|m-m_\ast|
\le
\frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]
Thus \(|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge\frac12Q^{-C_A}\) on \(J_\ast\), and integration gives
the stated row-energy lower bound.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** The wall-escape theorem currently invokes row mobility as an assumption. This makes it an explicit local lemma.

## Edit 6 — Add scalar-coordinate D4 fallback audit

**Where:** After Remark `\ref{rem:scalar-i-incidence-collapse-artifact}` or after Remark `\ref{rem:carrier-quotient-row-energy-admissible}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Scalar-coordinate fallback audit for the order-nine row]
\label{rem:scalar-coordinate-fallback-audit-order-nine}
The carrier-quotient formulation bypasses the scalar \(I\)-coordinate
cross-channel wall.  If, however, a downstream argument insists on collapsed
scalar \(I\)-coordinate energy, then the remaining finite D4 blocker is exactly
the order-nine correction incidence
\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}.
\]
Equivalently, one must control
\[
F_9^I:=
R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]
The scalar-coordinate D4 branch closes only if one proves one of the following:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \(R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}=0\);
\item \(R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}\) is \(H\)-divisible or belongs to the declared
nuisance/quotient submodule;
\item \(F_9^I\not\equiv0\) together with a quantitative avoidance estimate for
the incidence wall
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
F_9^I=0,\quad yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\right\};
\]
\item an order-eleven or ambient-row enlargement supplies an independent
\(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-observable row.
\end{enumerate}
Thus the scalar \(I\)-coordinate formulation is a fallback branch, not the
active carrier-quotient D4 route.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The draft has most of this information spread across definition, theorem, and remark. This insertion makes the fallback audit explicit and prevents confusion between the active carrier quotient theorem and the scalar \(I\)-coordinate obstruction.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Terminal conditional dependency ledger]
\label{rem:terminal-conditional-dependency-ledger}
The present draft should be read as a conditional architecture, not as a closed

three actual-zeta inputs:

\boxed{
\mathrm{O1}:\ \text{Fixed-width cell nonrecurrence}

}

\text{Gate 1}

L^2\text{-input real rigidity}
\Longrightarrow

\]
and

\text{Gate 2}
+

+

Thus the active downstream open work is finite and local: the \(L^2\)-input

D4 residual control, and row-mobility/row-energy admissibility.  These
downstream repairs do not discharge the upstream actual-zeta inputs
\(\mathrm{O1}\)--\(\mathrm{O3}\), \(\mathrm{S1}\), or the transition theorem.
\end{remark}
```

# One definition issue to keep

The definitions near the front are basically correct. I would **not** rewrite them substantially. The current block already defines

\[
q_\zeta=\mathcal D\Phi_\zeta,\qquad
q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q_\zeta,
\]

and then defines

\[
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_\zeta^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta,
\]

with the derived identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]

That is exactly the repair we wanted. I would only add the compatibility lemma in Edit 2 to bind these definitions to the downstream variables \(u,g,h\).

## Edit 3 — Add the real completed scalar proof near the canonical definition

**Where:** Immediately after Definition `\ref{def:canonical-actual-zeta-phase-curvature}` and before Definition `\ref{def:canonical-gate-two-anisotropy-functionals}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Reality of the completed critical-line scalar]
\label{lem:completed-critical-line-scalar-real}
Let
\[
\xi(s)=\frac12s(s-1)\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)\zeta(s).
\]
Then
\[
\Xi(t):=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)
\]
is real for all real \(t\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The completed function satisfies
\[
\xi(s)=\xi(1-s),
\qquad
\overline{\xi(s)}=\xi(\overline{s}).
\]
Thus, for \(s=\frac12+it\),
\[
\overline{\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)}
=
\xi\!\left(\frac12-it\right)
=
\xi\!\left(1-\left(\frac12+it\right)\right)
=
\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]
Hence \(\Xi(t)\in\mathbb R\).
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** You repeatedly rely on realness of the critical-line scalar. The proof is short and should be in the paper.

## Edit 5 — Add a primitive-recovery lemma, not just a remark

Right now primitive recovery appears only as a remark. Since it is now part of the minimal Gate 2 package, I would promote it to a lemma.

**Where:** After Remark `\ref{rem:gate-two-compatibility-residuals}` and before Lemma `\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Local primitive recovery from \(L^2\)-small \(g\)]
\label{lem:local-primitive-recovery-from-l2-small-g}
Let \(J_1\Subset J\) be intervals with polynomial separation from the boundary.
Assume
\[
u=q'',\qquad g=u-F(q),\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\]
and
\[
\|u\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le Q^C,
\qquad
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}\le \varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]
Then on \(J_1\),
\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
\]
Moreover, on any further polynomially shrunken interval \(J_2\Subset J_1\),
\[
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}\le Q^C.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since \(F(q)=u-g\),
\[
\|F(q)\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\|u\|_{L^2(J)}+\|g\|_{L^2(J)}
\le Q^C|J|^{1/2}.
\]
The cubic polynomial \(F(q)=6q-2q^3\) satisfies
\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2).
\]
Hence
\[
\|q\|_{L^6(J)}\le Q^C|J|^{1/6}.
\]
Since \(q''=u\in L^\infty(J)\), the one-dimensional interpolation estimate gives
\[
\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}\le Q^C.
\]
Finally, the Landau estimate gives
\[
\|q'\|_{L^\infty(J_2)}
\le
C\left(
\ell^{-1}\|q\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
+
\ell\|q''\|_{L^\infty(J_1)}
\right)
\le Q^C,
\]
where \(\ell=\operatorname{dist}(J_2,\partial J_1)\) and the shrinkage is
polynomial.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** This is now a real theorem, not just commentary. It allows the Gate 2 proof to avoid global primitive-transfer assumptions.

---

```latex
source interval.
```

## Edit 7 — Add a source-thickening + average anisotropy lemma

The current theorem combines these steps internally. I would add a standalone lemma because it is the exact replacement for old D1/D2 extraction.

**Where:** After Lemma `\ref{lem:source-thickening-one-large-point}` and before Theorem `\ref{thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Source-large interval with \(L^2\)-small anisotropy]
\label{lem:source-large-interval-l2-anisotropy}
Assume Gate~1:
\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]
source Lipschitz control
\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]
and Gate--2 failure at exponent \(A\):
\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]
Then there exists an interval \(J\subset I\) such that
\[
|u|\ge \tau:=\frac12Q^{-B/2}
\qquad\text{on }J,
\]
\[
|J|\ge Q^{-B/2-C_u-O(1)}|I|,
\]
and
\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:source-thickening-one-large-point}, there is an interval
\(J\subset I\) with the stated lower bound for \(|u|\) and for \(|J|\).
Since \(|u|^2\ge \tau^2\) on \(J\),
\[
\tau^2\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]
Using \(\tau^{-2}\asymp Q^B\) and
\[
|J|^{-1}\le Q^{B/2+C_u+O(1)}|I|^{-1}
\]
gives the claim.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** This isolates the new preferred Gate 2 extraction route and avoids future backsliding into Remez/Cartan.

---

## Edit 8 — Simplify the Gate 2 theorem proof by invoking the new lemma

**Where:** In Theorem `\ref{thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity}`, replace the proof from:

```latex
Assume, toward contradiction, that
...
Put
\[
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
\]
```

with:

```latex
Assume, toward contradiction, that
\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:source-large-interval-l2-anisotropy}, there is an interval
\(J\subset I\) such that
\[
|u|\ge \tau:=\frac12Q^{-B/2}\quad\text{on }J,
\]
and
\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
\]
Put
\[
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
\]
```

Then leave the rest of the proof unchanged.

**Why:** The theorem becomes cleaner and explicitly depends on the standalone extraction lemma.

## Edit 9 — Add row mobility lemma

I still do not see a standalone row mobility lemma in the draft.

**Where:** After Theorem `\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}` and its proof, before the remark `D3 is replaced by wall escape plus D4`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Row mobility from point sample to row energy]
\label{lem:row-mobility-point-sample-to-energy}
Let \(\mathbf A_N:I\to\mathcal H_N\) be the downstream row vector in the row norm
used for the final row-energy statement.  Assume
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]
for some \(m_\ast\in I\), and
\[
\|\mathbf A_N'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Choose a one-sided or two-sided interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) containing
\(m_\ast\) with
\[
|J_\ast|\asymp Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|.
\]
For \(m\in J_\ast\),
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)-\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\le
Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}|m-m_\ast|
\le
\frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]
Thus
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\]
on \(J_\ast\), and integration gives the result.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** Wall escape produces a sample. The row-energy architecture needs exactly this thickening step.

```latex
We develop a conditional local obstruction framework for the Riemann Hypothesis
```

## Edit 5 — Add a full ordinary Gate--1 named-input package

**Where:** Immediately after `Remark~\ref{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}` and before:

```latex
\section{No-go and audit ledger}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\section{Named actual-zeta inputs for ordinary Gate 1}
\label{sec:named-actual-zeta-inputs-ordinary-gate-one}

This section records the ordinary Gate--1 inputs that remain open after the
local Wronskian and packet-frequency reductions.  These are actual-zeta
arithmetic inputs, not local algebraic identities.

\begin{definition}[Ordinary Wronskian rows at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero]
\label{def:ordinary-wronskian-rows}
Let
\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]
where
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]
is the full canonical actual-zeta source curvature.  Let
\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\]
be the basis-normalized Wronskian formed from the rows \(G_0,\ldots,G_{R+1}\).
At a zero \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\), expansion along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row gives
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
}
\]
Here
\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]
and \(\mathbf M\) is the cofactor/Hodge-dual vector of the
\(q''_{\can}\)-jet block.
\end{definition}

\begin{hypothesis}[O1: Fixed-width cell nonrecurrence]
\label{hyp:O1-fixed-width-cell-nonrecurrence}
For every admissible ordinary zero \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),
\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
Equivalently, in the fixed-width packet-frequency cell formulation, the full
canonical cell vector satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\sum_r |B_r(m_0,\alpha)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
Here
\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E
\]
is the cell sum over a fixed normalized packet-frequency support
\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]
partitioned into cells of width \(\asymp R^{-1}\) in
\(x=\lambda\log n\).
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Internal structure of O1]
\label{rem:internal-structure-O1}
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:O1-fixed-width-cell-nonrecurrence} packages two
unproved actual-orbit statements.  First, same-branch cell mass:
\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-),
\]
where \(D^\pm\) are branch diagonal masses and \(O^\pm\) are same-cell
off-diagonal sums.  Second, folded main/dual nonalignment:
\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2).
}
\]
Diagonal mass alone does not prove the same-branch statement; phase-relaxed
models can choose independent phases so that every cell sum vanishes.  Thus O1
is an actual one-parameter prime-log nonrecurrence theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{hypothesis}[O2: Cofactor-vector nonrecurrence]
\label{hyp:O2-cofactor-vector-nonrecurrence}
For every admissible ordinary zero \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),
\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Averaged \(Z_\alpha\)-zero large sieve does not imply O2]
\label{rem:zero-large-sieve-does-not-imply-pointwise-O2}
A natural averaged route toward Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:O2-cofactor-vector-nonrecurrence}
is the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large sieve after subset-product resonance
quotienting.  Let
\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]
After clustering subset-product frequencies
\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,\qquad |S|=R+1,
\]
at scale \(|J|^{-1}\), the quotient kernel theorem would assert
\[
\boxed{
\left(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\right)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]
The argument-principle identity
\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds
\]
is only a representation; it does not prove the required medium-frequency
zero-correlation/operator lower bound.  Moreover, an averaged lower bound for
\(|\mathbf M|\) over \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros does not by itself imply the pointwise
statement in Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:O2-cofactor-vector-nonrecurrence}; isolated
bad zeros can survive.
\end{remark}

\begin{hypothesis}[O3: Wronskian angle nonalignment]
\label{hyp:O3-wronskian-angle-nonalignment}
At every admissible ordinary zero \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),
\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Why O3 is independent of O1 and O2]
\label{rem:O3-independent-of-norm-inputs}
The norm bounds
\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},\qquad |\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}
\]
do not imply Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:O3-wronskian-angle-nonalignment}.  Exterior
algebra identifies
\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\]
as the oriented volume of the \(Z_\alpha\)-row with the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet
block, but it supplies no lower bound for the angle.  Symbolic rank of
\(Z_\alpha\) against the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows is necessary but not
sufficient; accidental pointwise actual-orbit alignment can still make the
inner product small.  No sign, positivity, Hodge-dual, or Hermitian mechanism
currently proves O3.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[O1--O3 imply ordinary Gate~1]
\label{thm:O1-O2-O3-imply-ordinary-gate-one}
Assume ordinary scale
\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,\qquad R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]
Assume O1, O2, and O3.  Assume also the canonical analytic-complexity and
basis-conditioning estimates required to transfer the Wronskian lower bound
to finite-jet anti-design:
\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]
is used in every \(q''_{\can}\)-jet row, and the basis-normalization losses are
at most
\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]
Then ordinary Gate~1 holds:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At a zero \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),
Definition~\ref{def:ordinary-wronskian-rows} gives
\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]
By O1 and O2,
\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]
By O3,
\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A_3}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]
Therefore
\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_W}
\]
for some \(A_W\).

The standard Wronskian-to-finite-jet implication then gives ordinary
finite-jet anti-design for the normalized source curvature
\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x).
\]
Indeed, if all source-curvature jets up to order \(R\) were smaller than the
corresponding polynomial threshold, the basis-normalized Wronskian would be
smaller than \(Q^{-A_W}\), contradicting the displayed lower bound.  Finally,
finite-jet anti-design plus polynomial analytic complexity gives the interval
energy lower bound by the usual contrapositive: failure of Gate~1 would force
finite-jet flattening on the shrunken packet.  Hence
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** This records the entire ordinary Gate 1 stack instead of leaving O1/O2/O3 as terse items in the terminal ledger. It also captures the key no-go findings: phase-relaxed models break the cell theorem, averaged large sieve does not imply pointwise O2, and symbol rank does not imply angle nonalignment.

---

## Edit 6 — Add singular and transition named-input details

**Where:** Immediately after Theorem `\ref{thm:O1-O2-O3-imply-ordinary-gate-one}` from Edit 5.

**Insert:**

```latex
\section{Named singular and transition inputs}
\label{sec:named-singular-transition-inputs}

\begin{hypothesis}[S1: Singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion]
\label{hyp:S1-singular-explicit-formula-antidesign}
In the deep singular regime
\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]
let \(c=\lambda\), \(m=\gamma+cx\), and let
\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]
For \(3\le k\le R+3\), let \(h_{k,c}\) be the normalized singular test
functions extracting the singular sine moments.  Let
\[
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c),\qquad
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c),\qquad
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\]
denote respectively the prime, gamma/background, and regularized tail/trivial
vectors supplied by the explicit formula.  The singular anti-design exclusion
is
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Role of S1]
\label{rem:role-of-S1}
Deep singular packets are harmless by dominance unless the normalized singular
zero-side packet realizes finite sine-moment cancellation
\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]
The explicit formula translates this cancellation into
\[
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R\approx0.
\]
Thus S1 is exactly the actual-zeta input excluding deep singular anti-design.
Local singular geometry alone cannot prove it; deterministic quadrature can
fake the sine-moment cancellation.
\end{remark}

\begin{hypothesis}[T1: Mild singular transition control]
\label{hyp:T1-mild-singular-transition-control}
The transition region
\[
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \lambda Q\lesssim 1
\]
is covered by a separate transition-control theorem transferring either the
ordinary Wronskian/finite-jet anti-design mechanism or the singular
explicit-formula anti-design mechanism with only polynomial loss.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[Transition status]
\label{rem:transition-status}
The present draft does not discharge Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:T1-mild-singular-transition-control}.
It is listed separately because neither the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian
block nor the deep singular dominance argument automatically covers the entire
transition band.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The terminal ledger names S1 and transition control, but the paper should define them precisely.

## Edit 7 — Add no-go items to the No-go ledger

**Where:** In `\section{No-go and audit ledger}`, inside the existing `enumerate`, after the item:

```latex
\item \emph{Generic determinant nonvanishing is insufficient.}
...
```

**Insert these new items:**

```latex
\item \emph{Phase-relaxed cell models break O1.}
If the phases \(e^{-im\log n}\) are replaced by independent unit complex
numbers inside each fixed-width cell, one can arrange cellwise polygon closure:
\[
B_r^+=0,\qquad B_r^-=0
\qquad\forall r.
\]
Thus fixed-width cell nonrecurrence cannot follow from coefficient magnitudes,
cell geometry, or the scalar equation \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) alone.  It must use
the actual one-parameter prime-log orbit.

\item \emph{Averaged zero-set large sieve does not imply pointwise O2.}
An averaged estimate of the form
\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\]
does not imply
\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]
at a specified zero \(m_0\).  Isolated bad zeros can survive.  The pointwise
cofactor-vector nonrecurrence theorem is therefore a separate named input.

\item \emph{Symbol rank does not imply Wronskian angle nonalignment.}
The fact that the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol is not generated by the
\(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols does not force
\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|
\]
at the actual zero \(m_0\).  The latter is a pointwise actual-orbit incidence
theorem.

\item \emph{Low-prime plateau blocks are not determinant-admissible.}
Low-prime plateau blocks may show that \(Z_\alpha\) is not symbolically
redundant, but for the packet-scale Wronskian their normalized node spread is
\[
\lambda\log Q\asymp\frac{\log Q}{Q},
\]
which is too small.  The determinant-admissible ordinary blocks must instead
use packet-frequency support \(\lambda\log n\asymp1\).
```

**Why:** These are durable no-go findings from the conversation and should be preserved in the paper’s audit ledger.

## Edit 2 — Add a formal “cell mass implies \(\mathbf z'\)” lemma

Right now O1 is a cell-mass statement, and `Remark~\ref{rem:cell-mass-gives-z-derivative-row}` says this gives \(\mathbf z'\), but the later theorem uses it as a formal implication. I would promote this bridge into a lemma.

**Where:** Immediately after `Remark~\ref{rem:cell-mass-gives-z-derivative-row}` and before `\begin{definition}[O2: Cofactor-vector nonrecurrence]`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Fixed-width cell mass implies the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative row]
\label{lem:fixed-width-cell-mass-implies-z-derivative-row}
Assume the fixed-width cell setup of
Definition~\ref{def:O1-fixed-width-cell-nonrecurrence}.  Let
\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),
\qquad F(0)=0,
\qquad \lambda Q\asymp1.
\]
Assume the cell Gram/frame lower bound on the window \([-R,R]\),
\[
\lambda_{\min}(G_{\rm cell})\ge Q^{-C_G},
\]
and assume the full canonical cell error satisfies
\[
\|E_{\rm cell}\|_{L^2[-R,R]}^2
\le
\frac12 R Q^{-A-C_G}.
\]
If
\[
\sum_r |B_r(m_0,\alpha)|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]
then
\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]
If, moreover, \(Z_\alpha\) has polynomial analytic upper control on
\[
|t|\le R(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-A''}.
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Let \(\xi_r\) be the cell centers and write
\[
F_{\rm cell}(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}.
\]
The cell Gram lower bound gives
\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|F_{\rm cell}(t)|^2\,dt
\ge
R Q^{-C_G}\sum_r|B_r|^2
\ge
R Q^{-A-C_G}.
\]
After subtracting \(E_{\rm cell}\), this yields
\[
\int_{-R}^{R}|F(t)|^2\,dt
\ge
\frac12 RQ^{-A-C_G},
\]
and hence
\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]
The amplitude-to-derivative lemma applies because \(R\le(\log Q)^C\) and the
outer analytic control is available on a polylogarithmically larger disk.  The
basis-normalized operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) cost at most
\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]
so the monomial derivative lower bound gives
\[
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]
\end{proof}
```

**Then edit Theorem `\ref{thm:ordinary-gate-one-from-O1-O2-O3}` proof.**

Replace:

```latex
By O1 and Remark~\ref{rem:cell-mass-gives-z-derivative-row},
\[
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-A_1}.
\]
```

with:

```latex
By O1 and Lemma~\ref{lem:fixed-width-cell-mass-implies-z-derivative-row},
\[
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-A_1}.
\]
```

**Why:** This turns a key implication into a formal lemma. It also captures the multiblock/cell-sum “goodie” cleanly.

## Edit 3 — Add explicit same-branch and main/dual decomposition under O1

O1 currently defines the full cell vector. It would be useful to preserve the structural finding that O1 decomposes into same-branch mass plus folded main/dual nonalignment, and that same-branch mass is itself a true actual-orbit nonrecurrence input.

**Where:** After Lemma `\ref{lem:fixed-width-cell-mass-implies-z-derivative-row}` from Edit 2.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Internal decomposition of O1]
\label{rem:internal-decomposition-O1}
The full fixed-width cell nonrecurrence input may be decomposed into two
sub-inputs.

First, same-branch cell mass:
\[
\boxed{
|B^+(m_0)|_2^2+|B^-(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^++D^-),
\]
where \(D^\pm\) denote the branch diagonal masses and \(O^\pm\) the same-cell
off-diagonal sums.

Second, folded main/dual cell-vector nonalignment:
\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}\bigl(|B^+|_2+|B^-|_2\bigr).
}
\]
The first statement is not a consequence of diagonal mass alone: in a
phase-relaxed model, independent phases can make every same-branch cell sum
vanish.  The second statement is not a consequence of the scalar equation
\(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\), which only imposes total cancellation of the full cell
vector.  Thus both sub-inputs are actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic
statements.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This captures a durable structural decomposition and a no-go result from the conversation.

## Edit 4 — Add the amplitude-to-derivative lemma explicitly if not already present

I did not see a standalone lemma in the draft for the analytic step:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

If you do not already have such a lemma elsewhere, add it.

**Where:** Immediately before Lemma `\ref{lem:fixed-width-cell-mass-implies-z-derivative-row}` from Edit 2.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Polylog-local amplitude implies derivative-row nonflatness]
\label{lem:polylog-amplitude-implies-z-derivative-row}
Let
\[
F(t)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t),\qquad F(0)=0,
\]
and assume \(F\) is holomorphic on \(|t|\le A\).  Let
\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad L=R+1.
\]
Assume
\[
\sup_{|t|\le a}|F(t)|\ge Q^{-A_0},
\]
\[
\sup_{|t|\le A}|F(t)|\le Q^{A_1},
\]
with
\[
1\le a\le(\log Q)^{C_a},
\qquad
A/a\ge(\log Q)^{C_*},
\]
where \(C_*\) is sufficiently large relative to \(A_0,A_1,C_a\).  Then
\[
\boxed{
\max_{1\le k\le R+1}\frac{|F^{(k)}(0)|}{k!}\ge Q^{-A_2}.
}
\]
Consequently, after applying the basis-normalized operators
\(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\),
\[
\boxed{
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-A_3}.
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
F(t)=\sum_{k=1}^{L}a_kt^k+T_L(t),
\qquad
a_k=\frac{F^{(k)}(0)}{k!}.
\]
Cauchy estimates give, for \(|t|\le a\),
\[
|T_L(t)|\le C Q^{A_1}\left(\frac aA\right)^{L+1}.
\]
The radius condition makes the right-hand side at most
\[
\frac14Q^{-A_0}.
\]
Thus the degree-\(L\) Taylor polynomial has supremum at least
\[
\frac34Q^{-A_0}
\]
on \(|t|\le a\).  If every coefficient satisfied
\[
|a_k|<\frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4La^k},
\qquad 1\le k\le L,
\]
the polynomial would have supremum \(<Q^{-A_0}/4\), a contradiction.  Hence
for some \(k\le L\),
\[
|a_k|\ge \frac{Q^{-A_0}}{4La^L}.
\]
Since \(a\le(\log Q)^{C_a}\) and
\[
L\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]
we have
\[
a^L\le Q^{O(1)}.
\]
Therefore \(|a_k|\ge Q^{-A_2}\).  Passing to the basis-normalized operator
system costs at most
\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)},
\]
so \(\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A_3}\).
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** This is a central analytic reduction and should exist as a theorem, not only buried in conversation notes.

## Edit 6 — Add a no-go remark: low-prime plateau blocks are not determinant-admissible

I saw no explicit no-go in the final draft for the low-prime plateau block issue. This is worth preserving.

**Where:** In `\subsection{No-go archive for the ordinary Wronskian route}`, after `Remark~\ref{rem:local-packet-geometry-phase-relaxed-no-go}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Low-prime plateau blocks are not determinant-admissible]
\label{rem:low-prime-plateau-not-determinant-admissible}
Low-prime plateau blocks
\[
Q^a\le p\le Q^b
\]
are useful for diagnosing symbolic nonredundancy of \(Z_\alpha\), but they are
not admissible as the main packet-scale Wronskian determinant blocks.  In the
ordinary regime \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), their normalized nodes satisfy
\[
x_p=\lambda\log p\asymp \frac{\log Q}{Q}\ll1,
\]
and their node spread is
\[
\lambda(\log Q^b-\log Q^a)
\asymp\frac{\log Q}{Q}.
\]
This is far smaller than the \(R^{-C}\)-scale needed for a polynomially
conditioned rank-\(R\) packet-frequency determinant.  The determinant-admissible
ordinary blocks must instead satisfy
\[
\boxed{
\lambda\log n\asymp1,
}
\]
for example
\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,\qquad 0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This was a real negative result and prevents a common mistaken shortcut.

## Edit 7 — Add a no-go remark: spectral large sieve after quotienting is still open

You already have `Remark~\ref{rem:averaged-large-sieve-does-not-replace-O2}`, but it does not mention resonance quotienting and the medium-frequency kernel obstruction explicitly enough.

**Where:** After `Remark~\ref{rem:averaged-large-sieve-does-not-replace-O2}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Resonance quotienting does not prove the zero spectral large sieve]
\label{rem:resonance-quotienting-does-not-prove-zero-large-sieve}
For the cofactor-vector route, subset-product frequencies
\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S
\]
must first be clustered at scale
\[
\eta_0\asymp |J|^{-1},
\]
because if
\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\lesssim |J|^{-1},
\]
then zero-set sampling over \(J\) cannot distinguish the two modes and
\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\approx K_J(0)
\]
may occur.  After quotienting these near-resonance clusters, the remaining
kernel theorem is still open:
\[
\boxed{
\left(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\right)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]
The argument-principle identity
\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds
\]
is only a representation.  It does not prove the medium-frequency
zero-correlation/operator lower bound needed for O2.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This preserves the precise O2 blocker.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Common-small-value reformulation does not close O3]
\label{rem:common-small-value-does-not-close-O3}
O3 can be restated as a common-small-value exclusion:
\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

\[

one may impose both
\[
Z_\alpha=0
\]
and
\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=0
\]
because the active phase torus has many degrees of freedom.  Resultant-style
or Wronskian-of-Wronskians arguments also do not currently give a polynomial
separation estimate for the actual one-parameter zeta orbit.  Thus O3 remains
a named actual-orbit incidence input.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This captures the final stop condition for the angle/incidence attack.

## Edit 1 — Clarify that O1 cells partition the union of main and folded-dual supports

**Problem:** In the O1 definition, \(B_r^+\) uses \(x_n^+=\lambda\log n\), while \(B_r^-\) uses folded dual nodes \(x_n^-=\lambda\log(m_0/(2\pi n))\). For \(0<c_-<c_+<1/2\), these typically live on **different normalized intervals**. The definition should say the cells partition the union of both supports, not only the plus support.

**Where:** In `Definition~\ref{def:O1-fixed-width-cell-nonrecurrence}`, after:

```latex
and partition the normalized support into cells \(I_r\) of width
\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]
```

**Insert:**

```latex
Here the ``normalized support'' means the union of the plus and folded-dual
normalized supports:
\[
\{x_n^+=\lambda\log n:n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}\}
\cup
\left\{
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n}:n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
\right\},
\]
up to the precise completed-phase convention for the folded dual branch.  Thus
a cell may contain only plus modes, only folded-dual modes, or both.  The
vectors \(B^+\) and \(B^-\) are understood as elements of the same cell Hilbert
space, with zero entries in cells where the corresponding branch has no modes.
```

**Why:** Without this, later statements about \(B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\), cell mass, and main/dual nonalignment can be misread as requiring plus and dual modes to lie in the same physical cell interval.

---

## Edit 2 — Clarify the decomposition used in the cell-mass lemma

**Problem:** O1 defines \(B_r\) as a full canonical cell vector including \(B_r^{\rm bg}\) and \(B_r^E\), while Lemma `\ref{lem:fixed-width-cell-mass-implies-z-derivative-row}` also assumes a full canonical cell error \(E_{\rm cell}\). This is fine only if the decomposition

\[
F(t)=\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}+E_{\rm cell}(t)
\]

is explicit. Otherwise future readers may double-count background/error terms.

**Where:** In Lemma `\ref{lem:fixed-width-cell-mass-implies-z-derivative-row}`, after:

```latex
Assume the fixed-width cell setup of
Definition~\ref{def:O1-fixed-width-cell-nonrecurrence}.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
Assume the cell vector \(B=(B_r)_r\) and the residual \(E_{\rm cell}\) are chosen
so that on \([-R,R]\)
\[
Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)
=
\sum_r B_r e^{-it\xi_r}
+
E_{\rm cell}(t),
\]
where \(\xi_r\) is the representative center of the \(r\)-th cell.  In the
inclusive canonical formulation, the known background and \(E_2\)-type pieces
assigned to cells are included in \(B_r\), and only the remaining intra-cell,
tail, truncation, or unassigned pieces are included in \(E_{\rm cell}\).  In a
perturbative formulation, the omitted canonical pieces must instead be included
in \(E_{\rm cell}\) and satisfy the stated \(L^2\)-smallness bound.
```

**Why:** This makes O1 theorem-use unambiguous and prevents a serious bookkeeping error.

---

## Edit 3 — Add the safe primitive-bound hypothesis explicitly to the Gate 2 theorem

**Problem:** The Gate 2 theorem invokes Lemma `\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe}`, whose proof requires

\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C
\]

on the normalized source interval. The theorem currently says “assume the lemma holds on normalized source subintervals,” but it should explicitly state that the lemma’s safe hypotheses are available.

**Where:** In Theorem `\ref{thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity}`, after:

```latex
Assume source Lipschitz control
\[
\|u'\|_{L^\infty(I)}\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]
```

**Insert:**

```latex
Assume also that every source interval \(J\) produced by
Lemma~\ref{lem:source-large-interval-l2-anisotropy}, after normalization to the
model interval of Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe}, satisfies the
safe primitive bounds
\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]
or else that these bounds are recovered on a slightly shrunken interval by
Lemma~\ref{lem:local-primitive-recovery-from-l2-small-g}.
```

Then replace:

```latex
and assume Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe} holds on normalized
source subintervals with loss \(Q^{C_R}\).
```

with:

```latex
and assume Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe} is applied on such
normalized source subintervals with loss \(Q^{C_R}\).
```

**Why:** This prevents overclaiming that \(u,u'\)-transfer alone is sufficient in the **safe** proof. The primitive-free recovery is recorded, but not silently assumed.

---

## Edit 4 — Strengthen the O1 projected fallback warning

**Problem:** O1 states a projected fallback when more than \(R+2\) cells are used. It should explicitly say that raw cell mass may not imply the jet lower bound unless the Gram/projection lower bound is verified.

**Where:** In `Remark~\ref{rem:raw-projected-cell-formulations-O1}`, after:

```latex
where \(\Pi_{\le R+1}\) is the stable projection to cell polynomial modes of
degree at most \(R+1\).  This projected statement is the cell-coordinate form
of direct \(Z_\alpha\)-jet nonflatness.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
In particular, if the number of cells substantially exceeds the degree visible
to the \(R+1\) derivative row, the raw lower bound
\[
\sum_r|B_r|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]
is not by itself enough.  One must either prove the projected lower bound above
or prove a Gram/frame estimate showing that the raw cell energy has polynomially
large projection onto the derivative-visible subspace.
```

**Why:** This prevents a future false implication from raw high-frequency cell energy to \(\mathbf z'\)-nonflatness.

---

## Edit 5 — Add a precision caveat to the ordinary zero-separated transfer theorem

**Problem:** The proof of ordinary zero-separated source-complexity transfer uses local zero count and dyadic annuli. This is fine for the zeta completed scalar, but for a general \(\Xi\) the local zero count should be included as an explicit hypothesis.

**Where:** In Lemma `\ref{lem:ordinary-zero-separated-source-complexity-transfer}`, after:

```latex
where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is a fixed finite expression in the completed
logarithmic derivative
\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s)
\]
and finitely many derivatives \(L^{(r)}(s)\), together with regular
gamma/background terms and no denominators other than those implicit in
\(L=\Xi'/\Xi\).
```

**Insert:**

```latex
Assume moreover the standard local zero-count estimate for the completed
scalar:
\[
\#\{\rho\in\mathcal Z_\Xi: |s-\rho|\le R_0\}
\le Q^C(1+R_0)
\]
through the polynomial range of \(R_0\) used below.
```

**Why:** This makes the lemma self-contained and avoids silently assuming a zeta-specific zero-count property for an abstract completed scalar.

---

## Edit 6 — Add an explicit “not a theorem input” warning to numerical evidence

**Problem:** The empirical O1 section is good, but the status table already says “diagnostic evidence only.” Add one line to prevent future proof use.

**Where:** At the end of `Remark~\ref{rem:empirical-support-o1-local-amplitude-cell-tests}`, after:

```latex
They should not be cited as evidence for any theorem requiring uniform
polynomial lower bounds over all admissible heights.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
Accordingly, no later theorem may invoke these computations as a hypothesis or
as a proof substitute for O1; they are only adversarial model checks.
```

**Why:** This prevents numerical evidence from becoming an implicit theorem.

---

## Edit 7 — Add a one-line guardrail to D4 residual valuation ledger

**Problem:** The D4 valuation ledger is good, but the key danger is absolute residual floors. Add an explicit “same-scale terms are not errors” warning.

**Where:** In `Definition~\ref{def:d4-residual-valuation-ledger}`, after the paragraph introducing \(\mathbf R_{\rm same},\mathbf R_{\rm val},\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\).

**Insert:**

```latex
Terms with the same anisotropy-linear valuation as the leading row are not
automatically errors.  They must first be absorbed into the effective leading
matrix \(L_{\rm eff}\).  Only the component remaining after this absorption is
eligible to be estimated as a residual.
```

**Why:** This prevents accidentally imposing an impossible smallness estimate on same-scale linear terms that should change the leading matrix instead.

---

# Final assessment

I would not make broader changes. I found no critical need to modify the title, abstract, introduction, conclusion, Gate 2 theorem structure, wall-escape theorem, O1/O2/O3 dependency theorem, or carrier-quotient D4 route.

The critical fixes are the seven guardrails above. They address the only places where future work could accidentally introduce an error:

\[
\boxed{\text{plus/dual cell support ambiguity}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{cell vector versus residual double-counting}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{safe primitive bounds silently omitted from Gate 2}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{raw cell energy incorrectly used when projection is needed}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{zero-count assumption hidden in ordinary transfer}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{diagnostic numerics mistaken for proof input}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{same-scale D4 terms mistakenly treated as residual errors}}
\]
